# Project Memory ŌĆö Pyrycode

Repo-level session memory. Read this at the start of every session.

## What's Built

> **Convention (2026-05-10 onwards):** Per-ticket implementation summaries live in [`docs/knowledge/codebase/<ticket-number>.md`](knowledge/codebase/), one file per ticket. The blocks below are pre-2026-05-10 history ŌĆö frozen, kept for context. See [`docs/knowledge/codebase/README.md`](knowledge/codebase/README.md) for the convention rationale.

### Codebase (E2E regression coverage, ticket #263)
- **`internal/e2e/conv_sweep_test.go` ŌĆö single-test e2e that pins the conversations sweep loop's daemon-wiring + clean-shutdown invariants at the binary boundary.** Closes the gap that `internal/sessions.TestPool_Run_RegistersSweepLoop_HappyPath` cannot reach: the in-package test directly sets `pool.convReg` / `pool.convRegistryPath` after `helperPoolWithSleepArgs(t)` and exercises `Pool.Run`'s `if p.convReg != nil` arm, so a regression in `cmd/pyry/main.go`'s `sessions.Config` construction (e.g. forgetting to wire `ConversationsRegistry` or `ConversationsRegistryPath`) would silently leave `p.convReg == nil`, the in-package test would still pass, and production would lose auto-archive without any test signal. Same regression class as v0.10.1's hang ŌĆö daemon-wiring bugs that unit tests cannot see. Test diff: +98 LOC `internal/e2e/conv_sweep_test.go` (new, build tag `//go:build e2e`). Production diff: zero. Zero new harness infrastructure, zero new dependencies, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change.
- **`TestE2E_ConvSweep_RemovesUnpromotedKeepsPromoted` ŌĆö single-direction test, no subtests.** Seeds two conversations into `<home>/.pyry/test/conversations.json` via the canonical `conversations.Registry.Save` (NOT raw JSON): one promoted (`ID=11111111ŌĆ”, IsPromoted=true, Name=&"kept-channel", Cwd="/seed-promoted"`) and one unpromoted (`ID=22222222ŌĆ”, IsPromoted=false, Cwd="/seed-unpromoted"`), both at `LastUsedAt = time.Now().UTC().Add(-60 * 24 * time.Hour)` (60 days idle, well past the 30-day archive threshold so the `>=` boundary is not load-bearing). Spawns pyry via `StartIn(t, home, "-pyry-conv-sweep-interval=100ms")` against the #262 flag. Polls `conversations.Load(convPath)` every 50 ms with a 5 s deadline until `len(loaded.List()) == 1`; asserts `survivors[0].ID` is the promoted UUID and `survivors[0].IsPromoted == true`. Then `h.Stop(t)` (SIGTERM ŌåÆ 3 s grace ŌåÆ SIGKILL ŌåÆ 1 s grace = 4 s upper bound, comfortably under AC#4's 5 s budget) plus `processAlive(pid) == false` plus a panic / `runtime/` / `goroutine ` substring scan over `h.Stderr.Bytes()`.
- **Seeded via `conversations.Registry`, NOT a local mirror struct.** `restart_test.go` mirrors the (unexported) sessions registry shape locally because `internal/sessions`'s on-disk types are unexported and exporting them solely for one test would invert the dependency direction. This test does have a choice ŌĆö the `conversations` package's `Registry` / `Conversation` / `Load` / `Save` / `Create` / `List` are all exported ŌĆö so using the canonical writer kills two failure modes at once: (a) field-tag drift between a test's mirror struct and production, (b) atomic-write semantics (the seed file lands via the same temp+rename rename the daemon will use, not via raw `os.WriteFile`). Side benefit: the seed file exercises the same `Save` path that the sweep itself will exercise on tick ŌĆö the test's "before" and "after" use the same on-disk codec.
- **Polling cadence: 50 ms gap, 5 s deadline.** ~10 chances inside the 5 s budget against a 100 ms tick. Larger gaps risk flaky misses on slow CI runners; smaller gaps add no signal. The `time.NewTicker` inside `RunSweepLoop` does NOT fire immediately ŌĆö first tick is at +interval (~100 ms after `Pool.Run` registers the goroutine), well inside the envelope. Atomic-rename `Save` semantics inside `internal/conversations/registry.go` (temp file + Chmod + Encode + Sync + Close + Rename) make the cross-process read race-clean: each `Load` either sees the pre-Save bytes or the post-Save bytes, never a torn write. If the test starts flaking on heavily-loaded macOS CI runners, the right fix is to raise the budget (e.g. 10 s), NOT to lower the tick interval ŌĆö the daemon's `time.NewTicker` cadence is what's being measured, and a sub-100 ms interval would start interacting with the runner's scheduler granularity.
- **`h.Stop` plus `processAlive` plus stderr scan, not just `h.Stop`.** Stop is the harness's blessed graceful shutdown path: SIGTERM ŌåÆ daemon's `signal.NotifyContext` cancels parent ctx ŌåÆ `Pool.Run`'s errgroup ctx cancels ŌåÆ `RunSweepLoop`'s `<-ctx.Done()` returns nil ŌåÆ errgroup `Wait` returns ŌåÆ supervisor `Run` returns ŌåÆ `cmd.Process` exits ŌåÆ `cmd.Wait` returns ŌåÆ `doneCh` closes ŌåÆ Stop returns. Two follow-up assertions cover the failure modes Stop alone doesn't fail on: (a) Stop hit the killGrace path with `doneCh` still open (Stop only `t.Logf`'s that case, doesn't fail) ŌĆö `processAlive(pid)` catches it, and (b) the daemon panicked on its way down (Stop doesn't inspect stderr) ŌĆö the panic / `runtime/` / `goroutine ` substring scan, lifted verbatim from `cli_verbs_test.go`'s vocabulary, catches it. Neither case is hypothetical ŌĆö (a) is the regression class this whole test exists for; (b) is the v0.10.1 incident shape.
- **No fresh-and-unpromoted control entry; no goroutine-leak assertion.** A third "fresh, unpromoted" seed would prove the predicate is `IsPromoted`-aware AND `LastUsedAt`-aware in the same test ŌĆö already covered by the in-package `pool_conv_sweep_test.go` (which seeds `archivable=2, fresh=1` against the same predicate). This e2e exists to cover the daemon-wiring gap, not to re-assert predicate semantics. AC#4 explicitly says "a clean process exit is sufficient evidence" ŌĆö adding `runtime.NumGoroutine()` checks would require probing inside the daemon process from out-of-process, which we don't have access to.
- **Polling-timeout failure dumps the on-disk file via `mustReadFile`.** The most common failure mode if the daemon-side wiring regresses is the unpromoted entry never gets removed; the dumped file is critical for diagnosing whether the daemon never wrote the file (wiring regression, file unchanged) vs. wrote a wrong-shape file (envelope regression). Setup errors (`reg.Save`, `conversations.Load` while polling) ŌåÆ `t.Fatalf`. Post-Stop assertions (`processAlive`, stderr scan) ŌåÆ `t.Errorf` (not `Fatalf`) so a panic-on-shutdown failure still reports the still-alive case alongside, instead of one masking the other.
- **No new harness extensions.** All scaffolding reused: `newRegistryHome` from `restart_test.go` (its sessions-registry path return value is intentionally discarded ŌĆö we want only the `<home>/.pyry/test/` mkdir for `conversations.json`'s parent); `mustReadFile` from `restart_test.go` for the polling-timeout diagnostic dump; `processAlive` from `harness_test.go`; the panic / `runtime/` / `goroutine ` substring vocabulary from `cli_verbs_test.go`. Convpath derived locally as `filepath.Join(home, ".pyry", "test", "conversations.json")` ŌĆö no helper extracted (one consumer; "extract at three").
- **No new ADR.** Architect's spec ┬¦ "Open questions" is "None." Two implementer-choice points (whether to extend `newRegistryHome` to also return convPath; whether to set `Cwd` on the seed entries) ŌĆö chose lighter-touch (no helper edit) and non-empty Cwds (mildly more useful in failure diagnostics ŌĆö the dumped file shows which seeded entry survived). Both stylistic.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Any control-verb invocation (`create_conversation`, `promote_conversation`) ŌĆö Track C's domain, will get its own e2e once C1ŌĆōC5 ship. WS-level broadcast of the `conversation_updated` envelope ŌĆö Track C. Goroutine-leak assertions inside the daemon ŌĆö out-of-process can't observe that surface; AC explicitly accepts clean process exit as sufficient evidence. A custom shutdown helper ŌĆö `h.Stop`'s 4 s SIGTERMŌåÆSIGKILL escalation is already inside AC#4's 5 s budget. A fresh-and-unpromoted control entry ŌĆö predicate semantics are already pinned by `pool_conv_sweep_test.go`. Relying on the in-package `withConvSweepInterval` helper ŌĆö that seam was deleted in #262 and is unreachable from a subprocess by design.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ `conv_sweep_test.go` ŌĆö conversations sweep loop e2e (#263)](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/features/conversations-auto-archive.md ┬¦ E2E test (#263)](knowledge/features/conversations-auto-archive.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/263-e2e-conv-sweep-loop.md`](specs/architecture/263-e2e-conv-sweep-loop.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 wiring, ticket #262)
- **`-pyry-conv-sweep-interval` flag + `sessions.Config.SweepInterval` plumbing** ŌĆö adds a real seam through `sessions.Config` so out-of-process e2e tests (downstream of #251) can drive the conversations sweep loop at ~100ms without waiting an hour. Default behaviour is unchanged when the flag is absent ŌĆö production keeps `conversations.SweepInterval` (one hour). Production diff: +13 LOC `cmd/pyry/main.go` (new map entry, `fs.Duration`, `Config.SweepInterval` field set, one help line) + 25 LOC `internal/sessions/pool.go` (new Config field, new Pool field, New-time fallback, removed package-var seam). Test diff: +47 LOC `internal/sessions/pool_conv_sweep_test.go` (`withConvSweepInterval` helper removed, two new constructor tests added, two existing tests refactored). Zero new dependencies, zero wire-format change, zero behavioural change in production.
- **One seam, not two: package-private `var convSweepInterval` and the `withConvSweepInterval(t, d)` helper are removed.** The original (#243) wiring used a package-level var swapped via `t.Cleanup` save/restore; that works for in-package tests but is unreachable from a subprocess test. Spec considered keeping both as a fallback (Config field plus package var) and rejected ŌĆö dual seams invite future drift (a new test could set one but not the other). In-package tests now set `pool.convSweepInterval = 5*time.Millisecond` directly after `helperPoolWithSleepArgs`, mirroring the existing `pool.convReg` / `pool.convRegistryPath` pattern. PR description carries the "replace, don't keep both" decision per spec ┬¦ 1.
- **`Config.SweepInterval time.Duration`, zero = "use the default."** Field lives in `sessions.Config` immediately after `ConversationsRegistryPath` ŌĆö same lifecycle, same nil-registry coupling (ignored when `ConversationsRegistry` is nil; the sweep goroutine doesn't run in that case). `Pool.convSweepInterval` mirrors it on the Pool; resolved once in `New` via a hoisted local: `sweepInterval := cfg.SweepInterval; if sweepInterval <= 0 { sweepInterval = conversations.SweepInterval }`. The `<= 0` (not `== 0`) check makes negative inputs degrade gracefully to the production default rather than feeding an invalid interval into `RunSweepLoop` (whose precondition is `interval > 0`). Read-only after `New` ŌĆö no lock needed (matches `convReg` / `convRegistryPath` / `activeCap`).
- **`Pool.Run` switches `interval := convSweepInterval` ŌåÆ `interval := p.convSweepInterval`.** The `interval` local is retained because the closure passed to `g.Go` captures it; could equally be inlined. No semantic change beyond the seam swap. The `if p.convReg != nil` gate is unchanged; `RunSweepLoop`'s `nil`-on-cancel return path is unchanged.
- **`-pyry-conv-sweep-interval duration` flag in `cmd/pyry/main.go`.** Visible, listed in `printHelp()` after `-pyry-idle-timeout` with `(testing; 0 = production default of 1h)`. The flag is for testing but is not actively dangerous in production, and a visible flag is simpler to reason about than a hidden one ŌĆö operator who sets it gets the immediate help-text annotation. Default is `0` (NOT `conversations.SweepInterval`) so "user did not set the flag" and "use the default" share one definition ŌĆö the zero-value fallback inside `sessions.New`. Two definitions (flag default = 1h AND Config-zero = 1h) would invite drift. `pyry-conv-sweep-interval` is also added to `pyryFlagValues` so `splitArgs` consumes both the flag and its value before the claude-args split (same shape as `-pyry-idle-timeout` / `-pyry-active-cap`).
- **`flag.Duration` rejects malformed values at parse time.** `-pyry-conv-sweep-interval=banana` produces a `flag.Parse` error that `runSupervisor` already returns ŌĆö no new error path. Negative values pass `flag.Duration` (they're valid `time.Duration` values) but `cfg.SweepInterval > 0` in the New-time fallback treats `<= 0` as "use the default," so negative inputs degrade gracefully.
- **Two new constructor tests in `pool_conv_sweep_test.go`.** `TestPool_New_HonoursConfigSweepInterval` sets `Config.SweepInterval = 7*time.Millisecond`, calls `New`, asserts `pool.convSweepInterval == 7*time.Millisecond`. `TestPool_New_DefaultSweepIntervalWhenConfigZero` omits `SweepInterval`, asserts `pool.convSweepInterval == conversations.SweepInterval`. Pure constructor tests ŌĆö no `Pool.Run`, no goroutines, no timing. Both use a minimal Config with `Bootstrap.ClaudeBin = "/bin/sleep"` (no real claude needed; `New` doesn't spawn) and a discard logger. Pin the resolution rule (Config wins, zero falls back to constant) so future changes to the resolution path can't accidentally regress.
- **Existing tests refactored, not duplicated.** `TestPool_Run_RegistersSweepLoop_HappyPath` now sets `pool.convSweepInterval = 5*time.Millisecond` directly after `helperPoolWithSleepArgs(t)`; the prior `withConvSweepInterval(t, 5*time.Millisecond)` call is gone. `TestPool_Run_NoSweepLoopWhenRegistryNil` drops the override entirely ŌĆö it exercises the `convReg == nil` branch, so the interval is never read; an assignment would serve no behavioural purpose (spec ┬¦ 6 left this implementer's choice; chose to drop). Behavioural assertions unchanged.
- **No `cmd/pyry`-level unit test for the flag-to-Config plumbing.** `runSupervisor` has only integration-tier coverage (`internal/e2e`), and the e2e test that actually consumes the new flag lives downstream of #251. Per spec ┬¦ "Testing strategy ŌåÆ What is NOT tested at this layer" ŌĆö the production-side wiring is the AC for #262; the `pyry --help` text isn't asserted on either (no existing test asserts on `printHelp()` output).
- **No new ADR.** Spec ┬¦ "Open questions" is "None." Two implementer-choice points (hoisted local vs. inline IIFE in `New`; whether to keep the no-op `pool.convSweepInterval = ŌĆ”` assignment in the `convReg == nil` test) ŌĆö chose the hoisted local (reads marginally more naturally) and dropped the no-op assignment. Both stylistic; either choice was correct per spec.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Hidden flag (`os.Getenv("PYRY_CONV_SWEEP_INTERVAL")` instead) ŌĆö visible flag is simpler. Minimum-bound enforcement on the flag value (e.g. clamp to `>= 1ms`) ŌĆö let the test pick whatever interval it needs; production default protects users. Configurable threshold (`archiveIdleThreshold`) ŌĆö separate ticket if asked. Refactoring `runSupervisor`'s flag declarations into a sub-helper ŌĆö the file already follows the long-`fs.Duration`-list shape (#88 / #155 precedent); extract on the third instance, not the second. Adding metrics on the resolved interval ŌĆö no metrics surface yet.
- See [knowledge/features/conversations-auto-archive.md ┬¦ Single seam: `Config.SweepInterval` (#262)](knowledge/features/conversations-auto-archive.md), [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/262-pyry-conv-sweep-interval-flag.md`](specs/architecture/262-pyry-conv-sweep-interval-flag.md).

### Codebase (E2E release-acceptance gate, ticket #260)
- **`cmd/pyry/update_e2e_test.go` ŌĆö single-test e2e happy-path file gating the full `pyry update` chain end-to-end against an in-process fake release server.** First e2e coverage of the `pyry update` subcommand (#189) and its #190 daemon-restart wiring; locks the v0.10.1-shaped supervisor-startup-hang regression class at the release-acceptance tier (the precise evicted-bootstrap reproducer is exercised by `internal/e2e/bootstrap_warm_start_test.go` from #253). Test diff: +420 LOC `cmd/pyry/update_e2e_test.go` (new, build tag `//go:build (darwin || linux) && e2e_update`). Production diff: zero. No new harness infrastructure ŌĆö the `update_test.go` helpers (`fakeRelease`, `newFakeReleaseServer`, `buildTarGzForTest`) are reused verbatim because both files live in `package main` of `cmd/pyry` and `update_test.go` carries no build tag, so the AC's "extracted into a reusable helper" criterion is met structurally with zero textual extraction. Zero new dependencies, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change.
- **`TestUpdate_HappyPath_E2E` drives `doUpdate` directly with a real running daemon stapled onto the `runRestart` seam.** Phase 1: `buildPyryBinE2E` (honours `PYRY_E2E_BIN`) ŌåÆ `os.MkdirTemp("", "pyry-up-")` (sun_path-safe; `t.TempDir()` overflows macOS APFS's 104-byte limit when extended with `/pyry.sock`) ŌåÆ install srcBin into `<home>/bin/pyry` ŌåÆ spawn daemon 1 with `cmd.Stdin = nil` (Go's `os/exec` wires `/dev/null` automatically ŌĆö the structural satisfaction of AC#2's "stdin closed" requirement) ŌåÆ `waitForSocketE2E` until the control socket dials. Phase 2: `fakeRelease(t, "v999.0.0", runtime.GOOS, runtime.GOARCH, srcBytes)` + `newFakeReleaseServer(t, ...)` ŌåÆ call `doUpdate` with `Fetcher.BaseURL`/`releaseBaseURL` pointed at the test server, `replace = update.AtomicReplace`, `executablePath = func() string { return targetPath }`, a `RestartProbe` whose platform flag (`LaunchdPlistExists` on darwin, `SystemdUnitExists` on linux) makes `DetectRestartCommand` emit non-nil argv so `runRestart` fires. Phase 3: `runRestart` ignores the launchctl/systemctl argv it's handed and stands in for what supervisor-restart would do ŌĆö `stopDaemonE2E(cmd1)` (SIGTERM ŌåÆ 3s grace ŌåÆ SIGKILL ŌåÆ 1s grace) ŌåÆ `spawnDaemonE2E` from the same `targetPath` (now holding the new bytes via `AtomicReplace`'s rename) ŌåÆ `waitForSocketE2E` for the new socket. Phase 4: assert inode changed (`syscall.Stat_t.Ino` before vs after; `os.Rename` swaps in a fresh inode), PID changed (`cmd1.Process.Pid != cmd2.Process.Pid`), `pyry status` Phase advances past `starting` within 3s, `pyry sessions list` exits 0 within 10s.
- **`waitForPhasePastStartingE2E` polls Phase, doesn't single-shot.** `supervisor.Run` sets Phase to Running asynchronously after `onSpawn` fires; the control socket can be dialable a few ms before that. Single-shot `pyry status` after socket-ready would race the Phase update and flake. The poll loop runs `runVerbE2E(... "status")` every 50ms up to a 3s deadline, parses the `Phase:` line via `parsePhaseE2E` (returns `(string, bool)` ŌĆö distinguishes "no Phase: line" from "Phase: line present but empty"), returns on first non-`starting` value, and `t.Fatalf`s on timeout with the captured stdout. A v0.10.1-shaped hang would never clear within 3s; healthy startup clears in 50ŌĆō200 ms.
- **`runRestart` is a kill-and-respawn stand-in, NOT a launchctl/systemctl exec.** The test never touches the operator's real launchd/systemd ŌĆö see lessons.md "E2E against the operator's real systemd `--user` / launchd `gui/<uid>`". The probe-makes-argv-non-nil shape is what proves the wiring, not the argv content; the kill-and-respawn shape is what proves the daemon survives a binary swap, not which CLI executable triggers it.
- **Drive `doUpdate` directly from `package main` over a `--release-base-url` flag or `PYRY_RELEASE_BASE_URL` env var.** Adding either to production code would be the "hidden env var added 'just for the test'" pattern lessons.md rejects. Importing the package from `internal/e2e` is structurally impossible because `cmd/pyry` is `package main`. Same-package e2e is the only seam that satisfies both the AC and the env-var-discipline rule. Cost: the `internal/e2e` harness is unreachable, so the spawn/socket-dial/teardown scaffolding is replicated inline (~120 LOC of helpers, all `_E2E`-suffixed to avoid collision with `update_test.go`); same trade `update_test.go` already accepted for `buildTarGzForTest`/`fakeRelease`/`newFakeReleaseServer`.
- **`spawnDaemonE2E` returns stdout AND stderr buffers; both surface in readiness-failure diagnostics.** `bytes.Buffer` is fine here ŌĆö the test goroutine reads only after `waitForSocketE2E` returns (or after `cmd.Wait` closes the doneCh). The buffers are only attached to `cmd.Stdout`/`cmd.Stderr` while the child runs; concurrent read happens only after the child has exited. A v0.10.1-shaped hang dumps both streams in the failure message so the operator-style log comes through verbatim.
- **`cmd1Stopped` flag avoids double-stop in `t.Cleanup`.** The closure-side stop in `runRestart` and the `t.Cleanup`-side stop both target the same `cmd1`; the boolean ensures only one fires. Pairs with the `cmd2 == nil` guard in the post-test cleanup that handles the "runRestart never fired" case (where `doUpdate` errored before the restart step). `stopDaemonE2E` is also internally idempotent (short-circuits on `<-doneCh`), so the guards are belt-and-suspenders.
- **No new ADR.** Architect's spec ┬¦ "Open questions" is "None"; every design choice is anchored in an existing precedent (`update_test.go`'s helper-reuse, `internal/e2e/restart_test.go`'s sun_path-safe HOME, `internal/e2e/harness.go`'s childEnv shape, lessons.md's env-var-discipline + don't-touch-real-launchd rules).
- **Out of scope, by design.** Failure-path tests (separate ticket ŌĆö checksum mismatch, fetch failure, restart failure, permission-denied AtomicReplace, etc., all leaning on this ticket's `fakeRelease`/`newFakeReleaseServer`). Cross-architecture updates. A different `Version` string for the served binary (the happy path needs only "different inode + working binary", not behavioural drift). Refactoring `update_test.go`'s helpers into a new file or package (the AC's reusability requirement is met structurally ŌĆö same package, no build tag ŌĆö without textual extraction). Touching the operator's real launchd/systemd. Adding a `--release-base-url` flag or `PYRY_RELEASE_BASE_URL` env var to production code. CI tag wiring (existing `e2e_install` job pattern is the template; ops adds an `e2e_update` invocation when ready).
- See [knowledge/features/pyry-update-command.md ┬¦ E2E happy-path (#260)](knowledge/features/pyry-update-command.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/260-e2e-update-happy-path.md`](specs/architecture/260-e2e-update-happy-path.md).

### Codebase (E2E regression coverage, ticket #253)
- **`internal/e2e/bootstrap_warm_start_test.go` ŌĆö two-test e2e regression file pinning [ADR 016](knowledge/decisions/016-bootstrap-ignores-persisted-lifecycle-state.md) into CI.** Locks the v0.10.1 supervisor-startup-hang regression class (`Pool.New` ignoring persisted `lifecycle_state` on the bootstrap session) at the e2e tier so a future refactor that re-introduces `parseLifecycleState` for the bootstrap path fails CI on the user-visible signature (`Started at: 0001-01-01T00:00:00Z`, `Uptime: 2562047h47m16ŌĆ”`) rather than slipping through to release. Test diff: +212 LOC `internal/e2e/bootstrap_warm_start_test.go` (new, build tag `//go:build e2e`). Production diff: zero. No new harness infrastructure; all helpers (`newRegistryHome`, `writeRegistry`, `readRegistry`, `mustReadFile`, `waitForBootstrap`, `waitForSessionState`, `registryFile`/`registryEntry`) reused verbatim from `restart_test.go`/`cap_test.go`. Zero new dependencies, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change.
- **`TestE2E_BootstrapWarmStart_IgnoresEvictedOnDisk` ŌĆö drives the v0.10.1 regression class end-to-end via a two-phase mutate-and-restart shape.** Phase A: `StartIn` cold so the daemon picks its own bootstrap UUID and writes the registry, `waitForBootstrap` to capture it, `Stop`. Phase B: `readRegistry` / mutate `LifecycleState = "evicted"` on the bootstrap entry / `writeRegistry` between the two daemon lifetimes (race-free ŌĆö no concurrent writer). Phase C: `StartIn` warm against the mutated registry, poll `pyry status` for `Phase: running` within 5 s. Pre-fix the daemon parks indefinitely in `runEvicted`; post-fix the load layer forces `stateActive`, `Supervisor.Run` spawns claude, and Phase reaches running in ~1ŌĆō2 s. Negative-greps the failure-mode signatures: `Started at:    0001-01-01T00:00:00Z` and `Uptime:        2562047h47m16` (prefix-match; the rendered sentinel is the full `2562047h47m16.854775807s` because `Duration.Round(time.Second)` of `math.MaxInt64` overflows back to the input ŌĆö prefix-matching keeps the assertion robust to a future change that clamps before rounding). Cross-checks the wire view via `pyry sessions list --json` decoded into `[]control.SessionInfo`, asserts the bootstrap entry's `state == "active"` (`--json` form, not the table ŌĆö rides a stable wire field rather than tabwriter alignment).
- **`TestE2E_BootstrapWarmStart_NonBootstrapEvictedPersists` ŌĆö pins the carve-out boundary.** Single-phase: pre-seed two entries (bootstrap as `active`, non-bootstrap UUID `22222222ŌĆ”` as `evicted`), `StartIn`, `waitForSessionState` polls disk for the non-bootstrap UUID staying `"evicted"` across the warm-load reconciliation pass (5 s envelope). The on-disk check is the canonical observation point ŌĆö non-bootstrap sessions live on disk between minting and the next consumer-driven `Activate`, so disk is what the next process boundary will see. Cross-checks the bootstrap stays `active` via `sessions list --json` to confirm the non-bootstrap-evicted seed didn't cross-contaminate the bootstrap behaviour. A future refactor that "simplifies" the load layer to ignore `lifecycle_state` for *all* sessions trips this test even though Test 1 still passes.
- **Two-phase shape over pre-seeded-only or `-pyry-idle-timeout=1s` alternatives.** A pre-seeded registry with `bootstrap=true, lifecycle_state="evicted"` reproduces the bug structurally but not the user's trigger path (machine boots ŌåÆ daemon starts ŌåÆ idle eviction fires ŌåÆ daemon restarts via launchd / systemd / `pyry update` ŌåÆ hang). The two-phase mutate-and-restart is faithful to that flow and lets the bootstrap UUID be daemon-authored rather than test-invented. The mutation step edits `lifecycle_state` only, leaving `UUID` / `created_at` / `last_active_at` / `bootstrap` intact ŌĆö minimum-fidelity stand-in for "idle eviction had a chance to fire." The `-pyry-idle-timeout=1s` + cold-eviction alternative works but adds 1ŌĆō2 s of timer waiting and couples the regression to the idle-eviction subsystem (the regression is in the warm-load layer, not the eviction layer).
- **Stdout-grep on `Phase:         running` over the wire client, by precedent.** `internal/e2e/idle_test.go:35` already establishes the stdout-grep idiom for asserting phase. Reusing it keeps the new file's local vocabulary minimal and gives the test the same brittleness profile as the rest of the suite ŌĆö a stdout-format change breaks both `idle_test.go` and `bootstrap_warm_start_test.go` together. The negative `Started at` and `Uptime` greps ride the same vocabulary; whitespace `Phase:         ` (one colon, nine spaces) matches `cmd/pyry/main.go:549`'s format-string verbatim.
- **No new ADR.** Test-only ticket; ADR 016 (the production-side carve-out) was added in #202. The new file references the ADR in its package doc-comment so a future reader of the test lands on the rationale without grepping. The regression-class lesson in `lessons.md ┬¦ "Persisted lifecycle state needs a driver to exit it on warm-start"` gets a fourth bullet documenting the unit-tier-plus-e2e-tier coverage discipline.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Idle-eviction ŌåÆ restart ŌåÆ re-evict cycles (covered by `restart_test.go`). The unit-level load-layer test `TestPool_BootstrapEvictedOnDisk_StartsClaudeOnWarmStart` (already shipped in #204 alongside the production fix). Friendlier `pyry status` rendering for un-initialised supervisors (separate UX ticket; the negative-grep on `0001-01-01T00:00:00Z` is the *failure-mode signature*, not a UX assertion). Defensive `install.sh` post-install check (separately tracked, landed as #203/#204). Generalising the e2e mutate-and-restart pattern into a harness helper (one consumer, "extract at three" ŌĆö keep it in the test file).
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ `bootstrap_warm_start_test.go` ŌĆö bootstrap warm-start carve-out (#253)](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/decisions/016-bootstrap-ignores-persisted-lifecycle-state.md](knowledge/decisions/016-bootstrap-ignores-persisted-lifecycle-state.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/253-e2e-bootstrap-warm-start-ignores-persisted-lifecycle-state.md`](specs/architecture/253-e2e-bootstrap-warm-start-ignores-persisted-lifecycle-state.md).

### Codebase (CLI bug fix, ticket #167)
- **`pyry attach --stdio <id>` reaches `parseAttachArgs` and dispatches to `control.AttachStdio`.** The shared `parseClientFlags` helper used to build a `flag.FlagSet` registering only `-pyry-name` / `-pyry-socket` and call `fs.Parse(args)`, so any unknown flag (`--stdio`, `--create-if-missing`, future sub-verb flags) was rejected at the wrong layer. Fix splits `parseClientFlags` into a walk-and-extract `splitClientFlags` (sibling of `splitArgs`) that peels recognised `-pyry-*` tokens off the front and routes everything else into `rest` verbatim; the FlagSet only sees the extracted pyry args. Both flag orderings work (`pyry attach --stdio <id>` and `pyry attach -pyry-socket=/tmp/foo --stdio <id>`); `--create-if-missing` reaches the parser by the same mechanism. Production diff: +44 LOC `cmd/pyry/main.go` (new `splitClientFlags` + `clientPyryValueFlags` map + rewritten `parseClientFlags` + 3-line `len(rest) > 0` post-checks in `runStatus` / `runLogs` / `runStop`). Test diff: +176 LOC `cmd/pyry/args_test.go` (new `TestSplitClientFlags` table + `TestRunAttachArgPath` regression guard + extended `TestParseClientFlags_ReturnsRest` cases + replaced "unknown flag returns error" subtest). Zero new packages, zero new exported types, zero new dependencies, zero wire-format change.
- **`runStatus` / `runLogs` / `runStop` gain inline `len(rest) > 0` post-checks.** Verbs that take no positionals previously discarded `rest` (`_, _, err := parseClientFlags(...)`); after the fix an unknown flag would land in `rest` and be silently ignored, so each call site adds `if len(rest) > 0 { return fmt.Errorf("<verb>: unexpected arguments: %s", strings.Join(rest, " ")) }`. Inline at three sites ŌĆö no helper extraction (working-principle "don't introduce abstractions beyond what the task requires"; spec Open Question ┬¦1 left this to the developer's judgement, architect preferred inline). `runAttach` / `runSessions` already feed `rest` into verb-specific parsers (`parseAttachArgs`, `parseSessionsNewArgs`, ŌĆ”) which reject malformed input on their own ŌĆö no change needed there.
- **`splitClientFlags` stops at the first non-pyry-* token; `--` flows verbatim into `rest`.** Both `-pyry-socket=/tmp/x` (glued) and `-pyry-socket /tmp/x` (space-separated) forms supported, both `-` and `--` dash prefixes handled (reuses `parseFlagSyntax`). The "stop at first non-pyry-* token" rule matches the existing convention for client verbs ("`-pyry-*` flags must come before sub-verb flags"; see [ADR 010](knowledge/decisions/010-sessions-cli-sub-router.md) and the comment on `runSessions`). It is also the simplest rule that makes `-pyry-socket=ŌĆ” --stdio ŌĆ” <id>` work without introducing a "pyry flags can appear anywhere" feature that would interact poorly with sub-verb parsers. A trailing `-pyry-name` with no value is left in `pyryArgs` so the downstream `flag.FlagSet` produces the same error as before ŌĆö error path unchanged.
- **`fs.SetOutput(io.Discard)` added to `parseClientFlags`.** The previous code didn't set output, so flag parse errors printed to stderr automatically ŌĆö duplicating whatever the caller printed when wrapping. Matches `parseAttachArgs`'s posture. Suppresses the double-print without changing the error return path.
- **`TestRunAttachArgPath` is the regression guard.** Drives the full `runAttach` arg-parse composition (`parseClientFlags` ŌåÆ `parseAttachArgs`) and asserts the dispatch tuple (socket path + selector + `stdio` + `createIfMissing`). Without it, only the e2e harness catches a regression of #167's bug class ŌĆö exactly the gap that let the original bug ship. Eight rows: `--stdio <id>`, `-pyry-socket=ŌĆ” --stdio <id>`, `-pyry-socket ŌĆ” --stdio <id>` (space-separated), `--create-if-missing <id>` alone, `--stdio --create-if-missing <id>` (SDK shape), `-pyry-name ŌĆ” --stdio <id>` composing, bare `<id>`, no args.
- **`TestE2E_AttachStdio_BytesRoundTrip` skip rotated from #167 to #257.** Removing the #167 skip uncovered a pre-existing harness issue: `spawnAttachableDaemon` wires the Go test binary directly as `claude`, so `Pool.Create`'s appended `--session-id <uuid>` reaches the test framework's `flag.Parse()` and is rejected before `TestHelperProcess` runs. `auto_attach.go` (#163) already works around the same problem via a shell wrapper (`echoClaudeScript`); the stdio harness needs the same shape. Per #167's spec ┬¦"E2E removal" ("if it doesn't pass against the fixed binary, surface as a finding rather than fixing here"), surfaced as #257 rather than fixed in this ticket. `TestE2E_AttachStdio_NoPTYInProcessTree` (#162) carries the same rotated skip; both lift in one commit when #257 lands.
- **No new ADR.** The fix is mechanically the simplest of the two approaches the architect's spec listed (walk args manually and extract recognised `-pyry-*` prefixes vs. pre-splitting `args` at the first unknown flag). No design alternative was relitigated; the convention "pyry globals before sub-verb flags" is already pinned by [ADR 010](knowledge/decisions/010-sessions-cli-sub-router.md) and the `splitArgs` precedent.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Fixing the #257 harness bug (separate ticket ŌĆö needs a shell-wrapper claude in `spawnAttachableDaemon`). Refactoring the three `len(rest) > 0` post-checks into a shared `errIfExtraArgs` helper (architect's preferred shape was inline; switch only if the test ordering bites ŌĆö it didn't). Generalizing `splitClientFlags` to support "pyry flags can appear anywhere in argv" (would interact badly with sub-verb parsers; convention is "pyry globals first"). Documenting the lesson in a new ADR (the existing [Unit tests that bypass the global-flag parser hide CLI dispatch bugs](lessons.md#unit-tests-that-bypass-the-global-flag-parser-hide-cli-dispatch-bugs) lesson is the right place; updated with the fix and the unit-level regression-guard pattern).
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ `parseClientFlags` returns positionals (and passes verb-specific flags through)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [lessons.md ┬¦ Unit tests that bypass the global-flag parser hide CLI dispatch bugs](lessons.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/167-client-flag-passthrough.md`](specs/architecture/167-client-flag-passthrough.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 wiring, ticket #243)
- **Daemon-side wiring of the conversations registry + auto-archive sweep loop.** `cmd/pyry/main.go` now loads `~/.pyry/<sanitized-name>/conversations.json` at startup and plumbs the loaded `*Registry` + path through `sessions.Config` into `Pool.Run`'s errgroup, where `RunSweepLoop` (#242) runs as a sibling goroutine to the rotation watcher. First daemon-side runtime consumer of the conversations registry. Production diff: +30 LOC `cmd/pyry/main.go` (new `resolveConversationsRegistryPath` + `Load` call + two new `sessions.Config` fields filled), +57 LOC `internal/sessions/pool.go` (two new `Config` fields + two new `Pool` fields + `New` plumbing + 7-line `g.Go` block in `Run` + `convSweepInterval` package-level test seam + `Run` doc-comment update). Test diff: +23 LOC `cmd/pyry/args_test.go` (new `TestResolveConversationsRegistryPath`), +151 LOC `internal/sessions/pool_conv_sweep_test.go` (new file). Zero new dependencies, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change.
- **`resolveConversationsRegistryPath(name) string` mirrors `resolveRegistryPath` byte-for-byte.** Same `~/.pyry/<sanitized-name>/<file>.json` shape, same `os.UserHomeDir` failure ŌåÆ CWD-relative fallback. Co-located with `resolveRegistryPath` so the symmetry is obvious. Deliberately NOT refactored into a generic `resolveDataPath(name, filename string)` helper ŌĆö pyrycode "simplicity first" wins; two file-shaped resolvers is fine, the third is when extraction becomes interesting.
- **`conversations.Load` runs AFTER `tryAutoAttach`.** Auto-attach short-circuits the supervisor entirely; loading the registry on the auto-attach path would be wasted work and would surface a startup-style error in a foreground attach context. Error wrap is `fmt.Errorf("loading conversations: %w", err)` ŌĆö operator sees `pyry: loading conversations: registry: parse <path>: <inner>` on a malformed file. Missing file is benign cold start (per `Load`'s contract); zero-byte file is also benign.
- **`Load` happens in `cmd/pyry`, NOT inside `sessions.New`.** Per the package layout convention (and the conversations-registry feature doc), `internal/sessions` owns the sessions registry's lifecycle and `internal/conversations` is path-agnostic ŌĆö the consumer (cmd/pyry) does the I/O. Putting `conversations.Load` inside `sessions.New` would couple the two registries' lifecycles inside `internal/sessions`, blurring a boundary the package layout deliberately enforces. Side benefit: existing `helperPool` / `helperPoolWithSleepArgs` test fixtures don't have to deal with on-disk conversations files unless the test explicitly cares.
- **No flag for the conversations registry path.** The sessions registry path is also not flag-controlled ŌĆö both are derived from `-pyry-name` (or `PYRY_NAME`). Operators wanting isolation between pyry instances rely on `-pyry-name` which gives both registries their own subdirectory atomically.
- **`sessions.Config` gains two new fields.** `ConversationsRegistry *conversations.Registry` (nil disables the sweep goroutine ŌĆö preserves existing tests) and `ConversationsRegistryPath string` (passed to `RunSweepLoop`'s `Save` after each non-empty tick; required when registry is non-nil; ignored when nil). Mirrored by unexported `Pool.convReg` / `Pool.convRegistryPath`, set once in `New`, read-only after ŌĆö consulted only by `Pool.Run`. No lock needed (matches the `claudeSessionsDir` pattern). No validation that "non-nil registry implies non-empty path" ŌĆö the cmd/pyry call site sets both atomically; a misuse would surface as a Save failure on the first archive-eligible tick (logged + swallowed by `RunSweepLoop`, loop survives). Defensive validation is "Belt-and-Suspenders without an observed failure mode" ŌĆö skipped per the working principle.
- **No package cycle.** `internal/conversations` does not import `internal/sessions`; verified at architecture time. The `sessions.Config` doc-comment for `ConversationsRegistry` cross-links to `docs/knowledge/features/conversations-registry.md` so the boundary discipline is documented at the source.
- **`Pool.Run` errgroup wiring is a sibling registration to the rotation watcher.** `if p.convReg != nil { g.Go(func() error { return conversations.RunSweepLoop(gctx, p.convReg, p.convRegistryPath, convSweepInterval, p.log) }) }` ŌĆö placed after the rotation watcher block, before `g.Wait()`. Order within `Pool.Run`: bootstrap supervise ŌåÆ rotation watcher (conditional) ŌåÆ sweep loop (conditional) ŌåÆ `g.Wait()`. Order is correctness-irrelevant (errgroup composes them); the sequence reads logically as "session lifecycle ŌåÆ on-disk reconciliation ŌåÆ hygiene tasks." `RunSweepLoop` returns nil on `gctx.Done()`, so the errgroup's first-non-nil-wins post-mortem signal is never claimed by sweep cancellation ŌĆö whatever caused the cancellation surfaces cleanly.
- **`Pool.Run` doc-comment updated.** Two-line patch: `Run blocks until ctx is cancelled, supervising every session in the pool, running the rotation watcher (when ClaudeSessionsDir is set) and the conversations auto-archive sweep loop (when ConversationsRegistry is set) alongside it.` Documents the new conditional alongside the existing rotation-watcher conditional.
- **`var convSweepInterval = conversations.SweepInterval` is the test seam, lives in `pool.go` next to `newProbe`.** Unexported package-level var; production callers never touch it (stays at one hour for the life of the process). Integration test swaps it via `t.Cleanup`-driven save/restore. NOT a `Config.ConversationsSweepInterval` field ŌĆö there is no operator use case for tuning the cadence (one-hour ticks against a 30-day archive threshold), and a knob would create a documentation obligation and a "what does 5 minutes mean" support question for no production benefit. Test seams that have no production callers belong inside the package; package vars in Go are the canonical shape (rotation tests use `newProbe = rotation.DefaultProbe` for the same reason).
- **Integration test in `internal/sessions/pool_conv_sweep_test.go`, NOT `internal/e2e`.** AC explicitly permits in-package coverage when `Pool.Run` is awkward (e.g. the bootstrap session refuses to run without a real claude binary). Two tests, both built on `helperPoolWithSleepArgs(t)` so `Pool.Run` can shutdown cleanly via `/bin/sleep 3600` as the bootstrap (`Pool.Create`'s `--session-id` append breaks sleep, but bootstrap path is unaffected). (1) `TestPool_Run_RegistersSweepLoop_HappyPath` ŌĆö `withConvSweepInterval(t, 5ms)`, seed 2 archivable + 1 fresh via `seedConvRegistry(t, 2, 1)`, set `pool.convReg` / `pool.convRegistryPath` directly (after `helperPoolWithSleepArgs` returns), spawn `Pool.Run` in a goroutine, poll `conversations.Load(path)` until `len(reg2.List()) == 1` (2s deadline ŌåÆ `t.Fatalf` if exceeded), cancel, assert `Pool.Run` returned `nil` or `errors.Is(err, context.Canceled)` within 5s, final `Load` shows the single fresh survivor with `!ShouldArchive(survivor, time.Now())`. (2) `TestPool_Run_NoSweepLoopWhenRegistryNil` ŌĆö `withConvSweepInterval(t, 1ms)`, build pool via `helperPoolWithSleepArgs(t)` without setting `convReg`, run for 50ms, cancel, assert sentinel path under `t.TempDir()` was never created (`fs.ErrNotExist`). Pins the gate explicitly so a regression that flipped the `if p.convReg != nil` polarity would surface here rather than as a confusing failure in an unrelated test.
- **Helpers co-located in the test file (one consumer, not promoted).** `withConvSweepInterval(t, d)` does the t.Cleanup save/restore. `seedConvRegistry(t, archivable, fresh) (*Registry, string)` writes a `conversations.json` to `t.TempDir()` with `archivable` entries at `LastUsedAt = now - 60d` and `fresh` entries at `LastUsedAt = now`, then `Load`s and returns the loaded registry + path. ID format is `%08d-arch-4333-8444-555555555555` / `%08d-fres-4333-8444-555555555555` ŌĆö uses real-shaped UUIDv4 hex literals so `Registry.Save`'s sort-by-`LastUsedAt`-then-ID is deterministic.
- **`TestResolveConversationsRegistryPath` lives in `cmd/pyry/args_test.go`, NOT a new file.** Two-row test: happy path with `t.Setenv("HOME", t.TempDir())` asserts `~/.pyry/test/conversations.json`; `name = "../etc"` asserts the result stays inside `~/.pyry/` (via `filepath.Rel` check that the result doesn't begin with `..`). Pins both the symmetry with `resolveRegistryPath` and the `sanitizeName` traversal-defence integration. CWD-fallback path (`os.UserHomeDir` returning an error) is left untested ŌĆö not reliably reproducible without subprocess-env tricks; matches the precedent set by `TestResolveRegistryPath`.
- **No new ADR.** Architect's spec ┬¦ "Open questions" is "None"; every design choice is anchored in an existing precedent (sessions registry's `Config` plumbing shape, rotation watcher's errgroup-sibling structure, sweep-loop's #242 spec). Decisions are minor and well-covered by the spec + the feature-doc updates.
- **Out of scope, by design.** `--no-conversations` / `--ephemeral` flags to disable the registry (none exist today; AC explicitly says auto-archive runs regardless). Configurable sweep interval flag/env var (#242 already pinned out of scope; restated). Metrics emission for the sweep goroutine (no metrics surface in pyrycode yet; defer until one does). `internal/e2e` test (AC permits in-package). Refactoring `resolveRegistryPath` and `resolveConversationsRegistryPath` into a generic `resolveDataPath` (working-principle "simplicity first" ŌĆö extract at three, not two). Wiring `conversations.Save` to fire on registry mutation events outside the sweep loop (sweep is the only daemon-side mutation source today; non-sweep mutations land when the CLI promotion verb ships, and that ticket owns its own Save discipline). Validating `Config.ConversationsRegistry != nil` requires `Config.ConversationsRegistryPath != ""` (defensive without observed failure mode). Exercising `Pool.Run` shutdown on a real claude binary (`/bin/sleep 3600` is the test precedent for "Pool.Run blocks, ctx cancellation tears down" without involving claude).
- See [knowledge/features/conversations-auto-archive.md ┬¦ Daemon wiring (#243)](knowledge/features/conversations-auto-archive.md), [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/243-conv-daemon-wiring.md`](specs/architecture/243-conv-daemon-wiring.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #242)
- **`internal/conversations/sweep_loop.go` ŌĆö `RunSweepLoop(ctx, reg, path, interval, log) error` + unexported `sweepOnce` + exported `SweepInterval = time.Hour`.** New file (~63 LOC including doc comments). The I/O wrapper around the pure `Sweep` primitive (#237) ŌĆö owns the ticker, the conditional `Save` (only on non-zero count), and the INFO-on-archive / ERROR-on-Save-failure logging contract. Daemon-side wiring (loading `conversations.json` at startup, plumbing `*Registry` through `Pool.Run`'s errgroup, choosing the registry path) is sibling ticket #243; this ticket only owns the loop body in isolation. Production diff: +63 LOC `sweep_loop.go` (new). Test diff: +327 LOC `sweep_loop_test.go` (new). Zero new dependencies (`go.mod` unchanged), zero changes to existing methods, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change.
- **Loop body mirrors `internal/sessions/rotation/watcher.go:Run`** ŌĆö `t := time.NewTicker(interval); defer t.Stop(); for { select { case <-ctx.Done(): return nil; case <-t.C: sweepOnce(reg, path, log) } }`. One delta from the watcher: this loop returns `nil` on ctx cancellation where the watcher returns `ctx.Err()`. Both are valid errgroup citizens; AC pins `nil` for this loop because returning `ctx.Err()` (== `context.Canceled` or `context.DeadlineExceeded`) on a clean shutdown would compete in the "first non-nil wins" errgroup race with whatever caused the cancellation, blurring the post-mortem signal.
- **`sweepOnce` factored out as the single-tick body.** Lets unit tests drive Sweep + Save + log deterministically without spinning a ticker; the loop is then a thin contract over `sweepOnce` (interval, ctx-cancellation, return value). Body: `n := Sweep(reg, time.Now()); if n == 0 { return }; if err := reg.Save(path); err != nil { log.Error("conversations: sweep save failed", "err", err, "archived", n); return }; log.Info("conversations: archived idle conversations", "count", n)`. Returns nothing ŌĆö Sweep cannot fail, Save's error is swallowed-and-logged per AC, no error to propagate.
- **`if n == 0` short-circuit is the no-op-tick contract.** Without it, hourly fsyncs would churn on a fully-fresh registry indefinitely. Pinned at the unit level by `TestSweepOnce/no-op-tick` (asserts `os.Stat(path)` returns `fs.ErrNotExist`) AND at the loop level by `TestRunSweepLoop_NoOpDoesNotSave` (sleeps through Ōēź10 ticks at 1ms interval and asserts the same). Belt-and-suspenders is intentional: a regression that called Save unconditionally would only be caught by the unit test and could be papered over.
- **Save errors are ALWAYS non-fatal.** A failed `reg.Save` on a non-zero-count tick logs ERROR with the wrapped error and the count that *would have been* persisted, then continues. The next tick will retry. Disk file stays one hour stale; acceptable for an hourly loop. Stale-disk note for sibling #243: if Save fails on tick T and never recovers before the daemon exits, in-memory state has the deletions but the on-disk file does not. On next startup the entries reappear in memory and re-archive on the first tick. Idempotent; no data loss; one extra archive log.
- **No final on-shutdown sweep.** AC explicit. Rationale is durability symmetry: a final on-shutdown sweep would persist deletions that wouldn't have happened until up to one hour later under steady-state operation; not worth the extra complexity (and the failure mode of a sweep racing the daemon's other shutdown work is more bug surface than the missed sweep is worth recovering).
- **`SweepInterval = time.Hour` is the exported package-level constant.** Production tick interval. Justified relative to `archiveIdleThreshold = 30 * 24 * time.Hour`: missing one tick delays an archive by one hour, harmless. Exposed (rather than baked into a constructor) so the daemon-wiring caller in #243 can pass it explicitly to `RunSweepLoop` alongside the small interval the unit tests use. Not exposed as a flag or env var ŌĆö AC pins the value.
- **Logger is required, not optional.** No `if log == nil { log = slog.Default() }` guard. Caller passes one (sibling #243 plumbs `Pool.Run`'s logger); nil-logger panic is loud and fast. Log key conventions match `internal/sessions`: `"err"` for the wrapped error, `"count"` for the successful-archive integer, `"archived"` for the would-have-been integer in the ERROR record. Message strings prefixed `"conversations: "` to match the package's `Save`-error wrap convention ŌĆö gives operators one consistent grep target across log + wrapped-error text.
- **No `errgroup.Group` argument and no internal `g.Go`.** `RunSweepLoop` is the body of one goroutine, not an orchestrator. The caller (sibling #243) owns the errgroup; this function only owns its single goroutine's work. Passing in an errgroup would invert the lifecycle. Keeping it a plain blocking function makes it composable with any supervision shape (errgroup, raw `go`, future test harness, etc.).
- **No clock interface.** `time.Now()` is invoked once per tick from `sweepOnce`, which is testable directly. `Sweep` itself takes `now` as a parameter (#219 / #237 chose this over a clock for the same reason). A `Clock` type for one `time.Now()` call would be over-engineered against existing precedent.
- **`sweep_loop.go` is a new file, NOT additions to `sweep.go`.** `sweep.go` holds the pure primitive (no I/O, no clock, no logging ŌĆö its whole identity per #237). `sweep_loop.go` holds the I/O wrapper. Co-locating them in one file would erase the boundary that #237 deliberately drew. Matches the `archive.go` / `sweep.go` precedent (one orthogonal concern per file).
- **Tests in `sweep_loop_test.go`.** Five tests, stdlib only. (1) `TestSweepOnce` ŌĆö three parallel subtests (`happy-path` / `no-op-tick` / `save-error-non-fatal`) drive `sweepOnce` directly; no goroutine, no flake surface. (2) `TestRunSweepLoop_TicksAndCancels` ŌĆö the ONE test that drives a real ticker (`interval = 5ms`); polls `os.Stat(path)` with a 2s deadline as the "loop ticked at least once" signal, then cancels and asserts `nil` return + correct on-disk survivor. (3) `TestRunSweepLoop_NoOpDoesNotSave` ŌĆö `interval = 1ms`, sleep 50ms (Ōēź10 ticks), cancel, assert file never created. (4) `TestRunSweepLoop_SaveErrorContinues` ŌĆö broken path (file-as-directory trick), wait for Ōēź1 ERROR, re-seed via `seedArchivables(reg, 1, 100)` mid-run to force another Sweep+Save attempt, wait for Ōēź2 ERROR records, cancel, assert nil + zero INFO. The re-seed is load-bearing: after the first tick the registry is empty, so without re-seeding `Sweep` would return 0 forever and the `n == 0` short-circuit would silence subsequent ticks ŌĆö the test couldn't distinguish "loop kept running" from "loop crashed silently."
- **Save-failure injection: file-as-directory trick.** `os.WriteFile(tmpDir+"/notadir", "x", 0o600)` then pass `tmpDir+"/notadir/conversations.json"` as the path. `os.MkdirAll` inside `Registry.Save` returns ENOTDIR. Portable across Linux + macOS, self-cleaning via `t.TempDir()`, no special perms required. Chosen over `os.Chmod(tmpDir, 0o500)` (fragile under root and on some CI runners) and platform-specific device paths. Reused between `TestSweepOnce/save-error-non-fatal` and `TestRunSweepLoop_SaveErrorContinues` via a `brokenSavePath(t, tmpDir) string` helper.
- **Logger fixtures.** `discardLogger()` for tests that don't read logs; `captureLogger()` returns a logger writing to a `*syncBuffer` (mutex-wrapped `bytes.Buffer`). `bytes.Buffer` is NOT safe for concurrent use; the loop goroutine writes while the test reads, so the wrapper is required for the loop-level tests. Text handler is sufficient: `level=INFO` / `level=ERROR` / `count=N` / `archived=N` are visible substrings. Both fixtures co-located in the test file; not promoted (one consumer per package today).
- **No new ADR.** Architect's spec ┬¦ "Open questions" is "None"; every design choice is anchored in an existing precedent (rotation watcher loop shape, sessions logger conventions, sweep-primitive splitting rationale from #237). Decisions are minor and well-covered by the spec + the feature doc.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Loading `conversations.json` at daemon startup (sibling #243). Plumbing `*Registry` through `Pool.Run`'s errgroup or whatever supervision surface #243 picks (sibling #243). Choosing the registry path (sibling #243; likely `~/.pyry/conversations.json`). Configurable sweep interval flag or env var (AC pins `time.Hour`). Clock interface (`time.Now()` is the injection point). Final on-shutdown sweep (AC explicit). Metrics emission (no Phase 3 metrics surface yet). `ConversationsRegistry`-shaped fa├¦ade types or mockable interfaces (function takes the concrete `*Registry`; the package owns both ŌĆö interface seam premature). e2e via the daemon (explicitly sibling #243's territory).
- See [knowledge/features/conversations-auto-archive.md](knowledge/features/conversations-auto-archive.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/242-conv-sweep-loop.md`](specs/architecture/242-conv-sweep-loop.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #237)
- **`internal/conversations/sweep.go` ŌĆö `Sweep(reg *Registry, now time.Time) int` pure iterate-and-apply primitive.** New file (~25 LOC). Composes `reg.List()` (snapshot), `ShouldArchive(c, now)` (#219 predicate), and `reg.Delete(c.ID)` (also this ticket). Returns the count of entries archived. Stdlib only (`time`). No goroutines, no I/O, no logging, no clock ŌĆö runs on the caller's goroutine. The future daemon-side ticker (downstream ticket) calls `Sweep` on a timer and `reg.Save` after to persist the deletions. Production diff: +25 LOC `sweep.go` (new) + 18 LOC `registry.go` (new `Delete` method). Test diff: +107 LOC `sweep_test.go` (new) + 101 LOC `registry_test.go` (new `TestRegistry_Delete`). Zero new dependencies (`go.mod` unchanged), zero changes to existing methods, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change.
- **`Registry.Delete(id ConversationID) bool` ŌĆö the consumer-driven mutation primitive #217 deferred.** O(n) linear scan under `r.mu` using the slice-element-removal idiom (`append(r.conversations[:i], r.conversations[i+1:]...)`). Order-preserving ŌĆö surrounding entries' relative order is unchanged; pinned by the `preserves-order` test row against accidental swap-with-last optimisations. Returns `true` on hit, `false` on miss. Same shape as `Get` and `Update`: mutex-guarded, byte-exact `==` ID comparison, no validation, no `Save` (caller's concern, matching the `Create`/`Update`/`Promote` convention). #217 explicitly punted deletion ("conversations are not deleted in Phase 3 ŌĆö they're archived via `IsPromoted` flips and history retention; if a future API ticket needs deletion, that ticket adds it"); #237's sweep IS that consumer, so the two arrive together.
- **`Sweep` returns `int`, not `(int, error)`.** Body composes `List` (cannot fail), `ShouldArchive` (pure predicate), and `Delete` (cannot fail). An error slot would be permanently dead weight. The `if reg.Delete(c.ID)` guard is defensive against a hypothetical concurrent deletion between `List` and `Delete`; `n` only increments on confirmed removal. The daemon-wiring ticket downstream owns `Save` errors and any retry / observability around them ŌĆö those are the operations that can actually fail.
- **`Sweep` does NOT call `reg.Save` ŌĆö disk persistence is the daemon-wiring ticket's concern.** Pinned in the doc comment per AC. Splitting predicate (#219) / sweep-primitive (#237) / daemon-wiring (downstream) keeps each piece testable without setting up the others. The rule is a four-row table-driven unit test with `time.Date(...)` literals; the sweep is a six-row table-driven test seeding an in-memory `Registry` and asserting count + survivors; the daemon wiring will be tested by exercising its I/O contract (load failure, save failure, tick interleave) without re-testing rule or sweep.
- **`Sweep` lives in its own file (`sweep.go`), NOT in `registry.go` or `archive.go`.** `registry.go` is the registry's data-mutation surface; `archive.go` holds the predicate. `Sweep` composes both ŌĆö placing it in either file would couple unrelated concerns (a registry-internal change wouldn't necessarily touch sweep semantics). A third file matches the existing `archive.go` precedent and keeps the boundary clean.
- **Snapshot-safety contract pinned by `delete-snapshot-safety` test row.** `List()` returns a copy (per #217); `Sweep`'s for-range walks that copy detached from `r.conversations`. `Delete`'s mid-iteration mutation of the underlying slice cannot disturb the loop, even though both operations serialize through `r.mu`. The test row in `TestRegistry_Delete` makes the contract executable: seed 2 entries, take `snap := r.List()`, `Delete(snap[0].ID)`, assert `snap` is unchanged in length and element identity. Without that row, a future "optimisation" that returns the live slice from `List` would silently break `Sweep`.
- **Tests in `sweep_test.go`** ŌĆö single primary table, six rows, all anchored to `now := time.Date(2026, 6, 1, 12, 0, 0, 0, time.UTC)` (matches `archive_test.go`). Each row asserts (1) returned count, (2) post-sweep `len(reg.List())`, (3) every survivor passes `!ShouldArchive(c, now) || c.IsPromoted`. Rows: `empty-registry` (0 ŌåÆ 0), `all-archivable` (3 unpromoted at `now-31d` ŌåÆ 3, `List` empty), `none-archivable-fresh` (2 unpromoted at `now-7d` ŌåÆ 0, both survive), `none-archivable-promoted-but-idle` (2 promoted at `now-365d` ŌåÆ 0, both survive ŌĆö pins promoted-exempt at the sweep level), `mixed` (2+2+2 ŌåÆ 2), `boundary-exactly-30-days` (1 unpromoted at `now-30d` ŌåÆ 1 ŌĆö mirrors the predicate's inclusive-boundary row at the sweep level). Promoted-entry name fields stay zero (`*string` nil); `ShouldArchive` short-circuits on `IsPromoted` before touching `Name`.
- **Tests in `registry_test.go`** ŌĆö `TestRegistry_Delete` table-driven, six rows: `hit` / `miss-empty-registry` / `miss-non-matching` / `preserves-order` (seed `A`, `B`, `C`; delete `B`; `List` returns `[A, C]`) / `delete-snapshot-safety` (the contract pin above) / `delete-twice-second-misses`. `t.Parallel()`, stdlib only. Reuses existing UUID literal style (`11111111-2222-4333-8444-555555555555` family) and `mustParseTime` helper.
- **No new ADR.** Architect's spec ┬¦ "Open questions" is "None"; decisions are minor (return-int, file-placement, defensive-Delete-check) and well-covered by the spec + this entry. The pure-predicate / pure-loop split was already established by #219 and the predicate doc; #237 extends that split rather than relitigating it.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Daemon-side ticker goroutine, load-on-tick, save-after-sweep ŌĆö separate downstream ticket. Logging or metrics emitted by `Sweep` ŌĆö same. Clock interface or `Clock` type for injection (`now time.Time` is the injection point; tests pass deterministic literals). Map-based registry indexing for O(1) `Delete` (premature; the registry size and call frequency don't warrant it). Concurrent invocation of `Sweep` (runs on the caller's goroutine; existing `TestRegistry_ConcurrentReadWrite` already exercises `Registry`'s mutex discipline). Persistence in `Sweep`'s tests (the doc comment is the contract).
- See [knowledge/features/conversations-auto-archive.md](knowledge/features/conversations-auto-archive.md), [knowledge/features/conversations-registry.md ┬¦ Delete](knowledge/features/conversations-registry.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/237-conv-sweep-primitive.md`](specs/architecture/237-conv-sweep-primitive.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #218)
- **`internal/conversations/registry.go` ŌĆö `(*Registry).Promote(id ConversationID, name string) error` + four exported sentinels.** Adds the in-memory primitive that turns a discussion into a named channel: flips `IsPromoted` to `true` and sets `Name` to a non-nil pointer to `name`. Validation, name-uniqueness scan, and the two-field mutation all run under `r.mu` so a concurrent second `Promote` with the same name cannot slip through. On any refusal the registry is left untouched. Persistence stays with the caller ŌĆö `Promote` does not call `Save`, matching the `Create` / `Update` convention. Production diff: +65 LOC `registry.go` (new method + sentinels + one new stdlib import: `strings`). Test diff: +225 LOC `registry_test.go` (`TestRegistry_Promote` table + `TestRegistry_Promote_DoesNotPersist`). Zero new dependencies (`go.mod` unchanged), zero new types, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change. No consumers wired in this slice ŌĆö CLI `pyry conv promote` and the mobile `promote_conversation` frame (sentinel-to-wire-code mapping for `conversation.not_found` / `conversation.already_promoted` plus the still-TBD `name_in_use` / `name_empty` codes) are deferred consumers.
- **Four exported sentinels at the top of `registry.go` (after `registryFile`).** `ErrConversationNotFound`, `ErrConversationAlreadyPromoted`, `ErrPromotionNameInUse`, `ErrPromotionNameEmpty`. Strings follow the package `errors.New("conversations: <short lowercase sentence>")` convention (mirrors `internal/sessions`'s `ErrSessionNotFound` and `internal/update`'s sentinels). Returned naked (`return ErrPromotionNameEmpty`), not wrapped ŌĆö the primitive has no extra context to add (id and name are caller-supplied and the caller already has them). Distinguish via `errors.Is`. `ErrConversationNotFound` lives in this package even though `internal/sessions` has `ErrSessionNotFound`: the two registries are deliberately decoupled (per ADR 022 and the registry tech notes); a shared `ErrNotFound` would couple them and violate the "registries diverge" stance.
- **Refusal-to-wire-code mapping is the consumer's job, NOT the primitive's.** The primitive surfaces `errors.Is`-distinguishable sentinels per refusal case; `internal/control` (CLI) and the wire-protocol layer map them to the user-facing codes named in `protocol-mobile.md` ┬¦ "Errors and acks": `ErrConversationNotFound ŌåÆ conversation.not_found`, `ErrConversationAlreadyPromoted ŌåÆ conversation.already_promoted`, `ErrPromotionNameInUse ŌåÆ conversation.name_in_use` (TBD wire code, defined by the later mapping ticket), `ErrPromotionNameEmpty ŌåÆ conversation.name_empty` or 400-shape (TBD). Keeps the package boundary clean: `internal/conversations` has zero knowledge of the wire surface.
- **`Promote` is a NEW method, NOT a thin wrapper over `Update`.** `Update`'s `func(*Conversation)` callback returns no error, so building `Promote` on top of it would force the caller to thread refusal through a captured `*error` (closure capturing a local `var err error` and reading it after `Update` returns) ŌĆö uglier than just writing the dedicated method. Mutation logic itself is two field assignments under the same lock; duplication cost is trivial. ADR 022's lock-held-callback discipline still applies in spirit (mutation under `r.mu`); the dedicated method is an instance of the pattern, not a new pattern.
- **Empty-name check runs OUTSIDE the lock, FIRST.** `if strings.TrimSpace(name) == "" { return ErrPromotionNameEmpty }` short-circuits before `r.mu.Lock()`. Needs no registry state; short-circuiting outside the lock keeps the lock-held path uniform (every code path inside the critical section either mutates or returns a registry-visibility-relevant sentinel). `strings.TrimSpace` covers ASCII space/tab/newline plus Unicode whitespace, matching Go conventions. **The stored `Name` is the UNTRIMMED input** ŌĆö this is a refusal predicate, not a normalizer. `Promote(id, "  general  ")` accepts and stores the literal string with surrounding spaces. Trimming as a side effect would be a separate UX decision documented in a later ticket (likely the future `pyry conv name <id> <name>` rename/clear primitive).
- **Uniqueness scope is "another *promoted* conversation", byte-exact `==`, case-sensitive.** No Unicode normalization, no fold, no case-insensitive collation. The scan iterates every record under `r.mu`, skips the target's own index (`i == idx` guard so we don't compare its currently-nil name to itself), skips unpromoted records (`if !c.IsPromoted { continue }`), and only checks `c.Name != nil && *c.Name == name` for the rest. A historical unpromoted record with a stray non-nil `Name` (e.g. a future `pyry conv name` flow that names a discussion before promoting) does NOT block. Pinned by the `name-conflict-with-unpromoted-OK` row in `TestRegistry_Promote` ŌĆö without that row, an over-broad scan that ignored `IsPromoted` would still pass the rest of the table.
- **No partial mutation on refusal.** Every refusal returns BEFORE touching `r.conversations[idx]`. The mutation is two field assignments at the bottom of the happy path (`r.conversations[idx].IsPromoted = true; r.conversations[idx].Name = &n`); nothing earlier writes. A concurrent `Get` running through `r.mu` either sees the pre-state or the post-state, never a half-mutated record.
- **Pointer ownership: copy-into-fresh-local-then-take-address.** `n := name; r.conversations[idx].Name = &n` allocates a fresh string-header on the heap so the stored pointer does not alias a stack variable across the function return. Strings are immutable so the header copy is the only concern; this is defensive idiom matching the test file's existing `ptrTo[T any]` helper. Avoids any future refactor that takes `&name` directly (which would store a pointer to the caller's parameter local ŌĆö currently safe because the function returns immediately, but fragile under refactor).
- **No `LastUsedAt` bump on promote.** `Promote` only flips `IsPromoted` and sets `Name`. If a consuming layer wants `LastUsedAt = time.Now()` on promote, it calls `Update` after `Promote`. Two registry calls; no atomicity loss for this specific pair (consumer can wrap in its own coordinator if it ever needs a single atomic call). AC scopes the primitive to `IsPromoted` + `Name`; bumping `LastUsedAt` is a UX choice the consuming layer (CLI / wire-protocol) makes.
- **No `Cwd` move.** Mobile's `promote_conversation` payload carries an optional `cwd`; physically moving the conversation's working directory to a workspace folder is a separate UX flow layered on top of the primitive in a later ticket. The primitive does not touch `Cwd`.
- **Concurrency: identical lock discipline to `Update`.** Single `r.mu.Lock()` covers validation (post-trim check), the linear scan-for-id, the duplicate-already-promoted check, the uniqueness scan, and the two-field mutation. Lock-held window is `O(N)` over the in-memory slice for the uniqueness scan; at Phase 3 scale (O(10┬▓) conversations) this is ~┬Ąs and not a contention concern. No `fn` callback hazards from ADR 022 ŌĆö there is no caller-supplied callback. The whole body is in-package and provably never re-enters the registry. `Save` continues to snapshot under the same lock and write outside it; a `Promote` that lands during the snapshot copy either runs entirely before the copy (full mutation visible on disk) or entirely after (mutation observable only after a follow-up `Save`). No torn write.
- **Tests in `registry_test.go`** ŌĆö same-package, `t.Parallel()` everywhere, stdlib only. Two new test functions. (1) `TestRegistry_Promote` ŌĆö table-driven, seven rows mapping 1:1 to AC bullets: `success` (one unpromoted ŌåÆ flipped + named); `unknown-id` (`ErrConversationNotFound`, registry untouched); `already-promoted` (target with `Name=ptrTo("old")` ŌåÆ `ErrConversationAlreadyPromoted`, still `*Name=="old"`); `name-conflict-with-promoted` (one promoted `Name=ptrTo("dup")` + one unpromoted, promote second to `"dup"` ŌåÆ `ErrPromotionNameInUse`); **`name-conflict-with-unpromoted-OK`** (one unpromoted with `Name=ptrTo("dup")` + one unpromoted with no name, promote second to `"dup"` ŌåÆ success ŌĆö pins the uniqueness scope is *promoted-only*, not "anyone with a non-nil name"; without this row an over-broad scan still passes); `empty-name` (`""` ŌåÆ `ErrPromotionNameEmpty`); `whitespace-name` (`"   \t\n"` ŌåÆ `ErrPromotionNameEmpty`). Each refusal row asserts `Get(id)` after the call equals the pre-call state (the "left untouched" invariant). (2) `TestRegistry_Promote_DoesNotPersist` ŌĆö standalone (not table-driven): build registry, `Save` to a temp path, `Promote` successfully, `Load` from the same path, assert the loaded registry shows `IsPromoted == false` for the target. Pins "no implicit `Save`" the same way the AC pins "persistence stays with the caller". Reuses the existing `ptrTo[T any]` and `mustParseTime` helpers.
- **Defer: `TestRegistry_Promote_LockHeldDuringScan`.** Two-goroutines-hammering-`Promote`-with-the-same-name race-detector probe is achievable but the standard race detector primarily catches data-race-on-bytes, not "two writers both observed free." A correctness probe would need a goroutine that calls `Promote` mid-scan, which the primitive's structure makes impossible by construction (no callback hook). ADR 022 establishes the "uniqueness scan and mutation share the lock" discipline; this test would mostly assert "we trust ADR 022." Skip ŌĆö code review catches a future refactor that releases the lock between scan and mutation.
- **Out of scope, by design.** `pyry conv promote <id> <name>` CLI verb (later ticket ŌĆö calls `Promote` then `Save`, maps sentinels to exit codes / stderr). Mobile `promote_conversation` frame (later ticket ŌĆö wire-protocol layer maps sentinels to `conversation.not_found` / `conversation.already_promoted` / `conversation.name_in_use` / `conversation.name_empty` codes per `protocol-mobile.md`). Cwd-move on promote (separate UX flow; mobile payload's optional `cwd` is informational here). `LastUsedAt` bump on promote (consumer's call via `Update`). `pyry conv name <id> <name>` rename/clear primitive (would need its own validation, especially for the `*Name == ""` clear case which `ErrPromotionNameEmpty` currently disallows transitively for promoted records). Length caps or character restrictions on the name (no AC for them today; future validation gets its own sentinel; the existing `ErrPromotionNameEmpty` stays scoped to empty/whitespace). `Promote` taking a `Conversation`-shaped `apply` callback (deferred ŌĆö two registry calls coordinated by the consumer is enough for now). Auto-archive predicate + sweep (#219, #220).
- See [knowledge/features/conversations-registry.md ┬¦ Promote](knowledge/features/conversations-registry.md), [knowledge/decisions/022-conversations-update-callback-under-lock.md](knowledge/decisions/022-conversations-update-callback-under-lock.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/218-conversations-promotion-api.md`](specs/architecture/218-conversations-promotion-api.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 wiring, ticket #215)
- **`pyry pair revoke <name>` ŌĆö third sub-verb on the `runPair` dispatcher; remove the device entry whose `Name` matches and persist.** Thin wiring on top of `Registry.Remove` + `Registry.Save` (#209). Production diff: +66 LOC `cmd/pyry/pair.go` (one switch case + `pairRevokeArgs` type + `parsePairRevokeArgs` + `runPairRevoke`), +1 LOC `cmd/pyry/main.go` (one usage line under `pyry pair list`), `pairVerbList` const flips `"list"` ŌåÆ `"list, revoke"` in lockstep. Test diff: +156 LOC `cmd/pyry/pair_test.go` (3 new tests) + 125 LOC `internal/e2e/pair_test.go` (`TestPairRevoke_E2E` with three sub-tests). Zero new packages, zero new exported types, zero new dependencies.
- **Save-only-on-Remove invariant.** `Registry.Save` runs only when `Remove` returned `true`. Necessary for AC#5's "the on-disk registry is not rewritten" guarantee ŌĆö even though `Save` is idempotent for unchanged content, on an empty cold-start registry it would create the file at `~/.pyry/<name>/devices.json` (`MkdirAll` + atomic rename of an empty `{"devices":[]}\n`). The not-found branch must be byte-identical to the pre-call state, which means short-circuiting before `Save`. Pinned by the E2E "missing registry" sub-test asserting `os.Stat(<path>) == fs.ErrNotExist` after the call.
- **Exit-code mechanism asymmetry on exit `1` ŌĆö direct exit on not-found, returned error on I/O.** Not-found (`Remove` returns false, including the missing/empty registry case) calls `os.Exit(1)` directly with `pyry pair revoke: no device named <name>\n` to stderr ŌĆö bypasses `main.run`'s `pyry: ` prefix so the AC's byte-exact stderr text is met without a doubled `pyry: pyry pair revoke: ŌĆ”`. I/O errors (`devices.Load` / `registry.Save`) return `fmt.Errorf("pair revoke: %w", err)` and let `main.run` add the prefix for diagnostic value (`pyry: pair revoke: <wrapped>`). The architect chose direct exit over a sentinel error (`var errNoDevice` + `errors.Is` in `main.run`) because the sentinel would touch a second file for one consumer; AC#5 only constrains the byte-exact stderr text. Same pattern as `runPairList`'s exit-2 paths.
- **Exit `2` is reserved for usage errors only.** Flag parse failure, missing positional (`pyry pair revoke`), extra positional (`pyry pair revoke a b`), or unknown flag (`--bogus`) all flow through `parsePairRevokeArgs` returning an error which `runPairRevoke` maps to direct `os.Exit(2)` with `pyry pair revoke: <err>\n` + a usage line. `parsePairRevokeArgs` switches on `fs.NArg()` to produce the two arg-count error shapes (`missing device name`, `unexpected positional %q`); both fragments are stable and grep-able for table-driven parser tests.
- **Flag-after-positional NOT supported, by design.** `pyry pair revoke phone -pyry-name=foo` exits 2 because stdlib `flag` stops parsing at the first non-flag token. Same constraint as every other sibling subcommand (`runPairList`, `runSessions*`, `runPairDefault`); not a custom reorder pass. Architect's spec ┬¦ "Parser" calls this out explicitly so future contributors don't add `flag.ParseAll`-style handling on top.
- **`stdout` write goes through `fmt.Printf`, not a pure formatter.** Unlike #214's `renderPairList` (where the formatter has interesting layout logic worth unit-testing), the success message is a single `Printf` with one substitution. There is no benefit to extracting it; the AC's exact-string check is verified by the E2E test against `os.Stdout`. Asymmetry with `renderPairList` is intentional ŌĆö extract only when the formatter has logic worth isolating.
- **Concurrency: same last-writer-wins as bare `pair`.** Two concurrent `pair revoke` invocations against the same `devices.json` race at the `Load ŌåÆ Remove ŌåÆ Save` boundary; the later `Save` overwrites the earlier one. Out of scope for this XS ticket; the fix (file lock at the `internal/devices` boundary) belongs to all callers, not this verb. Inherited from #213's contract; #215 doesn't make it worse.
- **Tests: 3 unit tests + 1 e2e test (with 3 sub-tests).** Unit (`cmd/pyry/pair_test.go`): `TestParsePairRevokeArgs` (table ŌĆö happy `phone`, with-instance `-pyry-name=foo phone`, missing positional ŌåÆ `missing device name`, extra positional ŌåÆ `unexpected positional`, unknown flag ŌåÆ `flag provided but not defined`; pins `t.Setenv("PYRY_NAME", "")`); `TestRunPairRevoke_RemovesEntry` (two-device fixture; `runPairRevoke([]string{"alpha"})`; reload via `devices.Load`; assert single survivor `bravo` byte-for-byte across `Name`, `TokenHash`, `PairedAt.Equal`, `LastSeenAt.Equal`); `TestRunPairRevoke_SaveFailure` (fixture as above, `os.Chmod(<dir>, 0o500)`, assert returned error contains `pair revoke:`; skipped on root and on filesystems where `chmod 0500` doesn't block atomic rename inside a tempdir owned by the test user ŌĆö gated on a pre-flight `os.WriteFile` attempt). Not-found and missing-positional paths can't be unit-tested without `os.Exit` capture machinery (not present in this repo); covered E2E. E2E (`internal/e2e/pair_test.go`, `//go:build e2e`): `TestPairRevoke_E2E` three sub-tests using `RunBareIn(t, home, "pair", "revoke", ŌĆ”)` ŌĆö "removes one of two" (pair `phone-a`, pair `phone-b`, capture `phone-b`'s on-disk entry, `pyry pair revoke phone-a`, assert exit 0 + stdout exactly `Revoked phone-a.\n` + survivor's `TokenHash` and `PairedAt` byte-identical to the captured snapshot); "not found" (pair `phone-a`, snapshot file bytes, `pyry pair revoke ghost`, assert exit 1 + stderr exactly `pyry pair revoke: no device named ghost\n` + on-disk bytes unchanged via `bytes.Equal`); "missing registry" (fresh HOME, no prior pair, `pyry pair revoke ghost`, assert exit 1 + same stderr + `os.Stat == fs.ErrNotExist` after the call).
- **Out of scope, by design.** `flock` on `devices.json` (concurrent-`pair` race fix; belongs at `internal/devices` boundary, all callers benefit). Force-revoke-by-token-prefix (e.g. revoke by `TokenHash[:8]` to disambiguate duplicate `Name`s; `Registry.Add` documents that uniqueness is the caller's concern, but `runPairRevoke` removes the *first* match). Bulk revoke (`pyry pair revoke --all`, by date range, etc.). Daemon-side notification on revoke (the auth path may have a stale in-memory `Registry`; same daemon-staleness open question as bare `pair` ŌĆö owned by the future WS-handshake auth ticket). ADR (decisions inherit from #213's [ADR 021](knowledge/decisions/021-pair-cli-order-of-operations.md) ŌĆö load-fail-fast ŌåÆ mutate ŌåÆ save ŌåÆ render ŌĆö and #214's "no factor" verb-dispatch shape; promote to ADR only if a future sub-verb relitigates them).
- See [knowledge/features/pyry-pair-command.md ┬¦ `pyry pair revoke <name>` (#215)](knowledge/features/pyry-pair-command.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/215-pair-revoke.md`](specs/architecture/215-pair-revoke.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 wiring, ticket #214)
- **`pyry pair list` ŌĆö read-only operator inspection of the device registry.** Restructures `runPair` in `cmd/pyry/pair.go` from a single bare action into a sub-verb dispatcher (mirrors `runSessions` per [ADR 010](knowledge/decisions/010-sessions-cli-sub-router.md), without `parseClientFlags` since the pair family does not dial the daemon) and adds the `list` sub-verb. Bare `pyry pair`'s body moves to `runPairDefault` verbatim ŌĆö no logic change. Production diff: +125 LOC `cmd/pyry/pair.go` + 1 LOC `cmd/pyry/main.go` (one usage line). Test diff: +157 LOC `cmd/pyry/pair_test.go` (5 new tests) + 53 LOC `internal/e2e/pair_test.go` (`TestPairList_E2E` with two sub-tests).
