Zero new packages, zero new exported types, zero new dependencies.
- **Verb-dispatcher shape: switch on `args[0]`, with a leading-dash escape hatch.** `runPair` peels `args[0]`. Bare verb tokens (`list`) dispatch to `runPair<Verb>`; an unknown bare verb (`pyry pair revoke` before #215) hits the usage-error path ŌåÆ `os.Exit(2)` directly so the top-level `pyry: ` prefix doesn't appear on usage failures. Anything starting with `-` falls through to `runPairDefault` so existing flag-leading invocations (`pyry pair --name=foo`) keep working unchanged. The `pairVerbList` constant is `"list"` today; #215 will update it to `"list, revoke"` and add one switch case + one helper. Deliberately NOT factored into a generic helper ŌĆö the dispatcher is ~10 lines, and `runSessions`/`runPair`/(future)other carry their own switch by design (CLAUDE.md "Simplicity first"; spec ┬¦ "Open questions" ┬¦1 documents the no-factor rationale).
- **`runPairList` is a thin wrapper over `parsePairListArgs` + `devices.Load` + `renderPairList`.** Read-only ŌĆö never calls `Save`/`Add`/`Remove`. `parsePairListArgs` accepts only `-pyry-name` (no `--name`, no `--relay`); unknown flags or any positional ŌåÆ exit 2 with `pyry pair list: <err>` + a usage line. The registry path is resolved via the existing `resolveDevicesPath` (sanitized) ŌĆö same primitive as bare-pair, no new resolver. Returns `error` for exit-1 conditions (registry I/O, malformed JSON, stdout write error); `os.Exit(2)` directly for exit-2 conditions.
- **Pure formatter `renderPairList(list []devices.Device, w io.Writer) error`.** No globals, no `os.Stdout` access, no clock reads. Byte-for-byte deterministic function of `list`. Empty list ŌåÆ exactly `No paired devices.\n` and nothing else (no header, no trailing whitespace beyond the literal newline). Non-empty ŌåÆ header `NAME\tPAIRED\tLAST SEEN\tTOKEN-PREFIX` + one data row per device, padded by `text/tabwriter` (2-space padding, no minimum width). Columns: `NAME` verbatim from `Device.Name`; `PAIRED` is `time.RFC3339`; `LAST SEEN` is `time.RFC3339` or the literal string `never` when `LastSeenAt.IsZero()`; `TOKEN-PREFIX` is the first 8 lowercase hex chars of `Device.TokenHash` (visual identification only, never plaintext token).
- **Defensive sort on every render, even though `Save` already sorts on disk.** `sort.SliceStable` by `(PairedAt, Name)` ascending, using `time.Time.Equal` for the primary comparator (NOT `==`, which trips on monotonic-clock state stripped by JSON roundtrip ŌĆö see `docs/lessons.md` ┬¦ "Atomic on-disk writes"). The formatter's input is `Registry.List()` ŌĆö whatever `Load` decoded into memory. If a future writer skips `Save`'s sort step or the file was hand-edited, the formatter still produces the documented order. Cost: one stable sort on a tiny slice; benefit: the AC's determinism guarantee is local to `renderPairList`, not coupled to a sibling package's invariant.
- **Defensive token-prefix length check.** `len(prefix) >= 8` guard avoids `runtime error: slice bounds out of range` on a corrupt registry; `prefix = d.TokenHash` is the fallback. `Device.TokenHash` is documented as 64 hex chars, but `renderPairList` is a pure UI function and shouldn't panic on malformed input ŌĆö that's the wrong failure mode for a list command.
- **Empty-registry handling unifies three on-disk states at the formatter level.** `devices.Load` already collapses missing-file, zero-byte-file, and empty `devices` array into "registry with empty `devices` slice, no error" (#209's contract). `Registry.List()` returns an empty slice; `renderPairList`'s `len(list) == 0` branch handles all three uniformly. Cold start is a valid empty state, not an error ŌĆö consistent with the pyry-owned-state asymmetry vs. operator-owned config files (per #209's load semantics).
- **Tests: 5 unit tests + 1 e2e test (with 2 sub-tests).** Unit (`cmd/pyry/pair_test.go`): `TestRenderPairList_TwoDevices` (golden-string of entire byte-for-byte output ŌĆö header + two rows in `(PairedAt, Name)` order + `tabwriter` padding); `TestRenderPairList_NeverSeen` (single device, zero `LastSeenAt`, asserts literal `never` AND that `0001-01-01` does NOT appear); `TestRenderPairList_Empty` (`bytes.Equal(buf.Bytes(), []byte("No paired devices.\n"))`); `TestRenderPairList_SortOrder` (input slice in non-sorted order with a `(PairedAt, Name)` tiebreak case ŌĆö two devices with same `PairedAt`, different `Name`; asserts ascending output independent of input order); `TestParsePairListArgs` (table ŌĆö empty, `-pyry-name=foo`, positional rejected, unknown flag rejected). E2e (`internal/e2e/pair_test.go`, `//go:build e2e`): `TestPairList_E2E` two sub-tests ŌĆö "empty registry" runs `pyry pair list` on a fresh `t.TempDir()` HOME and asserts exact stdout `No paired devices.\n` + exit 0; "after pair" runs `pyry pair --name=phone-a` first, loads the registry directly to capture `TokenHash[:8]`, then runs `pyry pair list` and asserts both `phone-a` and the prefix appear in stdout.
- **`tabwriter`'s padding heuristic NOT tested directly.** Covered transitively by the golden-string test in `TestRenderPairList_TwoDevices`. If `tabwriter`'s behavior shifts across Go versions, the golden string updates with it; that's the right granularity. `devices.Load`'s cold-start path is also not duplicated here ŌĆö already pinned in `internal/devices/registry_test.go`; the list command's empty-registry behavior is tested at the formatter level (3) and end-to-end (6).
- **Out of scope, by design.** `pyry pair revoke <name>` (sibling #215 ŌĆö appends one switch case to `runPair` and one helper function; will update `pairVerbList` to `"list, revoke"` in lockstep). Machine-parseable output (no `--json` / `--quiet`; the AC explicitly does not require machine-parseability, and the protocol is the registry file itself). Filtering by name / token-prefix (defer; small registries don't need it). Pagination (defer; same reason). Sharing a verb-dispatch helper with the future `pair revoke` (rejected ŌĆö the dispatcher is ~10 lines and a generic helper is premature abstraction at two-verb scale; #215 inherits a working two-verb dispatcher and adds the third case in one line).
- See [knowledge/features/pyry-pair-command.md](knowledge/features/pyry-pair-command.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/214-pair-list.md`](specs/architecture/214-pair-list.md).

### Codebase (rotation fix, ticket #221)
- **`handleCreate` now canonicalises the probe-returned path per event.** `internal/sessions/rotation/watcher.go:178-187` builds `expected := filepath.Join(w.resolvedDir, base)`, then `openResolved, resolveErr := filepath.EvalSymlinks(open)`; on success it compares the resolved form, on error it logs at Debug and falls back to `filepath.Clean(open)`. ~5 production lines added; no signature, type, or interface changes (`Probe`, `Config`, `Watcher`, `SessionRef`, `New`, `Run` all unchanged); no consumer updates.
- **Closes the inverse case of #118.** #118 fixed "watched dir is a symlink, probe canonical" by resolving `cfg.Dir` once in `New`. #221 closes "watched dir is canonical, probe reports the symlink form" ŌĆö same operator-visible symptom (session UUID stops updating after `/clear` with no error surfaced), opposite direction. The asymmetry surfaced under e2e #55: `os.MkdirTemp` lands the watched dir under `/var/folders/...`, `New`'s `EvalSymlinks` canonicalises it to `/private/var/folders/...`, and `lsof` then returned the unresolved `/var/folders/...` form ŌĆö gate at `watcher.go:179` rejected, rotation event silently dropped.
- **Why per-event on the probe side.** The watched directory's lifetime spans the watcher's, so its `EvalSymlinks` is cheap and race-free at construction. The file the probe will report doesn't exist when the watcher starts ŌĆö there is no equivalent hoist. Cost is one `lstat`-walk per CREATE (microseconds); the `EvalSymlinks` race window (probe ŌåÆ unlink ŌåÆ resolve) is absorbed by the fallback path. `EvalSymlinks` returns `*PathError` for non-existent / dangling targets; we treat that as a benign mismatch ŌĆö the file the probe reported doesn't resolve under the watched dir, so it can't be the rotation target. `continue` falls through to the next ref.
- **Debug-level logging on resolve failure is intentional.** Probe-path resolution failures are expected on race-y CREATE events ŌĆö claude can unlink between the probe and the resolve ŌĆö and should not warn-spam the logs. Operators investigating a missed rotation will see the debug line if they raise log level; routine operation stays quiet.
- **`resolvedDir` is left untouched.** The asymmetry fix is one-sided by design ŌĆö re-resolving the watched dir per event would be redundant. Two distinct `EvalSymlinks` lifecycles is correct: directory at construction (race-free, cheap), file per event (necessary, with fallback).
- **Tests added (`internal/sessions/rotation/watcher_test.go`):** (1) `TestWatcher_DetectsRotationProbeReportsSymlinkPath` ŌĆö canonical watched dir, probe `pathFn` returns `filepath.Join(link, newUUID+".jsonl")` where `link ŌåÆ realDir`; assert `OnRotate(oldUUID, newUUID)` within 1s (mirrors `TestWatcher_DetectsRotationThroughSymlink`'s 1s/20ms poll loop). (2) `TestWatcher_ProbePathUnresolvableNoCrashNoRotate` ŌĆö probe returns a path through a dangling `os.Symlink` to a non-existent target; 300ms sleep covers `probeRetryDelays {0, 50ms, 200ms}` plus slack; assert `OnRotate` fires zero times, no panic. Both tests use explicit `os.Symlink` so they exercise both directions on Linux and macOS regardless of platform tempdir conventions. Existing `TestWatcher_DetectsRotation`, `TestWatcher_DetectsRotationThroughSymlink`, `TestWatcher_ProbePathMismatch` unaffected.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Re-evaluating `resolvedDir` on a directory rename / re-symlink during runtime (watcher lifetime is process-scoped). Switching the watch target itself to the canonical path (fsnotify works correctly through symlinks on macOS for our use case ŌĆö `TestWatcher_DetectsRotationThroughSymlink` proves it). ADR (textbook canonicalise-both-sides; the one-sided asymmetry analysis is documented in the feature doc and lessons; promote to ADR only if the fallback contract or asymmetry is later relitigated).
- See [knowledge/features/rotation-watcher.md ┬¦ Symlink-resolved match path](knowledge/features/rotation-watcher.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/221-watcher-resolve-symlink-probe-path.md`](specs/architecture/221-watcher-resolve-symlink-probe-path.md), [`docs/lessons.md` ┬¦ fsnotify reports as-watched, kernel probes report canonicalised ŌĆö match in one form](lessons.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #219)
- **`internal/conversations/archive.go` ŌĆö `ShouldArchive(c Conversation, now time.Time) bool` pure predicate.** New file (~25 LOC, 7 LOC of code) co-located with `conversation.go` (#216) and `registry.go` (#217). One exported function, one unexported `archiveIdleThreshold = 30 * 24 * time.Hour` const. Body is two lines: `if c.IsPromoted { return false }` then `return now.Sub(c.LastUsedAt) >= archiveIdleThreshold`. Stdlib only (`time`). Pure value semantics ŌĆö safe to call from any goroutine, cannot fail. **No consumers wired in this slice** ŌĆö #220 (auto-archive sweep) is the downstream consumer that will iterate `Registry.List()` and call this predicate per row on a timer.
- **Boundary is `>=`, not `>`.** AC pins "exactly 30 days idle archives (boundary inclusive)." Encoded as `>=`. The `unpromoted, just over threshold` test row (`now.Add(-(30*24*time.Hour + time.Second))`, expected true) pairs with the `exactly 30 days idle` row to lock in the direction of the inequality ŌĆö an accidental flip to `<=` (or `<`) fails one of the two.
- **`now` is a parameter, not `time.Now()`.** Established Go idiom for time-dependent rules: take `now time.Time` as an argument; let the caller pick. The sweep loop (#220) injects its tick time; tests use literal `time.Date(...)` values without a clock interface. Splitting predicate (this ticket) and sweep (#220) lets each piece be tested in isolation ŌĆö the rule is a four-row table-driven unit test with deterministic timestamps; the sweep is tested by exercising its I/O contract without re-testing the rule.
- **Threshold is an unexported package-level `const`, not an exported parameter.** AC pins `30 * 24 * time.Hour`. Naming it (`archiveIdleThreshold`) gives the test assertions a single source of truth and gives #220 a single point to reference if it ever wants to surface the value (e.g., in log messages). Stays unexported ŌĆö no caller currently needs to read or override it; an exported knob would be premature.
- **No zero-value guard on `LastUsedAt`.** Per #216, `LastUsedAt` is "always present" on a `Conversation` (no `omitempty`, bumped on every user activity by the future API layer). A zero-value `LastUsedAt` makes `ShouldArchive` return `true` (any unpromoted record older than 30 days archives, and `time.Time{}` is far older than any plausible `now`) ŌĆö that is the correct fallback if the invariant ever breaks. Adding a guard would defend against a failure mode the type's invariants already rule out.
- **Production diff: `internal/conversations/archive.go` +25 LOC (new). Test diff: `internal/conversations/archive_test.go` +59 LOC (new).** Zero new dependencies (`go.mod` unchanged), zero changes to existing code, zero new package surface beyond the one exported function, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change, zero changes to `conversation.go` / `registry.go` / any consumer.
- **Tests** (`archive_test.go`, ~59 LOC, table-driven, stdlib only, single test function `TestShouldArchive`): four rows anchored to `now := time.Date(2026, 6, 1, 12, 0, 0, 0, time.UTC)`, each row's `LastUsedAt` expressed as `now.Add(-d)`. (1) `promoted, very idle` (`-365d`, expect false ŌĆö pins the `IsPromoted` short-circuit); (2) `unpromoted, exactly 30 days idle` (`-30d`, expect true ŌĆö pins boundary inclusive); (3) `unpromoted, 29d23h idle` (`-(29d+23h)`, expect false ŌĆö pins just-under); (4) `unpromoted, just over threshold` (`-(30d+1s)`, expect true ŌĆö pins inequality direction). No "promoted with recent activity" row (tests the same short-circuit as row 1). Each `Conversation` literal is constructed inline; only `IsPromoted` and `LastUsedAt` matter; other fields stay at zero values. `time.Date(...)` (no monotonic component) keeps arithmetic deterministic per `lessons.md` ┬¦ "JSON roundtrip strips monotonic-clock state".
- **Out of scope, by design.** Sweep loop / archive action (#220 ŌĆö iterating the registry, calling the predicate, removing or moving rows on a timer). Archive destination / sidecar (`archived.json` for recoverable archive ŌĆö defer until a real ask). Configurable threshold (exported var or config field ŌĆö defer). Integration with `LastUsedAt` bumps (future conversations API; the predicate only reads). ADR (decisions are minor and well covered by the architect's spec; promote to ADR only if the sweep ticket relitigates them).
- See [knowledge/features/conversations-auto-archive.md](knowledge/features/conversations-auto-archive.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/219-auto-archive-predicate.md`](specs/architecture/219-auto-archive-predicate.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #217)
- **`internal/conversations/registry.go` ŌĆö `Registry` (mutex-guarded conversation list) + atomic-write `Save` + `Load` + `Create` / `Get` / `List(filter ...ListFilter)` / `Update(id, fn func(*Conversation)) bool` + `ListFilter{IsPromoted *bool}` envelope.** New file (~179 LOC) co-located with `conversation.go` (#216). Six methods on the new `Registry` type plus the `ListFilter` struct. Stdlib only (`encoding/json`, `errors`, `fmt`, `io/fs`, `os`, `path/filepath`, `sort`, `sync`). Sibling `internal/conversations/id.go` (~51 LOC) lands `NewID() (ConversationID, error)` + `ValidID(s) bool` ŌĆö byte-for-byte clone of `internal/sessions/id.go` with the typed-id alias swapped (the `ConversationID` doc-comment in `conversation.go` from #216 explicitly deferred the generator and validator to this ticket; that promise is now satisfied). Production diff: +51 `id.go` (new) + 179 `registry.go` (new). Test diff: +75 `id_test.go` (new) + 489 `registry_test.go` (new). Zero new dependencies (`go.mod` unchanged), zero changes to existing code, zero CLI surface. No consumers wired in this slice ŌĆö daemon-startup `Load` + post-mutation `Save` is a sibling ticket; #218 (promotion API), #219/#220 (auto-archive) are downstream consumers.
- **Atomic-write recipe is structurally identical to `internal/devices/registry.go:Save`.** `MkdirAll(dir, 0o700)` ŌåÆ `CreateTemp(dir, ".conversations-*.json.tmp")` ŌåÆ `defer os.Remove(tmp)` ŌåÆ `Chmod(0o600)` ŌåÆ `json.NewEncoder(f).SetIndent("", "  ")` ŌåÆ `Encode(...)` ŌåÆ `f.Sync()` ŌåÆ `f.Close()` ŌåÆ `os.Rename(tmp, path)`. SIGKILL anywhere before rename leaves the pre-existing target byte-identical; SIGKILL after leaves the new version. Partial JSON in the target is unreachable. The `0o600` chmod is unconditional even though `os.CreateTemp` defaults to that mode ŌĆö same belt-and-suspenders pattern as the sessions and devices recipes. No parent-directory fsync (per `lessons.md` ┬¦ "Atomic on-disk writes").
- **The atomic-write recipe is duplicated, NOT shared.** Per the issue tech note: "Resist over-DRY on the atomic-write helper ŌĆö duplicate until divergence becomes an observed problem." No shared `internal/registry` helper across `sessions` / `devices` / `conversations` / `identity`. Three registries already differ on sort key (`CreatedAt` / `PairedAt`+`Name` / `LastUsedAt`+`ID`), envelope shape (`{"sessions": ...}` / `{"devices": ...}` / `{"conversations": ...}`), and uniqueness invariants; sharing would hide divergence as Phase 3 grows. Revisit only if real divergence cost surfaces.
- **`Save` snapshots the slice under `mu`, releases, then performs sort + I/O outside the lock.** Inherits the divergence devices made from sessions's hold-across-I/O ŌĆö concurrent `Get` / `List` / `Update` are not blocked behind the syscall window. Two concurrent `Save` calls produce two complete temp files and two renames; the later rename wins (`os.Rename` is atomic per call). Snapshot is a shallow copy (`make([]Conversation, len) + copy`); safe today because nothing mutates `SessionHistory []string` in place outside the registry lock ŌĆö every mutation goes through `Update` and runs under `r.mu`. If a future caller starts mutating `SessionHistory` outside the lock, the snapshot will need a per-element `append([]string(nil), c.SessionHistory...)` deep copy.
- **Sort by `LastUsedAt` ascending, tiebreak `ID` byte-exact, on every Save.** Diverges from devices's `PairedAt`/`Name` ordering: `Conversation` is mutable (rename, promote, rotate sessions, bump `LastUsedAt`), so `LastUsedAt` is the natural "recently active" axis; `ID` is the determinism-only tiebreaker (`Cwd` is creation-time stable but less semantically meaningful as a sort axis). `time.Time.Equal` (not `==`) for the primary comparator ŌĆö JSON roundtrip strips monotonic-clock state and `==` would treat otherwise-equal timestamps as unequal (per `lessons.md`). Sort runs on the Save-side snapshot, not on the live in-memory slice ŌĆö `Create` insertion order in memory is preserved while disk output stays byte-deterministic.
- **Envelope shape is `{"conversations": [...]}`.** Reserves room for future top-level fields (schema version, archive cursor) without a wire break, jq-pipeline break, or stdlib-decoder discipline change. Same future-proofing rationale as sessions and devices envelopes. No `version` field today (out of scope per AC; defer until first migration).
- **Load semantics: missing ŌåÆ empty + nil; zero-byte ŌåÆ empty + nil; malformed ŌåÆ wrapped `registry: parse` error + nil registry; other I/O ŌåÆ wrapped `registry: read` + nil.** Empty-as-cold-start asymmetry vs. `internal/config.Load` (which surfaces zero-byte as a parse error) is deliberate: `conversations.json` is pyry-owned and zero bytes is a benign cold-start state; `config.json` is operator-owned and zero bytes is operator error. Malformed file returns an error AND a nil `*Registry`. Caller decides whether to halt startup (correct for production) or fall back to empty (incorrect ŌĆö masks operator error). `Load` does NOT auto-fall-back.
- **`Create(c)` does not validate uniqueness, well-formedness, or non-emptiness of `c.ID`.** AC pins the literal signature with no return value; match it exactly. Same convention as `devices.Add` ŌĆö keeping the registry I/O-thin lets the consuming layer (the conversations API in #218) own validation policy, which may evolve. `Get(id)` is byte-exact `==` over a linear scan; `(Conversation{}, false)` on miss. Linear scan is correct at this scale (O(10┬▓) conversations at the high end).
- **`List(filter ...ListFilter) []Conversation` is variadic for ergonomics, NOT for AND-composition.** When `len(filter) > 1`, only `filter[0]` is consulted ŌĆö documented in the doc comment. `ListFilter{IsPromoted *bool}` distinguishes three states a bare `bool` cannot: `nil` ("no filter"), `*true` ("only promoted"), `*false` ("only unpromoted"). The returned slice is a copy; callers may mutate it freely without affecting registry state. Test pins all three filter cases plus the "mutate the returned slice ŌåÆ subsequent `List` is unchanged" invariant.
- **`Update(id, fn func(*Conversation)) bool` runs `fn` with `r.mu` held and a pointer to the slice element.** Three caller obligations pinned in the doc comment: (1) `fn` MUST NOT call back into the registry ŌĆö `sync.Mutex` is non-reentrant, any `Registry` method would deadlock; (2) `fn` MUST NOT retain the `*Conversation` pointer past return ŌĆö slice reallocation by a future `Create` would dangle the pointer; (3) `fn` may read and mutate any field ŌĆö the registry does not validate post-mutation state (does not reject a flip that duplicates another entry's ID, does not reject `LastUsedAt` going backwards). Pointer-to-slice-element is the right shape because `Conversation` carries reference fields (`*string Name`, `[]string SessionHistory`); pass-by-value would force `fn` to construct a full replacement struct on every change, defeating the point. AC pins the `bool` (hit/miss) return ŌĆö not `(Conversation, bool)`; if a future caller needs a post-mutation snapshot, read it inside `fn` (the lock guarantees no concurrent mutation between read and any subsequent in-callback decision). See [ADR 022](knowledge/decisions/022-conversations-update-callback-under-lock.md) ŌĆö the snapshot-mutate-swap alternative was rejected because of lost writes under concurrent same-id updates and reference-field aliasing concerns.
- **`devices` doesn't need an `Update` because device records are append-only after pairing.** Conversations mutate (rename, promote, rotate the bound session, bump `LastUsedAt`), so this method is genuinely needed. `Update` is the canonical mutation entry point; new mutation surfaces (rename API, promote API, session rotation in #218) all funnel through `Update` rather than acquiring `Registry.mu` from the outside.
- **Concurrency model is the existing single-mutex contract.** All methods take `r.mu` exactly once; no new lock, no ordering, no callbacks (except `Update`'s `fn` which runs *inside* the critical section), no re-entrance. No goroutines spawned; no `context.Context` threaded ŌĆö registry operations are CPU-bound and fast (in-memory mutation; `Save`'s I/O is microseconds for the expected record count). If a future caller needs cancellation around `Save`, the right shape is a wrapper at that layer, not contaminating the package surface.
- **`id.go` is a byte-for-byte clone of `internal/sessions/id.go`, NOT a shared helper.** `NewID()` reads 16 bytes from `crypto/rand`, sets the version-4 nibble (`b[6] = b[6]&0x0f | 0x40`) and RFC 4122 variant nibble (`b[8] = b[8]&0x3f | 0x80`), formats canonical lowercase hex. `ValidID(s)` checks 36 chars, lowercase hex, dashes at 8/13/18/23, version-4 at 14, variant in `{8,9,a,b}` at 19. **Lowercase only** ŌĆö uppercase rejected (matches `sessions.ValidID`); the on-disk record is always the lowercase form `NewID` produces. Duplication is intentional per the same "resist over-DRY" rule that applies to the atomic-write recipe.
- **Tests in `registry_test.go`** (~489 LOC) ŌĆö same-package, `t.Parallel()` everywhere except permission-mutating tests, stdlib only. Mirrors `devices/registry_test.go` one-for-one (load missing/empty/malformed; round-trip with sort assertion; file permissions; stable ordering; atomic-rename-preserves-old; concurrent-readwrite race probe) plus four new tests for the conversation-specific surface: `TestRegistry_List_Filter` (table-driven nil/`*true`/`*false`/`filter[0]`-only/mutating-returned-slice-doesn't-affect-registry); `TestRegistry_Update_Hit` (bumps `LastUsedAt`, flips `IsPromoted`, sets `Name`; subsequent `Get` reflects the mutation); `TestRegistry_Update_Miss` (absent id returns `false`, `fn` never invoked via test-controlled flag, registry untouched); `TestRegistry_Update_PointerStability` (mutating `*Conversation` inside `fn` propagates to subsequent reads ŌĆö pins the contract). `id_test.go` (~75 LOC) mirrors `sessions/id_test.go`: format regex + 1000-iteration uniqueness + table-driven valid/empty/wrong-length/wrong-dashes/wrong-version/wrong-variant/uppercase-rejected.
- **Out of scope, by design.** No `Remove` method (not in AC; conversations are not deleted in Phase 3 ŌĆö they're archived via `IsPromoted` flips and history retention; if a future API ticket needs deletion, that ticket adds it with its own tests). No schema versioning (defer until first migration). No daemon wiring (this ticket lands the package; the supervisor / API layer that calls `Load` at startup and `Save` after mutations is a separate ticket). No promotion API (#218). No auto-archive predicate + sweep (#219, #220). No migration from existing `Session` registry (TBD ticket once Conversations is proven on disk; Phase 1/2 sessions stay untouched). No shared atomic-write helper across `devices` and `conversations` packages (issue tech note explicitly forbids; revisit only if real divergence cost surfaces). No `Update`-returns-`(Conversation, bool)` shape (AC bool-only; additive change later costs nothing if a Phase 3 caller needs the post-state).
- See [knowledge/features/conversations-package.md](knowledge/features/conversations-package.md), [knowledge/features/conversations-registry.md](knowledge/features/conversations-registry.md), [knowledge/decisions/022-conversations-update-callback-under-lock.md](knowledge/decisions/022-conversations-update-callback-under-lock.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/217-conversations-registry-crud.md`](specs/architecture/217-conversations-registry-crud.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 wiring, ticket #213)
- **`cmd/pyry/pair.go` ŌĆö `pyry pair` one-shot CLI verb.** New file (~110 prod LOC) + 6 LOC of edits to `cmd/pyry/main.go` (one switch case for `pair`, one usage line in `printHelp`, one entry in the reserved-verbs comment block). Composes the seven Phase 3 foundation primitives (`config.Load`, `devices.Load`, `identity.LoadOrCreate`, `crypto/rand.Read`, `devices.HashToken`, `Registry.Add` + `Save`, `pair.Render`) into a single CLI verb. **No new types, no new packages**, no daemon dependency. Production diff: +110 `pair.go` (new) + 6 `main.go` + 25 `internal/e2e/harness.go` (new `RunBareIn` helper) = ~140 prod LOC across three files. Test diff: +140 `pair_test.go` (new) + 106 `internal/e2e/pair_test.go` (new). Zero new dependencies (`go.mod` unchanged), zero changes to existing primitives, zero CLI-side breakage of any sibling verb.
- **Order of operations is structural, enforced by code position.** (1) Parse flags ŌåÆ exit 2 on error. (2) `config.Load(~/.pyry/config.json)` ŌåÆ exit 1. (3) `resolveRelay(flag, cfg)` ŌåÆ exit 2 if empty. (4) `devices.Load(~/.pyry/<name>/devices.json)` ŌåÆ exit 1. (5) `identity.LoadOrCreate(~/.pyry/<name>/server-id)` ŌåÆ exit 1. (6) `crypto/rand.Read(32)` ŌåÆ hex-encode ŌåÆ exit 1 on rng error. (7) `HashToken(plain)`. (8) deviceName resolution. (9) `Registry.Add`. (10) `Registry.Save` ŌåÆ exit 1. (11) `pair.Render(payload, os.Stdout)` ŌåÆ exit 1 on write error. **All loads before mint** (steps 1ŌĆō5 before step 6) ŌĆö a misconfigured relay or unreadable file fails before the token is generated. **Save before Render** (step 10 before step 11) ŌĆö if `Save` fails, `Render` is skipped, and the plaintext token never escapes the process. Reverse ordering (Render before Save) would be wrong: a printed-but-unsaved token is silent at pair-time and fatal at connect-time (the daemon would `auth.invalid_token` because the hash isn't in `devices.json`). See [ADR 021](knowledge/decisions/021-pair-cli-order-of-operations.md).
- **Three path resolvers in `pair.go`, two MUST sanitize.** `resolveDevicesPath(name)` ŌåÆ `~/.pyry/<sanitizeName(name)>/devices.json`. `resolveServerIDPath(name)` ŌåÆ `~/.pyry/<sanitizeName(name)>/server-id`. `resolveConfigPath()` ŌåÆ `~/.pyry/config.json` (per-user, no instance-name segment, no sanitization needed). The two per-instance resolvers MUST call `sanitizeName` (the existing helper at `cmd/pyry/main.go:121-138`) for the same reason `resolveRegistryPath` and `resolveSocketPath` do ŌĆö `PYRY_NAME=../../etc` or `-pyry-name=../etc` must not let an unprivileged user write to a sibling directory. Pinned by `TestResolveDevicesPath` / `TestResolveServerIDPath` via a `filepath.Rel(~/.pyry, <result>)` containment check that fails if the result escapes. The three resolvers live in `cmd/pyry/pair.go` for now; lift to `main.go` if a future ticket needs them elsewhere.
- **Flag surface: three flags, only two named in the AC.** `-pyry-name` (instance-scoping; matches every other pyry verb), `--name` (device label), `--relay` (override). `-pyry-name` is added because `devices.json` and `server-id` are per-instance ŌĆö the AC named only `--name` and `--relay`, but the AC also says the verb writes to `~/.pyry/<name>/devices.json`, which forces the scoping. Default for `-pyry-name` is `defaultName()` ŌĆö `PYRY_NAME` env or literal `"pyry"` ŌĆö same as the supervisor and every control verb. Single-instance users get a consistent state directory across every verb. The `parsePairArgs` helper is `flag.NewFlagSet("pyry pair", flag.ContinueOnError)` with three `String` flags + `fs.SetOutput(io.Discard)` (so `flag.Parse`'s default usage doesn't double-print) + a positional check (`fs.NArg() > 0` ŌåÆ `unexpected positional %q` error).
- **Auto-name is `device-<hash[:8]>`, derived AFTER hashing.** Stable per-token, derivable from the on-disk registry entry alone, never reveals plaintext (8 hex chars = 32 bits of hash, no preimage). Empty `--name` triggers; non-empty `--name` is used verbatim ŌĆö no validation, no uniqueness check (`Registry.Add` documents that uniqueness is the caller's concern, and lookup is by `TokenHash`, not by `Name`, so duplicate-name entries coexist harmlessly).
- **Relay URL precedence in `resolveRelay`: flag ŌåÆ cfg.RelayURL ŌåÆ DefaultConfig().RelayURL.** First non-empty wins. The third leg is normally redundant ŌĆö `config.Load` already overlays `DefaultConfig` per [ADR 018](knowledge/decisions/018-config-overlay-decode.md) ŌĆö but the AC names it explicitly so the explicit fall-through stays in code (makes the AC text traceable). Empty result is reachable only if all three are empty (built-in default unset *and* config.json absent/unset *and* flag unset); triggers exit 2 with a stderr hint naming both knobs (`pyry pair: relay URL is empty (set --relay or relay_url in ~/.pyry/config.json)`).
- **Exit codes: 0 success / 1 I/O or render error / 2 parse error or empty relay.** `runPair` returns `error` for exit-1 conditions (which `main()` already maps to `os.Exit(1)` with a `pyry: ` prefix) and calls `os.Exit(2)` directly for exit-2 conditions so the `pyry: ` prefix doesn't appear on usage-style failures. The AC names "registry I/O error" for exit 1 and "empty relay" for exit 2; the implementation extends that contract: `config.Load` / `identity.LoadOrCreate` / `crypto/rand.Read` / `pair.Render` write errors all map to exit 1 because they share the same operator-remediation shape (fix filesystem / pipe / retry).
- **Token visibility: plaintext escapes only via `pair.Render(payload, os.Stdout)`.** `cmd/pyry/pair.go` never constructs a `*slog.Logger`, never calls `slog.*`, and never embeds `plain` / `payload` / `Encode(payload)` into any error wrapping. All operator-visible strings are stderr human strings (the empty-relay hint, parse-error usage line) or bare `fmt.Errorf("pair: %w", err)` wraps of underlying primitives ŌĆö none of which carry token bytes by construction (each layer's contract is reviewed separately). The discipline mirrors `internal/pair/render.go:23-30` and `internal/devices/device.go`'s package doc-comment.
- **Concurrency: none.** Single goroutine, top-down. Two race-against-other-process scenarios named in the spec, both out of scope for #213. (a) Daemon staleness: if a daemon is running with the same `-pyry-name`, its in-memory `devices.json` becomes stale after `pair`. Structurally empty in #213 because no daemon-side consumer of `devices.json` exists yet (the WS-handshake auth path is a future ticket; that ticket will add reload-on-write or a daemon-side `pair` control verb). (b) Two concurrent `pyry pair` invocations: both `Load`, both `Add`, both `Save` ŌĆö second's atomic-rename overwrites first's append. The first invocation has already printed a QR; the user thinks they paired but the on-disk record is gone. Failure mode is "phone fails to auth," not credential leakage. Fix is `flock`/`fcntl` on `devices.json` at the `devices.Registry` layer, not in this verb.
- **`RunBareIn(t, home, args...)` e2e helper added to `internal/e2e/harness.go`.** Mechanical copy of `RunBare` with one line spliced: `cmd.Env = childEnv(home)`. Pins HOME to a caller-supplied directory so verbs that read `~`-relative state can be driven against a `t.TempDir()` in isolation. Like `RunBare`, does NOT auto-inject `-pyry-socket` ŌĆö there is no daemon spawned. ~25 LOC. First consumer is `TestPair_E2E` (#213); future daemon-free verbs that touch `~/.pyry/*` reuse it.
- **Tests: 4 unit tests in `cmd/pyry/pair_test.go` + 1 e2e test in `internal/e2e/pair_test.go` (`//go:build e2e`, two sub-tests).** Unit: `TestParsePairArgs` (table ŌĆö empty, `--name`, `--relay`, both, name-space-form, positional rejected, unknown flag rejected); `TestResolveRelay` (table ŌĆö flag wins, config wins when flag empty, default wins when both empty); `TestResolveDevicesPath` / `TestResolveServerIDPath` (HOME isolation via `t.Setenv`, asserts joined path AND that path-traversal `../etc` is neutralized via `filepath.Rel` containment check); `TestResolveConfigPath` (per-user layout, no sanitization). E2e: `TestPair_E2E` two sub-tests ŌĆö "with explicit name" and "auto-name when --name omitted"; both assert exit 0, decode payload via `pair.Decode`, load `<home>/.pyry/pyry/devices.json` via `devices.Load`, assert one entry with the expected `Name` and `devices.VerifyToken(payload.Token, entry.TokenHash)` true. The empty-relay (exit 2) path is unit-tested only because it's not reachable through real config (the default constant is non-empty; an e2e would require swapping it at build time).
- **Out of scope, by design.** `pyry pair revoke <name>` (sibling ŌĆö calls `Remove(name)` then `Save`). `pyry pair list` (sibling ŌĆö surfaces `Registry.List()`; display rule for token-hash prefix lives in `protocol-mobile.md:663`). Daemon-side `pair` control verb (mirroring `pyry sessions new` once a WS-handshake auth path consumes `devices.json` in-process). `flock`/`fcntl` on `devices.json` (fix for two-concurrent-`pair` races; belongs at the `devices.Registry` layer, not in this verb). `--relay` mutating `~/.pyry/config.json` (explicitly rejected; `--relay` overrides the printed payload only ŌĆö edit `config.json` directly to persist a relay change). Empty-relay e2e test (would require swapping the default constant at build time; pinned by unit test instead).
- See [knowledge/features/pyry-pair-command.md](knowledge/features/pyry-pair-command.md), [knowledge/decisions/021-pair-cli-order-of-operations.md](knowledge/decisions/021-pair-cli-order-of-operations.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/213-pair-command.md`](specs/architecture/213-pair-command.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #210)
- **`internal/devices/auth.go` ŌĆö `(*Registry).Validate(plain string) (Device, bool)`.** New file (~25 prod LOC) co-located with `device.go` (#208) and `registry.go` (#209). One new exported method on the existing `Registry`; zero new exported types, zero new sentinels, zero new packages. Stdlib only (`time`). Production diff: +25 LOC `auth.go` (new). Test diff: +158 LOC `auth_test.go` (new). Zero new dependencies, zero changes to existing code, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change. No consumers wired in this slice ŌĆö the WS-handshake auth handler that calls `Validate` is a follow-up Phase-3 ticket.
- **The WS-perimeter auth predicate.** Single entry point composing the three #208/#209 primitives that previously had to be wired by hand at every prospective call site: `HashToken(plain)` ŌåÆ byte-exact scan against `Registry.devices[i].TokenHash` ŌåÆ in-memory `LastSeenAt = time.Now()` advance on hit. Handler call site is a one-line `d, ok := reg.Validate(plain)`; the empty-plain early-out, the constant-time-vs-byte-exact split, and the locked mutation are co-located so they cannot drift across handler implementations.
- **Method on `*Registry`, not a free function.** AC permitted either; method chosen because the `LastSeenAt` mutation is a registry-side operation and methods on `*Registry` already own `mu` and `devices`. Free-function `Validate(r *Registry, plain string)` would either re-export `mu` / `devices` (encapsulation leak) or call an unexported helper for no abstraction win. Mirrors the existing `Add` / `Remove` / `List` / `FindByTokenHash` shape; `Validate` is the fifth method.
- **Body is five points of structural discipline.** (1) Empty-plain early-out is FIRST ŌĆö before `HashToken`, before the lock ŌĆö enforcing the AC's "no registry lookup" structurally and (cheaply) defending the unreachable case of a `Device` persisted with `TokenHash == HashToken("")`. (2) `HashToken` runs OUTSIDE the lock ŌĆö SHA-256 over a short string is microseconds but moving it outside keeps the critical section to scan + mutate + return-value materialization, which matters because the auth path is the high-frequency reader. (3) Indexed loop (`for i := range r.devices`) ŌĆö value-loop `for _, d := range r.devices` would copy the element and the `LastSeenAt = ...` assignment would silently no-op. (4) Mutation and snapshot both INSIDE the lock ŌĆö return value is `r.devices[i]` (value-type copy taken before the deferred unlock fires), so callers observe the just-written timestamp. (5) Byte-exact `==` on `TokenHash`, NOT `subtle.ConstantTimeCompare` ŌĆö constant-time at the plainŌåöhash boundary is owned by `HashToken`; once the wire plain has been hashed, comparing two 64-char hex strings reveals only a public derivative. Inherits the chain from #208 + #209 verbatim; do not relitigate.
- **`Validate` does NOT call `Save`.** Disk persistence is the caller's job. Validate runs on the WS hot path and an fsync per auth is a perf footgun. The follow-up consumer ticket schedules `Save` (periodic ticker / graceful-shutdown hook); in-memory `LastSeenAt` is the source of truth for runtime decisions.
- **`Validate` has no `context.Context`, no `*slog.Logger`, no error path.** Body is microseconds at p99 and never blocks (`mu` is uncontended in steady state ŌĆö pairing is rare, auth is solo per-connection). ctx-cancel plumbing for that window is ceremony without value. Auth-event logging belongs at the WS handler (it has `conn-id`, `remote-host`, attempt counter that the registry doesn't see). AC pins the signature as `(Device, bool)`; the constraint "no log/error/panic contains plain, hash, or device name" stands for any future error path but no error path is added today.
- **Why NOT iterate `VerifyToken` over all devices.** Two reasons. (1) Performance: `VerifyToken` recomputes `HashToken(plain)` internally per call ŌĆö N devices means N SHA-256 computations vs. one for "hash plain once, byte-exact scan." (2) The constant-time concern is the plainŌåöhash boundary, which `HashToken` satisfies (deterministic, no early-exit on input). Once hashed, comparing 64-char hex strings is byte-exact; timing of `==` on a hash leaks only what the attacker could compute themselves from any candidate plain. See #208 ┬¦ "Constant-time compare" and #209 ┬¦ "Should `FindByTokenHash` use `subtle.ConstantTimeCompare`?" for the full chain. Sibling decisions stand.
- **Concurrency: one critical section under existing `Registry.mu`, no new lock, no ordering.** Two concurrent `Validate` calls on the same token serialize on `mu`; first writes `T1`, second observes `T2 Ōēź T1` (Go's `time.Now()` is monotonic per process ŌĆö same-value reads at clock-granularity edges still satisfy `>=`) and writes `T2`. Final stored `LastSeenAt` is `T2` ŌĆö the AC's "monotonically-non-decreasing" invariant. Concurrent `Save` snapshots whatever value sits in memory at its lock-acquisition (any of `T1`, `T2`, or pre-update is correct ŌĆö same durability semantics as #209). Concurrent `Remove` between two `Validate` calls makes the second return `(Device{}, false)` cleanly (no torn read; second scan runs after splice committed).
- **`time.Now()` directly, no clock injection.** Tests verify `after.After(before)` (wall-clock advancing under real concurrency) and `final.After(when)` (the field was actually written) ŌĆö neither needs a fake clock. Inherits #209's convention (`PairedAt` is caller-filled; the registry doesn't take a clock). If a future test needs deterministic timestamps (e.g. snapshot golden-file diff), introduce a `Clock` interface then.
- **Tests in `auth_test.go`** ŌĆö same-package, `t.Parallel()` everywhere, stdlib only. Five tests: `TestRegistry_Validate_Hit` (valid token returns matching device + asserts both the returned snapshot AND the in-memory mutation via `List()`; `PairedAt` unchanged), `TestRegistry_Validate_MissUnknown` (`(Device{}, false)` + no mutation observed via `List()`), `TestRegistry_Validate_MissEmpty` (empty plain ŌåÆ `(Device{}, false)` + no mutation; the "no registry lookup" half is enforced structurally by the early-out, the test asserts the observable consequence), `TestRegistry_Validate_EmptyRegistry` (defends against panic on a zero-init `*Registry`), `TestRegistry_Validate_ConcurrentSameToken` (16 goroutines, race-detector probe; sorts the per-goroutine observed `LastSeenAt` values and asserts each `>=` previous; `final.After(when)` proves a structurally-correct lock didn't accidentally skip the mutation due to a value-receiver bug ŌĆö race detector catches a missing lock on the slice-element write).
- **Out of scope, by design.** WS-handshake auth handler that calls `Validate` (sibling Phase-3 ticket ŌĆö owns logging with `conn-id`/`remote-host`, returns `auth.invalid_token` per `protocol-mobile.md:97-98` on miss). `Save` cadence policy for `LastSeenAt` durability (consumer's concern ŌĆö periodic ticker / graceful-shutdown hook; this predicate intentionally does not fsync per auth). Rate-limiting / per-token attempt counters / per-IP lockout (handler ticket; the predicate is a leaf primitive). Structured auth-event metrics. Auto-revocation after N consecutive misses (defer). Per-device session-bind enforcement after Validate succeeds. `ValidateE(plain) (Device, error)` per-cause structured-error sibling (defer until a daemon-side audit-log consumer needs it). Deprecating `FindByTokenHash` in favor of `Validate` ŌĆö they're different surfaces (read-only inspector vs. auth predicate); revisit only if `FindByTokenHash` ends Phase 3 with zero callers.
- See [knowledge/features/devices-registry.md](knowledge/features/devices-registry.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/210-pair-token-validation-predicate.md`](specs/architecture/210-pair-token-validation-predicate.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #216)
- **`internal/conversations/conversation.go` ŌĆö `ConversationID` typedef + `Conversation` struct.** New leaf package, stdlib only (`time`); two new files (`conversation.go` ~73 LOC, `conversation_test.go` ~99 LOC). Two exports: `ConversationID` (string newtype, distinct from `sessions.SessionID` to make the swap a compile error at call sites that handle both), `Conversation` (pure value type ŌĆö `ID ConversationID`, `Name *string`, `Cwd string`, `CurrentSessionID string`, `SessionHistory []string`, `IsPromoted bool`, `LastUsedAt time.Time`). Snake_case JSON tags mirror `internal/sessions/registry.go`'s style. `,omitempty` on `Name` / `CurrentSessionID` / `SessionHistory`; never on `ID` / `Cwd` / `IsPromoted` / `LastUsedAt` so the unpromoted-default ("discussion") is explicit on disk. No constructors, no I/O, no consumers wired in this slice ŌĆö foundation for the `conv:` ticket series (#217 registry CRUD, #218 promotion API, #219 auto-archive predicate, #220 auto-archive sweep). Greenfield alongside `internal/sessions`; Phase 1/2 sessions untouched.
- **`ConversationID` is a typedef, not bare `string`.** A conversation carries both its own ID and an embedded `CurrentSessionID`; both being plain `string` would make them swappable at any call site. Distinct nominal types make the swap a compile error. Cost is one extra line and the occasional `ConversationID(s)` conversion at the package boundary ŌĆö accepted. Mirrors the `SessionID` pattern from `internal/sessions/id.go`. Validity predicate (`ValidConversationID`) is **not** defined here ŌĆö #217 owns the generator and validator, mirroring `sessions.ValidID` if conversation IDs are also UUIDv4.
- **`SessionHistory` is chronological (oldest-first).** Rotation appends in place: `append(SessionHistory, prevID)`. Chronological ordering matches the natural append pattern and avoids O(n) shifts on every rotation; presentation layers that want newest-first reverse on read (one O(n) traversal per render, vs. O(n) shifts on every rotation if newest-first is stored). The most recently retired session sits at the tail (`SessionHistory[len-1]`). Documented in the field comment so the choice survives the type definition.
- **`Name` is `*string`, not `string`.** Pointer distinguishes "absent" (nil ŌĆö the user has never named this conversation) from "explicitly empty" (non-nil pointer to `""`). Unpromoted conversations typically leave this nil; promoted conversations (channels) usually carry a name. A future `pyry conv name <id> ""` UX would set a non-nil empty string; "rename to nothing" and "never named" are different states.
- **`CurrentSessionID` and `SessionHistory[i]` are typed as `string`, NOT `sessions.SessionID`.** Keeps `internal/conversations` decoupled from `internal/sessions` while Phase 3 lives alongside Phase 1/2. If a future refactor unifies the two packages, those fields can be retyped without touching the JSON wire format.
- **`omitempty` placement is load-bearing.** `Name`, `CurrentSessionID`, `SessionHistory` carry `,omitempty` so unpromoted/unnamed conversations and conversations with no session bound serialize without those keys. `IsPromoted`, `Cwd`, `ID`, `LastUsedAt` do **NOT** use `omitempty` ŌĆö they must always appear, even at zero value. The `IsPromoted: false` default ("discussion") must be explicit on disk because the field is meaningful in both states; an absent `is_promoted` is ambiguous. `TestConversation_OmitemptyAbsentForUnpromoted` pins both halves: asserts `"name"` / `"current_session_id"` / `"session_history"` are absent from the marshaled bytes, AND spot-checks that `"id"` / `"cwd"` / `"is_promoted"` / `"last_used_at"` are present (the always-present half is otherwise easy to break by accidentally adding `,omitempty` later).
- **No concurrency primitives.** Pure value type ŌĆö no goroutines, no channels, no mutexes. Safe to copy by value. Safe to pass across goroutines provided the usual "no concurrent mutation of `SessionHistory` slice header" Go rules are followed by the future owner (#217's registry).
- **Tests in `conversation_test.go`** ŌĆö same-package, table-driven, stdlib `testing` only. Two tests: `TestConversation_JSONRoundTrip` (two cases ŌĆö promoted + named + non-empty history with Ōēź2 entries to verify ordering, and unpromoted + unnamed + nil history; each marshals to JSON, unmarshals back, asserts `reflect.DeepEqual(in, out)`), `TestConversation_OmitemptyAbsentForUnpromoted` (marshals the unpromoted case, asserts the three `omitempty` keys are absent and the four always-present keys are present, via `bytes.Contains` against literal byte slices). Test inputs use `time.Date(...)` (no monotonic clock component) so `DeepEqual` on `time.Time` survives the round-trip, per `lessons.md` ┬¦ "JSON roundtrip strips monotonic-clock state". `SessionHistory == nil` round-trips to nil under `omitempty`; the unpromoted case sets the input to `nil` (not `[]string{}`) so `DeepEqual` holds.
- **Production diff: `internal/conversations/conversation.go` +73 LOC (new file). Test diff: `internal/conversations/conversation_test.go` +99 LOC (new file).** Zero new dependencies (`go.mod` unchanged), zero changes to existing code, zero new exported names outside the new package, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Persistence (#217 ŌĆö `~/.pyry/<name>/conversations.json` registry CRUD with the same atomic-rename + `0600` recipe `internal/sessions/registry.go` and `internal/devices/registry.go` use). Validity predicate `ValidConversationID` (#217 owns it, mirroring `sessions.ValidID` if UUIDv4). Promotion API `pyry conv promote` / `pyry conv name` (#218). Auto-archive predicate (#219) + sweep (#220). Migration from existing `Session` registry (TBD ticket once Conversations is proven on disk; Phase 1/2 sessions stay untouched). Schema versioning (defer until first migration).
- See [knowledge/features/conversations-package.md](knowledge/features/conversations-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/216-conversation-type.md`](specs/architecture/216-conversation-type.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #212)
- **`internal/pair/render.go` ŌĆö `Render(p Payload, w io.Writer) error`.** New file (~58 LOC) that wraps the #211 `Encode` output in a QR symbol (UTF-8 half-blocks via `qrterminal.GenerateHalfBlock` at error-correction level `M`), a blank line, the encoded payload string, and a fixed instruction line, all written to a caller-supplied `io.Writer` in that exact order. One new exported function (`Render`); one unexported helper type (`errTrackingWriter`). Production diff: +58 LOC `render.go` (new). Test diff: +158 LOC `render_test.go` (new). One new module dependency: `github.com/mdp/qrterminal/v3 v3.2.1` (pure-Go, MIT, built on `rsc.io/qr v0.2.0` ŌĆö also pure-Go, MIT, by Russ Cox / the Go team). Zero changes to existing code, zero new exported names outside `Render`, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change. No consumers wired in this slice ŌĆö the eventual `pyry pair` CLI ticket will pass `os.Stdout`.
- **`GenerateHalfBlock` over `Generate`.** `qrterminal/v3` exposes both. `Generate` uses one terminal cell per QR module (`Ō¢ł` and space); the printed shape is roughly twice as tall as wide on typical 2:1 terminal cell aspect ratios, which trips up phone-camera QR detectors that expect a square symbol. `GenerateHalfBlock` packs two QR rows per terminal row using `Ō¢Ć`/`Ō¢ä`/`Ō¢ł`/space; the printed shape comes out roughly square and scans more reliably. The AC explicitly named "the half-block variants emitted by `qrterminal/v3`," and `protocol-mobile.md`'s security model #3 names unscannable QR codes as a UX-degrading failure mode.
- **Error-correction level `M`** (medium, ~15% recovery) ŌĆö library default for `Generate*`. Fits the ~120-140 base64-character payload at QR version 5ŌĆō6, well within an 80-column terminal. `L` shrinks the symbol slightly but is fragile to terminal font glitches; `Q`/`H` enlarge the symbol and risk wrapping. Locked at the call site as a literal `qrterminal.M` ŌĆö no package-level var, no config knob, no exposing the choice in the function signature. If the trade-off ever needs revisiting, change it here.
- **`errTrackingWriter` propagates writer errors through qrterminal's no-error-return API.** `qrterminal.GenerateHalfBlock` has signature `func(text string, l Level, w io.Writer)` ŌĆö no error return, internally calls `w.Write` and discards errors. To honor AC #3 ("returns an error if the writer fails; does not panic on writer failure; does not partially-render-and-swallow"), `Render` passes a small unexported wrapper that captures the first non-nil write error and short-circuits all subsequent `Write` calls (returning `(0, t.err)` once errored). After the four ordered writes complete, `Render` returns `tw.err`. The pattern matches the stdlib idiom (cf. `bufio.Writer.flush` short-circuit on `b.err`); `TestRender_DoesNotPanicOnBrokenWriter` is the belt-and-suspenders proof that a writer panicking on the second call is never reached.
- **The returned error is the bare underlying writer error, NOT wrapped.** `errors.Is(err, io.ErrShortWrite)` matches in `TestRender_WriterError` because the bare error propagates. The AC says "returns an error if the writer fails," not "returns an error annotated with context." The stdlib idiom for "you handed me a writer; here's what your writer told me" is the bare error; `pyry pair`'s top-level error handler is the wrapping site, not `Render`.
- **Output is plain ASCII + the half-block code points qrterminal emits.** No ANSI color codes, no emoji, no terminal control sequences. Paste-fallback users in non-TTY contexts (logs piped to a file) need ANSI-free output; the AC's "instruction line" is a fixed-copy string the developer must not paraphrase: `"Scan the QR with the Pyrycode mobile app, or paste the string above into the app's pairing screen."`.
- **`Render` does NOT validate `p` or call `Decode` on the encoded string before writing.** Same posture as `Encode`: a zero `Payload` produces a string `Decode` and the phone reject ŌĆö the failure surfaces on scan, not on render. Round-trip is `payload.go`'s invariant proven by `TestEncodeDecodeRoundTrip`; re-running it inside `Render` would couple this surface to that test for no protocol benefit. `Render` also caches `Encode(p)` in a local ŌĆö `Encode` is deterministic, but one call is one call.
- **`Render` adds NO surrounding framing.** No banner, no server-id summary, no relay summary, no warning copy. AC #2 pins exactly four output sections in fixed order; the eventual `pyry pair` CLI ticket owns the surrounding presentation. The illustrative CLI lines in `protocol-mobile.md:705-714` (`==> Server-id: ŌĆ”`, `==> Scan QR or paste this:`, ŌĆ”) are the future ticket's concern, NOT this slice's contract.
- **`Render` adds NO terminal-width sizing.** `qrterminal/v3` produces a symbol whose width is fixed by the QR version (encoded length); narrower terminals wrap, that is the user's concern. Sizing detection is later-ticket scope at best.
- **Token-secrecy contract continues at the render layer.** Render's output **contains the plaintext device-token** (visible inside the QR symbol and verbatim on the paste-fallback line). The function doc-comment instructs callers explicitly: never log the writer's destination, never capture this output into any persisted context (CI logs, telemetry, error reports), treat the calling goroutine's stdout as the only intended sink. The future `pyry pair` ticket will pass `os.Stdout`; tests pass a `bytes.Buffer` that goes out of scope at function exit. `Render` itself does not log, persist, or otherwise duplicate the rendered bytes ŌĆö pure write-to-supplied-writer; no `slog` calls, no error wrapping that would echo bytes, no telemetry. Aligns with `protocol-mobile.md:608` ("Paste-fallback is one-time-only") and `:603` ("QR screenshots auto-uploaded to cloud backup" is the user's risk; the render layer does not introduce a *third* exposure surface beyond the two already documented).
- **Test-failure logging discipline extends from `payload_test.go`.** No `t.Logf("rendered: %s", buf.String())`, no `t.Logf("encoded: %s", Encode(p))` anywhere in `render_test.go`. Test failures report category-only messages: "did not contain a QR block code point," "Encode(p) substring not found in rendered output," etc. The `testToken` constant is a fixed test-file value (not a real device token), but writing the discipline into tests exercises the muscle for when this code path runs against real tokens in the future `pyry pair` integration test.
- **Tests in `render_test.go`** ŌĆö same-package, stdlib `testing` only, `t.Parallel()` everywhere. Five tests: `TestRender_Format_Happy` (non-empty buffer; contains at least one of `{Ō¢ł, Ō¢Ć, Ō¢ä}`; contains `Encode(p)` as substring; contains the exact instruction string), `TestRender_FieldOrder` (split buffer at `Encode(p)` substring; QR block code point in prefix; instruction line in suffix; at least one blank line between QR and encoded payload), `TestRender_Deterministic` (Render twice into two buffers; assert `bytes.Equal` ŌĆö phone re-scanning doesn't see a different symbol; pinned via JSON marshal determinism + `qrterminal/v3`'s stateless `Generate*`), `TestRender_WriterError` (writer returning `io.ErrShortWrite` on every `Write`; assert `errors.Is(err, io.ErrShortWrite)` ŌĆö bare error propagated, not wrapped), `TestRender_DoesNotPanicOnBrokenWriter` (writer that panics if called more than once after the first error ŌĆö pins the `errTrackingWriter` short-circuit). No fixtures, no `t.TempDir`, no PTY; runs under `go test -race ./...` in milliseconds.
- **Dependency justification.** `github.com/mdp/qrterminal/v3` (~200 LOC, MIT, single-call API `Generate*(text, level, w)`) + `rsc.io/qr` (~1500 LOC, MIT, by Russ Cox / the Go team ŌĆö well-maintained QR encoder). Both pure-Go, no cgo, stdlib-only otherwise. CODING-STYLE.md "Stdlib over dependencies" allows external deps when they "provide significant value (like `creack/pty`)" ŌĆö a QR encoder is not in the stdlib and writing one is a multi-hundred-LOC undertaking that duplicates a battle-tested, widely-used library. `go.sum` checksum verification (Go default) is the supply-chain defense.
- **Out of scope, by design.** `pyry pair` CLI itself (later phase-3 ticket ŌĆö mints token, builds `Payload`, calls `Render(p, os.Stdout)`, prints surrounding banner with server-id summary + warning copy). Token generation / hashing / persistence (#208 hashes; minter is later). Anything mobile-side: QR alphabet selection, error-correction trade-offs, app-side decoding. Terminal-width sizing detection. Configurable error-correction level. Color codes / ANSI sequences. Logging or persistence of rendered bytes anywhere.
- See [knowledge/features/pair-package.md](knowledge/features/pair-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/212-pair-qr-render.md`](specs/architecture/212-pair-qr-render.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #209)
- **`internal/devices/registry.go` ŌĆö `Registry` (mutex-guarded device list) + atomic-write `Save` + `Load` + `Add` / `Remove` / `List` / `FindByTokenHash`.** New file (~154 LOC) co-located with `device.go` (#208). Six exports on the new `Registry` type. Stdlib only (`encoding/json`, `os`, `path/filepath`, `sort`, `sync`). Production diff: +154 LOC `registry.go` (new). Test diff: +354 LOC `registry_test.go` (new). Zero new dependencies, zero changes to existing code, zero CLI surface, zero wire-format change.
- **Atomic-write recipe is structurally identical to `internal/sessions/registry.go:saveRegistryLocked`.** `MkdirAll(dir, 0o700)` ŌåÆ `CreateTemp(dir, ".devices-*.json.tmp")` ŌåÆ `defer os.Remove(tmp)` ŌåÆ `Chmod(0o600)` ŌåÆ `json.NewEncoder(f).Encode(...)` ŌåÆ `f.Sync()` ŌåÆ `f.Close()` ŌåÆ `os.Rename(tmp, path)`. SIGKILL anywhere before rename leaves the pre-existing target byte-identical; SIGKILL after leaves the new version. Partial JSON in the target is unreachable. The `0o600` chmod is unconditional even though `os.CreateTemp` defaults to that mode ŌĆö same belt-and-suspenders pattern as `saveRegistryLocked`. No parent-directory fsync (per `lessons.md` ┬¦ "Atomic on-disk writes").
- **`Save` snapshots the slice under `mu`, releases, then performs sort + I/O outside the lock.** Diverges from `internal/sessions`'s hold-across-I/O specifically because the auth path is the high-frequency reader (`FindByTokenHash(HashToken(presented))` per WS handshake) and pairing is the rare writer. Holding the mutex across the syscall window (`MkdirAll` + `CreateTemp` + `Chmod` + encode + `Sync` + `Close` + `Rename`) would block every concurrent `List` / `FindByTokenHash`. `Device`'s all-value-type fields make a shallow snapshot fully decoupling ŌĆö no field aliases the registry's storage, so the snapshot is strictly safe. Two concurrent `Save` calls produce two complete temp files and two renames; the later rename wins (`os.Rename` is atomic per call). See [ADR 020](knowledge/decisions/020-devices-registry-snapshot-then-write.md). If a future `Device` field becomes a reference type (slice/map/pointer), the snapshot logic must deep-copy that field; today's value-type invariant is what makes the pattern correct.
- **Sort by `PairedAt` ascending, tiebreak `Name` byte-exact, on every Save.** `time.Time.Equal` (not `==`) for the primary comparator ŌĆö JSON roundtrip strips monotonic-clock state and `==` would treat otherwise-equal timestamps as unequal (per `lessons.md` ┬¦ "JSON roundtrip strips monotonic-clock state"). Sort runs on the Save-side snapshot, not on the live in-memory slice ŌĆö `Add` insertion order in memory is preserved (a future "most recently added first" UI is unaffected) while disk output stays byte-deterministic (`TestRegistry_SaveStableOrdering` pins this ŌĆö same logical content + different `Add` permutations produce byte-identical files).
- **Envelope shape is `{"devices": [...]}`, not a bare top-level array.** Reserves room for future top-level fields (schema version, push-token registration metadata per `protocol-mobile.md:495`) without a wire break, jq-pipeline break, or stdlib-decoder discipline change. Same future-proofing rationale as `sessions.json`'s `{"sessions": [...]}` envelope (per `lessons.md` ┬¦ "Don't pick a real verb name as the still-unknown placeholderŌĆ”"). No `version` field today (out of scope per AC; defer until first migration).
- **Load semantics: missing ŌåÆ empty + nil; zero-byte ŌåÆ empty + nil; malformed ŌåÆ wrapped `registry: parse` error + nil registry.** Empty-as-cold-start asymmetry vs. `internal/config.Load` (which surfaces zero-byte as a parse error) is deliberate: `devices.json` is pyry-owned and zero bytes is a benign cold-start state; `config.json` is operator-owned and zero bytes is operator error.
- **`Add` does not validate uniqueness.** AC pins the signature as `Add(d Device)` returning nothing. Pair-mint-side uniqueness check (`Name` collision, `TokenHash` collision) belongs in the consumer (`pyry pair` sibling), not the storage primitive. `Remove(name)` returns `true` iff a device with matching `Name` was found and removed ŌĆö consumers can assert "the device I just revoked actually existed" before logging.
- **`FindByTokenHash` is byte-exact `==` over a linear scan, not `subtle.ConstantTimeCompare`.** Constant-time concern is the plainŌåöhash boundary (owned by `VerifyToken` from #208). Once the wire-presented plain has been hashed (deterministic SHA-256), comparing two 64-char hex strings is byte-exact ŌĆö and any timing leak from `==` early-exit reveals a public derivative (a hash the attacker could compute themselves), not a secret. A linear scan with `==` is the simpler, correct shape.
- **`List` returns a shallow copy.** Callers may mutate the returned slice and its elements without affecting registry state. Deep copy is unnecessary because `Device`'s fields are all value types (`string`, `time.Time`); no field is a reference type that would alias.
- **Path is caller-supplied; the registry doesn't store it.** `Load(path)` and `Save(path)` take the absolute path each call. Daemon-startup wiring (Phase 3 sibling ticket) resolves `~/.pyry/<sanitized-name>/devices.json` alongside the existing `resolveSocketPath` / `resolveRegistryPath`. Storing the path inside the `Registry` would couple it to a single file location and prevent test patterns that load/save against `t.TempDir()`. Mirrors `internal/sessions`'s `loadRegistry(path)` / `saveRegistryLocked(path, reg)` discipline.
- **No logger, no `context.Context`, no `Config`.** Leaf primitive over the filesystem; the existing `slog` discipline applies to *callers* (the pair command logs "paired device <name>" after Save returns; the daemon's startup `Load` failure is fatal). Atomic-write is two syscalls (`Sync`, `Rename`) totaling a few hundred microseconds at p99 on a healthy local fs ŌĆö adding ctx-cancel plumbing for that window would be ceremony without value. Mirrors `internal/sessions/registry.go`'s no-logger pattern.
- **Tests in `registry_test.go`** ŌĆö same-package, table-driven, `t.Parallel()` everywhere, stdlib only. Ten tests: `TestRegistry_LoadMissingFile`, `TestRegistry_LoadEmptyFile`, `TestRegistry_LoadMalformedJSON` (asserts wrapped `registry: parse` prefix), `TestRegistry_AddSaveLoadRoundTrip` (two devices, all four `Device` fields preserved; compares times via `time.Time.Equal`), `TestRegistry_RemovePresent`, `TestRegistry_RemoveAbsent`, `TestRegistry_FindByTokenHash` (table: hit, miss-empty, miss-non-matching, miss-empty-registry), `TestRegistry_SaveFilePermissions` (asserts parent dir mode `0o700` + file mode `0o600`; skipped on Windows), `TestRegistry_SaveStableOrdering` (two `Add` permutations ŌåÆ byte-identical bytes), `TestRegistry_SaveAtomicRenamePreservesOldFile` (chmod-the-dir-readonly trick proves the pre-existing file survives a failed save unchanged; skipped on Windows), `TestRegistry_ConcurrentReadWrite` (8 goroutines, mixed `Add` / `List` / `FindByTokenHash`; race-detector probe ŌĆö if any method drops the lock, `go test -race` flags the slice header / element accesses).
- **Out of scope, by design.** `pyry pair` mint (sibling ŌĆö builds a `Device`, calls `Add` then `Save`). `pyry pair revoke <name>` (sibling ŌĆö calls `Remove(name)` then `Save`). WS-handshake auth (Phase 3 ŌĆö calls `Load` once at daemon startup, `FindByTokenHash(HashToken(presented))` per phone connect). Per-device `last_seen_at` updates on each WS connect (auth-handler concern; this ticket persists the field, doesn't update it). Push-token registration metadata (future top-level field per `protocol-mobile.md:495`; the envelope shape supports additive growth). Schema versioning (defer until first migration). Encrypting `devices.json` at rest (defer; current threat model doesn't justify the operator UX cost). Migration to a database (defer).
- See [knowledge/features/devices-registry.md](knowledge/features/devices-registry.md), [knowledge/decisions/020-devices-registry-snapshot-then-write.md](knowledge/decisions/020-devices-registry-snapshot-then-write.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/209-pair-devices-registry-crud.md`](specs/architecture/209-pair-devices-registry-crud.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #207)
- **`internal/identity/store.go` ŌĆö `LoadOrCreate(path) (ServerID, error)` first-run bootstrap.** New file (~96 LOC) co-located with the existing `server_id.go` (#206); package doc-comment relaxed to drop the "Pure types and validation; no I/O" claim. Production diff: +96 LOC `store.go` (new) + 5 LOC `server_id.go` (doc-comment edit). Test diff: +200 LOC `store_test.go` (new). Zero new dependencies, zero changes to existing exported names, zero CLI surface.
- **Atomic-write recipe is structurally identical to `internal/sessions/registry.go:53-92`.** `MkdirAll(dir, 0o700)` ŌåÆ `CreateTemp(dir, ".server-id-*.tmp")` ŌåÆ `Chmod(0o600)` ŌåÆ `Write(<id>+"\n")` ŌåÆ `Sync` ŌåÆ `Close` ŌåÆ `Rename(tmp, path)`, with `defer os.Remove(tmp)` cleanup. SIGKILL between any two syscalls either commits cleanly or leaves no observable change. The temp's `0600` is set *before* writing data; rename preserves mode, so the final file is `0600` from byte one.
- **`strings.TrimSuffix(s, "\n")`, NOT `strings.TrimSpace`.** AC says "tolerates an *optional* trailing newline but otherwise validate strictly." `TrimSuffix` strips at most one terminal `\n` and leaves leading whitespace, `\r`, tabs, internal spaces in place ŌĆö `ParseServerID` then rejects them. `TrimSpace` would tolerate `\r\n`, surrounding spaces, form-feeds, broadening the parser's accept set for no concrete reason. The corrupt-file test table pins this: CRLF, double-newline, leading-whitespace all return `ErrInvalidServerID`.
- **Corruption is operator-escalated, structurally.** A file failing `ParseServerID` returns `fmt.Errorf("identity: parse %s: %w", path, err)` ŌĆö `errors.Is(err, ErrInvalidServerID)` matches via the `%w` chain. The loader does **NOT** call `mintAndPersist` on the parse-fails path; the no-rewrite invariant is enforced by code structure (parse arm has no fallback into mint), not a flag a future maintainer could flip. Paired devices bind tokens to a specific server-id; silently regenerating would invalidate every pairing without operator awareness ŌĆö this is a one-way decision.
- **Error strings include the path, never file contents.** A future log site that formatted corrupt bytes into a record would create an exfiltration vector for whatever happened to be in the file (operator's `/etc/shadow` if a symlink trick worked). The bare sentinel from `ParseServerID` carries no caller bytes; the wrap adds the path and nothing else. Operators investigate via the path, not via the error log.
- **No parent-directory fsync.** Per `lessons.md` ┬¦ "Atomic on-disk writes": the rename's directory-entry update is durable enough on Linux ext4 / macOS APFS for operator-recoverable identity data. Stays consistent with `sessions.json`'s recipe.
- **No locking, no `context.Context`.** Bootstrap runs once on daemon startup before any goroutines fan out. Two pyry processes sharing HOME both observe ENOENT, both mint, both rename ŌĆö the later rename wins; this is undefined behavior at the application level (two daemons sharing HOME is itself a misconfiguration). No security property is violated; the AC explicitly says no locking required. Documented in the function doc-comment.
- **Symlink/hardlink TOCTOU surface.** Write path: `Rename(tmp, path)` replaces the directory entry ŌĆö a pre-existing symlink at `path` is unlinked; the original target is never touched (no write-through-symlink). Read path: `os.ReadFile` follows symlinks; an attacker-pre-created symlink to a readable file returns its contents, which fail `ParseServerID` and surface as `ErrInvalidServerID`. The path-only error message ensures contents do not leak via the loader's return value. Pre-existing parent-dir perms (e.g. `~/.pyry` already at `0o755` from an earlier tool) are NOT tightened by `MkdirAll(dir, 0o700)` ŌĆö install/setup tooling owns that, not the loader.
- **Package boundary: `internal/identity` keeps the loader; the package doc-comment is relaxed.** `LoadOrCreate` lives at `internal/identity/store.go` rather than a sibling `internal/identitystore`. The loader has no API surface beyond `ServerID` ŌĆö splitting forces every caller to dual-import for no abstraction win. Future identifier-loaders (e.g. `~/.pyry/devices.json` for the paired-device list) compose by adding files within `internal/identity` / `internal/devices`, not by adding packages. The "no I/O" claim was a #206-scope claim, not a permanent invariant. See [ADR 019](knowledge/decisions/019-identity-loader-co-located.md).
- **Caller resolves the absolute path.** `LoadOrCreate` takes an absolute path so tests can use `t.TempDir()`. The Phase-3 wiring ticket calls it from `cmd/pyry/main.go` against `~/.pyry/server-id` resolved alongside `resolveSocketPath` / `resolveRegistryPath`. Path resolution belongs to the daemon-startup site, not the loader (mirrors the `internal/config.Load(path)` discipline from #205).
- **Tests in `store_test.go`** ŌĆö same-package, table-driven, `t.Parallel()` everywhere, stdlib only. Five tests: `TestLoadOrCreate_FirstRunGeneratesAndPersists` (path under a non-existent subdir to verify `MkdirAll`; asserts file contents `<id>\n`, parent dir mode `0700`, file mode `0600`, second-call returns same id), `TestLoadOrCreate_ExistingFileRoundTripsWithoutRewrite` (pre-seeded canonical UUIDv4 + newline; asserts mtime unchanged via `time.Time.Equal` AND bytes byte-identical ŌĆö mtime granularity on some filesystems is 1s, bytes are the harder check), `TestLoadOrCreate_ToleratesNoTrailingNewline` (pre-seed without newline, no rewrite), `TestLoadOrCreate_CorruptFileReturnsErrInvalidServerID` (six rows: not-a-uuid, empty, uppercase, leading whitespace, CRLF, double newline; each asserts `errors.Is(err, ErrInvalidServerID)`, returned id `""`, **file bytes unchanged after the call**), `TestLoadOrCreate_ReadFileError` (make `path` itself a directory so `os.ReadFile` returns EISDIR; asserts non-nil error that is **not** `Is(ErrInvalidServerID)` ŌĆö I/O errors distinguishable from corruption). Mode assertions use `info.Mode().Perm()`.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Path resolution (caller's job ŌĆö `~/.pyry/server-id` is resolved at startup wiring). Caller wiring at daemon startup (Phase-3 ticket calls `LoadOrCreate` from `cmd/pyry/main.go`). `devices.json` persistence (sibling concern with multiple records, same atomic-write recipe). CLI surface (`pyry server-id` to print). Mode tightening for pre-existing parent dirs (install/setup tooling, not the loader). JSON round-trip (string newtype, library behavior).
- See [knowledge/features/identity-package.md](knowledge/features/identity-package.md), [knowledge/decisions/019-identity-loader-co-located.md](knowledge/decisions/019-identity-loader-co-located.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/207-server-id-store.md`](specs/architecture/207-server-id-store.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #211)
- **`internal/pair/payload.go` ŌĆö QR pairing payload `Payload` + `Encode`/`Decode`.** New leaf package, stdlib only (`bytes`, `encoding/base64`, `encoding/json`, `errors`, `fmt`, `io`) plus `internal/identity` for `ServerID`; two new files (`payload.go` ~108 LOC, `payload_test.go` ~165 LOC). Four exports: `Payload` struct (`Server identity.ServerID` + `Relay string` + `Token string`, JSON tags `server`/`relay`/`token` ŌĆö order pinned by `protocol-mobile.md`'s pairing-flow appendix lines 705-714), `Encode(p Payload) string` (`json.Marshal` ŌåÆ `base64.RawURLEncoding.EncodeToString`), `Decode(s string) (Payload, error)`, `ErrInvalidPayload` sentinel. No consumers wired in this slice ŌĆö QR rendering and paste-fallback display are sibling #212; `pyry pair` CLI glue lands later.
- **Wire format is JSON then base64url with the URL-safe alphabet and NO padding** (`base64.RawURLEncoding`, not `URLEncoding` which has padding, not `StdEncoding` which uses `+/=`). Chosen for QR alphanumeric-mode compatibility and for paste-fallback robustness in URL contexts. Round-trip is byte-stable: same `Payload` produces a byte-identical encoded string twice (JSON marshaller emits fields in struct-declaration order) ŌĆö the QR symbol scanned twice is the same QR symbol. `TestEncode_StableFieldOrder` pins this.
- **`Encode` panics on `json.Marshal` error rather than returning `(string, error)`.** `json.Marshal` of a struct whose fields are all stdlib string types with no `MarshalJSON` methods cannot fail. The AC pins the signature as `Encode(p Payload) string` (no error). Surfacing the impossible case via `panic` keeps the pure-function signature and makes the impossibility loud ŌĆö silently returning a corrupt string would let an unreachable bug ship. The defensive branch is a `panic(fmt.Errorf("pair: json.Marshal of Payload failed: %w", err))`; operators will never see it on supported platforms.
- **`Encode` does NOT validate `p`.** The encoder's contract is "marshal what you're given." Empty fields produce a string `Decode` will reject; the round-trip surfaces the error. The minter (sibling ticket) is responsible for handing in a `ServerID` produced by `identity.NewServerID`, a token from `crypto/rand`, and a relay URL from `internal/config`. `Encode` does not log, redact, persist, or transform the token; pure function.
- **`Decode` applies five rejection categories in order, returning the first failure.** (1) Base64 ŌĆö `base64.RawURLEncoding.DecodeString` is already strict (rejects characters outside the URL-safe alphabet, padding chars `=`, trailing bits not aligned to a byte; no extra check needed). (2) JSON ŌĆö `json.Decoder.Decode(&p)` against a `bytes.Reader`. (3) Trailing bytes ŌĆö a second `Decoder.Decode(&trailing)` MUST return `io.EOF`; `json.Unmarshal` silently consumes only the first JSON value, trailing bytes are lost, and the second-decode-must-be-EOF idiom catches `{"server":ŌĆ”}garbage` and `{"server":ŌĆ”}{"another":1}` (concatenated payloads ŌĆö usual symptom of a malformed paste). Same idiom `internal/control`'s JSON framing already uses. (4) Field presence ŌĆö `Server`, `Relay`, `Token` all non-empty strings; the error names the JSON tag (`server`, `relay`, `token`) ŌĆö public protocol vocabulary, not secrets. (5) Server-id shape ŌĆö `identity.ParseServerID(string(p.Server))` re-validates canonical UUIDv4 form. Package contract: `Decode` returns a `Payload` whose `Server` field is parse-validated.
- **Relay URL is NOT parsed/validated here.** Protocol contract is "the relay's domain is part of the pairing payload and trust-on-first-use from the phone's POV"; the binary doesn't dial it from this code path. Validation belongs to whichever caller actually dials. Token is NOT length- or alphabet-checked ŌĆö protocol fixes the token at "256-bit random, hex-encoded" but that's the minter's contract, not the encoding layer's. `Decode` rejects empty; that's the contract this slice owns.
- **On any error, `Decode` returns the zero `Payload`.** Matches the `config.Load` discipline ("on any error the returned Config is the zero value"). Callers that ignore `err` see empty fields and break loudly rather than working with partial data. `TestDecode_ZeroPayloadOnError` pins this for every rejection case.
- **Sentinel + wrap shape mirrors `internal/identity`'s `ErrInvalidServerID`.** `var ErrInvalidPayload = errors.New("pair: invalid payload")`; every rejection path returns `fmt.Errorf("%w: <category>", ErrInvalidPayload)`. `errors.Is(err, ErrInvalidPayload)` is the only matcher callers should use. Categories: `"invalid base64url encoding"`, `"invalid JSON"`, `"trailing data after JSON object"`, `"missing field: <name>"`, `"invalid server id"`. Bounded-length category strings; field NAMES (`server`/`relay`/`token`) are safe to include ŌĆö public protocol vocabulary; field VALUES are never echoed.
- **SECURITY: error strings never include input bytes or decoded field values.** The `Token` field carries the plaintext bearer; `protocol-mobile.md:608-609` and `:663` pin "visibility ends when the QR symbol is dismissed" / "MUST never display the device-token in plaintext after initial pairing."
