Three discipline points enforce this: (a) `Decode` errors are category strings only, no input echo ŌĆö `TestDecode_Errors` asserts the error string contains no character of the input on every row; (b) the package doc comment instructs callers to never log `Payload`, `Encode` output, or `Decode` errors in any context that may persist user-visible output; (c) `Encode` does not log, redact, or persist anything (pure function). The QR screenshot itself is the user's risk (auto-uploaded cloud backup is the documented threat); this package contributes the encoding layer that does NOT introduce a second exposure surface.
- **Why a separate `internal/pair` package** ŌĆö pairing is its own concern, owned by neither `internal/identity` (typed identifiers, no transport encoding) nor `internal/devices` (on-disk device entries + token-hash) nor `internal/config` (operator-editable settings). The name mirrors the user-visible verb (`pyry pair`); future siblings (QR/paste rendering #212, `pyry pair` CLI implementation, `pyry pair list` surface) land naturally without bloating an unrelated package.
- **Tests in `payload_test.go`** ŌĆö same-package, table-driven, `t.Parallel()` everywhere, stdlib `testing` only. Five tests: `TestEncodeDecodeRoundTrip` (AC #4 ŌĆö 100 iterations against fresh `identity.NewServerID()` ids), `TestEncode_Format` (AC #3 ŌĆö encoded string non-empty, only base64url-safe chars `[A-Za-z0-9_-]`, no `=` padding, decodes via `RawURLEncoding` to a valid JSON object ŌĆö pins wire format so future encoder swap can't pass round-trip silently), `TestEncode_StableFieldOrder` (encode-twice byte-identical), `TestDecode_Errors` (table covers empty, non-base64, non-JSON, missing-each-field, present-but-empty-each-field, invalid server-id, uppercase server-id, trailing JSON object, trailing garbage, padded base64; each row asserts `errors.Is(err, ErrInvalidPayload)` AND error string contains no character of input ŌĆö token-leakage defense), `TestDecode_ZeroPayloadOnError`. No fixtures, no `t.TempDir`, no PTY; runs under `go test -race ./...` in milliseconds.
- **Production diff: `internal/pair/payload.go` +108 LOC (new file). Test diff: `internal/pair/payload_test.go` +165 LOC (new file).** Zero new dependencies (`go.mod` unchanged), zero changes to existing code, zero new exported names outside the new package, zero CLI surface, zero wire format change.
- **Out of scope, by design.** QR rendering and paste-fallback display (sibling #212 ŌĆö this package owns the string, #212 owns the surface that displays it). `pyry pair` CLI (later phase-3 ticket ŌĆö wires `identity.NewServerID()` + token mint + `config.Load().RelayURL` into a `Payload`, calls `Encode`, hands string to #212). Token minting (later phase-3 ticket ŌĆö `crypto/rand` 256-bit + hex). On-disk persistence of paired devices (#208 owns hashing; registry-CRUD sibling loads/saves rows). Envelope versioning (a future v2 encrypted payload would land as a separate `EncodeV2`/`DecodeV2` pair or a versioned wire format). Relay URL syntax validation (owned by whichever caller dials). Token alphabet/length checks (minter owns format).
- See [knowledge/features/pair-package.md](knowledge/features/pair-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/211-pair-qr-payload-encoding.md`](specs/architecture/211-pair-qr-payload-encoding.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #208)
- **`internal/devices/device.go` ŌĆö `Device` struct + token hashing primitives.** New leaf package, stdlib only (`crypto/sha256`, `crypto/subtle`, `encoding/hex`, `time`); two new files (`device.go` ~48 LOC including doc comment, `device_test.go` ~98 LOC). Three exports: `Device` (on-disk shape with `TokenHash string`, `Name string`, `PairedAt time.Time`, `LastSeenAt time.Time`; snake_case JSON tags, no `omitempty`), `HashToken(plain) string` (lowercase SHA-256 hex via `sha256.Sum256` + `hex.EncodeToString`), `VerifyToken(plain, hash) bool` (`subtle.ConstantTimeCompare` on `HashToken(plain)` vs `hash`). No exported errors; the verify primitive returns bool by design ŌĆö auth-decision-as-error belongs to the caller. No consumers wired in this slice ŌĆö registry CRUD, token minting, and WS-handshake auth wiring are sibling tickets.
- **`subtle.ConstantTimeCompare` is the only comparison.** Returns 0 (false) when slice lengths differ, in constant time relative to the slice arguments. Empty `hash`, malformed `hash`, any-length-ŌēĀ-64 `hash` all fall out via the length-mismatch path ŌĆö there is intentionally **no early-return guard on `hash == ""`**. The unguarded shape is shorter, makes the constant-time discipline auditable in one line, and the AC bullet "false on empty/malformed hash" is satisfied by `ConstantTimeCompare`'s documented semantics. `==`, `bytes.Equal`, `strings.EqualFold` on hash material are forbidden by review.
- **No bcrypt, no per-token salt.** Recorded in the feature doc so the next reviewer doesn't relitigate it. The token is 256 bits of `crypto/rand` (sibling minting ticket); brute force across 2^256 is infeasible regardless of hash speed. The hash exists only to prevent plaintext-at-rest ŌĆö if `devices.json` leaks, the attacker holds hashes, not tokens. Bcrypt is designed for low-entropy human passwords (irrelevant at 256 bits; also caps input at 72 bytes ŌĆö a footgun for future format changes). Per-token salt defends against precomputation on shared-keyspace inputs (irrelevant for 256-bit random). Both add complexity for no defensive gain. Aligns with `protocol-mobile.md:62` ("binary stores `sha256(token)` in `devices.json`, never the plaintext") ŌĆö protocol spec already commits the binary to plain SHA-256.
- **JSON tags are snake_case, no `omitempty`, mirror `internal/sessions/registry.go:17-29`'s `registryEntry` shape.** Required fields round-trip at zero value. The sibling registry-CRUD ticket can marshal `Device` with stdlib `encoding/json` unchanged. The struct definition is in this ticket; the registry CRUD that marshals it is in a sibling ticket ŌĆö adding the tags here keeps that sibling trivial. Tags are pure addition (compiler sees them, runtime only via `encoding/json`); the AC bullet's literal field list is satisfied ŌĆö the tags are metadata, not new fields.
- **SECURITY contract is in the package doc comment**, not just review tribal knowledge. The package doc names: callers MUST NOT log a plain device-token, MUST NOT wrap a plain token into error context, MUST NOT pass a plain token across log/slog fields. The plain appears at exactly two sites ŌĆö pairing (QR + paste-fallback string) and per-WS-connect (phone presents) ŌĆö outside those, only the SHA-256 hex hash exists on disk and in memory. Neither `HashToken` nor `VerifyToken` logs anything; the package returns no error and never embeds caller input ŌĆö leaks can only originate in callers. Code review enforces this on any future caller that accepts plain.
- **Determinism is intentional.** Same plain produces the same hash across runs, machines, processes ŌĆö what makes verify trivial (compute once, compare). The cost is "two binaries with the same plain token would store identical hashes" ŌĆö irrelevant because each binary mints its own tokens for its own paired devices; tokens don't cross binaries.
- **Pure functions, no concurrency primitives.** No package-level state, no goroutines, no mutexes. Concurrent callers are safe by construction. No `*slog.Logger` parameter (neither function logs), no `context.Context` (no I/O, no cancellation point), no `Config` (SHA-256 is the chosen primitive, not a switch).
- **Tests in `device_test.go`** ŌĆö same-package, table-driven, `t.Parallel()` everywhere. `TestHashToken_Deterministic` (same input ŌåÆ same output, length 64, all lowercase hex; pins `HashToken("abc") == ba7816bf...015ad` ŌĆö published SHA-256("abc") test vector ŌĆö as a regression guard against accidental swap to SHA-1 or different encoding). `TestVerifyToken` (seven-row table covering AC's four bullets plus three malformed-hash rows): matching token (true), non-matching token (false), empty hash, too-short hash, too-long hash, non-hex `"zzz...zzz"` (proves no accidental hex-decode of either side), uppercase hex hash (documents on-disk is canonical lowercase; the package does not silently normalise ŌĆö a caller storing uppercase by mistake gets `false` and discovers the bug at first authentication). No fuzz target (input space fully covered by the table). No `-race` test (pure functions, no shared state).
- **Production diff: `internal/devices/device.go` +48 LOC (new file). Test diff: `internal/devices/device_test.go` +98 LOC (new file).** Zero new dependencies, zero changes to existing code, zero new exported names outside the new package, zero CLI surface, zero wire format change.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Token minting (sibling: `crypto/rand` 256-bit + hex encode + QR display + paste-fallback). Registry CRUD (sibling: load/save `Device` rows to `~/.pyry/<name>/devices.json` via the same atomic-rename + `0600` pattern `saveRegistryLocked` uses). Auth wiring (Phase 3: WS handshake calls `VerifyToken(presented, device.TokenHash)`; on false returns `auth.invalid_token` per `protocol-mobile.md:97-98`). `pyry pair revoke <name>` (per-device revocation falls out of removing the row; structurally supported ŌĆö each row is independent). `Device.TokenHashPrefix() string` for `pair list` UI (defer; display rule lives in `protocol-mobile.md:663`). `[]byte` overload for `HashToken` (rejected ŌĆö AC fixes signature as `string`; both call sites naturally hold strings). Memory-zeroing `plain` after hashing (Go strings are immutable; runtime exposes no "secure erase" ŌĆö rely on protocol-level discipline instead).
- See [knowledge/features/devices-package.md](knowledge/features/devices-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/208-pair-device-entry-and-token-hashing.md`](specs/architecture/208-pair-device-entry-and-token-hashing.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #206)
- **`internal/identity/server_id.go` ŌĆö typed `ServerID` + UUIDv4 generation + canonical validation.** New leaf package, stdlib only (`crypto/rand`, `errors`, `fmt`); two new files (`server_id.go` ~83 LOC, `server_id_test.go` ~94 LOC). Three exports: `ServerID` (string newtype, public routing identifier for one pyrycode-binary instance), `NewServerID() ServerID` (fresh UUIDv4 from `crypto/rand`, version + variant nibbles set, formatted canonical lowercase hex), `ParseServerID(s string) (ServerID, error)` (validates canonical UUIDv4 shape, returns `ErrInvalidServerID` on failure). One sentinel: `ErrInvalidServerID`. Empty `ServerID("")` is the unset sentinel; never a valid generated id. No consumers wired in this slice ŌĆö persistence sibling and Phase 3 pairing/relay tickets land separately.
- **Pattern mirrors `sessions/id.go` almost verbatim**, with three AC-forced divergences: (1) `NewServerID` returns `ServerID` (no error) ŌĆö `crypto/rand.Read` is documented infallible on supported platforms, so the impl panics on the impossible-on-supported-platforms branch rather than returning an error the AC's signature can't carry; silently degrading to a zero-entropy id would break the unguessability the relay-routing security model depends on. (2) `ParseServerID` returns `(ServerID, error)`, not a bool ŌĆö wraps the same validation logic as `sessions.ValidID`. (3) **No code reuse between packages** ŌĆö `internal/identity` does NOT import `internal/sessions`; the dependency direction is wrong (sessions are an implementation detail that should be free to import identity later, not the reverse), so the six-line `validUUIDv4` switch/case is duplicated intentionally.
- **`internal/identity` is a separate package from `internal/sessions`** because `sessions.ServerID` would suggest a per-session id, which is wrong (one server-id per binary instance, independent of session lifecycle). Splitting also frees `internal/identity` to grow with future identifier types (device-id, paired-device-id) without bloating sessions. The package is positioned as the home for typed identifiers that span subsystems.
- **No caller-input embedding in `ErrInvalidServerID`.** The error is returned as the bare sentinel ŌĆö no `fmt.Errorf("...%q...", s, ErrInvalidServerID)` wrap with the input string. Embedding caller-supplied bytes in the error message is a needless log-injection vector for a function that may run on relay-supplied input. Callers that need richer context wrap themselves; `errors.Is(err, ErrInvalidServerID)` is the contract.
- **`crypto/rand`-failure panics, not silently degrades.** The defensive branch is `panic(fmt.Errorf("identity: crypto/rand failed: %w", err))`. Operators will never see this on supported platforms; if they do, the alternative (returning a zero-entropy `ServerID`) is strictly worse ŌĆö silently broken unguessability vs. an immediate crash that surfaces the missing system rng.
- **Package boundary forbids `ServerID(rawString)` outside `internal/identity`.** Go's type system can't strictly prevent direct conversion in another package since `ServerID` is exported. The rule is documented in the type comment and review-enforced; `internal/` visibility contains the exposure to the pyrycode module itself, which is sufficient (no public API surface here).
- **Tests in `server_id_test.go`** ŌĆö same-package, table-driven, `t.Parallel()` everywhere. `TestNewServerID_Format` (regexp tighter than sessions/id_test.go's because `ParseServerID` enforces version + variant). `TestNewServerID_Unique` (1000-iteration uniqueness; catches a constant-zero rng wiring bug, mirrors `sessions/id_test.go`). `TestParseServerID` (table covers valid variants 8/9/a/b, empty, length 35/37, uppercase, wrong version, wrong variant, non-hex char, missing dash, dash at wrong position; negative assertions use `errors.Is(err, ErrInvalidServerID)` so the sentinel is verified reachable, not just "some error"). `TestNewServerID_RoundTripsParseServerID` is AC #4's first item directly: generate ŌåÆ parse ŌåÆ equal.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Persistence (sibling ticket ŌĆö load raw string from disk, feed to `ParseServerID`). JSON round-trip tests (`encoding/json` on a string newtype is library behavior; persistence sibling covers JSON disk format). Human label suffix in QR (per `protocol-mobile.md:61`'s "may have a human label suffix in the QR for UX" ŌĆö that's a QR-encoding concern, not an id-type concern). CLI surface (`pyry server-id` print verb ŌĆö defer). Pairing payload / relay handshake wiring ŌĆö Phase 3 follow-ups.
- **Production diff: `internal/identity/server_id.go` +83 LOC (new file). Test diff: `internal/identity/server_id_test.go` +94 LOC (new file).** Zero new dependencies, zero changes to existing code, zero new exported names outside the new package.
- See [knowledge/features/identity-package.md](knowledge/features/identity-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/206-server-id-type-and-generation.md`](specs/architecture/206-server-id-type-and-generation.md).

### Codebase (Phase 3 foundation, ticket #205)
- **`internal/config/config.go` ŌĆö typed schema + overlay loader for `~/.pyry/config.json`.** New leaf package, stdlib only (`encoding/json`, `errors`, `fmt`, `io/fs`, `os`); two new files (`config.go` ~46 LOC, `config_test.go` ~82 LOC). Three exports: `Config` struct (one field today, `RelayURL string` with `json:"relay_url"`, no `omitempty` so the field round-trips when set to its zero value), `DefaultConfig() Config` (returns `Config{RelayURL: "wss://relay.pyrycode.dev"}` ŌĆö placeholder domain, real one TBD when the relay is provisioned), and `Load(path string) (Config, error)`. No consumers wired in this slice ŌĆö daemon startup and `pyry pair` will import from their own tickets. No `Save`, no watcher, no path resolution, no URL validation, no schema versioning. Foundation for Phase 3 (mobile + relay) work.
- **Overlay-decode is the load-bearing trick.** `Load` initializes `cfg := DefaultConfig()` *before* `json.Unmarshal(data, &cfg)`. `encoding/json` only writes fields present in the document ŌĆö absent fields keep their pre-decode value. So `{}` returns `DefaultConfig()`, and `{"relay_url": "wss://my-relay.example/"}` returns defaults with only `RelayURL` overridden. Adding a Phase 3 field is then additive: append to the struct, append a default, no migration code, no schema version bump. Existing config files pick up new defaults automatically; users who pinned a value are unaffected. See [ADR 018](knowledge/decisions/018-config-overlay-decode.md).
- **Five behaviors, three error wraps.** Missing file ŌåÆ `DefaultConfig(), nil` (canonical `errors.Is(err, fs.ErrNotExist)` predicate, same one `loadRegistry` uses). Valid JSON ŌåÆ merged config + nil. `{}` ŌåÆ `DefaultConfig()` (overlay no-op). Malformed JSON ŌåÆ `Config{}, fmt.Errorf("config: parse %s: %w", path, err)`. Read errors (perms, IO) ŌåÆ `Config{}, fmt.Errorf("config: read %s: %w", path, err)`. Empty file (0 bytes) falls out as a wrapped JSON-parse error naturally ŌĆö `json.Unmarshal([]byte{}, ...)` returns `unexpected end of JSON input`. Asymmetry vs. `loadRegistry`'s empty-as-missing is deliberate: the registry is pyry-owned, the config is user-owned; an empty config file is operator error.
- **Error path returns `Config{}`, not `DefaultConfig()`.** Callers that ignore `err` see an empty `RelayURL` and break loudly rather than silently using the placeholder default. Returning defaults on error would mask real problems (e.g. a typo in `relay_url` would silently keep talking to the placeholder relay).
- **`config:` wrap prefix matches the `registry:` convention** `loadRegistry` established. Same `errors.Is`-friendly shape ŌĆö callers can branch on `fs.ErrPermission` / `fs.ErrInvalid` etc. without losing context.
- **Default lives in the function body, not a package-level `const`.** Two reasons: (1) the surface stays minimal ŌĆö one exported function, no exported constant for callers to confuse with "the current value"; (2) when more fields land, the constructor grows naturally to a multi-line struct literal, the canonical Go idiom for default-with-options.
- **Tests in `config_test.go`** ŌĆö same-package, table-driven, `t.Parallel()` on every case (no shared state ŌĆö each writes its own `t.TempDir()`). `TestDefaultConfig` pins the literal default (will fail loudly when the real relay domain lands ŌĆö that's the right signal). `TestLoad` table covers the four file-path AC bullets: missing file ŌåÆ defaults, valid full file ŌåÆ override, partial file `{}` ŌåÆ defaults preserved (regression guard for the overlay property when more fields land), malformed JSON ŌåÆ wrapped error containing `"config: parse"`. `Config` is a small comparable struct ŌåÆ direct `==` works, no `reflect.DeepEqual`. No checked-in golden files, no `testdata/` directory. Inline `ptr := func(s string) *string { return &s }` for the optional-fileBody table column over importing a generics utility.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Path resolution (`Load` takes any `path` string; the consumer ticket adds `resolveConfigPath()` alongside `resolveSocketPath` / `resolveRegistryPath` in `cmd/pyry/main.go` ŌĆö doing it here would bind to `os.UserHomeDir` semantics that some future caller with a `--config` override wants to compose differently). `Save` (read-only this slice; future ticket adds atomic-rename write primitive if/when needed). Hot reload (one-shot read at startup; if needed later, a separate seam ŌĆö most likely `sync/atomic.Pointer[Config]` swapped on file-watcher events). Schema versioning (per the ticket: "if `Config` ever grows incompatibly, version it at that point" ŌĆö `encoding/json`'s default lenient handling covers backward-additive changes for free; mirrors `registryFile.Version`'s "reserved but unused" posture). URL validation (`pyry pair` validates before connecting; the config package's contract is "decode JSON into a struct"). Permission-denied test row (hard to make portable across CI users; one-line read-error wrap is covered by inspection).
- **Production diff: `internal/config/config.go` +46 LOC (new file). Test diff: `internal/config/config_test.go` +82 LOC (new file).** Zero new dependencies (`go.mod` unchanged), zero changes to existing code, zero new exported names outside the new package, zero CLI surface.
- See [knowledge/features/config-package.md](knowledge/features/config-package.md), [knowledge/decisions/018-config-overlay-decode.md](knowledge/decisions/018-config-overlay-decode.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/205-config-load-and-schema.md`](specs/architecture/205-config-load-and-schema.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #203)
- **`install.sh` ŌĆö post-install smoke check**, ~80 LOC appended after the existing "next: see deployment.md" line. New helpers: `service_present_darwin`/`service_present_linux` (running-state detection), `restart_darwin`/`restart_linux`, `classify_status` (pure classification of captured `pyry status` output + exit code), `smoke_check` (orchestrator). New `fail_with_code` helper next to `err` for structured-exit errors (4 = restart-fail). The script's `set -euo pipefail` contract is preserved: detection helpers are called from `if`-guards (consumes the non-zero return); restart and `pyry status` are wrapped in `set +e` / `set -e` bands so their exit codes can be inspected without aborting the script.
- **Bash, not Go.** The probe runs at the install chokepoint (curl-piped + the `deployment.md`-documented "Updating the binary" command), which is `install.sh`. A Go subcommand would have added a new public CLI surface and a chicken-and-egg problem on first install (the freshly-extracted binary needs to know its service-management context). The ticket's technical-notes section asked for "Bash, grep, awk only ŌĆö no new binary dependencies"; the impl honors that. See [ADR 017](knowledge/decisions/017-install-script-smoke-check.md).
- **Detection gates on currently-running services**, not "unit file present." `launchctl print "gui/$(id -u)/dev.pyrycode.pyry" | grep -q 'state = running'` on darwin; `systemctl --user is-active --quiet pyry` on linux (preceded by a `is-system-running` D-Bus-availability check that returns false for `offline`/`unknown`/empty ŌĆö CI runners). The architect's open-question note flagged this: gating on "loaded" would auto-start a unit the operator deliberately disabled. `is-active` matches the population at risk (the update path where #202 manifested), not first-install where the operator hasn't yet run `enable --now`.
- **Four exit codes, four messages.** `0` healthy, `2` sentinel detected (the canonical #202 observable), `3` dial-fail (`pyry status` non-zero ŌĆö control socket unreachable inside its own retry+timeout window), `4` restart-fail (service manager rejected `kickstart`/`restart`). AC #4 explicitly distinguishes sentinel from dial-fail; the four-code split preserves the diagnostic for downstream automation. Each message names the symptom, the issue link (#202 for the sentinel case), and a next action (e.g. `journalctl --user -u pyry` / `tail /tmp/pyry.{out,err}.log`).
- **Sentinel match is one anchored grep**: `^Uptime: +2562047h47m16\.854775807s$` against captured stdout+stderr from `${INSTALL_DIR}/pyry status`. The `+` (not single-space) allows `runStatus`'s variable-width column padding when other keys (`Last uptime:`) are wider. We deliberately do NOT also parse `Started at: 0001-01-01T00:00:00Z` ŌĆö two checks against the same observable add zero coverage and one risks false negatives if the format drifts.
- **No manual `sleep` before the probe.** `pyry status` already retries `ENOENT`/`ECONNREFUSED` for ~1.5s via `internal/control.dialWithRetry` (#199) and times out at 5s total via `runStatus`'s context deadline. That window IS the AC's "brief grace period." Adding `sleep 5` on top would double the wall-clock cost on the healthy path.
- **Probes `${INSTALL_DIR}/pyry`, not bare `pyry`.** First-time install may not have `INSTALL_DIR` on `$PATH` yet (the existing PATH-advisory block warns about this). Calling the freshly-installed binary directly is robust.
- **`internal/install/test_smoke_classify.sh` is a bash-only unit test for `classify_status`.** Sources only the `# ---------- post-install smoke check` to `# ---------- main` band of `install.sh` (extracted via `awk`) so `main()` doesn't run, then feeds three pre-canned `pyry status` outputs and asserts return codes 0 / 2 / 3. Not wired into Go's test runner ŌĆö XS bash test for the bash classifier. Manual round-trip on each platform is the load-bearing coverage; this script is the cheap regression net for the pure rule.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Custom `-pyry-name foo` deployment detection (operator already off the default; falls through to skip with the same generic message). `--no-smoke-check` / `--dry-run` flags (no observed need; the detection branch IS the no-op path). Detection of failure classes other than the canonical `Uptime` sentinel ŌĆö broader liveness checks belong in `pyry status` itself or a separate health-check ticket. Automated `install.sh` integration tests in `internal/e2e/` ŌĆö extending those would balloon scope; manual round-trip on each platform is the agreed coverage for an XS bash change.
- **Production diff +117 LOC `install.sh` (no Go code touched), +96 LOC `internal/install/test_smoke_classify.sh` (new file), zero changes to the published binary surface, zero new dependencies.**
- See [knowledge/features/install-script.md](knowledge/features/install-script.md), [knowledge/decisions/017-install-script-smoke-check.md](knowledge/decisions/017-install-script-smoke-check.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/203-install-smoke-check.md`](specs/architecture/203-install-smoke-check.md), [ADR 016](knowledge/decisions/016-bootstrap-ignores-persisted-lifecycle-state.md) for the underlying #202 fix this probe defends.

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #202)
- **`internal/sessions/pool.go:275` ŌĆö bootstrap-only carve-out at the load layer.** Two-line production-code fix: `Pool.New`'s `pickBootstrap` arm replaces `lcState = parseLifecycleState(entry.LifecycleState)` with `lcState = stateActive` plus an explicit `_ = entry.LifecycleState` to flag the field is intentionally read-and-ignored. Doc comment names the reason verbatim ("daemon-mode startup contract is 'claude is available' ŌĆ” persisting `evicted` for the bootstrap and waking with no attach client to drive `Activate` would hang the daemon forever"). Non-bootstrap sessions still go through `parseLifecycleState` ŌĆö lazy respawn on attach is correct for them.
- **Symptom: `pyry --dangerously-skip-permissions </dev/null` hangs forever on v0.10.1** under non-TTY stdin (launchd / systemd / piped wrapper). Daemon reaches `"pyrycode starting"` and the control server (`pyry status` and `pyry stop` answer) but never logs `"spawning claude"`. `pyry status` reports `Started at: 0001-01-01T00:00:00Z` and `Uptime: 2562047h47m16.854775807s` ŌĆö `time.Duration(math.MaxInt64).String()`, the smoking-gun zero-time tell that `Supervisor.Run` was never called. `sample <pid>` shows the main goroutine parked on `pthread_cond_wait`.
- **Latent since #40 (idle eviction, v0.8.0); surfaced by #190's `pyry update` auto-restart (v0.10.1).** Sequence: cold start ŌåÆ bootstrap active ŌåÆ claude spawns ŌåÆ idle timer fires after 15min with no attach ŌåÆ `transitionTo(stateEvicted)` writes `lifecycle_state: "evicted"` to disk ŌåÆ daemon restart (`pyry update` post-replace, machine reboot, manual `launchctl kickstart`, crash-loop) ŌåÆ `Pool.New.pickBootstrap` loads `lcState = stateEvicted` ŌåÆ `Session.Run` enters `runEvicted` ŌåÆ `select { case <-ctx.Done(): ŌĆ” case <-s.activateCh: ŌĆ” }` ŌåÆ nothing ever sends on `activateCh` because `Pool.Run` only calls `p.supervise(bootstrap)` then `g.Wait()`; consumer-driven `Activate` paths (attach, `sessions.new`, `GetOrCreate`) don't fire under `</dev/null`. Pre-#190, kickstart cycles were operator-driven and rare; users typically restarted the daemon before the first idle window elapsed, so `sessions.json` still had `lifecycle_state: "active"`. #190's auto-restart is the trigger that exposed the latent bug, not the cause.
- **The fix lives at the load layer, not in `Pool.Run`.** Architect explicitly considered and rejected three alternatives: (1) `p.Activate(ctx, p.bootstrap)` after `p.supervise` in `Pool.Run` ŌĆö extra disk write at every evicted-bootstrap warm-start plus a synchronous park inside `Activate`'s wait; (2) raw send on `activateCh` from `Pool.Run` ŌĆö bypasses the `Activate` / `Evict` contract and is brittle to future refactors of the lifecycle goroutine's drain order; (3) special-case `runEvicted` to peek for the bootstrap ŌĆö conflates concerns inside the lifecycle goroutine. Load-layer carve-out keeps the state machine uniform; only the bootstrap's initial condition differs. See [ADR 016](knowledge/decisions/016-bootstrap-ignores-persisted-lifecycle-state.md).
- **AC#3 (`pyry status` shows real `Started at`, not zero-time) is satisfied structurally.** Once `lcState = stateActive` on warm-load, `Session.Run` goes straight into `runActive`, which spawns `Supervisor.Run`, which sets `State.StartedAt = time.Now()` at `supervisor.go:156`. The zero-time sentinel becomes unreachable on the supervisor-mode startup path. No changes to the `status` verb or `Supervisor.State`.
- **Disk consistency: warm-start does NOT rewrite the registry.** The on-disk `lifecycle_state: "evicted"` is left untouched per the existing "warm start is not a state change" invariant in `Pool.New`. The first state transition the running daemon makes (almost always the next idle eviction) rewrites the registry with the then-current state. Brief disk/memory disagreement during the warm-start window is harmless; in-memory state is the source of truth for a running daemon.
- **Tests in `internal/sessions/pool_test.go`** (+101 LOC). `TestPool_BootstrapEvictedOnDisk_StartsClaudeOnWarmStart` (new): pre-writes `sessions.json` with a single bootstrap entry whose `lifecycle_state` is `"evicted"` (the exact on-disk shape after one idle-eviction-then-restart cycle), runs `Pool.New` + `Pool.Run` against `/bin/sleep 3600` as the supervised child via `Bridge` mode, polls `sess.State()` for `Phase == PhaseRunning && ChildPID > 0` within a 5s deadline, asserts `StartedAt` is non-zero. Verified to fail against the pre-fix v0.10.1 binary (the supervisor never reaches `PhaseRunning` because `runEvicted` parks). `TestPool_BootstrapWarmStart_IgnoresPersistedEvicted` (renamed from `TestPool_BootstrapWarmStartsEvicted`): asserts the new contract directly via `pool.Default().LifecycleState() == stateActive`. `TestSession_ActivateBlocksUntilPersisted` (rewritten in `session_persist_test.go`): the previous "warm-start in evicted" fixture is no longer reachable for the bootstrap; the persist-blocks-wake contract is now exercised by `Evict-then-Activate` instead of `warm-start-from-evicted`.
- **Bridge mode mirrors the non-TTY supervisor path the user reproduces** (`cmd/pyry/main.go:373` ŌĆö non-TTY stdin selects supervisor mode with the bridge wired up). It also keeps the supervisor's I/O pumps off `os.Stdin` so the test doesn't contend with `go test`'s stdin.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Friendlier `pyry status` rendering for un-initialised supervisors (the technical-notes paragraph in the ticket; correctly flagged as out of scope because the fix makes the zero-time sentinel structurally unreachable on the supervisor-mode startup path). Defensive `install.sh` post-install check for the same failure mode (split out as a sibling ticket per the issue body). Auditing whether non-bootstrap sessions need similar warm-start activation logic ŌĆö they don't; non-bootstrap sessions are designed for lazy respawn on attach (Phase 1.3's whole point), and persisted `evicted` is the correct steady state for them between daemon restarts.
- **Production diff +12 LOC `internal/sessions/pool.go`. Test diff +101 LOC `pool_test.go` + 45 LOC reshape `session_persist_test.go`.** Zero new files, zero new dependencies, zero changes to the lifecycle state machine itself, zero changes to `Pool.Run`, zero changes to `Session.Run` / `runEvicted` / `runActive`.
- See [knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md ┬¦ Registry schema delta](knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md), [knowledge/decisions/016-bootstrap-ignores-persisted-lifecycle-state.md](knowledge/decisions/016-bootstrap-ignores-persisted-lifecycle-state.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/202-supervise-bootstrap-evicted-warm-start-hang.md`](specs/architecture/202-supervise-bootstrap-evicted-warm-start-hang.md), [`docs/lessons.md` ┬¦ Persisted lifecycle state needs a driver](lessons.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #199)
- **`internal/control/dial.go` ŌĆö bounded retry loop wrapping the existing `dial()` primitive.** Consumes #198's `isTransientStartupError` predicate. Production diff: `dial.go` +75 LOC (existing file, predicate already there); `client.go` -13 LOC (the old `dial()` body relocated, `net` import dropped). Test diff: `dial_test.go` +114 LOC (new `TestDialWithRetry` with three subtests against a shared `fakeDialer`). Zero behaviour change on the non-transient exit; zero server-side changes; zero new exports; zero new dependencies. Wire output for budget-exhaustion is byte-identical to pre-#199 single-shot dial ŌĆö preserved structurally via three identical `fmt.Errorf("dial %s: %w", socketPath, err)` exit-door wraps.
- **One site covers every client verb.** `pyry status`, `pyry sessions list/new/rename/rm`, `pyry attach`, `pyry attach --stdio` all route through `request()` ŌåÆ `dial()` ŌåÆ `dialWithRetry`. The two attach paths (`attach_client.go:53`, `attach_stdio_client.go:34`) don't need their own retries ŌĆö they call the same package-private `dial`. The PO ticket's "single-site wrap of the dial primitive" framing held literally.
- **`dialWithRetry(ctx, socketPath, fn dialFunc, budget, interval)` is the test-driven loop; `dial()` is a one-line wrapper passing production constants and `netDialUnix`.** Constants (`dialRetryBudget = 1500 * time.Millisecond`, `dialRetryInterval = 50 * time.Millisecond`) are package-level `const`, not `var` ŌĆö production behaviour is fixed; tests parameterise via `dialWithRetry`'s arguments rather than mutating package state. ~30 attempts fit inside the budget. Sized for the launchctl-kickstart and `pyry update` self-restart window observed 2026-05-08 during the v0.9.1 ŌåÆ v0.10.1 Mac upgrade.
- **`dialFunc` is the test seam** ŌĆö an unexported function-typed alias (`func(ctx context.Context, socketPath string) (net.Conn, error)`). Production passes the package-private `netDialUnix` (thin `net.Dialer.DialContext("unix", ŌĆ”)` wrapper, kept as a named function rather than a closure so each call avoids capturing a `net.Dialer` per invocation). Tests pass a `fakeDialer.dial` method satisfying the same shape. Same pattern as `updateOptions`'s function-typed seams (#190's `runRestart` / `probeRestart`) ŌĆö function-typed field on a callable, not a package-level var or build tag.
- **Default-deadline fallback moved into `dialWithRetry`, not `dial`.** The `if _, ok := ctx.Deadline(); !ok { ctx, cancel = context.WithTimeout(ctx, DialTimeout) }` block that used to live in `dial()` now sits at the top of `dialWithRetry` so production `dial` stays a one-liner. Caller-deadline behaviour is unchanged from pre-#199.
- **Three exit doors, all preserving the original transient error.** Non-transient: return `fmt.Errorf("dial %s: %w", socketPath, err)` immediately. Budget exhaustion (`!time.Now().Before(deadline)`): same wrap. Ctx cancel during the inter-attempt sleep: same wrap. Use `Before` with negation rather than `After` to handle the boundary tick ŌĆö at `t = deadline` exactly we exit with the wrapped transient error rather than sleeping past the budget. The three wraps are identical strings so a future grep on the wrap shape finds all three.
- **First attempt is immediate.** No pre-sleep. The fast-path "daemon is up" stays one `connect(2)` + return ŌĆö no behavioural cost when the daemon is healthy.
- **`time.NewTimer` + `Stop()` on ctx cancel**, not `time.After`. The `time.After` leak is bounded (interval = 50 ms) but harmless to fix and matches the "no leaks under cancel" discipline already in the codebase.
- **`ctx.Done()` short-circuits the inter-attempt sleep, not the dial call.** A caller-side context cancel during the sleep returns the most recent transient error wrapped (not `ctx.Err()`). During a dial attempt itself, the cancel propagates through `net.Dialer.DialContext` per the stdlib contract and surfaces as a wrapped `context.Canceled` ŌĆö *not* a transient startup error, so the next loop iteration takes the non-transient exit immediately. Two propagation paths, both correct, both preserve the wrap shape.
- **No new goroutines, no new shared state, no mutexes.** Same shape as the pre-#199 per-call dial ŌĆö synchronous loop driven by `time.NewTimer` and `ctx.Done()`. The retry is per-`dial()`-call; concurrent `pyry status` invocations each run their own loop independently. Same per-call concurrency model the rest of the control client uses.
- **Tests in `dial_test.go`** ŌĆö three subtests under one new `TestDialWithRetry` driven by a shared `fakeDialer{seq []error, calls int}` whose `dial` method counts calls and returns the next entry from `seq` (or `syscall.ENOENT` when exhausted, so an under-counting test doesn't accidentally succeed). On `nil` entries it returns `net.Pipe()`'s c1 (with c2 closed inline) ŌĆö the cheapest stdlib `net.Conn` that doesn't need a listener. Tests close the returned conn before exiting. Subtests: (1) **recovers after N transient failures** ŌĆö `seq: [ENOENT, ENOENT, ENOENT, nil]`, `budget = 200 ms`, `interval = 10 ms`, asserts non-nil conn, `f.calls == 4`, elapsed Ōēż `N*interval + 50 ms`; (2) **always-transient exhausts budget** ŌĆö empty `seq` (defaults to ENOENT), `budget = 100 ms`, `interval = 10 ms`, asserts `errors.Is(err, syscall.ENOENT)`, error string contains `"dial /fake/path:"`, elapsed Ōłł `[budget, budget + 50 ms]` ŌĆö lower bound proves retries actually ran for the full budget; (3) **non-transient error fails immediately** ŌĆö `seq: [io.EOF]` with production constants (safe since failure is immediate regardless of budget), asserts `f.calls == 1`, `errors.Is(err, io.EOF)`, elapsed Ōēż 50 ms.
- **+50 ms slack on timing assertions, documented in code comment as "for CI scheduling".** Architect's "+~5 ms" was the loop's steady-state intent, not the assertion margin ŌĆö 5 ms is too tight under loaded `-race` runs. If real flakes appear under CI's `-race` we raise to 100 ms; the slack is modest enough that "no retry" or "wrong budget" still fails.
- **No e2e in this ticket.** Driven by `dialFunc` injection; the real dial path is exercised by every existing `pyry status` / `pyry sessions list` e2e that already routes through `dial`. AC #1 ("success after `launchctl kickstart -k`") is satisfied structurally ŌĆö the wrapper covers all client verbs at one site, so a later e2e for any client verb that runs against a freshly-kickstarted daemon will exercise the retry transparently.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Server-side ready signaling (launchd has no `sd_notify` equivalent; would be platform-specific code in the daemon). A `pyry wait` UX verb (client-side retry covers more cases ŌĆö manual kickstart, `pyry update` auto-restart, `install-service`). Dispatcher-side restart-then-wait. Tuning the retry budget after observation (start with 1.5 s / 50 ms; revisit only when a real workload bumps the cap). A "context cancelled mid-loop" test case (no production surface triggers it today ŌĆö `pyry status -timeout=Xms` style doesn't exist; cancel propagation is correct by inspection of `dialWithRetry`'s body).
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Client dial: transient-startup retry (#198 + #199)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/199-dial-with-retry.md`](specs/architecture/199-dial-with-retry.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #198)
- **`internal/control/dial.go` ŌĆö `isTransientStartupError(err error) bool` predicate.** New file (~20 LOC including doc comment), one new pure unexported function. No new exported API, no callers ŌĆö the bounded retry loop that consumes this predicate lands in #199. Body is `errors.Is(err, syscall.ENOENT) || errors.Is(err, syscall.ECONNREFUSED)`. Imports are exactly `errors` + `syscall`; no `net`, `os`, `io`, no `context`, no goroutines.
- **Why `errors.Is` against the leaf `Errno`, not `errors.As(*net.OpError)`.** `errors.Is` walks the full unwrap chain ŌĆö through `client.go:282`'s `fmt.Errorf("dial %s: %w", socketPath, err)`, through `*net.OpError.Unwrap`, through `*os.PathError.Unwrap` / `*os.SyscallError.Unwrap`, matching at the leaf `syscall.Errno`. The wire-shape (`*net.OpError`) is incidental; the contract is "did the unwrap chain reach one of the two named errnos?" Resisted the urge to add `errors.As(*net.OpError)` plumbing for "shape verification" ŌĆö that pins the predicate to today's wrapping shape, which is precisely what `errors.Is` is designed to make irrelevant. `errors.Is(nil, sentinel)` returns `false` for any non-nil sentinel, so the nil case falls out for free with no guard.
- **Why the predicate is unexported.** The only intended consumer is the retry wrapper in the same `internal/control` package (#199). Exporting now would be speculative API surface ŌĆö the public verbs (`Status`, `Attach`, `SessionsList`, etc.) all route through `request` ŌåÆ `dial`; downstream packages neither call `dial` directly nor need to classify dial errors. If a future consumer materialises, lift to exported then.
- **File placement: `internal/control/dial.go`, NOT a refactor that moves the existing `dial()` from `client.go:273-285`.** The architect explicitly scoped this as predicate-only and rejected the "move dial helpers into a sibling file while we're here" cleanup as out-of-scope refactor cascade. `dial.go` will house future dial-related helpers from #199 (the retry wrapper); `dial_test.go` lives there for obvious co-location.
- **Two-errno scope ŌĆö no `io.EOF`, no timeouts, no protocol errors.** The two transient shapes the daemon-restart race produces: (a) socket file absent (`*net.OpError` Ōćó `*os.PathError{Err: ENOENT}`), (b) socket file present + no listener accepting (`*net.OpError` Ōćó `*os.SyscallError{Err: ECONNREFUSED}`, also covers a stale socket file from a crashed previous daemon). Every other dial outcome means "the daemon answered and something is wrong" ŌĆö retrying would mask real failures. The misclassification ledger: false negative = client surfaces immediately (today's no-retry behaviour, acceptable); false positive = #199 retries to its bounded budget then surfaces (slower failure, not incorrect).
- **No syscall-shape sentinel test (e.g. `*net.OpError`-pinning).** Architect's call: "don't test that `errors.Is` works (it's stdlib); don't test `*net.OpError` traversal independently (covered transitively by the live-ENOENT row)". The live-ENOENT case is the structural proof that the unwrap chain runs end-to-end against a real kernel error.
- **Tests in `internal/control/dial_test.go`** (~62 LOC, single `TestIsTransientStartupError` with six rows). True cases: (1) **real** `net.Dial("unix", filepath.Join(t.TempDir(), "missing.sock"))` against a never-created path ŌĆö pins the production-shape unwrap chain end-to-end; (2) synthetic `&net.OpError{Op: "dial", Net: "unix", Err: &os.SyscallError{Syscall: "connect", Err: syscall.ECONNREFUSED}}` ŌĆö synthetic because live construction via `Listener.Close` differs across macOS (leaves socket file) / Linux (removes socket file) and adds nothing the synthetic shape doesn't cover. False cases: (3) `nil`; (4) `io.EOF` (protocol-level, no syscall in chain); (5) synthetic `*net.OpError` wrapping `context.DeadlineExceeded` (timeout shape); (6) plain `errors.New("kaboom")` (opaque, no unwrap chain ŌĆö pins no-false-positive on bare strings).
- **Production diff +20 LOC `internal/control/dial.go` (new file). Test diff +62 LOC `internal/control/dial_test.go`** (new file). Zero changes to `client.go`, zero new dependencies, no public API surface, no wire change.
- **Out of scope, by design.** The bounded retry wrapper that consumes this predicate (sister ticket #199 ŌĆö wires the loop into the dial path with a backoff schedule appropriate for the 100msŌĆō2s daemon-restart window). Server-side ready-signaling (separate consideration). A `pyry wait` UX verb (separate decision). Live-ECONNREFUSED via short-lived listener (flaky cross-OS; synthetic case 2 is the canonical shape). Exporting the predicate (defer until a downstream consumer exists).
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Client dial: transient-startup predicate (#198)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/198-transient-startup-error-predicate.md`](specs/architecture/198-transient-startup-error-predicate.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #190)
- **`cmd/pyry/update.go` ŌĆö daemon-restart wiring on `pyry update`**, the cap on the `internal/update/restart.go` pure-decision slice (#181) that has been sitting unused since #189 landed. Production diff is +56 LOC inside the existing file (no new files): three new fields on `updateOptions` (`noRestart bool`, `probeRestart func() update.RestartProbe`, `runRestart func(ctx context.Context, argv []string) error`), one new flag on `runUpdate` (`--no-restart`), two new package-private helpers (`defaultProbeRestart` / `defaultRunRestart`), and an eight-line restart block at the end of `doUpdate`. The `==> Updated to <v>.` line moved to be terminal in the happy path so the success line is the very last thing printed (was: immediately after replace).
- **Probe lives inline in `cmd/pyry/update.go`, NOT in `internal/update`.** Boundary established at #181 reaffirmed here: `internal/update/restart.go` stays a pure function (`DetectRestartCommand(probe) ŌåÆ argv`) with no filesystem dependencies; the `os.Stat` calls on `~/Library/LaunchAgents/dev.pyrycode.pyry.plist` and `~/.config/systemd/user/pyry.service` are co-located with the subcommand handler that consumes them. `defaultProbeRestart` stats both paths regardless of `runtime.GOOS` (Linux's launchd plist won't exist anyway ŌåÆ bool false; one extra wasted stat removes a `runtime.GOOS` branch). Stat errors of any kind collapse to "not present"; if `os.UserHomeDir()` fails, both stats fail ŌåÆ `DetectRestartCommand` returns nil ŌåÆ silent skip. See [ADR 015](knowledge/decisions/015-update-restart-probe-inline.md).
- **Restart executor is an injectable function-typed seam on `updateOptions`** mirroring the existing `replace` / `executablePath` pattern. Production default `defaultRunRestart` uses `exec.CommandContext` (so a cancelled `doUpdate` propagates to a slow `launchctl kickstart`) with stdio wired to the real terminal so launchctl/systemctl diagnostics reach the user verbatim. Tests substitute a closure that records argv into a captured slice or returns a sentinel error ŌĆö no globals, no build tags, one consistent pattern across all `updateOptions` seams.
- **Probe seam separate from executor seam.** Could fold both behind one `restartIfManaged func(ctx) error`; rejected because the progress line `==> Restarting daemon (<manager>: <unit>)...` derives the manager label from the `RestartProbe` directly (rather than string-matching `argv[0]`), and keeping probe + decide + execute as three composable pieces matches the natural decomposition of the work.
- **Manager label tie-break uses the probe, not argv parsing.** `DetectRestartCommand`'s tie-breaker is "launchd wins when both are present"; the wiring reads `probe.SystemdUnitExists && !probe.LaunchdPlistExists` to switch the label to `systemd`, otherwise stays on `launchd`. The decision lives in one place (`internal/update/restart.go`) and the wiring trusts it.
- **Progress-line shape `==> Restarting daemon (launchd: gui/501/dev.pyrycode.pyry)...`** matches the issue body example exactly. The argv's last element is the unit identifier ŌĆö for launchd it's the domain target; for systemd it's `pyry` (without `.service` suffix). Acceptable as-is per the architect's open-question note.
- **`--no-restart` is a silent skip, not a warning.** Both the no-flag-but-no-unit-detected case and the `--no-restart` case print nothing about restart ŌĆö only the existing `==> Updated to <v>.` line. Matches the issue body's framing. With `--no-restart` the probe is not even called (cheap optimisation; also avoids a stat on systems where the user explicitly opted out).
- **Restart-failure error message foregrounds "binary replaced".** Wrapped as `update: binary replaced to <v>, but daemon restart failed: <inner>` so under `main()`'s `pyry: <err>` prefix the user sees `pyry: update: binary replaced to v0.9.2, but daemon restart failed: exit status 1`. The new version is on disk; the user retries the restart manually. Single line, exit 1. AC #4 satisfied.
- **`==> Updated to <v>.` is now last in the happy path.** Moved from "immediately after replace" to "after the restart step." Reads "doing the last step ŌåÆ all done" rather than "we're done ŌĆö oh, and one more thing." If the restart fails, `doUpdate` returns early and the success line never prints, which is correct: a failed restart is partial-success the user must act on.
- **Renamed daemons (`pyry install-service --name elli`) are silently skipped on update.** The probe hardcodes `dev.pyrycode.pyry.plist` / `pyry.service`. A renamed install means no managed unit detected ŌåÆ silent skip ŌåÆ user manually restarts. Known limitation, follow-up ticket if observed.
- **Tests in `cmd/pyry/update_test.go`** (+168 LOC, five new tests). `TestUpdate_RestartLaunchd` (probe `{LaunchdPlistExists: true, UID: "501"}`, asserts argv == `[launchctl kickstart -k gui/501/dev.pyrycode.pyry]` and the `(launchd: ...)` progress line), `TestUpdate_RestartSystemd` (probe `{SystemdUnitExists: true}`, asserts argv == `[systemctl --user restart pyry]` and `systemd:` label), `TestUpdate_NoRestartFlag` (`noRestart: true` plus a probe that *would* match ŌåÆ `runRestart` is `t.Fatalf` sentinel, proves flag short-circuits before probe runs), `TestUpdate_NoManagedUnit` (zero-value `RestartProbe{}` ŌåÆ success line prints, no restart progress, `runRestart` never called), `TestUpdate_RestartFailure` (`runRestart` returns `errors.New("exit status 1")` ŌåÆ asserts wrapped error contains both `binary replaced to v0.9.2` and `daemon restart failed`, and that the success line is NOT in captured output because we returned early). Updates to existing tests: `TestUpdate_Success` and `TestUpdate_PinVersion` reach the replace step and therefore execute the new restart block ŌĆö both populate `probeRestart: func() update.RestartProbe { return update.RestartProbe{} }` and `runRestart: t.Fatalf` sentinels. The other three (`AlreadyAtLatest`, `CheckOnly`, `DevBuildSkips`) short-circuit before replace and need no changes.
- **Real `defaultProbeRestart` and `defaultRunRestart` are not unit-tested.** Manual smoke test on a Mac with `pyry install-service`-installed daemon covers the production paths. Both are short and well-understood; a tempdir-based `$HOME` rig + fake `launchctl` on `$PATH` would be heavier than the duplication.
- **Production diff: `cmd/pyry/update.go` +56 LOC (existing file). Test diff: `cmd/pyry/update_test.go` +168 LOC.** Zero new dependencies, zero new files in production, zero changes to `internal/update/restart.go` or any other primitive ŌĆö the architect's "purely the wiring slice" framing held.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Renamed-daemon detection (silent skip is the documented behaviour). Real-`os.Stat` and real-`exec.CommandContext` unit tests (manual smoke test instead). Real-PTY for the executor (stdout/stderr to terminal is fine for one-shot CLI; `launchctl kickstart` and `systemctl restart` don't need a PTY). Concurrent restart (sequential, single-goroutine; `exec.CommandContext` blocks until child exits ŌĆö intentional, user wants to see the kick complete or fail before pyry's process exits). Retry on restart failure (the user retries `launchctl kickstart` / `systemctl --user restart pyry` manually if they want).
- See [knowledge/features/pyry-update-command.md ┬¦ Daemon-restart wiring (#190)](knowledge/features/pyry-update-command.md), [knowledge/decisions/015-update-restart-probe-inline.md](knowledge/decisions/015-update-restart-probe-inline.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/190-update-daemon-restart-wiring.md`](specs/architecture/190-update-daemon-restart-wiring.md), [`docs/guide.md` ┬¦ Updating pyry](guide.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #189)
- **`cmd/pyry/update.go` ŌĆö `pyry update` CLI verb wiring**, the cap on the six `internal/update` primitive slices (#179, #180, #181, #182, #186, #187). New file (~159 LOC) plus 2-line dispatch in `cmd/pyry/main.go:165` and a 3-line entry in `printHelp`. The verb-level command composes the primitives in the documented order: print current version ŌåÆ resolve target tag (latest via `Fetcher.FetchLatestRelease` + `ParseLatestRelease`, or `--version <tag>` pin) ŌåÆ `CompareVersions` short-circuit on `Same` / `ErrInvalidVersion` (dev) ŌåÆ `AssetName` + URL-template ŌåÆ `Fetcher.FetchAsset` (tarball + `checksums.txt`) ŌåÆ `ParseChecksumsFile` ŌåÆ `VerifySHA256` ŌåÆ `ExtractBinary` ŌåÆ `AtomicReplace(os.Executable(), bin, 0o755)` ŌåÆ print `==> Updated to <v>.`. Daemon restart deliberately out of scope; `DetectRestartCommand` (#181) is unused by this verb until the follow-up ticket lands.
- **`runUpdate(args []string) error` parses flags (`--check`, `--version <tag>`); `doUpdate(ctx, updateOptions) error` runs the flow.** Splitting them lets the integration tests drive `doUpdate` directly with an `updateOptions` literal (httptest server + tempdir target + capture buffer) without intercepting `flag.Parse` or `os.Stdout`. The `updateOptions` struct bundles four field-level seams the tests need: `Fetcher.BaseURL` (already a Fetcher field), `releaseBaseURL` for the tarball/checksums URL templating, `executablePath` so the test points at `tempdir/pyry` instead of `/usr/local/bin/pyry`, and `out io.Writer` for capturing progress lines. No `init()`, no global vars, no `httptest` import in production code.
- **URL-template the asset URLs (`<base>/<tag>/<asset>`, `<base>/<tag>/checksums.txt`) rather than parsing `assets[*].browser_download_url` from the release JSON.** `ParseLatestRelease` extracts `tag_name` only; expanding the parser would grow #179's surface for no value because the GitHub `releases/download/<tag>/<filename>` scheme is documented stable and matches what `.goreleaser.yaml` produces. The same `.goreleaser.yaml`-coupling caveat that already applies to `AssetName` covers this ŌĆö both values live in this repo, both move together if GitHub ever changes the scheme. Tests stub `releaseBaseURL` against `srv.URL + "/releases/download"`.
- **`Version == "dev"` short-circuits via `errors.Is(err, update.ErrInvalidVersion)` from `CompareVersions` and prints `==> Running a development build (dev); skipping update.` then returns nil.** Failing with `ErrInvalidVersion` would force every `pyry update` invocation in a development worktree to exit 1, which fights the developer's muscle memory ("I run `pyry update` to refresh"). The skip is the user-friendly path: dev builds came from `go install` or `make build`; replacing them with a release tarball would silently revert the working copy. This consumes the `ErrInvalidVersion` sentinel exactly the way #179's PROJECT-MEMORY entry forecast.
- **Homebrew hint when `os.Executable()` resolves under `/opt/homebrew/`** prints `Hint: this pyry was installed via Homebrew; consider 'brew upgrade pyry' instead.` before the rest of the flow runs. Non-blocking ŌĆö refusing would block the rare Homebrew user who knowingly wants the GitHub-release version, and a Homebrew install hits `AtomicReplace` cleanly anyway. The hint nudges the user to the right command without forcing pyry to detect-and-refuse.
- **`resolveExecutable()` falls back to `os.Args[0]` if `os.Executable()` errors** (rare; mostly `/proc` unavailability on exotic platforms). Tests bypass the wrapper by overriding `executablePath` in `updateOptions`.
- **Sequential, single-goroutine flow.** No `errgroup`, no parallel fetch of tarball+checksums (would shave ~1s on fast networks but complicates the `==> Downloading <asset>...` progress-line ordering for no observed user benefit). One `context.Background()` from `runUpdate`; tests pass `t.Context()`. Ctrl-C / SIGINT handling deferred ŌĆö swap to `signal.NotifyContext(ctx, os.Interrupt)` if the need arises. The Fetcher already honours context cancellation per #182's AC.
- **HTTP timeout is 60s via `&http.Client{Timeout: 60 * time.Second}`** baked into the Fetcher in `runUpdate`. Generous for a ~20 MiB tarball on a slow connection but bounded enough that a hung `pyry update` doesn't sit forever. `--http-timeout` flag is YAGNI ŌĆö users can re-run.
- **`fmt.Fprintf` to `out`, not `slog`.** This is a one-shot CLI verb, not a daemon. Output is human-facing progress lines on stdout, not structured-logging events. `runInstallService` already uses `fmt.Printf` for the same reason ŌĆö the convention is preserved.
- **Errors propagate as `update: <step>: %w` and are printed by `main()`'s wrapper as `pyry: update: <step>: <inner>` to stderr** (exit 1). Each step contributes its own context prefix: `update: fetch latest release: ŌĆ”`, `update: parse latest release: ŌĆ”`, `update: download tarball: ŌĆ”`, `update: download checksums: ŌĆ”`, `update: parse checksums: ŌĆ”`, `update: verify checksum: ŌĆ”`, `update: extract binary: ŌĆ”`, `update: replace binary: ŌĆ”`. On checksum mismatch the verify-line prints `FAIL` before the wrapped error surfaces. No retry, no fallback ŌĆö a checksum miss after a clean download is either GitHub serving a corrupt asset or a hostile MITM, and silently retrying masks both.
- **Tests in `cmd/pyry/update_test.go`** (~292 LOC, five integration tests). `TestUpdate_Success` (AC #2 happy path: on-disk binary swapped at `tempdir/pyry`, all six progress lines print verbatim including `==> Updated to v0.9.2.`), `TestUpdate_AlreadyAtLatest` (current==latest short-circuit; injects a `replace` that `t.Fatal`s if called), `TestUpdate_CheckOnly` (AC #3: `--check` prints versions and exits without downloading; injects a `replace` that fails if called), `TestUpdate_PinVersion` (AC #3: `--version <v>` skips the latest-release API call ŌĆö the fake handler 500s if hit ŌĆö and downloads from the pinned URL), `TestUpdate_DevBuildSkips` (`currentVersion == "dev"` exits 0 with "skipping update", `replace` not called). Each test stands up its own `httptest.NewServer` with three handlers (`/repos/.../releases/latest`, `/releases/download/<tag>/<asset>`, `/releases/download/<tag>/checksums.txt`); helpers `buildTarGzForTest` + `fakeRelease` + `newFakeReleaseServer` are inline in the test file, not shared with `internal/update/install_test.go` (the duplication is ~10 lines; an `internal/testutil` package would be heavier).
- **Production diff: `cmd/pyry/update.go` +159 LOC (new file). `cmd/pyry/main.go` +2 LOC dispatch + 3 LOC `printHelp`. `docs/guide.md` +1 paragraph "Updating pyry" section.** Test diff: `cmd/pyry/update_test.go` +292 LOC (new file).
- **Out of scope for #189, by design.** Daemon restart (the explicit follow-up ticket ŌĆö `DetectRestartCommand` from #181 sits unused until then; the user manually `launchctl kickstart -k gui/$(id -u)/dev.pyrycode.pyry` (macOS) or `systemctl --user restart pyry` (Linux), documented in the guide). `--no-restart` flag (lands with the restart follow-up). Rollback / `.bak` of the old binary (deferred entirely; `AtomicReplace`'s crash-safety covers in-progress writes, but undoing a *successful* update is a separate feature ŌĆö where to store the old binary, how to garbage-collect, how the user invokes it). Scheduled auto-update / channel selection (deferred; only the `latest` GitHub release is consulted, pre-release tags ignored). Ctrl-C / SIGINT handling. Retry on transient network failure (Fetcher's AC forbids it). Exposing the asset list via `pyry update --list`.
- See [knowledge/features/pyry-update-command.md](knowledge/features/pyry-update-command.md), [knowledge/features/update-package.md](knowledge/features/update-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/189-update-subcommand-wiring.md`](specs/architecture/189-update-subcommand-wiring.md), [`docs/guide.md` ┬¦ Updating pyry](guide.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #187)
- **`internal/update/replace.go` ŌĆö fourth slice of `pyry update`, the atomic in-place binary replacement primitive.** New file (~64 LOC) in the existing `internal/update` package, alongside #179's `version.go`, #180's `checksum.go`, and #181's `restart.go`. Stdlib-only (`fmt`, `os`, `path/filepath`); first member of the package to perform I/O. The wiring ticket calls this *after* extracting the new pyry binary from the downloaded tarball (#186) and *before* running the `DetectRestartCommand` argv (#181) to kick the daemon. Sister tickets #186 (in-memory tar extraction ŌåÆ produces the `[]byte` input) and #182 (HTTP fetcher) are still in flight; this slice's file-level non-overlap with both lets it land in any order.
- **`AtomicReplace(targetPath string, newData []byte, mode os.FileMode) error`.** Standard POSIX safe-overwrite dance: `os.CreateTemp(filepath.Dir(targetPath), "."+base+".*.tmp")` so the temp file lands in the same directory as the target (eventual `os.Rename` never crosses a mount point ŌĆö `rename(2)` returns `EXDEV` and degrades to copy-then-unlink across filesystems, not atomic), then **write ŌåÆ fchmod ŌåÆ fsync ŌåÆ close ŌåÆ rename**. SIGKILL anywhere before the rename leaves `targetPath` byte-identical to its pre-call state; SIGKILL after, the new bytes are durable. On Linux a target currently mmap'd for execution is handled cleanly: the rename unlinks the old inode while leaving its open-for-execution refcount intact, so running pyry processes keep their old binary mapped and the on-disk path now points to the new one.
- **Order is `write ŌåÆ fchmod ŌåÆ fsync ŌåÆ close ŌåÆ rename`, not `write ŌåÆ fsync ŌåÆ fchmod ŌåÆ ŌĆ”`.** Chmod-then-fsync ensures the mode change is durably persisted along with the contents in the same fsync; the reverse would leave the mode change un-fsynced ŌĆö a needless durability gap. `f.Chmod` (fchmod on the open fd) over `os.Chmod(path, ŌĆ”)` avoids a TOCTOU between create and chmod (`os.CreateTemp` opens at 0o600; the requested mode is applied via the open fd before any other process could swap the file underneath us).
- **Each f-method failure closes the file before returning** rather than relying on a single `defer f.Close()`. Ordering with respect to the cleanup `defer` is then unambiguous ŌĆö the `os.Remove(tmp)` in the cleanup defer always runs after the explicit close. A `renamed` bool gates the cleanup `defer`: after `os.Rename` succeeds, `tmp` no longer names a file; calling `os.Remove(tmp)` would either fail with `ENOENT` (harmless) or, in a freak race, remove an unrelated file some other process subsequently created at the same temp name. The flag closes that gate cheaply.
- **Temp-file naming `"."+base+".*.tmp"` (e.g. `.pyry.123456789.tmp`).** Leading dot keeps stragglers (which only appear in failure modes) hidden from `ls`; embedding `base` makes accidental collisions during concurrent updates structurally impossible and gives ops a hint about origin if one ever does leak. `os.CreateTemp` substitutes a random suffix for `*` (no caller-side counter, no race).
- **Mirrors `internal/sessions/registry.go`'s `saveRegistryLocked` pattern** (the in-tree precedent for atomic file writes) with two deliberate differences: raw bytes instead of a JSON encoder; **no `os.MkdirAll`** on the parent. The wiring ticket guarantees the install directory already exists (it's where `pyry` is currently running from); creating it here would mask a configuration bug in the caller. The "parent missing" error path is tested explicitly to pin this contract.
- **Caller MUST pass a path whose parent directory exists and is writable.** Doc comment names the same-filesystem caveat verbatim because the `CreateTemp(filepath.Dir(targetPath), ŌĆ”)` choice is what makes the rename atomic; a future refactor that "helpfully" moves the temp file to `os.TempDir()` or `~/tmp` would silently break atomicity across the install-dir / `/tmp` mount-point boundary common on Linux.
- **No sentinel errors.** None of the AC's error cases need `errors.Is`-style branching; the wiring ticket will log-and-fail uniformly. `CreateTemp`'s wrapped `*PathError` already lets a future caller introspect with `errors.Is(err, fs.ErrNotExist)` if they ever need to. Adding sentinels speculatively would violate "Don't add ... for scenarios that can't happen".
- **Concurrency.** Reentrant in the formal sense (no package-level state) but two concurrent calls *with the same `targetPath`* race at the rename step: temp names are unique random suffixes from `CreateTemp` (no collision there), but whichever rename runs last wins on `targetPath` and the loser's bytes are silently overwritten. No corruption; lost update only. The `pyry update` flow is single-goroutine in the wiring ticket, so we don't defend against this; the doc comment doesn't promise anything about concurrent calls. No `context.Context` parameter ŌĆö a single sub-megabyte buffered write isn't meaningfully cancellable, and the wiring ticket can wrap the whole update with its own ctx.
- **Out of scope, by design.** **Parent-directory fsync after the rename.** The crash-durable-rename pattern includes `open(dir, O_RDONLY) + fsync + close` after the rename so the directory entry survives a power loss between rename and the next dirent flush. `saveRegistryLocked` omits it; we omit it; both rest on "process interrupt (signal/SIGKILL)" being the threat model rather than "power loss". If/when a `pyry update` user reports a missing binary after a power outage, revisit. **`os.MkdirAll` on the parent** (configuration-bug exposure, see above). **Backup/rollback of the old binary** as a `.bak` artifact ŌĆö wiring layer's call (it can `AtomicReplace` to `.bak` first if it wants belt-and-suspenders rollback). **Linux `renameat2(RENAME_NOREPLACE)` for the new-file case** (single-goroutine update flow; not in threat model). **`io.Reader` variant** ŌĆö today's binary is ~12 MiB and #186 already produces `[]byte`; streaming would force #186 to expose a reader instead, not worth the contract change.
- **Tests in `internal/update/replace_test.go`** (~90 LOC, four targeted subtests using `t.TempDir()` exclusively). `TestAtomicReplace_CreatesNewFile` (target absent), `_OverwritesExistingFile` (target seeded with `0o644` "OLD" ŌåÆ overwrites with `0o755` "NEW"), `_PreservesMode` (request `0o755`, assert `os.Stat().Mode().Perm() == 0o755`), `_ParentDirMissing` (path inside a non-existent subdir ŌåÆ assert error AND `os.ReadDir` of the surrounding tempdir is empty ŌĆö the "no stray `.pyry.*.tmp` stragglers on the error path" pin). Targeted subtests over a single table because the error case has different setup; mirrors `checksum_test.go`'s style (`t.Parallel()` per subtest, inline assertions, no helpers, no `testdata/`).
- **No umask test.** Asking for `0o755` and asserting `0o755` is robust under any sane umask (`0o022`, `0o002`, `0o077` all preserve the requested 0o755 ŌĆö wait, `0o077` would mask group/other and produce `0o700`). To stay deterministic across CI environments we'd need `syscall.Umask(0)` + restore in `t.Cleanup`; the AC doesn't demand it and CI runs default umask, so deferred to implementer judgment per the spec. If a maintainer ever runs CI with `0o077` and sees this test fail spuriously, harden then.
- **Production diff +64 LOC `internal/update/replace.go` (new file in existing package). Test diff +90 LOC `internal/update/replace_test.go`** (new file). Zero new callers (#187 is the replace primitive only); CLI surface unchanged.
- See [knowledge/features/update-package.md ┬¦ Atomic in-place replace](knowledge/features/update-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/187-update-atomic-replace.md`](specs/architecture/187-update-atomic-replace.md), [`internal/sessions/registry.go`](../internal/sessions/registry.go) for the in-tree precedent, [`lessons.md ┬¦ Atomic on-disk writes`](lessons.md) for the canonical write-temp + fsync + rename rules.

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #182)
- **`internal/update/fetch.go` ŌĆö HTTP fetcher slice of `pyry update`.** Stdlib-only `net/http` wrapper exposing one struct (`Fetcher`) and two methods (`FetchLatestRelease(ctx, repo)` + `FetchAsset(ctx, url)`). Sits alongside #179's `version.go` and #180's `checksum.go` in the same `internal/update` package; no package doc comment (lives on `version.go`). The wiring ticket composes it with the pure functions: `Fetcher.FetchLatestRelease` ŌåÆ `ParseLatestRelease` ŌåÆ `CompareVersions` + `AssetName` ŌåÆ `Fetcher.FetchAsset(checksums.txt)` ŌåÆ `ParseChecksumsFile` ŌåÆ `Fetcher.FetchAsset(tarball)` ŌåÆ `VerifySHA256` ŌåÆ `ExtractBinary` ŌåÆ next ticket's atomic-replace.
- **`Fetcher` is a struct with zero-value-usable defaults** (vs a `New(opts) *Fetcher` constructor). Three independently-optional fields: `BaseURL` (default `"https://api.github.com"`), `HTTPClient` (default `http.DefaultClient`), `UserAgent` (default `"pyry/dev"`; the wiring ticket sets `"pyry/" + main.Version`). Same shape as `http.Client` itself. Defaults resolved per-call inside the methods via private helpers (`baseURL` / `httpClient` / `userAgent`) so a caller mutating package-level `http.DefaultClient` after `Fetcher{}` construction is supported. Tests need to override `BaseURL` and `HTTPClient` ŌĆö direct field assignment is the readable form. No invariants between fields require a constructor.
- **Two methods over one** because the latest-release endpoint needs URL templating (`<BaseURL>/repos/<repo>/releases/latest`) and asset fetches do not (caller passes a fully-formed URL extracted from the release JSON, e.g. `assets[].browser_download_url`). The fetcher cannot template asset URLs ŌĆö it doesn't know the GoReleaser asset-name conventions and shouldn't. Implementation core (`get` helper: build request ŌåÆ set User-Agent ŌåÆ Do ŌåÆ status check ŌåÆ drain-on-non-2xx ŌåÆ ReadAll) is shared and unexported. `*Fetcher` receivers (not value) so a shared `Fetcher{}` can't be accidentally copied with all-zero fields.
- **`http.NewRequestWithContext` (not `http.NewRequest`).** Propagates `ctx` to the transport so cancellation interrupts an in-flight read, not just a queued send. This is what makes `errors.Is(err, context.Canceled)` fire mid-transfer rather than only at request-construction time. `*url.Error.Unwrap` participates in the unwrap chain transparently ŌĆö no special handling in the fetcher.
- **Non-2xx error contract: `fmt.Errorf("GET %s: unexpected status %d", url, resp.StatusCode)`** ŌĆö bare `Errorf`, no `%w`, because there's no inner error to wrap. The AC's "wrapped error containing status code and URL" is satisfied by this single line. **No new exported sentinel.** The wiring ticket cannot retry (forbidden) and therefore cannot branch on transient-vs-permanent ŌĆö a typed sentinel would be unused. If a future caller needs typed branching, add `ErrUnexpectedStatus` then; defer until observed (Pipeline Principle: Evidence-Based Fix Selection).
- **Drain-then-discard up to 1 KiB on non-2xx** via `io.Copy(io.Discard, io.LimitReader(resp.Body, 1<<10))`. Lets the underlying TCP connection back into the pool; the bound caps reading megabytes of error HTML from a misconfigured server. Errors from the drain are ignored ŌĆö we already have a status to report. Transport-hygiene optimisation, not correctness; documented in `net/http`.
- **No retries, no caller-imposed timeouts.** Stdlib only. Caller passes `&http.Client{Timeout: 60*time.Second}` if it wants a budget. GitHub's API blanket-rejects no-User-Agent requests, which is why the header is unconditionally set rather than optional. The `pyry/<Version>` shape (vs `pyry/v<Version>`) matches the binary's self-report so log correlation stays grep-friendly.
- **`io.ReadAll` on the response body is acceptable** despite tarballs being 10ŌĆō30 MiB ŌĆö the wiring ticket holds the bytes in memory anyway to compute SHA-256 (`VerifySHA256(data []byte, ŌĆ”)`) and feed tar extraction. Streaming would force the wiring layer to either tee or hash twice. Revisit only if profiling shows pressure.
- **Concurrency: stateless across calls, safe for concurrent use.** All fields are read-only after construction; `*http.Client.Do` is concurrency-safe; each call constructs a fresh `*http.Request`. No goroutines, no mutexes, no internal channels in the fetcher itself.
- **Tests in `internal/update/fetch_test.go` (~158 LOC).** Six tests, all `t.Parallel()`, each with its own `httptest.NewServer` + `t.Cleanup(ts.Close)`. `TestFetcher_FetchLatestRelease_OK` (path + User-Agent inbound, body verbatim), `_FetchAsset_OK` (16 bytes binary fixture), `_DefaultUserAgent` (zero-value default `"pyry/dev"`), `_NonOKStatus` (table over 404/500/503; substring assert on status code AND `ts.URL` in error message ŌĆö the one place substring-match is the right shape per the AC), `_ContextCancelled` (handler blocks until either `release` channel closes or `r.Context().Done()`; `time.AfterFunc(50ms, cancel)` triggers cancellation; assert `errors.Is(err, context.Canceled)`), `_FetchLatestRelease_RepoSlugInPath` (URL templating shape with `owner/different-name`).
- **Production diff +115 LOC `internal/update/fetch.go` (new file in existing package). Test diff +158 LOC `internal/update/fetch_test.go`** (new file). Zero new callers (#182 is fetcher only); CLI surface unchanged. Stdlib-only ŌĆö no new dependencies.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Parsing JSON / checksums.txt (#179, #180 ŌĆö already merged). Verifying SHA-256 (#180). Tar extraction (#186 ŌĆö already landed). Atomic on-disk replace. `pyry update` CLI verb wiring. Retries / exponential backoff (AC explicitly forbids). Caller-side timeouts (caller's responsibility via `*http.Client`). `If-None-Match` / ETag-based caching (anonymous 60/hr limit fine for interactive use). `Fetcherer` / `Mockable` interface (tests use `httptest.NewServer` directly; the wiring ticket may add a 2-method consumer-defined interface there if needed). Exposing GitHub 4xx body content in errors (URL is in the message ŌĆö operators can `curl` it; revisit if real failures generate complaints).
- See [knowledge/features/update-package.md](knowledge/features/update-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/182-update-http-fetcher.md`](specs/architecture/182-update-http-fetcher.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #186)
- **`internal/update/install.go` ŌĆö fourth pure-function slice of `pyry update`.** New file (~63 LOC) in the existing `internal/update` package, alongside #179's `version.go`, #180's `checksum.go`, and #181's `restart.go`. Stdlib-only (`archive/tar`, `bytes`, `compress/gzip`, `errors`, `fmt`, `io`, `path/filepath`); no I/O, no goroutines, no `context.Context`. The wiring ticket consumes this between `VerifySHA256` and the still-pending atomic on-disk replace step.
- **`ExtractBinary(tgzData []byte, binaryName string) ([]byte, error)` reads a gzipped tar archive entirely from memory and returns the bytes of the regular-file entry whose tar header `Name` (under `filepath.Base`) matches `binaryName`.** Memory-only: no temp files, no streaming-to-disk. The function is a pure (input-bytes ŌåÆ output-bytes) transform; callers who need the binary on disk apply the future atomic-replace function to the returned bytes.
- **`filepath.Base(hdr.Name)` matching, not exact-`hdr.Name` equality.** GoReleaser lays files at the archive root (`pyry`, `LICENSE`, `README.md`) but docs and unit templates carry directory prefixes (`docs/INSTALL.md`, `systemd/pyry.service`). `filepath.Base` matching is robust against a future GoReleaser change that wraps everything in a top-level `pyry_v0.9.1/` directory (a common archives layout) without requiring `ExtractBinary` to change. The cost is that a hypothetical archive with a `subdir/pyry` entry would also match ŌĆö accepted because GoReleaser does not produce such archives, and a stricter exact-`hdr.Name` check would force this slice to be revisited the moment GoReleaser's layout changes.
- **Skips non-regular entries (`hdr.Typeflag != tar.TypeReg`).** `tar.TypeReg` is the only file type GoReleaser emits. Skipping `TypeDir`, `TypeSymlink`, `TypeLink`, etc. defends against a quirky archive that names its top-level directory `pyry/` (which would otherwise be returned as a zero-length "binary"). Cheap check, silent-and-weird failure mode without it. Returns the first matching regular-file entry ŌĆö a duplicate-name archive is malformed and there is no documented preference.
- **No size cap (`io.LimitReader`), no streaming variant.** Release tarballs are ~10ŌĆō20 MiB. The wiring ticket already holds `tgzData` in memory for checksum verification (HTTP GET body fully buffered), so streaming in this layer wins nothing. A defensive cap is **not** added ŌĆö evidence-based-fix call: no malicious archive observed, the operator's update flow is bounded by HTTP content-length and `tgzData`'s in-memory size, and the wiring ticket checksum-verifies before extraction (forecloses the attacker-controlled-tarball path entirely). Revisit only if pyry ever ships a 1 GiB binary.
- **Two new exported sentinel errors for `errors.Is` branching.** `ErrBinaryNotInArchive` (iterated to `io.EOF` without finding a regular-file entry matching `binaryName`) and `ErrMalformedArchive` (gzip-open failure or any `tar.Next` / `io.ReadAll` error). Both wrapped with context at the return site (`fmt.Errorf("opening gzip stream: %w", ErrMalformedArchive)`, `fmt.Errorf("reading tar header: %w", ErrMalformedArchive)`, `fmt.Errorf("looking up %q: %w", binaryName, ErrBinaryNotInArchive)`, `fmt.Errorf("reading %q from tar: %w", binaryName, ErrMalformedArchive)`). No error path returns the sentinel bare ŌĆö matches `checksum.go`'s convention.
- **Tests in `internal/update/install_test.go`** (~120 LOC, single `t.Parallel` table mirroring `checksum_test.go` shape). Five rows: `binary_present_returned_unchanged` (asserts `bytes.Equal` on the pyry bytes; the fixture also contains `LICENSE` plus a directory-prefixed `docs/INSTALL.md` to demonstrate the `filepath.Base` matcher), `binary_missing` (`ErrBinaryNotInArchive`), `garbage_not_gzip` (plain text, fails at `gzip.NewReader`; `ErrMalformedArchive`), `valid_gzip_garbage_tar` (gzip wrapper around non-tar payload ŌĆö forces the code path past `gzip.NewReader` so `tar.Next`'s error path is exercised, distinguishing it from the previous case; `ErrMalformedArchive`), `empty_input` (`ErrMalformedArchive`). Two helpers: `buildTarGz(t, map[string][]byte) []byte` constructs an inline tarball via `bytes.Buffer` ŌåÆ `gzip.NewWriter` ŌåÆ `tar.NewWriter`; `gzipOf(t, []byte) []byte` is a one-liner for the gzip-only fixture. No `testdata/` ŌĆö suite is hermetic.
- **Production diff +63 LOC `internal/update/install.go` (new file in existing package). Test diff +119 LOC `internal/update/install_test.go`** (new file). Zero new callers (#186 is extraction-only); CLI surface unchanged.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Atomic on-disk replacement (the wiring ticket lands `os.CreateTemp` + `os.Rename` in `install.go` alongside `ExtractBinary` and consumes its `[]byte` output).
