HTTP fetcher (sister ticket). Checksum verification (#180, already landed). Restart detection (#181, already landed). `pyry update` CLI verb wiring + `--dry-run` flag (wiring ticket). A streaming-extraction variant (`io.Reader` input or pipe-out output) ŌĆö defer until tarball size demands it. A defensive size cap on `io.ReadAll(tr)` ŌĆö defer pending evidence.
- See [knowledge/features/update-package.md](knowledge/features/update-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/186-update-extract-binary.md`](specs/architecture/186-update-extract-binary.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #181)
- **`internal/update/restart.go` ŌĆö third pure-function slice of `pyry update`.** New file (~37 LOC) in the existing `internal/update` package, alongside #179's `version.go` and #180's `checksum.go`. Stdlib-only; no I/O, no goroutines, no `context.Context`, no errors. The wiring ticket calls this after the binary has been swapped to kick the running daemon.
- **`RestartProbe` struct.** Three fields: `LaunchdPlistExists bool` (does `~/Library/LaunchAgents/dev.pyrycode.pyry.plist` exist?), `SystemdUnitExists bool` (does `~/.config/systemd/user/pyry.service` exist?), `UID string` (numeric uid as string, templated into the launchctl `gui/<uid>/dev.pyrycode.pyry` domain). Struct rather than three positional bools so the call site labels each signal and survives signal additions in future tickets (e.g. SMF on illumos, Windows service entry) without breaking existing callers.
- **`DetectRestartCommand(probe RestartProbe) []string` returns the argv (program plus args) of the restart command, or `nil` when no managed daemon is detected.** Two-branch switch, launchd checked first so the tie-breaker falls out naturally: `launchctl kickstart -k gui/<uid>/dev.pyrycode.pyry` (launchd) or `systemctl --user restart pyry` (systemd). The `nil` return is the foreground / unknown case ŌĆö caller prints "restart your pyry yourself" guidance; not an error because foreground users running `pyry` from a terminal are a supported deployment.
- **Tie-breaker: launchd wins when both probes return true.** Rationale (verbatim in doc comment per AC): macOS is pyrycode's primary daily-driver platform, so a stray systemd user unit on a Mac (e.g. left over from a dotfiles sync) is more likely cruft than the active manager. The reverse case ŌĆö a launchd plist on Linux ŌĆö cannot occur because `launchctl` does not exist on Linux; the probe will return false. No `runtime.GOOS` filter inside `DetectRestartCommand`: the probe **is** the OS filter, and filtering by GOOS would re-introduce non-purity (tests would need to set GOOS) and forbid the legitimate "wrong-OS file lying around" case from being deterministic.
- **Why `kickstart -k` over `unload`/`load`.** `kickstart -k` SIGTERMs the running instance and starts a fresh one in a single command. `unload`/`load` would round-trip the plist and race with `KeepAlive=true`. The `-k` flag is the canonical way to tell launchd "restart this label now" per `man launchctl`.
- **Why `systemctl --user restart` over `try-restart` or `reload`.** `restart` is unconditional and matches the user's intent (the binary changed; restart it). `try-restart` would silently no-op if the unit is inactive; `reload` requires `ExecReload=` which the unit file doesn't define.
- **Tests in `internal/update/restart_test.go`** (~48 LOC, single `t.Parallel` table mirroring `checksum_test.go` shape). Four rows from the AC: `launchd_only` (`UID: "501"` ŌåÆ `gui/501/dev.pyrycode.pyry`), `systemd_only` (no UID needed), `both_present_launchd_wins` (`UID: "1000"` so the hard-coded `"501"` from the first row would fail this case ŌĆö UID-templating verification falls naturally out of the differing UIDs), `neither_present` (`nil`). Compares with `slices.Equal` (Go 1.21+, idiomatic for `[]string`); `nil` and `[]string{}` are equal under it but the implementation returns `nil` matching the AC.
- **Production diff +37 LOC `internal/update/restart.go` (new file in existing package). Test diff +48 LOC `internal/update/restart_test.go`** (new file). Zero new callers (#181 is restart-detect only); CLI surface unchanged.
- **Out of scope, by design.** The probe half (the wiring ticket performs `os.Stat` on the launchd plist + systemd unit file paths and `os.Getuid()`, then calls `DetectRestartCommand` with the results). Actually running the restart argv (`exec.Command`) and watching for restart success. HTTP fetcher, tar extraction, atomic binary replacement (sister tickets). `pyry update` CLI verb wiring + `--dry-run` flag (wiring ticket).
- See [knowledge/features/update-package.md](knowledge/features/update-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/181-update-restart-detect.md`](specs/architecture/181-update-restart-detect.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #180)
- **`internal/update/checksum.go` ŌĆö second pure-function slice of `pyry update`.** Three new exported functions plus four new sentinel errors, all stdlib-only (`crypto/sha256`, `encoding/hex`, `errors`, `fmt`, `strings`); no I/O, no goroutines, no `context.Context`. Sits alongside #179's `version.go` in the same `internal/update` package ŌĆö package doc comment on `version.go` already forward-stated this ticket, so `checksum.go` adds none. The wiring ticket consumes #179 + #180 together (`ParseLatestRelease` ŌåÆ `CompareVersions` ŌåÆ `AssetName` ŌåÆ fetch ŌåÆ `ParseChecksumsFile` ŌåÆ fetch tarball ŌåÆ `VerifySHA256` ŌåÆ next ticket's untar + atomic-replace).
- **`AssetName(version, goos, goarch string) (string, error)`** mirrors `.goreleaser.yaml`'s `archives.name_template` verbatim. Returns `pyry_<X.Y.Z>_<Darwin|Linux>_<arm64|x86_64>.tar.gz`; strips a leading `v` via `TrimPrefix` (no-op when absent). Two package-level lookup tables: `osTitles = {"linux":"Linux","darwin":"Darwin"}`, `archNames = {"amd64":"x86_64","arm64":"arm64"}`. Any other os/arch combo wraps `ErrUnsupportedPlatform` ŌĆö both unsupported-OS and unsupported-arch use the same sentinel; the error message names the inputs (`"asset name for windows/amd64: ŌĆ”"`) so logs are unambiguous, but `errors.Is(err, ErrUnsupportedPlatform)` is the single branch. Does **not** validate that `version` parses as semver ŌĆö that's `CompareVersions`'s job upstream; double-validating would create two error contracts to keep in sync. Empty `version` is permitted (produces `pyry__Darwin_arm64.tar.gz`), since the wiring ticket guarantees `version` has already passed `CompareVersions`; a stray empty would surface as a 404 from the HTTP fetcher.
- **`ParseChecksumsFile(text, assetName string) (string, error)`** parses GoReleaser-produced `checksums.txt` (one line per asset: `<sha256-hex>  <filename>`, two spaces, matching `sha256sum` output). Returns the lowercase hex digest for the matching asset. `strings.SplitN(line, "  ", 2)` so future filenames containing single spaces survive; per-line `TrimRight(line, "\r")` defensively handles CRLF. Lines that don't split into exactly two non-empty parts are skipped silently ŌĆö forward-compatible with future header comments or trailing blanks. The `sawAny` flag distinguishes "checksums.txt was junk" (`ErrMalformedChecksums` ŌĆö upstream broken) from "checksums.txt was a valid file but didn't list our asset" (`ErrAssetNotInChecksums` ŌĆö built without our platform, unrecoverable for this host). Different sentinels because they imply different upstream actions. Per-line digest length / hex-ness is **not** validated ŌĆö `VerifySHA256` will catch any mangling, and a regex check would couple two layers without observed benefit.
- **`VerifySHA256(data []byte, expectedHex string) error`** computes `sha256.Sum256(data)`, hex-encodes via `hex.EncodeToString(sum[:])`, compares with `strings.EqualFold` (so a future caller passing mixed-case `expectedHex` works ŌĆö `ParseChecksumsFile` already lowercases). Mismatch error message normalises both digests to lowercase so logs are consistent regardless of input casing: `"expected %s, got %s: %w"`. Takes `[]byte` rather than `io.Reader` because the wiring ticket already needs the full tarball in memory for tar extraction (release tarballs are <10 MiB); switching to streaming would force the wiring ticket to either tee the body or hash twice. Revisit only if tarball size ever demands it.
- **Four new exported sentinel errors for `errors.Is` branching.** `ErrUnsupportedPlatform` (any os/arch combo not in `.goreleaser.yaml`'s build matrix), `ErrAssetNotInChecksums` (asset not listed in checksums body ŌĆö built without our platform), `ErrMalformedChecksums` (empty input or no parseable lines at all ŌĆö upstream broken), `ErrChecksumMismatch` (digest mismatch). All wrapped with context at the return site (`fmt.Errorf("looking up %q: %w", assetName, ErrAssetNotInChecksums)`, etc.).
- **`AssetName` returning `""` and `ParseChecksumsFile` returning `""` on error are conventional** ŌĆö callers must check the error first; the value is meaningless when err != nil. Same bias as `CompareVersions` returning `Same` on error: a misuse silently routes through "no match" rather than a wrong match.
- **GoReleaser-template coupling is intentionally fragile.** The `osTitles` / `archNames` maps and the `pyry_<v>_<OS>_<arch>.tar.gz` skeleton duplicate `.goreleaser.yaml:24-46`. We own both files in the same repo; `pyry update` only ever reads releases produced by this repo's own `release.yml` workflow ŌĆö no upstream-consumer compatibility concern. If `.goreleaser.yaml` changes, `checksum.go` changes. No CI drift-check today; deferred follow-up could run `goreleaser release --snapshot` and grep filenames against `AssetName`'s output.
- **Tests in `internal/update/checksum_test.go`** (~219 LOC, three `t.Parallel` tables). 9 `TestAssetName` rows (all four supported os/arch combos, leading-`v` no-op, four unsupported combos: `windows/amd64`, `freebsd/amd64`, `linux/386`, `linux/riscv64`). 8 `TestParseChecksumsFile` rows (asset present first/last, asset missing, empty input, whitespace-only, no parseable lines, CRLF normalised, uppercase-hex normalised, garbage-then-valid). 6 `TestVerifySHA256` rows (empty-data correct hash `e3b0c442ŌĆ”b855`, nonempty correct, mismatch, mismatch-message-includes-both-digests substring assertion, case-insensitive match, empty `expectedHex` rejects). All sentinel-error rows assert via `errors.Is(err, sentinel)`. `t.Parallel()` at outer + subtest level (no shared state ŌĆö package-level maps are read-only post-init).
- **Production diff +102 LOC `internal/update/checksum.go` (new file in existing package). Test diff +219 LOC `internal/update/checksum_test.go`** (new file). Zero new callers (#180 is asset-name + checksum-parser + verifier only); CLI surface unchanged.
- **Out of scope, by design.** HTTP fetcher (sister ticket ŌĆö GET `releases/latest`, GET `<release>/checksums.txt`, GET `<release>/<assetName>`, retries, timeouts, takes `context.Context`). Tar extraction (separate ticket). Atomic binary replacement / restart detection (separate ticket). `pyry update` CLI verb wiring (wiring ticket). A `MapHostPlatform()` helper wrapping `runtime.GOOS`/`runtime.GOARCH` (the wiring ticket can pass the raw runtime constants ŌĆö adding a host-detection helper before the wiring ticket exists is YAGNI). Streaming-hash variant of `VerifySHA256` (defer until tarball size demands it). CI drift-check between `AssetName` and `.goreleaser.yaml` (deferred follow-up).
- See [knowledge/features/update-package.md](knowledge/features/update-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/180-update-checksum.md`](specs/architecture/180-update-checksum.md).

### Codebase (Phase ?, ticket #179)
- **`internal/update` ŌĆö pure-function half of `pyry update`.** First slice of self-update wiring: `ParseLatestRelease(jsonBytes []byte) (string, error)` extracts `tag_name` from a GitHub Releases API JSON payload; `CompareVersions(current, latest string) (Comparison, error)` returns `Older`/`Same`/`Newer`. Stdlib-only (`encoding/json`, `strconv`, `strings`); no I/O, no goroutines, no `context.Context`. Safe for concurrent use by definition. Sister tickets land the HTTP fetcher, checksum verification, and binary replacer; the wiring ticket adds the `pyry update` CLI verb and consumes both functions.
- **`Comparison` is `int`-typed `-1`/`0`/`1`** mirroring `cmp.Compare` / `strings.Compare`. No `String()` method (YAGNI per architect's spec; add when a caller needs `slog`-friendly formatting).
- **Two exported sentinel errors for `errors.Is` branching.** `ErrMalformedRelease` (invalid JSON, non-object top-level, missing/empty/non-string `tag_name`) and `ErrInvalidVersion` (non-semver input, including the `main.Version == "dev"` sentinel). Both wrapped with context at the return site (`fmt.Errorf("decoding release JSON: %w", ErrMalformedRelease)`). On error, `CompareVersions` returns `Same` rather than `Older`/`Newer` ŌĆö the safer bias when a caller forgets to check the error: silently reports "no update needed" rather than spurious downgrade.
- **Tag preserved verbatim by the parser; comparator does the stripping.** `ParseLatestRelease` returns whatever string GitHub put in `tag_name` (leading `v`, whitespace, pre-release suffixes flow through unchanged). `CompareVersions` strips a leading `v` via `TrimPrefix` (no-op when absent ŌĆö handles `"v0.9.1"` and `"0.9.1"` symmetrically) and strips pre-release / build-metadata suffixes at the first `-` or `+` before the dot split. Deliberate simplification: pyry's tags are plain `major.minor.patch` and the comparator does not implement SemVer 2.0.0 pre-release precedence ŌĆö `v0.10.0-rc1 == v0.10.0` after suffix strip. Document in the doc comment so reviewers see the deferred behaviour; revisit only when pyry actually publishes a pre-release operators must distinguish.
- **Default `encoding/json` decoder, NOT `DisallowUnknownFields`.** GitHub's payload has dozens of fields we don't read; strict decoding would convert "GitHub adds a field" into a load failure. Same convention as `sessions.json` (`lessons.md ┬¦ Atomic on-disk writes`). Whitespace in `tag_name` is **not** trimmed ŌĆö that's GitHub's own value, never operator-typed; trimming would mask a real upstream bug.
- **`"dev"` is documented as out-of-band.** `cmd/pyry/main.go:53`'s `var Version = "dev"` produces `ErrInvalidVersion` when passed through `CompareVersions`; the wiring ticket will branch on this with `errors.Is(err, ErrInvalidVersion)` and print "running a dev build, skipping update check" or similar. Empty-string, too-few-components (`v0.9`), too-many (`v0.9.1.2`), non-numeric components, empty components (`v0..1`), and negative components (`v-1.0.0`) all reject identically. Negatives are explicitly rejected via post-`Atoi` `< 0` check (Atoi *will* parse `-1`); leading zeros (`v01.02.03`) are accepted ŌĆö SemVer 2.0.0 forbids them, we don't care because GitHub never produces them.
- **Tests** in `internal/update/version_test.go` (~155 LOC, two `t.Parallel` tables). 13 `TestParseLatestRelease` rows cover the happy path + every reject branch (malformed/truncated JSON, non-object top level, missing/empty/null/wrong-type `tag_name`, empty input, extra fields tolerated, `v` prefix preserved verbatim, prerelease tag preserved verbatim). 20 `TestCompareVersions` rows cover all three results across major/minor/patch boundaries (numeric not lexical: `v0.10.0 > v0.9.99`), `v` prefix tolerance on either side or both, prerelease + build-metadata suffix stripping, and every reject branch. Both error tables assert via `errors.Is(err, sentinel)`. `t.Parallel()` at outer + subtest level (no shared state).
- **Production diff +127 LOC `internal/update/version.go` (new package + new file). Test diff +155 LOC `internal/update/version_test.go`.** Zero new callers (#179 is parser + comparator only); CLI surface unchanged.
- **Out of scope, by design.** HTTP fetcher (sister ticket ŌĆö GET `releases/latest`, retries, timeouts, takes `context.Context`). Checksum verification of the downloaded binary (separate ticket). Atomic binary replacement / restart detection (separate ticket). `pyry update` CLI verb wiring + `--dry-run` flag (wiring ticket). `Comparison.String()` (defer until `slog` consumer needs it). SemVer 2.0.0 pre-release precedence (defer until pyry ships a real pre-release).
- See [knowledge/features/update-package.md](knowledge/features/update-package.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/179-update-version-parsing.md`](specs/architecture/179-update-version-parsing.md).

### Codebase (0.x polish, ticket #177)
- **`pyry install-service` defaults `WorkingDirectory` to the install-time cwd, with `--workdir` (now `~`-expanding) as the explicit override.** Replaces the previous hardcoded `~/pyry-workspace` (launchd) / `%h/pyry-workspace` (systemd). Surfaced 2026-05-08 setting up the Mac Claudian daemon: running install-service from the Obsidian vault root wrote a plist pointing at `~/pyry-workspace`, which doesn't exist on the Mac; `launchctl load` reported success but the daemon's `chdir` failed (exit 78) and the socket was never bound. Cwd default matches `pyry start`'s mental model ("set up the daemon HERE") and removes the silent-pre-create footnote.
- **New exported helper `install.ResolveWorkDir(flag, cwd, homeDir) (string, error)`.** Sole resolver: empty flag ŌåÆ cwd; `~` / `~/sub` ŌåÆ expand against `homeDir`; absolute path ŌåÆ `filepath.Clean`; relative path ŌåÆ `filepath.Abs` (resolves against the test process's cwd). Always returns an absolute path. The CLI is the only caller; the previous `Options.WorkDir == ""` default branch in `install.Install` is removed ŌĆö passing an empty `WorkDir` to `Install` now leaves the unit's `WorkingDirectory` blank (programming error). Tests that previously relied on the implicit default now pass an explicit value.
- **CLI prints `WorkingDirectory: <resolved-path>` before any file I/O, above the existing "Inherited PATH" block.** Surfaces the effective value to the user even if `install.Install` errors. If the resolved directory does not exist on disk (`errors.Is(err, fs.ErrNotExist)` on `os.Stat`), prints `warning: <path> does not exist; create it with: mkdir -p <path>` and continues ŌĆö does NOT abort. Other Stat errors (EACCES, etc.) are silently ignored: the daemon's own runtime error will be clearer than a guess at install time.
- **Symlinks in cwd are baked verbatim.** `os.Getwd()` returns whatever the kernel reports, which may include or exclude symlinks depending on how the shell got there. Users who want the canonical path pass `--workdir "$(pwd -P)"` explicitly.
- **Out of scope.** Migrating already-installed `~/pyry-workspace`-pointing plists / unit files (separate PR or manual edit). Auto-creating the WorkingDirectory if missing (warning is enough; users may want specific perms). Multi-instance installer (`--name claudian` for a second pyry alongside the default). Foreground-mode (`pyry start`) cwd handling ŌĆö already uses cwd, no change.
- **Production diff ~24 LOC `cmd/pyry/main.go` + ~38 LOC `internal/install/install.go`. Test diff +93 LOC `internal/install/install_test.go`** (`TestResolveWorkDir` table + `TestInstall_Systemd_CwdWorkDir` + `TestInstall_Launchd_CwdWorkDir`; existing `TestInstall_Systemd_BareTemplate` / `TestInstall_Launchd_BareTemplate` updated to pass explicit `WorkDir`).
- See [`docs/specs/architecture/177-install-service-cwd-workdir.md`](specs/architecture/177-install-service-cwd-workdir.md), [`docs/deployment.md`](deployment.md) (flag table + macOS section).

### Codebase (Phase 0)
- **Supervisor core** ŌĆö PTY spawn via `creack/pty`, raw-mode stdin/stdout bridging in foreground mode, Bridge-mediated I/O in service mode, exponential backoff restart with stability reset, `--continue` injection on restart for session persistence
- **SIGWINCH forwarding** ŌĆö terminal resizes propagate from controlling terminal to child PTY in foreground mode (`internal/supervisor/winsize.go`) and in service mode via the live-resize loop landed across #136 (`Bridge.Resize` seam) + #137 (`VerbResize` wire + server applier) + #133 (client-side `startWinsizeWatcher` in `pyry attach`)
- **Control plane** ŌĆö Unix domain socket (`~/.pyry/<name>.sock`, 0600), line-delimited JSON protocol, verbs: `status`, `stop`, `logs`, `attach`
- **CLI transparency** ŌĆö unknown args forward verbatim to claude; pyry's own flags use `-pyry-*` prefix; `-pyry-name` plus `PYRY_NAME` env var for named multi-instance
- **Graceful shutdown** ŌĆö SIGINT/SIGTERM cancel the supervisor context, child is killed via `exec.CommandContext`, socket removed on exit
- **Service configs** ŌĆö systemd user unit (`systemd/pyry.service`), macOS launchd plist (`launchd/dev.pyrycode.pyry.plist`)
- **~1700 source + ~1100 test Go lines** as of late Apr 2026, 10+ PRs merged

### Codebase (Phase 1.3c-2, ticket #158)
- **Foreground `pyry --session-id <uuid>` auto-attaches to a daemon-hosted session via stdio when the daemon hosts that UUID.** Closes the "point Claudian at pyry" loop: setting Claudian's "claude binary path" UI to `~/.local/bin/pyry` now Just Works against a running daemon, without a wrapper script and without socket-name management. The auto-attach branch is byte-identical on the wire to `pyry attach --stdio <uuid>` ŌĆö same `control.AttachStdio` call, same `os.Stdin`/`os.Stdout` wiring, same `createIfMissing=false` (existence already proved via has-id), same `context.Background()`, no human-affordance stderr lines.
- **Two private helpers in `cmd/pyry/main.go`: `extractSessionID(claudeArgs)` + `tryAutoAttach(socketPath, claudeArgs)`.** No new exported surface, no new packages, no wire changes. `extractSessionID` peeks `claudeArgs` (already split out by `splitArgs` ŌĆö `--session-id` is unambiguously a claude flag) for the four shapes claude itself accepts: `--session-id <v>`, `--session-id=<v>`, `-session-id <v>`, `-session-id=<v>`. First match wins; last-arg-without-value returns `""`; UUID validation is the daemon's job. `tryAutoAttach` is the foreground gate, called from `runSupervisor` after `socketPath` is resolved and before any supervisor-mode side effect (logger, ring buffer, Bridge, Pool init).
- **Conservative posture ŌĆö every probe failure mode falls through.** Returns `(false, nil)` for: `PYRY_NO_AUTO_ATTACH=1` in the env (strict equality with `"1"`, matches `GODEBUG`/`GOTRACEBACK` convention); no `--session-id` in claudeArgs; `os.Stat(socket)` returns ENOENT or any other error (EACCES, EPERM, ŌĆ”); dial timeout / unresponsive daemon (1s probe ctx); `SessionsHasID` returns `(_, err)` for any reason; `SessionsHasID` returns `(false, nil)`. Returns `(true, err)` only when has-id said yes ŌĆö `err` is the `AttachStdio` result (nil for clean EOF detach, transport / handshake error otherwise). Existing pyry users (no daemon, or no `--session-id`) see no behavioural change.
- **AC#3 (<50ms in the no-daemon case) satisfied structurally.** `os.Stat`'s ENOENT branch returns before any dial / context allocation / goroutine. Real numbers are sub-millisecond; the 50ms ceiling is the AC contract, not the steady-state expectation. Pinned by `TestTryAutoAttach_SocketAbsent_FastPath` and `TestTryAutoAttach_NoSessionID` (both wall-clock-bounded).
- **`PYRY_NO_AUTO_ATTACH=1` escape hatch.** First check inside `tryAutoAttach`, before `extractSessionID`, before any syscall. Strict-`"1"` semantics (env=`"true"` still probes ŌĆö pinned by `TestTryAutoAttach_EnvOptOutNonOne`). Used by the e2e tests in #163/#164 that need to assert "supervised spawn fired" without first having to confirm the daemon is down, and as a debug knob for operators pinning a regression to the supervised path. No flag ŌĆö env var only, matches `PYRY_NAME` precedent.
- **Reuses the existing daemon-name resolution chain (`-pyry-name` flag ŌåÆ `PYRY_NAME` env ŌåÆ `DefaultName`) verbatim.** AC's "use the same resolution chain" is load-bearing for "point Claudian at pyry" with `PYRY_NAME` set ŌĆö a multi-instance setup where the operator runs separate daemons per project should auto-attach against the right one. `resolveSocketPath` is called once in `runSupervisor`; both auto-attach and supervised-spawn branches consume its result.
- **Why splice in `runSupervisor`, not `run()`.** `run()`'s top-level verb-switch dispatches on a closed set (`version`, `status`, `stop`, `logs`, `attach`, `sessions`, `install-service`, `help`, `-v`, `--version`, `-h`, `--help`); none can ever be `--session-id`. Splicing inside `runSupervisor` reuses the existing `splitArgs` + `resolveSocketPath` parse for free; splicing in `run()` would force a duplicate flag parse for socket resolution.
- **Concurrency: strictly sequential probe.** stat ŌåÆ dial ŌåÆ encode ŌåÆ decode ŌåÆ branch. No new goroutines beyond what `AttachStdio` already spawns internally (one output-copy goroutine, joined before return ŌĆö see #154's spec). No new lock-order edges. Signal handling is unchanged: when we fall through, the existing `signal.NotifyContext(SIGINT, SIGTERM)` setup applies; when we attach, kernel delivers the signal to pyry's pid ŌåÆ `io.Copy` returns ŌåÆ `AttachStdio` propagates ŌåÆ `runSupervisor` returns ŌåÆ `main` wraps and exits.
- **Tests in `cmd/pyry/auto_attach_test.go` (~230 LOC).** `TestExtractSessionID` (table ŌĆö 12 rows: all four flag shapes, absent, no-args, last-arg-no-value, empty-value, empty-glued-value, value-with-dashes, first-match-wins, embedded-in-args). `TestTryAutoAttach_*` exercises every fall-through arm: no-session-id (wall-clock budget pin), env opt-out under `=1`, env opt-out non-`1` value still probes, socket absent fast path (50ms budget), daemon unresponsive (listen but never accept; returns within 1.5s via the 1s probe ctx), has-id false, has-id invalid (server returns `Response.Error`). Stub server is a tiny in-test Unix-socket accept loop that decodes one Request and writes back a canned Response ŌĆö no full server harness, no `internal/control` test helper extraction (the architect's preferred shape per the design doc). The attach-commit branch (has-id true ŌåÆ `AttachStdio` runs) is intentionally **not** unit-tested; e2e is split into siblings #163 (happy path) and #164 (fallback scenarios).
- **Production diff ~75 LOC in `cmd/pyry/main.go`** (~20 for `extractSessionID` + ~50 for `tryAutoAttach` + ~5 for the splice block). Test diff ~230 LOC (`cmd/pyry/auto_attach_test.go` new).
- **Out of scope, by design.** WS / remote attach (Phase 3 + 5 ŌĆö auto-attach is local-Unix-socket only). Multi-daemon-name discovery (always single resolved name via the existing chain). A `--no-auto-attach` flag on pyry itself (env var covers the bypass case). E2E tests of the full auto-attach flow (#163 happy path, #164 fallback). Logging from the auto-attach path (foreground binary has no logger configured at the splice point; `PYRY_VERBOSE=1` could opt-in via a future ticket if a real operator asks). Telemetry counter for "auto-attach fired" ŌĆö not on any observability surface today.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Foreground binary auto-attach (1.3c-2)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/158-foreground-auto-attach.md`](specs/architecture/158-foreground-auto-attach.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.3c-2-e2e-happy, ticket #163)
- **`internal/e2e/auto_attach.go` + `auto_attach_happy_test.go` ŌĆö e2e proof that `pyry --session-id <uuid>` (no `attach` verb) auto-attaches to a daemon-hosted session.** Sibling to #161's `StdioAttachClient`, mirrors the surface (`Write` / `ReadUntil` / `Close`). Test `TestE2E_ForegroundAutoAttach_AttachesWhenDaemonHasSession` writes a nonce-tagged line into the foreground pyry's stdin pipe, asserts the same line round-trips back through control socket ŌåÆ bridge ŌåÆ supervisor PTY ŌåÆ echo helper ŌåÆ foreground stdout pipe within 5s, **then** asserts the foreground pyry has zero direct children via `pgrep -P <pid>`. The pgrep assertion is the orthogonal check ŌĆö a bug that wired auto-attach correctly *and* spawned a competing supervisor would still echo bytes (the daemon's helper returns them regardless of the foreground pid's children).
- **Argv shape is the *foreground binary* invocation, not `pyry attach --stdio`.** `pyry -pyry-socket=<sock> -- --session-id <uuid> --input-format stream-json --output-format stream-json` ŌĆö no `attach` verb. `os.Args[1]` is `-pyry-socket=ŌĆ”`, doesn't match any verb in `run()`'s switch, so `runSupervisor(os.Args[1:])` runs and `tryAutoAttach` fires. The `--input-format`/`--output-format` flags are functionally inert (auto-attach short-circuits before any claude binary is consulted) but mirror Claudian's invocation literal so the test pins intent. The `--` separator is defensive ŌĆö `splitArgs` already tips into claudeArgs at the first non-pyry flag, but `--` is forward-compatible if pyry ever adds a flag whose name overlaps.
- **#167 doesn't reach this code path.** `tryAutoAttach` calls `control.AttachStdio` *directly* from inside `runSupervisor` ŌĆö no verb dispatch, no `parseClientFlags`, no `parseAttachArgs`. The `pyry attach --stdio` CLI bug (#167) blocks #161's `TestE2E_AttachStdio_BytesRoundTrip` but not this test. Confirmed against `cmd/pyry/main.go:304` (the in-process `control.AttachStdio` call).
- **`pgrepChildren(pid) ([]int, error)` is the test-side process-tree primitive ŌĆö also reused by sibling #164.** `pgrep -P <pid>` is one syscall and one parse, identical surface on linux + darwin (no GOOS branch needed). Exit 1 with empty stdout means "no children" ŌåÆ returns `(nil, nil)` (success path for #163; failure path for #164's fallback tests). `exec.LookPath("pgrep")` failure ŌåÆ returns an error the caller turns into `t.Skip` (matches the precedent in `openPTYDeviceTargetsDarwin` for `lsof`). Kept in `auto_attach.go` rather than `harness.go` ŌĆö co-location with the feature follows the `attach_pty.go` / `attach_stdio.go` precedent, and the architect's spec marks the "add to `harness.go` once" hint as non-binding.
- **`spawnAutoAttachDaemon` is a slim variant of `spawnAttachableDaemon`, not a verbatim reuse.** Reason: `Pool.Create` appends `--session-id <uuid>` to the supervised claude's argv on every non-bootstrap session (`internal/sessions/pool.go:852`). The Go test binary's `flag.Parse()` rejects `-session-id` and exits 2 before `TestHelperProcess` runs ŌĆö `SessionsNew` produces a dead session that can't echo bytes. Workaround: a `<home>/echo-claude.sh` shell wrapper that ignores its argv and `exec`s the test binary with fixed args (`-test.run=TestHelperProcess`), mirroring `cap_test.go`'s `writeSleepClaude` pattern. Helper-mode env vars (`GO_TEST_HELPER_PROCESS`, `GO_TEST_HELPER_MODE`) and `E2E_HELPER_BIN` are preserved across the shell exec. The existing `#161` stdio harness has the same latent bug (its skipped test will fail the same way once #167 lands and the skip lifts) ŌĆö left untouched here per scope discipline; resolve in #167's ticket or a follow-up.
- **`safeBuffer` (mutex-wrapped `bytes.Buffer`) for the foreground pyry's `Stderr` field.** `cmd.Stderr = &bytes.Buffer{}` races with test-goroutine reads of `.String()` because os/exec's stderr-copy goroutine writes the buffer concurrently. The race is real on `-race` even when the buffer is empty in steady state. `StdioAttachClient.Stderr` has the same latent race but is only exercised through a `t.Skip`'d test today ŌĆö not refactored here per scope discipline. Two methods: `Write` (forwards under lock), `String` (snapshot under lock).
- **Test diff ~365 LOC across 2 new files** (`auto_attach.go` ~290, `auto_attach_happy_test.go` ~50). Production diff is zero. Default `go test -race ./...` unaffected; `go test -tags e2e -race ./internal/e2e/` clean.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Foreground binary auto-attach (1.3c-2)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/163-e2e-foreground-auto-attach-happy.md`](specs/architecture/163-e2e-foreground-auto-attach-happy.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.3c-2-e2e-fallback, ticket #164)
- **`internal/e2e/auto_attach_fallback_test.go` + helpers in `auto_attach.go` ŌĆö three e2e tests pinning `tryAutoAttach`'s fall-through arms.** Sibling to #163's happy-path test, inverse direction. `TestE2E_ForegroundAutoAttach_FallsThroughWhenSessionMissing` (daemon up, UUID not registered), `_FallsThroughWhenNoDaemon` (no daemon, no socket), `_RespectsEnvOverride` (daemon up, UUID registered, `PYRY_NO_AUTO_ATTACH=1` in foreground env). Each asserts `pgrepChildren(c.Pid) Ōēź 1` (supervised claude child exists, the inverse of #163's zero-children assertion); the daemon-running tests also snapshot `control.SessionsList` before/after the foreground run and assert byte-equivalent equality (`time.Time.Equal` for `LastActive` to absorb the JSON-roundtrip monotonic-clock strip).
- **All three tests fall through via the same gate (`os.Stat(socketPath) ŌåÆ ENOENT`) by design.** The forced architectural choice: after fall-through, `runSupervisor` runs `ctrl.Listen()` on `socketPath` *before* `pool.Run` spawns the supervised child. If the foreground binary shared the daemon's socket (so its `tryAutoAttach` probe really hit `SessionsHasID == false` for test #1, or skipped a probe that *would* have succeeded for test #3), `Listen` would return `bind: address already in use` and the foreground would exit before any claude child appeared ŌĆö the pgrep-Ōēź1 assertion couldn't fire. So the foreground gets its **own** socket path, distinct from any daemon's; its socket doesn't exist before its own `Listen` runs, so `tryAutoAttach`'s `os.Stat` returns ENOENT and `tryAutoAttach` falls through. The test environment differentiates (daemon present / env var set / UUID registered) but the gate exercised is always ENOENT. Adding a foreground-only `-pyry-no-listen` flag (or splitting probe-bind paths) to exercise the real `has-id-false` gate at e2e is out of scope for #164 ŌĆö gate-discrimination is the unit-tier contract (six tests in `cmd/pyry/auto_attach_test.go` shipped with #158: `TestTryAutoAttach_NoSessionID`, `_EnvOptOut`, `_SocketAbsent_FastPath`, `_DaemonUnresponsive`, `_HasIDFalse`, `_HasIDInvalid`); e2e pins the orthogonal contract that fall-through, however triggered, lands the foreground in supervisor mode with a real claude child.
- **New helpers in `auto_attach.go` (additive, +199 LOC).** `ForegroundSupervisedClient` is the simpler inverse-direction sibling of `ForegroundAutoAttachClient` ŌĆö no bidirectional pipes (`cmd.Stdin = /dev/null`, `cmd.Stdout = io.Discard`), only `Pid` (for `pgrepChildren`) + `Stderr` (`safeBuffer`, expected non-empty in steady state because supervisor mode emits slog lines) + `SocketPath`/`HomeDir` (diagnostics). `startForegroundSupervised(t, sessionID, extraEnv)` argv: `pyry -pyry-socket=<own-sock> -pyry-claude=<sleep-claude> -pyry-idle-timeout=0 -pyry-resume=false -- --session-id <uuid>`. Two-phase readiness ŌĆö 500ms settle window (early-death detector mirroring `startForegroundAutoAttach`) + `awaitClaudeChild(pid, 5s)` polling `pgrepChildren` every 50ms (closes the race where pgrep outruns the supervisor's first `os.StartProcess` inside `Pool.Run`). `spawnDaemonWithRegisteredSession(t, label) (socket, sessionID)` wraps `spawnAutoAttachDaemon` + `waitDaemonReady` + `control.SessionsNew` for the "daemon present" tests, returning the registered id so tests can confirm the registry-unchanged invariant. Skip-on-`pgrep`-unavailability up front (sandboxed CI). Inline test helpers `mustSessionsList` / `sessionsEqual` / `newCanonicalUUID` (~25 LOC) live in the test file rather than a shared file ŌĆö three tests of byte-similar duplication, no ongoing churn.
- **Sleep-claude over echo-claude for the supervised stand-in.** Reuses `writeSleepClaude` from `cap_test.go` (#116) ŌĆö `#!/bin/sh\nexec sleep 99999\n` ignores the `--session-id <uuid>` that `Pool.Create` appends. The happy-path test (#163) needed echo-claude because it round-trips bytes; the fallback tests don't, and `sleep` is the simpler stand-in. Both wrappers exist for the same `Pool.Create`-appends-`--session-id` reason ŌĆö see `lessons.md`.
- **`extraEnv` parameter is the env-override surface.** `extraEnv` is appended verbatim to `childEnv(home)` before exec, so test #3 injects `PYRY_NO_AUTO_ATTACH=1` into the foreground process's env without polluting any daemon's env. `nil` for tests #1 and #2.
- **Stale-socket-file scenario (AC bullet #2 marks optional) deliberately skipped.** `TestTryAutoAttach_DaemonUnresponsive` already pins the "socket file present, dial fails" gate at unit tier; arranging the e2e fixture (manually create a socket file with no listener, hope `os.Stat` succeeds and `net.Dial` fails) would add complexity for a path the unit test already pins.
- **Cleanup ordering ŌĆö LIFO via `t.Cleanup`.** Foreground tears down first (close stdin sink ŌåÆ `killSpawned` foreground ŌåÆ `os.Remove(c.SocketPath)`); SIGTERM to the foreground reaps the supervised sleep-claude child via the foreground's process group ownership through `exec.CommandContext` semantics inside the supervisor. Daemon teardown follows on tests #1 and #3.
- **Production diff is zero.** Test diff +342 LOC across 2 files: `auto_attach.go` (+199 additive) + `auto_attach_fallback_test.go` (+143 new). Default `go test ./...` unaffected; `go test -tags e2e -race ./internal/e2e/...` clean.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Sharing a socket between daemon and foreground (would conflict on bind ŌĆö see "separate sockets"). Discriminating gate decisions at e2e (unit-tier contract). Stale-socket-file scenario (unit-tested as `TestTryAutoAttach_DaemonUnresponsive`). Latency / perf assertions (#158's unit test pins the structural fast-path). `PYRY_NO_AUTO_ATTACH` non-`1` values (unit-tested as `TestTryAutoAttach_EnvOptOutNonOne`). Asserting on the foreground's stderr being empty (supervisor mode emits slog lines ŌĆö non-empty stderr is expected, surfaced only in failure diagnostics).
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ Foreground Auto-Attach Fallback Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/164-e2e-foreground-auto-attach-fallback.md`](specs/architecture/164-e2e-foreground-auto-attach-fallback.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.3c-1, ticket #157)
- **`VerbSessionsHasID` + `SessionsHasIDResult` in `internal/control` ŌĆö wire-only addition for one-bit UUID-existence queries.** Fifth `sessions.*` namespace member after `new`/`rm`/`rename`/`list`. New verb `"sessions.has-id"` reuses the existing `SessionsPayload.ID` field (introduced by #98 for `sessions.rm`, reused by #90 for `sessions.rename`) for "the session this verb operates on" ŌĆö no new `SessionsPayload` field. Cheap focused alternative to `sessions.list` for the single-id case the 1.3c-2 foreground auto-attach path needs (~36-byte input + ~30-byte output instead of an O(N) registry table). The verb body is a pure registry read ŌĆö no claude spawn, no state transition.
- **No new Sessioner sub-interface ŌĆö handler reaches through the existing `SessionResolver.Lookup` seam.** Departure from the `Remover`/`Renamer`/`Lister`/`GetOrCreator` pattern of "one named sub-interface per verb embedded in `Sessioner`." For has-id, the registry-read primitive is **already** reachable via `SessionResolver.Lookup`'s `(*Session, ErrSessionNotFound)` contract: a known id returns `(*Session, nil)`, an unknown id returns `(nil, ErrSessionNotFound)`. `*sessions.Pool` already satisfies the seam through the `poolResolver` adapter. Adding a parallel `HasIDer` interface + `Pool.HasID` method would double the surface for the same map read. As a consequence, `VerbSessionsHasID` answers correctly even when `sessioner == nil`; `NewServer`'s signature is unchanged. The "one sub-interface per verb" pattern remains the right shape when the seam needs a method that doesn't already exist on the resolver ŌĆö re-evaluate per future verb, not as a rule.
- **`Has bool` is deliberately NOT omitempty.** The wrapper-pointer `Response.SessionsHasID` is omitempty (so other verbs' byte-output stays unchanged); the inner `Has` is not. Reason: `omitempty` on `bool` elides the zero value, so `{Has: false}` would marshal to `{"sessionsHasID":{}}` ŌĆö indistinguishable from a malformed response that forgot to populate the field. Emitting the boolean unconditionally costs ~10 bytes and produces an unambiguous shape: `{"sessionsHasID":{"has":false}}` for absent, `{"sessionsHasID":{"has":true}}` for present. Pinned by `TestProtocol_SessionsHasIDResult_HasNotOmitempty` at the marshal layer.
- **Strict-UUID validation at the seam boundary, before `Lookup`.** Two-step boundary check: missing payload / empty `ID` ŌåÆ `Response{Error: "sessions.has-id: missing id"}`; `!sessions.ValidID(payload.ID)` ŌåÆ `Response{Error: "sessions.has-id: invalid uuid"}`. `Pool.Lookup` would already return `ErrSessionNotFound` for any non-canonical string, but failing fast at the seam distinguishes "client typed garbage" from "well-formed UUID that happens to be absent" ŌĆö the AC's contract. The empty-id branch could fold into `ValidID` (which also returns false on `""`); kept separate for the more useful error message, mirroring `handleSessionsRm` / `handleSessionsRename`. No prefix resolution ŌĆö has-id is strict-UUID by design (the verb answers "given the canonical UUID I expect, does it exist?"; prefix ambiguity is meaningless in that context).
- **No new `ErrorCode`, no `context.WithTimeout`.** `Pool.Lookup`'s only typed error is `ErrSessionNotFound`, and that case is *not* propagated as an error ŌĆö it's the absence-signal the verb returns as `Has: false`. Boundary-validation errors are plain strings; the typed-sentinel envelope #98 introduced is unused here. The handler skips `context.WithTimeout`: `Pool.Lookup` is an O(1) map read under `Pool.mu` RLock, and the conn's existing handshake deadline already bounds slow-write clients. A non-`ErrSessionNotFound` Lookup error (theoretically unreachable on `*sessions.Pool` today) is surfaced verbatim as `Response{Error: "sessions.has-id: <err>"}` ŌĆö defensive against future Pool.Lookup error growth.
- **Client wrapper `SessionsHasID(ctx, sock, id) (bool, error)` mirrors `SessionsList`'s shape.** Single result + error, no typed-sentinel switch. Server-side validation errors flow through `Response.Error` verbatim. Empty-response guard returns `errors.New("control: empty sessions.has-id response")` for symmetry with the other client wrappers. The 1.3c-2 foreground auto-attach path is the intended in-process consumer; no CLI verb exists today (out of scope by AC).
- **Concurrency: `Pool.mu` (RLock) only.** Handler runs on the per-conn goroutine; no new goroutines, no `Session.lcMu` involvement, no new lock-order edges. Read consistency: a session minted between the handler's read and the client's decode will not appear; one removed will still appear. Acceptable for a yes/no query ŌĆö the caller (1.3c-2's startup detection) treats the answer as a decision input, not a durable contract. Any acted verb (rm/new) serializes against this read through `Pool.mu`.
- **Backward-compat: existing verbs' wire output is byte-identical.** `TestProtocol_SessionsRoundTripBackCompat` extended with a `SessionsList` row (the new `SessionsHasID` field's omitempty pin) plus reaffirmed `Response{}` and `Response{OK: true}` rows. Existing rows pass unmodified.
- **Test coverage in `sessions_has_id_test.go` (~378 LOC).** Reuses `startServerWithSessioner` and `fakeResolver` verbatim ŌĆö no `fakeSessioner` extension (the verb does not consult the sessioner). `fakeResolver` extended with a `present map[SessionID]bool` field for the present/absent split. Mandatory tests: present (Lookup recorded, `Has: true`); absent (`ErrSessionNotFound` ŌåÆ `Has: false`, no error ŌĆö pins the AC's "well-formed but absent ŌåÆ false, not error"); missing ID (zero Lookup calls); invalid-UUID guard (zero Lookup calls ŌĆö pins fast-fail at the boundary); non-`ErrSessionNotFound` Lookup error (defensive contract for future Pool.Lookup growth); client wire shape (hand-rolled `net.Listen` captures `{"verb":"sessions.has-id","sessions":{"id":"..."}}\n` exactly ŌĆö pins omitempty on `Label`/`JSONLPolicy`/`NewLabel`); empty-response-as-error; `Has`-not-omitempty pin.
- **Production diff ~106 LOC across 3 files** (`internal/control/protocol.go` ~34 for `VerbSessionsHasID` + `SessionsHasIDResult` + `Response.SessionsHasID`; `internal/control/server.go` ~43 for dispatch + `handleSessionsHasID`; `internal/control/client.go` ~29 for `SessionsHasID`). Test diff ~389 LOC (`sessions_has_id_test.go` +378 + `sessions_new_test.go` +11 for the back-compat row). CLI surface unchanged; runtime wiring is implicit (`s.sessions` already non-nil by `NewServer` precondition).
- **Out of scope, by design.** The 1.3c-2 foreground auto-attach detection that consumes this verb. A `pyry sessions has-id` CLI verb (AC scopes the caller to a Go in-process client wrapper). Prefix resolution / loose-input acceptance. A `Pool.HasID` primitive or `HasIDer` interface.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Sessions: has-id seam (1.3c-1)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/157-control-sessions-has-id.md`](specs/architecture/157-control-sessions-has-id.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.3b, ticket #155)
- **`pyry attach --create-if-missing <uuid>` + `Pool.GetOrCreate` ŌĆö take-or-create attach for SDK consumers.** New flag on `pyry attach` that lets Claudian / `@anthropic-ai/claude-agent-sdk` issue one attach call instead of two (`pyry sessions new --id <uuid>` + `pyry attach <uuid>`). The SDK mints UUIDv4 per chat upstream and passes it through; pyry must accept the SDK's id even when it has never seen it before. Composes orthogonally with `--stdio`; the SDK's primary invocation is `pyry attach --stdio --create-if-missing <uuid>`. Without the flag, attach against an unknown id continues to fail with the existing `"sessions: session not found"` ŌĆö opt-in semantics, no behaviour change for existing callers.
- **`Pool.GetOrCreate(ctx, id, label) (SessionID, error)` ŌĆö take-or-create primitive (over `CreateWithID` insert-or-error).** Returns the canonical SessionID whether the session already existed or this call created it. The handler treats both branches identically from the call site onward (`Lookup ŌåÆ Activate ŌåÆ Attach`). Insert-or-error would force a follow-up `Lookup` after `ErrIDInUse`, re-introducing a TOCTOU window ŌĆö see [ADR 014](knowledge/decisions/014-get-or-create-take-or-create.md). Pairs with `Pool.Lookup` and `Pool.Create`.
- **`ValidID(s string) bool` next to `NewID` in `id.go`.** Canonical UUIDv4 validator: 36 chars, lowercase hex, dashes at 8/13/18/23, version-4 nibble at 14, RFC 4122 variant at 19. Empty input ŌåÆ false. `GetOrCreate` rejects non-canonical input with `ErrInvalidSessionID` before any Pool state is touched. Validation lives at the Pool boundary so all future callers (direct Go consumers, test harnesses, future verbs) pick it up adapter-free. Belt-and-suspenders version + variant check is free; SDK-produced UUIDs are uuidv4 by construction.
- **Atomic registration ŌĆö the load-bearing change.** Unlike `Pool.Create` (which releases `p.mu` between persist and supervise), `GetOrCreate` holds `p.mu` across **all five** of: duplicate-id short-circuit ŌåÆ registry-map insert ŌåÆ `saveLocked()` ŌåÆ `registerAllocatedUUIDLocked(id)` ŌåÆ `g.Go(sess.Run)`. Without holding the lock across the schedule, a concurrent same-id observer could see the registered entry under `if existing, ok := p.sessions[id]`, return id, call `Activate`, and block ~30s until ctx times out (the winner's lifecycle goroutine hasn't parked on `activateCh` yet). Race detector cannot catch it; failure mode is "long hangs at attach time on the loser." `g.Go` is non-blocking ŌĆö the spawned goroutine parks on `activateCh` / `runCtx.Done()` before doing any pool work ŌĆö so holding `p.mu` across it is safe. `Activate(ctx)` happens AFTER `p.mu` is released; its `capMu`/`lcMu` discipline would deadlock under `p.mu`.
- **Helper extraction shared with `Pool.Create`.** Two new private helpers: `buildSession(id, label) (*Session, error)` constructs the per-session supervisor + Session (touches no Pool state); `registerAllocatedUUIDLocked(id)` is the lock-held variant of `RegisterAllocatedUUID`. `Pool.Create` is updated to call `buildSession` (replacing its inlined block) and `RegisterAllocatedUUID` delegates to `registerAllocatedUUIDLocked`. `Pool.Create`'s body shrinks; behaviour byte-identical.
- **Wire field: `AttachPayload.CreateIfMissing bool` (`json:"createIfMissing,omitempty"`).** Omitempty is load-bearing for the same v0.5.x byte-identical contract that pins `SessionID`'s tag. Pinned by `TestAttach_CreateIfMissingOnWire` (companion to the existing `TestAttach_EmptySessionIDOmittedOnWire`).
- **Server-side branch + `GetOrCreator` 1-method interface.** `handleAttach` gains one branch at the front of the resolve step: with the flag set, dispatch to `s.sessioner.GetOrCreate` (validates UUIDv4, skips ResolveID's prefix logic ŌĆö a "prefix that doesn't match" being interpreted as a fresh UUID would create non-canonical ids). Without the flag, today's two-step `ResolveID ŌåÆ Lookup` path. The 30s `activateCtx` is built earlier so `GetOrCreate`'s internal `Pool.Activate` shares the budget; the existing `sess.Activate` below the branch reuses it. New `GetOrCreator` interface mirrors the `Remover`/`Renamer`/`Lister` pattern, embedded into `Sessioner`. `*sessions.Pool` satisfies it structurally; tests fake it directly.
- **Skipping ResolveID's prefix path under the flag is a deliberate hazard guard.** The flag's intended caller is the SDK, which always passes a full UUID. Prefix-resolution is a human affordance not relevant to that path. A typo registering as a fresh non-canonical id (`b`, `0d1`) would corrupt the registry and `pyry sessions list` rendering.
- **CLI flag: `parseAttachArgs(args) (sessionID, stdio, createIfMissing, err)`.** `--create-if-missing` registered alongside `--stdio` on the same `flag.NewFlagSet("pyry attach", flag.ContinueOnError)`. `--create-if-missing` with no positional does NOT error at parse time ŌĆö empty SessionID flows through to the server, where `GetOrCreate`'s empty-id rejection produces `ErrInvalidSessionID`. Parse-time vs. semantic boundary: parsing is purely about shape; semantic rejection lives at the Pool. Both `control.Attach` and `control.AttachStdio` extend their signatures with `createIfMissing bool` ŌĆö single edit each, single production call site each.
- **Concurrent same-UUID safety.** Two `GetOrCreate(sameID)` callers race. One wins the lock, registers, persists, schedules `sess.Run`, releases the lock, proceeds to `Activate`, returns id. The other acquires the lock, observes the now-registered session via the duplicate-id short-circuit, releases the lock, returns id (no error). Both then `Lookup ŌåÆ Activate ŌåÆ Attach`; `Activate` is idempotent. Net result: exactly one registry entry, exactly one supervised child, exactly one rotation skip-set entry. AC #4 falls out of the atomic critical section.
- **Tests** (in `internal/sessions/pool_get_or_create_test.go`, ~406 LOC; `internal/control/attach_create_if_missing_test.go`, ~226 LOC; `cmd/pyry/args_test.go` extension; existing `attach_stdio_client_test.go` and `sessions_new_test.go` updates for the new wire field): `TestValidID` (table ŌĆö empty/short/long/wrong-dash/non-hex/v3/non-RFC-4122-variant + canonical-NewID-output); `TestPool_GetOrCreate_Take_ReturnsExisting` (existing label preserved on take); `TestPool_GetOrCreate_Create_Persists` (caller's id written verbatim, claude spawned); `TestPool_GetOrCreate_PersistsPostDetach` (AC #1 ŌĆö the test that surfaced ticket #169's persist-ordering race against `-race`); `TestPool_GetOrCreate_InvalidID`; `TestPool_GetOrCreate_PoolNotRunning`; `TestPool_GetOrCreate_ConcurrentSameID` (AC #4 ŌĆö N=8 goroutines racing on one id, exactly one entry, label is one of the inputs, `-race`-clean); `TestPool_GetOrCreate_HonorsCap` (cap=1; bootstrap evicted via `Pool.Activate`'s cap-aware path); wire/dispatch/no-sessioner/invalid-id end-to-end via fakeSessioner.
- **Out of scope, by design.** E2E coverage of `pyry attach --stdio --create-if-missing` against a real daemon is deferred to a sibling Phase 1.3 ticket that wires up the broader stdio harness ŌĆö same posture as #161 / #162 sit alongside #154's unit tests. Foreground auto-attach (Phase 1.3c) is independent. `pyry sessions new --id <uuid>` (the alternative two-call shape) is a separate ticket and does not exist today.
- **Production diff ~129 LOC across 8 files** (`internal/sessions/get_or_create.go` ~104 new + `internal/sessions/id.go` ~37 for `ValidID` + `internal/sessions/pool.go` ~83 net for helper extraction + `internal/control/protocol.go` ~7 + `internal/control/server.go` ~73 + `internal/control/attach_client.go` ~9 + `internal/control/attach_stdio_client.go` ~8 + `cmd/pyry/main.go` ~34 across `parseAttachArgs` + `runAttach` + help text). Test diff ~700+ LOC. PTY-mode `pyry attach` without `--create-if-missing` is byte-unchanged.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md ┬¦ Pool.GetOrCreate (1.3b)](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md), [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Attach: --create-if-missing (1.3b)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [ADR 014](knowledge/decisions/014-get-or-create-take-or-create.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/155-attach-create-if-missing.md`](specs/architecture/155-attach-create-if-missing.md).

### Codebase (race fix, ticket #169)
- **`Session.Evict` / `Session.Activate` wait for the registry persist before returning.** `transitionTo` previously closed the per-direction wake channel under `lcMu` before calling `pool.persist`, so `Evict`/`Activate` waiters could observe the post-transition in-memory state and read **pre**-transition state from disk. Surfaced by `TestPool_GetOrCreate_PersistsPostDetach` (#155, PR #166) ŌĆö that test polls `LifecycleState() == stateEvicted`, then reads the registry, and intermittently sees the pre-eviction state. Fix reorders `transitionTo` into three phases: (1) flip `lcState` + allocate the *opposite-direction* wake channel under `lcMu`; (2) release `lcMu` and run `pool.persist`; (3) re-acquire `lcMu` to close the *current-direction* channel. The persist now runs strictly between the state flip and the wake. New invariant: **`activeCh` is closed iff `lcState == stateActive` AND the persist for that transition has completed**; same for `evictedCh`. Cold-start init in `Pool.New` / `Pool.Create` already encoded this; no init change needed.
- **`Activate` / `Evict` lose their already-in-target-state early-return; always wait on the channel.** When fully transitioned, `<-ch` on a closed channel returns immediately (same wall-clock as the old short-circuit); mid-transition (state flipped, persist still running), the receive correctly blocks. Eliminates a second-shape race where a caller short-circuits on `lcState == stateActive` from a *prior* transition whose persist is still in flight.
- **Lock-order rule (`Pool.mu ŌåÆ Session.lcMu`) preserved.** `lcMu` is released before `pool.persist`; the post-persist re-acquire is sequential, not nested. The old comment at `session.go:347-349` ("releases lcMu before calling pool.persist so saveLocked's per-session lcMu re-acquire doesn't deadlock") still holds. Approach (1) from the ticket (move persist inside `lcMu`) was rejected for this reason; approach (3) (serialise transitions through a goroutine) was rejected as overkill ŌĆö `Session.Run` is already the sole caller of `transitionTo`, transitions are already serialised by construction.
- **Channel close fires even on persist failure.** A permanently-stuck waiter is a worse failure mode than waking to stale disk. `Run` already treats persist failure as fatal (`return fmt.Errorf("persist evicted: %w", err)`), terminating the lifecycle goroutine ŌĆö operator sees the failure via the errgroup's first-error propagation.
- **`Pool.Activate`'s cap path is unchanged.** Calls `sess.LifecycleState()` (in-memory) and `sess.touchLastActive()` (in-memory). No disk read at this caller; no race; no fix needed. The fix is local to three methods of `Session`.
- **Production diff ~60 LOC `internal/sessions/session.go`. Test diff ~191 LOC new file `internal/sessions/session_persist_test.go`.** Three regression tests: `TestSession_EvictBlocksUntilPersisted` (immediate `loadRegistry` shows `"evicted"`, no poll), `TestSession_ActivateBlocksUntilPersisted` (warm-start in `stateEvicted`, `Activate`, immediate disk read shows post-active state), and a stress wrapper looping 20 evictŌåöactivate transitions asserting disk consistency at each step. Pass deterministically under `go test -race -count=20 ./internal/sessions/...`.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Other lifecycle transitions beyond `stateActive Ōåö stateEvicted`. The un-skip of `TestPool_GetOrCreate_PersistsPostDetach` is part of #155's PR #166 rebase (its `t.Skip("blocked on #169")` line is removed when #166 lands on the new `main`).
- See [knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md ┬¦ Persist seam](knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md), [ADR 013](knowledge/decisions/013-evict-activate-persist-ordering.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/169-evict-activate-persist-ordering.md`](specs/architecture/169-evict-activate-persist-ordering.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.3a, ticket #154)
- **`pyry attach --stdio [<id>]` + `control.AttachStdio` ŌĆö no-PTY byte forwarding for SDK consumers.** New flag on the existing `pyry attach` verb (not a new verb ŌĆö see [ADR 012](knowledge/decisions/012-attach-stdio-flag-vs-verb.md)) and a sibling client function in `internal/control/attach_stdio_client.go`. Reuses `VerbAttach` unchanged: handshake sends `Cols=0, Rows=0`, `omitempty` drops both fields off the wire so the bytes are byte-indistinguishable from a v0.5.x client; the existing `payload.Cols > 0 && payload.Rows > 0` guard in `handleAttach` (#136) skips the resize seam. Server side is **byte-identical-input**, zero changes. Client side is straight `io.Copy(out, conn)` (output goroutine, joined via `done chan`) + `io.Copy(conn, in)` (main) ŌĆö no `term.MakeRaw`, no SIGWINCH, no `copyWithEscape` state machine. EOF on `in` returns nil (clean detach; lazy-eviction semantics ŌĆö detach ŌēĀ destroy); server hangup after ack returns nil via the existing `writerErr` coercion.
- **Output goroutine is joined, not fire-and-forget.** Small upgrade over `Attach`'s shape ŌĆö `Attach` can fire-and-forget because `defer term.Restore` doesn't depend on the goroutine completing; `AttachStdio` has no terminal state to restore but joining gives the caller a deterministic "all server bytes flushed to `out`" guarantee, useful for SDK consumers reading `out` until the spawned process closes the pipe. Closing `conn` is the cross-goroutine wake-up ŌĆö no channels-with-cancel.
- **Sibling functions, not a shared core.** `Attach` and `AttachStdio` share the dial-and-handshake prologue (~10 lines); the diverging tails (raw mode + SIGWINCH watcher + `copyWithEscape` vs. plain `io.Copy`) are large enough that an attempted shared core would be a sea of `if stdio { ŌĆ” }` branches. Two functions, one wire protocol. If a third transport ever lands, factor at that point.
- **Flag-set parsing in `parseAttachArgs(args) (sessionID, stdio, err)`.** Fresh `flag.NewFlagSet("pyry attach", flag.ContinueOnError)` for `--stdio` after `parseClientFlags` peels globals; positionals routed through the existing `attachSelectorFromArgs`. Mirrors `runSessionsNew`'s precedent (ADR 010). Flag-ordering rule: `--stdio` must precede the positional ŌĆö Go's `flag` package stops at the first non-flag arg, so `pyry attach <id> --stdio` is rejected as `errTooManyAttachArgs` (pinned in `cmd/pyry/args_test.go:TestParseAttachArgs`). The unit-testable helper avoids dialling the socket.
- **Affordance stderr lines suppressed under `--stdio`.** `"pyry: attached. Press Ctrl-B d to detach."` and `"pyry: detached."` are noise on a programmatic parent's stderr channel. One-line `if !stdio { ŌĆ” }` guards. No flag, no env var ŌĆö the mode is the signal.
- **Rejected: auto-detect via `term.IsTerminal`.** Implicit mode switching is hostile in both directions ŌĆö a test suite running `pyry attach` under a captured stdin would silently produce stream-json behaviour; an operator piping a heredoc into `pyry attach` would silently lose the escape-key surface. The flag is the explicit signal: SDKs pass it, humans don't, nothing changes accidentally.
- **Wire byte-shape pinned by `TestAttachStdio_NoGeometryOnWire`.** Captures raw bytes off the conn before decode and asserts neither `"cols"` nor `"rows"` nor `"sessionID"` appears ŌĆö a future change that sets `Cols: 0` explicitly via a struct literal would still pass an `encoded.Cols == 0` check but break the wire-bytes promise this test enforces. Foreground-mode wire string flows through verbatim ŌĆö `TestAttachStdio_AckErrorPropagates` pins parity with `TestServer_AttachOnForegroundSession`.
- **Production diff ~135 LOC** (`internal/control/attach_stdio_client.go` ~80 new + `cmd/pyry/main.go` ~55 for `parseAttachArgs` + `runAttach` dispatch + help text). Test diff ~500 LOC (`internal/control/attach_stdio_client_test.go` ~460 + `cmd/pyry/args_test.go` ~40). PTY-mode `pyry attach` is byte-unchanged when `--stdio` is absent.
- **Out of scope for #154**: E2E process-level harness driving `pyry attach --stdio` against a real daemon (#161); no-PTY-in-fd-table assertion via `lsof` / `/proc/<pid>/fd` (#162). `--create-if-missing` semantics is Phase 1.3b (#155); foreground-binary auto-attach is Phase 1.3c-2 (#158).
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Attach: stdio mode (1.3a)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [ADR 012](knowledge/decisions/012-attach-stdio-flag-vs-verb.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/154-attach-stdio-mode.md`](specs/architecture/154-attach-stdio-mode.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #161)
- **`internal/e2e/attach_stdio.go` + `attach_stdio_test.go` ŌĆö stdio-attach test harness + byte-flow proof-of-life.** Sibling to #125's PTY-mode `AttachHarness`. New `StdioAttachClient` struct + `startStdioAttach(t, label) *StdioAttachClient` constructor under `//go:build e2e` (no installer-test consumer; gate is `e2e`-only, narrower than the PTY harness's `e2e || e2e_install`). Reuses `spawnAttachableDaemon` and `waitDaemonReady` from `attach_pty.go` verbatim ŌĆö the supervised claude is the same e2e test binary running `TestHelperProcess` in echo mode (line-buffered). Two test files compile into one test binary and share the helper; only one `TestHelperProcess` in the package. Creates a fresh session via in-process `control.SessionsNew(label)` (same shape as every other e2e test in the package ŌĆö spawning a third subprocess for one wire call is pure cost), then spawns `pyry attach -pyry-socket=<sock> --stdio <id>` with stdin/stdout wired to plain `os.Pipe()` ends ŌĆö **no PTY anywhere on the client side**, exactly the SDK consumer shape Claudian / `@anthropic-ai/claude-agent-sdk` exercise in production.
- **Public API: `Write`, `ReadUntil(needle, deadline)`, `Close(t) int`.** `Write` writes to the parent's `inputW`; the child's stdin is `inputR`. `ReadUntil` reads from `outputR` in a background goroutine and selects against a deadline ŌĆö `os.Pipe` ends share the no-`SetReadDeadline` trait with PTY masters on darwin (`lessons.md ┬¦ PTY master fds on darwin do not support SetReadDeadline` is the adjacent shape), so the timeout is enforced caller-side. Returns `(seen []byte, err error)` with seen populated regardless of outcome. `Close(t) int` closes `inputW` (delivering EOF to the child's `AttachStdio` input loop), waits up to ~2s for the child, returns its exit code; idempotent via `sync.Once` with `t.Cleanup`.
- **Pipe-handle ownership and EOF discipline.** After `attachCmd.Start()`, the kernel has dup'd `inputR` and `outputW` into the child. The parent's copies must be closed: `inputR.Close()` so EOF flows from `inputW` alone, `outputW.Close()` so `outputR.Read` sees EOF when the child closes its stdout. Skipping either silently breaks the EOF semantics. Documented in `attach_stdio.go` next to the `Start` call.
- **Cleanup ordering ŌĆö load-bearing.** `sync.Once`-wrapped: (1) `inputW.Close()` ŌåÆ child stdin EOF ŌåÆ clean detach ŌåÆ exit 0; (2) wait `attachDone` Ōēż 2s, escalate via `killSpawned` (SIGTERM ŌåÆ grace ŌåÆ SIGKILL) on timeout; (3) `outputR.Close()` *after* the child has exited (don't race the child's stdout writes); (4) `killSpawned(daemonCmd)`; (5) `os.Remove(socket)` defensive against the SIGKILL escape. Mirrors the PTY harness's discipline minus the master/slave close pair.
- **Skip-on-no-pipe at `os.Pipe()`, not at handshake.** AC#3 ("CI hosts without spawn capability skip cleanly") is gated structurally ŌĆö `os.Pipe()` exercises kernel fd allocation directly, faster than spawning pyry and tearing it down. Never fires on the project's CI matrix; defensive against future restrictive sandboxes. `t.Skipf` shape mirrors #125's `pty.Open` skip.
- **Handshake-failure detector mirrors `attach_pty.go:137-146`.** After `attachCmd.Start()`, the harness selects on `attachDone` vs `time.After(500ms)`: if the child exits within 500ms, `t.Fatalf` with the captured exit code + `Stderr` buffer + daemon stderr. Catches "no attach provider configured" if the daemon somehow landed in foreground mode, wire-decode errors if the protocol shifted, and (today) the #167 CLI-parse failure.
- **`os.MkdirTemp("", "pyry-as-*")` for HOME.** Same `sun_path` budget rationale as the restart / rotation / attach harnesses ŌĆö long test names + `t.TempDir()` overflow macOS's 104-byte limit. Short prefix keeps the socket path well under.
- **Round-trip test currently `t.Skip`'d on #167.** `TestE2E_AttachStdio_BytesRoundTrip` is **the harness's first consumer** but is `t.Skip("blocked on #167 ŌĆö pyry attach --stdio rejected by parseClientFlags")`. The harness body works end-to-end against `internal/control` and the daemon; the bug surfaces at `parseClientFlags`, which rejects `--stdio` *before* `parseAttachArgs` ever sees it. Existing unit tests (`internal/control/attach_stdio_client_test.go`, `cmd/pyry/args_test.go`) bypass `parseClientFlags` so they didn't catch it. The harness was the surface that surfaced the bug. Once #167 lands, removing the `t.Skip` should make the test pass against the harness body unchanged.
- **No new harness API on the daemon side.** `spawnAttachableDaemon` already does what stdio needs (helper-as-claude, echo mode, idle timeout off, `-pyry-resume=false`). Reuse without parameter growth ŌĆö no options struct, no shared `AttachHarness` interface across PTY/stdio modes (the surfaces differ in a load-bearing way: PTY exposes a `*os.File` master; stdio exposes line-aware `Write`/`ReadUntil`).
- **Out of scope, by design.** No-PTY-fd assertion (`/proc/<pid>/fd` Linux / `lsof -p` macOS) ŌåÆ #162. Foreground auto-attach scenarios ŌåÆ 1.3c-2-e2e-*. Multi-attach exclusivity, server-initiated detach, binary-safe transport for arbitrary byte sequences ŌåÆ unit boundary in `internal/control/attach_stdio_client_test.go`.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~321 LOC across 2 new files** (`attach_stdio.go` ~265, `attach_stdio_test.go` ~56). Default `go test ./...` unaffected; `go test -tags e2e -race ./internal/e2e/...` clean.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ Stdio-Attach Harness Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Attach: stdio mode (1.3a)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/161-e2e-stdio-attach-harness.md`](specs/architecture/161-e2e-stdio-attach-harness.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #162)
- **`internal/e2e/attach_stdio_no_pty_test.go` ŌĆö binary-level no-PTY-fd assertion for `pyry attach --stdio`.** Sibling consumer of #161's `startStdioAttach` harness. Asserts the *negative* property the byte-flow test cannot: while attached, the attach client process holds zero PTY-device fds (`/dev/ptmx`, `/dev/pts/*` on linux, `/dev/ttys*` on darwin, `/dev/tty` on both). Unit tests in `internal/control/attach_stdio_client_test.go` already prove the client function imports no `creack/pty`; this is the binary-level defence ŌĆö a future refactor that pulls a `pty.Open` into `cmd/pyry/runAttach`'s `--stdio` branch (or a "wrap stdio in a pty for raw-mode safety" helper) would slip past every unit boundary, and this test catches it. A regression that allocates a useless PTY but still passes bytes through fails only here, not `ŌĆ”_BytesRoundTrip`.
- **`runtime.GOOS` dispatch over build-tagged `_linux.go` / `_darwin.go` files.** One file, two helpers (`openPTYDeviceTargetsLinux` reads `/proc/<pid>/fd/`, `openPTYDeviceTargetsDarwin` shells out to `lsof -p <pid> -Fn`), one shared matcher (`isPTYDevicePath`). Build-tagged platform files would force the matcher into a third shared file or duplicate it; `runtime.GOOS` keeps everything in ~110 LOC. `unsupported GOOS` (and any inspection-mechanism failure: missing `/proc`, missing `lsof`, ESRCH from a raced child exit) returns an error which the test treats as `t.Skipf` per AC#2.
- **Matcher set is conservative + explicit.** Matched: `/dev/ptmx` (PTY master multiplexer ŌĆö canonical "this process allocated a PTY" signal, both platforms), `/dev/pts/*` (linux PTY slaves), `/dev/ttys*` (darwin PTY slaves ŌĆö `exec.Cmd` with explicit Stdin/Stdout/Stderr does not propagate the parent's tty fds, so any `/dev/ttysNNN` in the child's table was opened by the child), `/dev/tty` (controlling-terminal device, both platforms ŌĆö a `--stdio` client with stdio wired to pipes has no business opening it; surfaces terminal-mode dispatch on the wrong code path). Not matched: `/dev/null` / `/dev/urandom` (not PTYs), BSD-legacy `/dev/pty[m-z]*` / `/dev/tty[m-z]*` (unreachable on supported macOS). Extend the matcher if a real regression escapes it; do not pre-enumerate hypothetical kernel device paths.
- **Probe runs immediately on harness return, no extra wait.** The harness's 500ms early-exit detector means `startStdioAttach` only returns once the child is past handshake, so any PTY allocation during init is already visible by probe time. Probe is a synchronous call from the test goroutine ŌĆö no new goroutines, no channels, no deadlines. Linux symlink-read race (fd closes between `ReadDir` and `Readlink`) is silently dropped via `continue` ŌĆö biases toward false-negative on a closing fd, acceptable; a stable PTY fd would not race a single-pass directory read.
- **No helper extraction, no shared matcher package.** `isPTYDevicePath` is 6 lines of pure string matching; `openPTYDeviceTargets{Linux,Darwin}` are thin syscall / `lsof` wrappers ŌĆö mocking the filesystem or `lsof` would test the mock, not the behaviour. The test *is* the strategy: one assertion against one running binary. YAGNI per CLAUDE.md "simplicity first."
- **Carries the same `t.Skip("blocked on #167 ŌĆö pyry attach --stdio rejected by parseClientFlags")` as `ŌĆ”_BytesRoundTrip`.** Both skips lift in one commit when #167 lands.
- **Out of scope, by design.** Stress / repeated-spawn / fd-leak testing (one-shot inspection at one moment is sufficient ŌĆö the matcher would still trip on at least some runs of an intermittent regression). Daemon-side PTY assertions (the supervised claude runs under a PTY by design ŌĆö this test inspects only the attach client's pid). Windows. A dedicated `pyry debug fds` verb (would expose internal state for one test's benefit, inspect the wrong process, and `/proc` + `lsof` are stable and well-known).
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~110 LOC, one new file** (`internal/e2e/attach_stdio_no_pty_test.go`). Default `go test ./...` unaffected; `go test -tags e2e -race ./internal/e2e/...` clean.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ No-PTY-fd assertion](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/162-e2e-stdio-attach-no-pty.md`](specs/architecture/162-e2e-stdio-attach-no-pty.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1b-B2, ticket #88)
- **`pyry sessions list [--json]` operator-facing CLI verb.** Final read-side member of the Phase 1.1 `sessions.<verb>` family (rounds out `new`, `rm`, `rename`). Plugs into the `runSessions` router (#76) as `case "list":` and consumes the `sessions.list` wire layer (#87) via `control.SessionsList`. First text-table sink in `cmd/pyry`: `text/tabwriter` (stdlib, no deps) renders a four-column table ŌĆö `UUID`, `LABEL`, `STATE`, `LAST-ACTIVE` ŌĆö with two-space padding (Go-CLI convention; matches `go list -m`/`go env`). UUIDs render in their full 36-character canonical form (no truncation ŌĆö operators copy/paste them); `LAST-ACTIVE` formats as RFC3339 in the table. `--json` swaps the renderer for a single object with a top-level `"sessions"` array (intentionally not a bare array ŌĆö leaves room for future top-level fields like `generated_at` without a breaking change). Per-element shape is `control.SessionInfo` JSON-encoded verbatim ŌĆö no second timestamp conversion. The renderer re-sorts by `LastActive` desc with `ID` asc tiebreak (defensive against future wire changes; `Pool.List` already returns this order). 5s timeout (matches `runStatus`/`runLogs`; in-memory server-side handler, no `Pool.mu` waiting). Production diff ~75 LOC in `cmd/pyry/main.go`; test diff ~430 LOC across 2 files (`cmd/pyry/sessions_test.go` ~250 LOC unit; `internal/e2e/sessions_list_test.go` ~210 LOC e2e). Existing `TestSessionsNew_E2E_UnknownVerb` switched its placeholder unknown verb from `list` to `bogus` in the same edit (one-line conceptual change).
- **JSON envelope ŌĆö anonymous struct, not `control.SessionsListPayload`.** Locally-declared `struct { Sessions []control.SessionInfo \`json:"sessions"\` }` documents the CLI presentation intent without coupling stdout shape to the wire payload type ŌĆö adding CLI-only top-level fields later (e.g. `"generated_at"`) won't touch `protocol.go`. Wire bytes are identical either way; the cost is one struct declaration and the win is clean separation between "what the wire returns" and "what we print to stdout".
- **No retry, no `--state`/`--label` filters, no relative timestamps, no colour.** Snapshot read; user re-runs to refresh. `--json | jq` covers filtering today. Locale-aware "3m ago" formatting deferred ŌĆö RFC3339 is unambiguous across timezones and across log-paste-into-issue boundaries; revisit on operator feedback. ANSI colour for STATE could land later as `--color=auto` if asked.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Sessions: list CLI renderer](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/88-cli-sessions-list.md`](specs/architecture/88-cli-sessions-list.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1a-B2, ticket #76)
- **`pyry sessions <verb>` sub-router + `pyry sessions new [--name LABEL]` first verb.** Operator-facing CLI surface for the `sessions.*` namespace. The top-level switch in `cmd/pyry/main.go run()` gains exactly one case (`case "sessions": return runSessions(os.Args[2:])`); `runSessions` peels global pyry flags via `parseClientFlags("pyry sessions", args)`, then dispatches on the first positional. Phase 1.1b (#61), 1.1c (#63), 1.1d (#65), and 1.1e (#49) each plug in as one switch case + one `runSessions<Verb>` helper + one token in `sessionsVerbList` + one word in help text ŌĆö no top-level switch edit. `runSessionsNew` opens a `flag.NewFlagSet("pyry sessions new", flag.ContinueOnError)` (mirrors `runInstallService`'s precedent) for `--name`, then calls `control.SessionsNew(ctx, socketPath, label)` with a 30s `context.WithTimeout` matching the server-side ceiling in `handleSessionsNew`. Stdout is exactly `<uuid>\n` per AC#1 ŌĆö `fmt.Println(id)` produces a canonical UUIDv4 + single newline, no surrounding text.
- **Sub-router takes a parsed `socketPath`, not raw args** ŌĆö load-bearing for the global-flags-first convention. Two reasons: (1) one canonical parse path for every future `sessions.*` verb, with the existing helper's error wording; (2) structurally enforces "globals before sub-verb" ŌĆö a `-pyry-name` placed *after* the sub-verb reaches `runSessionsNew`'s own `FlagSet` and produces "flag provided but not defined" instead of silently shadowing. Pinned by `TestRunSessions_GlobalFlagAfterSubcommand_FailsCleanly`. Mirrors the pre-existing top-level "pyry flags before claude args" rule (`splitArgs` lines 184-196).
- **`sessionsVerbList` is a constant, not a derived list.** A `map[string]func` would force a sort (map iteration is randomised) and an iteration cost that only amortises at Ōēź3 verbs. With one verb today and four 1-line additions in 1.1b/c/d/e, the duplication is one token per verb in two places (switch case + constant). Dead-simple beats indirection here. The 1.1b ticket extends both in the same edit ŌĆö no new pattern, no map. The "one line per future verb" invariant the issue calls out is satisfied by structure, not by discipline.
- **`parseSessionsNewArgs(args) (label, err)` extracted from `runSessionsNew`** ŌĆö keeps `cmd/pyry/sessions_test.go` table-driven over flag forms (`--name`, `-name`, `--name=`, `--name=glued`, extra positional, unknown flag) without dialling the socket. Mirrors `attachSelectorFromArgs`'s split (1.1e-D). The arity rule itself is trivial (zero positionals); the helper exists for the unit-test target, not for arity complexity.
- **AC#3 ("unknown sub-verb does not fall through to claude") satisfied structurally.** `runSessions` is reached from the top-level switch and returns through `errSessionsUsage` ŌĆö control never falls through to `runSupervisor`. Pinned by `TestRunSessions_UnknownVerb` (unit, error-message check) and `TestSessionsNew_E2E_UnknownVerb` (e2e, registry session count unchanged before/after ŌĆö proves the daemon's pool was not touched).
- **AC#4 ("activation failure leaves the registry entry in place") satisfied server-side.** `Pool.Create` (#73) saves the registry entry inside its critical section *before* `Pool.Activate` is called; an activation failure surfaces as `Response.Error` over the wire, but the entry persists for a future `pyry attach <uuid>` retry once 1.1e ships. The CLI is a 4-line synchronous wrapper; activation-vs-create error distinction is not visible at the wire boundary by design (the wire has no separate "id valid despite error" channel).
- **No retry / activation poll on transient dial failure.** `pyry status` / `pyry stop` / `pyry logs` don't retry; "no daemon" is a clean failure for the operator to act on. The no-daemon error surfaces as `pyry: sessions new: dial /path/sock: connect: no such file or directory` ŌĆö same shape as `pyry status` against a stopped daemon. Pinned by `TestSessionsNew_E2E_NoDaemon` (asserts non-zero exit, non-empty stderr, no `panic`/`goroutine `/`runtime/` substrings ŌĆö clean error, not a crash).
- **No new `--workdir` / `--cwd` / `-pyry-active-cap` flags.** `Pool.Create` inherits the daemon's bootstrap workdir; per-session workdir is Phase 2.x. `-pyry-active-cap` already shipped in #116 ŌĆö defaults to `0` (uncapped) and stays a daemon-startup flag, not a `sessions new` argument.
- **Production diff ~82 LOC** (`cmd/pyry/main.go`: top-level switch case + `sessionsVerbList` + `errSessionsUsage` + `runSessions` + `parseSessionsNewArgs` + `runSessionsNew` + reserved-verb comment + help text). Test diff ~270 LOC across 2 files (`cmd/pyry/sessions_test.go`: ~100 LOC unit; `internal/e2e/sessions_new_test.go`: ~165 LOC e2e under `//go:build e2e` reusing `writeSleepClaude` / `newRegistryHome` / `readRegistry` / `waitForBootstrap` from #116). Default `go test ./...` runs unit tests only; e2e gated by build tag.
