- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Sessions: CLI Router (1.1a-B2)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [ADR 010](knowledge/decisions/010-sessions-cli-sub-router.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/76-cli-sessions-new.md`](specs/architecture/76-cli-sessions-new.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.0, tickets #28 + #29)
- **`internal/sessions` package** ŌĆö `SessionID` (UUIDv4 via `crypto/rand`, stdlib only), `Session` (wraps one `*supervisor.Supervisor` + optional `*supervisor.Bridge`), `Pool` (single-bootstrap registry with `RWMutex`-protected map). Sentinel errors `ErrSessionNotFound`, `ErrAttachUnavailable`. `Pool.Lookup("")` resolves to the bootstrap entry ŌĆö the seam Phase 1.1's `Request.SessionID` plugs into.
- **Production consumers wired (#29)** ŌĆö `cmd/pyry/main.go` constructs `*sessions.Pool` (with the supervisor.Config template inside `SessionConfig`); `internal/control` consumes a single `SessionResolver` interface (replaces Phase 0's `StateProvider` + `AttachProvider` pair). A 5-line `poolResolver` adapter in `cmd/pyry` bridges `Pool` ŌåÆ `SessionResolver` (covariant-return workaround). Wire protocol unchanged; `pyry status`/`stop`/`logs`/`attach` byte-identical to Phase 0. Foreground-mode attach error string preserved verbatim via `errors.Is(err, sessions.ErrAttachUnavailable)` mapping in `handleAttach`.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md), [knowledge/features/control-plane.md](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), and [ADR 003](knowledge/decisions/003-session-addressable-runtime.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #116)
- **`internal/e2e/cap_test.go` ŌĆö `TestE2E_ActiveCap_EvictsLRU` + `TestE2E_ActiveCap_IdleInterleave`.** Two tests under `//go:build e2e` close the binary-boundary gap on the concurrent active cap (#41). The package-level race test had to switch to Bridge mode to avoid PTY contention; #116 verifies the LRU policy at the binary boundary against real PTY-backed children, plus the cap+idle interleave that two policies sharing `Session.Evict` couldn't otherwise exercise together. `EvictsLRU` runs cap=2, mints ╬▒/╬▓/╬│ via `control.SessionsNew` (`Request{Verb:"sessions.new", Sessions:&SessionsPayload{Label}}`) with 50ms gaps so `lastActiveAt` timestamps are distinguishable for `pickLRUVictim`, asserts each new spawn cap-evicts the LRU peer (bootstrap ŌåÆ ╬▒). `IdleInterleave` adds idle=2s, 1s wait between ╬▒ and ╬▓ activations: Phase 1 asserts cap-evict of bootstrap with ╬▒/╬▓ still active; Phase 2 asserts ╬▒ idle-evicts ~2s after its own activation while ╬▓ is still active; final ╬▓ idle-evict pins absence of state-machine wedge.
- **Three production wirings closed by this ticket** (all `cmd/pyry/main.go`, ~7 production LOC): (1) `-pyry-active-cap=N` flag (default `0` = uncapped) flowing into `sessions.Config.ActiveCap` ŌĆö negative values map to "unset" via `Pool.New`'s `<=0` contract, no validation in `runSupervisor`; (2) registration in `pyryFlagValues` so `splitArgs` keeps the flag on pyry's side instead of forwarding to claude; (3) `pool` wired as `control.NewServer`'s `Sessioner` argument (was `nil` after #75's wire-only slice ŌĆö `*sessions.Pool` satisfies `Sessioner` directly because `Pool.Create` returns `sessions.SessionID`, no adapter needed).
- **Tiny shell-script claude stand-in over extending fakeclaude.** `Pool.Create` constructs new-session args as `append(slices.Clone(tpl.ClaudeArgs), "--session-id", string(id))`. With the harness default `claudeBin=/bin/sleep` + `claudeArgs=["99999"]`, the new-session exec is `/bin/sleep 99999 --session-id <uuid>` ŌĆö both BSD and GNU `sleep(1)` reject the unknown arg. Lifecycle state would still flip to `stateActive` (Pool tracks lifecycle independently of supervisor health), so cap-evict logic uncouples from this ŌĆö but it generates noisy stderr and risks flakiness on backoff timing. Solution: a two-line `#!/bin/sh\nexec sleep 99999\n` script written to `<home>/sleep-claude.sh`, made executable, passed via `-pyry-claude=<path>` through `StartIn`'s variadic `extraFlags`. Both bootstrap (`<script> 99999`) and new sessions (`<script> 99999 --session-id <uuid>`) ignore positional args and `exec sleep`. Preferred over extending `internal/e2e/internal/fakeclaude` with a "no-rotation" mode (rotation-test binary, mixing concerns).
- **Four file-local helpers, no harness-side changes.** `writeSleepClaude(t, home)` writes the script. `waitForBootstrap(t, regPath, timeout)` discovers the bootstrap id by polling for `Bootstrap == true` (tolerates the registry file not yet existing ŌĆö Pool's first save races the readiness gate). `waitForSessionState(t, regPath, id, want, timeout)` polls for a *known* id to reach `"evicted"` or `"active"` (the active arm tolerates either empty/missing or literal ŌĆö same convention as `waitForBootstrapState` from #115). `assertActive(t, regPath, id)` is a one-shot checkpoint; fails if the session is `"evicted"` *right now*. Distinct from `waitForSessionState(..., "active", ...)` which returns on first observation; `assertActive` is "X must be true at this exact moment", used in the interleave test's gate between Phase 1 and Phase 2 to catch a session that flips active then evicts before the next poll. None promoted to `harness.go` ŌĆö rule of three; one consumer.
- **Three `sessions.new` calls (four sessions total) instead of two in `EvictsLRU`.** AC asks "creates three sessions"; bootstrap is the fourth. The third call (╬│) is the one whose LRU pick is non-trivial ŌĆö it must skip ╬▓ (just activated) and evict ╬▒ (older). Two calls would only test "the new session evicts the oldest active peer once"; three exercises the LRU comparison across two non-bootstrap sessions, the regression-shaped failure mode the package-level race test (Bridge mode, no PTY) couldn't hit at the binary boundary.
- **Interleave timing: 1s gap between idle fires.** Idle timers are one-shot, armed at `runActive` entry (effectively at Activate moment); the 1s wait between ╬▒ and ╬▓ activations becomes a 1s gap between their idle fires. That window is the CI slack ŌĆö bigger than typical Go scheduler jitter (~100ms) and registry poll cadence (50ms). 2s is the minimum useful idle timeout per the AC ("wait past idleTimeout"); if CI flakes, raise to idle=3s + wait=1.5s.
- **No `pyry status` cross-check.** `VerbStatus` resolves to the bootstrap session today (`Lookup("")`). For `EvictsLRU` the bootstrap is cap-evicted, so `pyry status` reports a non-running phase ŌĆö same shape as #115. Including it would re-test the same surface as the registry assertion; skipped.
- **Production diff ~7 LOC; test diff ~204 LOC, single new file.** Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ Active-Cap Eviction Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md](knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md), [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Server Construction](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), `lessons.md ┬¦ Pool.Create appends --session-id, breaking naive claude stand-ins`.

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #126)
- **`internal/e2e/attach_pty_test.go` ŌĆö `TestE2E_Attach_HandlesSIGWINCH`.** End-to-end cover for the live-resize chain through compiled `pyry` and `pyry attach` binaries. Reuses #125's `AttachHarness` + `StartAttach(t, "")` with no harness-side changes. Test resizes the harness's client-side master via `pty.Setsize(a.Master, &pty.Winsize{Rows:42, Cols:117})`, then `readUntilContains` matches the literal `winsize rows=42 cols=117\n` line emitted by the helper. Path under test: `pty.Setsize(master) ŌåÆ kernel SIGWINCH on attach client process group ŌåÆ startWinsizeWatcher (#133) ŌåÆ SendResize ŌåÆ handleResize (#137) ŌåÆ Session.Resize ŌåÆ Bridge.Resize (#136) ŌåÆ pty.Setsize(supervisor.ptmx) ŌåÆ kernel SIGWINCH on helper ŌåÆ helper emits the marker`. If any of the four halves regresses (client watcher, wire, server applier, supervisor seam), the test fails.
- **`TestHelperProcess` echo mode gains a SIGWINCH watcher.** Pattern mirrors `internal/supervisor/winsize.go`: `signal.Notify` + buffered `chan(1)` + goroutine + `pty.GetsizeFull(os.Stdin)` guarded by `term.IsTerminal`. On every signal, emits `fmt.Fprintf(os.Stdout, "winsize rows=%d cols=%d\n", size.Rows, size.Cols)` ŌĆö single `Write` per emission, so `poll.FD.fdmu` serialises with the echo loop's writes (no byte interleaving). No teardown plumbing ŌĆö helper exits on stdin EOF / `__EXIT__`, which terminates the goroutine implicitly. Watcher installed *between* `MakeRaw`+`PYRY_E2E_STARTED` bootstrap and the input loop, so by the time `StartAttach` returns the watcher is wired.
- **Extend the existing helper rather than add a second mode.** Per ticket: "reuse the harness's stub-claude program rather than introducing a second one." The new `winsize ŌĆ”\n` line is purely additive. Sibling tests are insulated by their match shape: `TestE2E_Attach_RoundTripsBytes` (#125) uses `bytes.Contains` for a nonced payload; `TestE2E_Attach_DetachesCleanly` (#127) drains master and asserts on `attachDone`; `TestE2E_Attach_SurvivesClaudeRestart` (#128) regex-matches `PYRY_E2E_STARTED pid=(\d+)\n` and a nonce. None collide with `winsize rows=N cols=M\n`. A second mode would force `spawnAttachableDaemon` to grow a "which mode?" parameter for no reuse benefit.
- **Dimensions chosen to avoid handshake collision.** `Rows: 42, Cols: 117` are deliberately distant from any sane terminal default. If the handshake's initial `Bridge.Resize` ever fires (slave default ŌēĀ 0├Ś0), the helper emits a winsize line for the default size *before* the test's resize ŌĆö `readUntilContains` accumulates and matches the second emission. The test does not care which size came first.
- **Bursts coalesce.** Two SIGWINCH delivered before the watcher goroutine processes the first collapse to one queued event in the buffered `chan(1)`. On wake, `pty.GetsizeFull` returns the *current* (most recent) dimensions ŌĆö the test's target. Same coalescing posture as the daemon-side watcher.
- **Skip-on-no-PTY inherited from the harness.** `StartAttach` calls `pty.Open` first and `t.Skip`s on failure (AC#4 satisfied without re-probing).
- **What the test deliberately does not pin.** Multi-SIGWINCH burst (covered by `TestStartWinsizeWatcher_SIGWINCHEmitsResize` from #133); detach-cancels-watcher (`TestStartWinsizeWatcher_StopIsSynchronousAndLeakFree` from #133); server clamps oversize dims (`TestServer_Resize_ClampsOversizeDims` from #137); foreground-mode silent resize (`TestServer_Resize_ForegroundSessionSilent` from #137 ŌĆö the harness only runs bridge mode).
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~64 LOC, single file** (`internal/e2e/attach_pty_test.go`: helper extension + new test function + two new imports `os/signal`/`syscall` + the `creack/pty` import). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ Attach SIGWINCH Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #68)
- **`internal/e2e` harness ŌĆö spawn + cleanup primitive** ŌĆö build-tag-isolated package (`//go:build e2e`, invoked via `go test -tags=e2e ./internal/e2e/...`) that builds pyry once per test process (`sync.Once`; `PYRY_E2E_BIN` short-circuits for CI), spawns it in a `t.TempDir()` `$HOME` with `/bin/sleep infinity` as the supervised "claude" and `-pyry-idle-timeout=0`, polls the Unix socket via `os.Stat` + `net.Dial` (5s deadline, 50ms gap, doneCh short-circuit on early exit), and tears down via `t.Cleanup`: SIGTERM ŌåÆ 3s grace ŌåÆ SIGKILL ŌåÆ 1s grace ŌåÆ `os.Remove(socket)`. Three exported names: `Harness`, `Start(t)`, plus the struct fields (`SocketPath`, `HomeDir`, `PID`, `Stdout`, `Stderr`).
- **`HOME` redirection contains every ~-relative path with one env var** ŌĆö pyry resolves the socket, registry, and claude sessions dir all under `os.UserHomeDir()`, so `t.TempDir()` as `$HOME` isolates the daemon completely. Belt-and-suspenders `-pyry-socket=<HomeDir>/pyry.sock` flag for the load-bearing path; no new `-pyry-registry` flag needed. `PYRY_NAME` is stripped from the child env so the operator's shell alias can't leak in.
- **Failure-injection verification via test-binary re-exec** ŌĆö `t.Fatal` in a same-process `t.Run` subtest propagates to the parent and ends the test before it can inspect leak state. `TestHarness_NoLeakOnFatal` re-execs `os.Args[0] -test.run=^TestInnerFatalChild$` with `PYRY_E2E_INNER_FATAL_OUT=<state-file>` so the failing path runs in a fresh process; the child writes (pid, socket) before `t.Fatal`; the parent reads the state file and asserts `processAlive(pid)` is false (`os.FindProcess` + `Signal(syscall.Signal(0))`, the POSIX zero-signal probe) and the socket is `fs.ErrNotExist`.
- **No `Option`s yet, no CLI-driver wrappers** ŌĆö `Start(t)` is the only constructor; AC's "or equivalent" parenthetical covers the fail-fast `t.Fatalf` shape. `Harness.Status()`/`Stop()`/`Attach()`/`Run(args...)`, options, the first feature e2e, and CI wiring are deferred to the #51 follow-up. Build-tag isolation means existing `go test ./...` CI keeps passing untouched.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #81)
- **`internal/e2e/install_darwin_test.go` ŌĆö `pyry install-service` ├Ś launchd `gui/<uid>` round-trip on macOS.** Three tests under `//go:build darwin && e2e_install`, mirroring #80's Linux shape: `TestE2EInstall_RoundTrip_macOS` writes the plist via `install.Install` ŌåÆ `launchctl bootstrap gui/<uid>` ŌåÆ `waitForRunning` (polls `launchctl print` for `state = running`, 10s deadline, 100ms gap) ŌåÆ `pyry status -pyry-name=<name>` (asserts exit 0 + `Phase:` in stdout) ŌåÆ `launchctl bootout` ŌåÆ `waitForUnloaded` ŌåÆ cleanup; `TestE2EInstall_PathInheritance_macOS` extracts `EnvironmentVariables.PATH` via `plutil -extract ... raw` and asserts each non-empty `$PATH` entry appears verbatim ŌĆö note **no `$HOME/` ŌåÆ `%h/` substitution** (`derivePathEnv` gates the rewrite on `PlatformSystemd`); `TestE2EInstall_CleanupOnFatal_macOS` re-execs `TestInstallFatalChild` (same name as the Linux file, non-overlapping build tags) which installs + bootstraps + `t.Fatal`s, parent verifies `stat(plistPath)` is `ErrNotExist` and `launchctl print gui/<uid>/<label>` exits non-zero.
- **Same `e2e_install` build tag as the Linux sibling.** Single `go test -tags=e2e_install ./internal/e2e/...` invocation covers both platforms in CI when intended. Default `go test ./...` compiles neither file.
- **Plist parsing via Apple's `plutil`, not Go's `encoding/xml`.** The plist's key/value alternation pattern is awkward to walk with the stdlib XML decoder. `plutil -extract EnvironmentVariables.PATH raw -o - <plist>` returns just the PATH string ŌĆö one shell-out, fails loudly on missing keys, no XML parser. `plutil` is part of `/usr/bin` on macOS; absence is a broken host, not a skip condition. ~30 lines of Go XML walking rejected as anti-simplicity.
- **`launchctl bootstrap` is async ŌĆö poll `launchctl print` for `state = running`.** Bootstrap returns once launchd has *accepted* the request; the job transitions to `state = running` asynchronously. Polling loop is 100ms-gap, 10s-deadline; failure dumps the last `print` output for diagnosis. `launchctl print` is a debug command whose format Apple has reserved the right to reformat ŌĆö `state = running` has been stable since macOS 10.10; if it ever breaks, the test fails loudly with a clear diagnostic.
- **Cannot isolate `$HOME` for the round-trip ŌĆö same shape as Linux.** `launchctl bootstrap gui/<uid>` runs services in the user's GUI domain with `HOME` inherited from the GUI session, not from the test process. Round-trip and cleanup-on-fatal use the operator's real `~/Library/LaunchAgents/`; `PathInheritance` (no launchd dependency) keeps `t.TempDir()` isolation. Cleanup helper is idempotent best-effort (`bootout` + `os.Remove(plist)`) and additionally wipes runtime artefacts: `~/.pyry/<name>` registry dir, `<name>.sock` socket file, and the launchd template's hardcoded `/tmp/pyry.<name>.{out,err}.log` log files (unlike systemd which streams to journald).
- **Skip discipline.** `skipIfNoLaunchctl` (defensive ŌĆö should never fire on macOS), `skipIfRoot` (`gui/<uid>` is non-root only; system-domain bootstrap requires root and is out of scope), `os.UserHomeDir()` failure ŌåÆ `t.Skip` (CI without HOME set).
- **Helper identifiers (`uniqueName`, `fatalNameEnv`, `fatalOutEnv`, `TestInstallFatalChild`) duplicated across the Linux and Darwin files with identical bodies.** The two files have non-overlapping build tags (`linux && e2e_install` vs `darwin && e2e_install`) so they never compile together ŌĆö duplicate identifiers are legal and the simplest path. Names mirror exactly so a reader switching between files relies on muscle memory. Extracting into a third platform-neutral file deferred until a third platform appears.
- **Open question ŌĆö headless macOS CI.** `gui/<uid>` requires a logged-in GUI session for that uid. GitHub `macos-latest` runners do have one; if not, the fallback is `launchctl bootstrap user/<uid>` (background-only domain). Defer until observed on real CI ŌĆö AC specifies `gui/<uid>`.
- See [knowledge/features/install-e2e.md](knowledge/features/install-e2e.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #80)
- **`internal/e2e/install_linux_test.go` ŌĆö `pyry install-service` ├Ś systemd `--user` round-trip on Linux.** Three tests under `//go:build linux && e2e_install`: `TestE2EInstall_RoundTrip_Linux` writes a unit via `install.Install` ŌåÆ `daemon-reload` ŌåÆ `start` ŌåÆ `waitForActive` (10s deadline, 100ms gap) ŌåÆ `pyry status -pyry-name=<name>` (asserts exit 0 + `Phase:` in stdout) ŌåÆ `stop` ŌåÆ `waitForInactive` ŌåÆ cleanup; `TestE2EInstall_PathInheritance_Linux` reads back the rendered unit and asserts each non-empty `$PATH` entry appears in `Environment="PATH=..."` with `$HOME/` ŌåÆ `%h/` substitution (bug-#19 regression guard, no real systemd needed); `TestE2EInstall_CleanupOnFatal_Linux` re-execs `TestInstallFatalChild` which installs + starts + `t.Fatal`s, parent verifies `stat(unitPath)` is `ErrNotExist` and `is-active` is not `"active"` externally ŌĆö same shape as #68's `TestHarness_NoLeakOnFatal`.
- **Tag is `e2e_install`, separate from `e2e`.** Default e2e CI runs (using `e2e`) don't need a running user-systemd. `harness.go`'s build tag widened to `//go:build e2e || e2e_install` so the install tests reuse `ensurePyryBuilt` / `binPath` / `childEnv` without duplicating boilerplate. `runTimeout` (the CLI driver's 10s wrapper budget) is reused for the direct `pyry status` invocation in the round-trip test.
- **`install.Install` called directly, not via the CLI binary.** `install.Install` defaults `Options.Binary` to `os.Executable()` ŌĆö for a test process, that's the test binary. The CLI exposes no `--binary` override; rather than add a hidden `PYRY_INSTALL_BINARY` env-var test seam (the pattern #34/#38/#69 rejected), the tests import `internal/install` and call `install.Install(opts)` with `opts.Binary = bin` set explicitly. The CLI mapping is unit-tested in `install_test.go`; the e2e value here is in the systemd round-trip and the rendered PATH line, not in re-testing flag parsing. `Options.EnvPath` (already exposed for testing) is reused as the path-inheritance test seam ŌĆö no new seam invented.
- **Cannot isolate `$HOME` for the round-trip.** `systemctl --user` runs unit files in the operator's real session, not the test's redirected HOME. The round-trip and cleanup-on-fatal tests use the operator's real `~/.config/systemd/user/`; `PathInheritance` (no systemd dependency) keeps `t.TempDir()` isolation. Mitigations: unique `pyry-e2e-<pid>-<unixnano>` unit names guard collision; `t.Cleanup` registered *before* the state-changing `install.Install` so a failure between there and the end of the test still removes the unit; the cleanup helper is idempotent best-effort (`stop`/`disable`/`remove`/`daemon-reload` each ignore errors and `t.Logf`); also wipes runtime artefacts (`~/.pyry/<name>` registry dir + `<name>.sock` socket file).
- **`pyry status` invoked directly in the round-trip, not via `Harness.Run`.** The harness auto-injects `-pyry-socket=<h.SocketPath>`, but here the systemd-spawned daemon's socket is at `~/.pyry/<name>.sock`, derived by `resolveSocketPath` from `-pyry-name`. Direct `exec.CommandContext(ctx, bin, "status", "-pyry-name="+name)` exercises the same machinery the operator uses on a real install.
- **Skip discipline.** `skipIfNoUserSystemd` checks `systemctl` on PATH, then runs `systemctl --user is-system-running`. Skips on `offline` (no manager) / `unknown` (no D-Bus, the `ubuntu-latest`-runner shape) / empty + non-zero exit. Other non-zero states (`degraded`, `maintenance`, `starting`, `stopping`) are usable ŌĆö proceed. Service accounts may need `loginctl enable-linger <user>` once.
- See [knowledge/features/install-e2e.md](knowledge/features/install-e2e.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #69)
- **`Harness.Run(t, verb, args...) RunResult` CLI driver** ŌĆö invokes the cached pyry binary with `<verb> -pyry-socket=<h.SocketPath> <args...>`, waits for it to exit (10s `context.WithTimeout`), returns `RunResult{ExitCode int, Stdout, Stderr []byte}`. Auto-injects the socket flag after the verb so callers don't thread it through; reuses `binPath` (set by `ensurePyryBuilt` under `sync.Once`) and `childEnv(h.HomeDir)`. Verb is positional because pyry dispatches subcommands on `os.Args[1]` ŌĆö encoding that into the signature prevents the `h.Run(t, "-pyry-socket=other", "status")` footgun. Caller-side override is naturally available via Go `flag`'s "last value wins" rule, no special case in the harness.
- **Failure asymmetry: non-zero exit returned, exec/timeout fatal** ŌĆö `*exec.ExitError` populates `RunResult.ExitCode` for the caller to assert on; non-`ExitError` exec failure (binary missing, fork error) and 10s deadline expiry both `t.Fatalf` because there's no useful test recovery. The 10s wrapper budget is comfortably above `pyry status`'s own 5s socket-dial timeout (`runStatus` ŌåÆ `control.Status`). No regression test for the deadline branch ŌĆö constructing a daemon that hangs `pyry status` for >10s requires real-claude unresponsiveness or test-only socket injection, both more invasive than the safety net buys; per evidence-based fix selection, defer until observed.
- **Struct over tuple for the result type** ŌĆö `RunResult` future-proofs for `Duration`/`Combined`/`OOMed` additions without call-site churn; named fields prevent the `[]byte` mix-up between stdout and stderr that a positional tuple invites. Cost is one type declaration; worth it.
- **`TestStatus_E2E` ŌĆö first feature-flavoured e2e** ŌĆö spawns the daemon, runs `pyry status`, asserts exit 0 + `bytes.Contains(r.Stdout, []byte("Phase:"))`. `"Phase:"` is the leading literal in `runStatus`'s output (`fmt.Printf("Phase:         %s\n", resp.Phase)`) and is stable across phase values, restart counts, and future field additions; asserting on the *value* would couple the test to claude-child startup timing, which is exactly what `/bin/sleep infinity` was chosen to avoid. `pyry version` was rejected as the proof-of-life verb because it short-circuits in `main.go` before parsing flags ŌĆö wouldn't exercise the socket plumbing the harness sells.
- **Package doc updated with copy-pasteable CLI-driver example** ŌĆö replaces the bare smoke pattern from #68; godoc now surfaces a `Start(t) ŌåÆ Run(t, "status") ŌåÆ assert` recipe that downstream session-verb tickets (#52, #54, #55, #56) can copy.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ CLI Driver](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #52)
- **`internal/e2e/cli_verbs_test.go` ŌĆö e2e coverage for the remaining shipped non-interactive verbs.** Four tests under `//go:build e2e`: `TestStop_E2E` spawns the daemon, runs `pyry stop`, asserts exit 0 + `bytes.Contains(r.Stdout, []byte("stop requested"))`, then bounded-polls (3s deadline, 50ms gap) until both `!processAlive(pid)` AND `os.Stat(sock)` returns `fs.ErrNotExist` ŌĆö both conditions in the same iteration so the test doesn't race the supervisor's deferred socket cleanup. `TestStatus_E2E_Stopped` uses `RunBare("status", "-pyry-socket="+bogusSock)` against a fresh `t.TempDir()` non-existent path: exit != 0, non-empty stderr, no `panic` / `goroutine ` / `runtime/` substrings (clean error, not a crash). `TestLogs_E2E` runs `pyry logs` against a healthy daemon and asserts exit 0 + non-empty `bytes.TrimSpace(r.Stdout)` ŌĆö the supervisor's in-memory ring captures startup lines, no specific wording asserted. `TestVersion_E2E` uses `RunBare("version")`: exit 0, output starts with literal `"pyry "` prefix, remaining token non-empty (`dev` in test builds, real version under `-ldflags`).
- **`RunBare(t, args...) RunResult` ŌĆö daemon-free sibling of `Harness.Run`.** Same binary cache (`ensurePyryBuilt`), same `runTimeout` (10s), same exit-code mapping ŌĆö but no daemon spawn, no auto-injected `-pyry-socket`, no `childEnv(h.HomeDir)` HOME redirection. Two motivated cases: verbs that don't touch the socket (`version` short-circuits in `main.go` before flag parsing), and negative tests against a known-bad socket path (avoids the spawn-then-stop-then-race-the-teardown ordering glue). The *only* harness API added in #52 ŌĆö `Harness.Stop()` mid-test, typed `Status()`/`Logs()` wrappers, etc. were explicitly declined to keep the harness surface minimal.
- **Bogus-socket vs. spawn-then-stop for stopped-status.** Spawn-then-stop-then-status needs the test to wait for the daemon to actually shut down (otherwise status hits a still-listening socket and succeeds, defeating the test). That's the same poll loop as `TestStop_E2E`, plus ordering glue, plus a second `Run` call. Bogus-socket exercises the same code path (`net.Dial` fails ŌåÆ error surfaces clean to stderr ŌåÆ non-zero exit) without any timing dependency. Strictly simpler, strictly more deterministic.
- **Negative-assertion vocabulary for "clean error, not a crash".** Three conservative substrings ŌĆö `panic`, `goroutine ` (Go's stack-trace header `goroutine N [state]:`), `runtime/` (Go runtime frames in tracebacks) ŌĆö catch panics and stack traces without coupling to the exact dial-failure wording (today: `pyry: status: ... connect: no such file or directory`; allowed to evolve). Same pattern fits any "verify the failure is clean" assertion across future verbs.
- **File split: `cli_verbs_test.go` vs. appending to `harness_test.go`.** New file. `harness_test.go` is about *harness behaviour* (smoke, no-leak-on-fatal, the canonical `TestStatus_E2E` proof-of-life); `cli_verbs_test.go` is about *CLI surface coverage*. `processAlive` stays in `harness_test.go` and is reused via package scope (no duplication, no move). Build tag identical: `//go:build e2e` (not `e2e_install`).
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~155 LOC across 2 files** (`harness.go`: +42 for `RunBare`; `cli_verbs_test.go`: +112 new file). Default `go test ./...` is unchanged ŌĆö both files are gated by build tags.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ Bare CLI Driver](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #106)
- **`internal/e2e` restart primitive ŌĆö `StartIn` + `Stop`.** `StartIn(t, home)` is the new workhorse: same body as the old `Start`, but uses the caller-supplied directory instead of allocating `t.TempDir()`. `Start(t)` becomes a one-line `return StartIn(t, t.TempDir())` ŌĆö every existing call site unchanged. `Stop(t)` is a public wrapper around the internal `teardown` (name kept private to make the public/private split obvious); `cleanupOnce` (existing `sync.Once`) makes it idempotent with `t.Cleanup` ŌĆö whichever fires first wins, the other is a no-op. Two ~10-line additions in `harness.go`; net public surface grew by exactly two names. No `Options` struct, no "respawn-in-place" method on `Harness` ŌĆö adding either today would be speculative; struct migration is mechanical and non-breaking when a second knob lands.
- **`TestE2E_Restart_PreservesActiveSessions` ŌĆö Phase 1.2's restart-survival proof at the binary boundary.** Pre-writes a registry with two `lifecycle_state: active` entries (one bootstrap, one non-bootstrap, hand-written canonical UUIDv4-shaped strings) ŌåÆ `StartIn` ŌåÆ `Stop` ŌåÆ `StartIn` against the same HOME ŌåÆ asserts `version` field, session count, per-session `lifecycle_state` and `bootstrap` flag preserved. Deliberately *not* asserted: byte-identity of the file (`MarshalIndent` output is allowed to evolve), `LastActiveAt` equality (would couple to today's no-save invariant in a way that breaks the moment a benign state-change ships).
- **Why this works against today's pyry without code changes.** Restart-time path against a pre-populated registry: `loadRegistry` reads ŌåÆ `pickBootstrap` selects the lone `bootstrap: true` entry; non-bootstrap entries are *not* materialised into `Pool.sessions` ŌåÆ `reg != nil` skips the cold-start save ŌåÆ `reconcileBootstrapOnNew` no-ops because `~/.claude/projects/<encoded-cwd>` doesn't exist under the test HOME ŌåÆ bootstrap enters `runActive`, idle timer disabled (`-pyry-idle-timeout=0`) ŌåÆ SIGTERM cancels ctx ŌåÆ `runActive` returns `ctx.Err` *before* `transitionTo(stateEvicted)`, no terminal save fires. Net: nothing in pyry calls `saveLocked` between pre-write and the second `loadRegistry` ŌĆö the on-disk file is byte-stable across the restart. The non-bootstrap entries persist *because pyry doesn't touch them*, not because pyry materialises them. The test locks in the no-save-without-state-change invariant; future tickets that materialise non-bootstrap entries will need to preserve their lifecycle state across restart explicitly, and this test will catch any regression in either direction.
- **`os.MkdirTemp` over `t.TempDir()` for the HOME ŌĆö Unix-socket `sun_path` budget.** `sun_path` caps at 104 bytes on macOS (108 on Linux). `t.TempDir()` embeds the test name into its path; `TestE2E_Restart_PreservesActiveSessions` + `pyry.sock` overflows the macOS budget. `os.MkdirTemp("", "pyry-rs-*")` + `t.Cleanup(os.RemoveAll)` keeps the prefix tiny. Tests with short names are unaffected; only path-budget-tight cases need to switch. See `lessons.md ┬¦ Unix-socket sun_path limits and t.TempDir()`.
- **Same socket path across both spawns is the realistic case.** Both `StartIn` calls derive `socket := filepath.Join(home, "pyry.sock")`. The second daemon's `Server.Listen` handles a stale socket file via dial-probe ŌåÆ ECONNREFUSED ŌåÆ `os.Remove` ŌåÆ `net.Listen`; no test-level coordination needed. By the time `Stop` returns, `cmd.Wait` has reaped the first process and the listener fd is closed; ECONNREFUSED is deterministic. The defensive `os.Remove(h.SocketPath)` in teardown belt-and-suspenders the SIGKILL path. Two harnesses (`h1`, `h2`) own independent `cleanupOnce`/`doneCh`/`cmd`; `t.Cleanup`'s LIFO order means `h2.teardown` fires first against the live second daemon, then `h1.teardown` no-ops.
- **File split: `restart_test.go`, not extending `cli_verbs_test.go`.** The latter is *CLI surface coverage* (one test per shipped verb); this is *daemon-level disk-state survival* and doesn't drive a CLI verb. Mirrors the `harness_test.go` (mechanics) vs. `cli_verbs_test.go` (verb surface) split #52 established. Local `registryFile`/`registryEntry` mirror types are duplicated intentionally ŌĆö `internal/sessions`'s on-disk types are unexported, and exporting them solely for one test would invert the dependency direction. Schema is small and stable; if a field is added, the mirror grows it too.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~184 LOC across 2 files** (`harness.go`: +44 for `StartIn` + `Stop` + package doc; `restart_test.go`: +140 new file). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ Restart Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #107)
- **Two more restart-survival e2e tests on top of #106's `StartIn` + `Stop` primitive ŌĆö no new harness API.** `TestE2E_Restart_PreservesEvictedSessions` pre-writes a registry with a bootstrap-active anchor + a non-bootstrap `lifecycle_state: "evicted"` entry + a non-bootstrap-active control, cycles `StartIn ŌåÆ Stop ŌåÆ StartIn`, and asserts the evicted entry is *still* `"evicted"` on disk after the second daemon is ready (catches silent warm-promotion to active during bootstrap ŌĆö the property `parseLifecycleState` and `pool.New` rely on for #38's warm-start semantics). `TestE2E_Restart_LastActiveAtSurvives` pre-writes three sessions whose `lastActiveAt` values are spread by 10 min and 1 hour, restarts, asserts every value roundtrips via `time.Time.Equal` (catches a re-stamp to `time.Now()` during bootstrap that would silently break the cap-policy LRU order from #41). Both tests scoped to non-bootstrap survival; bootstrap-evicted (warm-starting the bootstrap *itself* in `stateEvicted`) deferred to its own ticket ŌĆö functionally distinct path (`runEvicted` instead of spawning the child).
- **`newRegistryHome(t)` file-local helper ŌĆö rule of three.** With three restart-survival tests sharing the same four-line HOME bootstrap (`os.MkdirTemp` for sun_path safety, `t.Cleanup(RemoveAll)`, `mkdir -p <home>/.pyry/test`), #107 extracted the prefix into a file-local helper and refactored `TestE2E_Restart_PreservesActiveSessions` to call it. Intentionally not promoted to `harness.go`'s public surface ŌĆö three callers ŌēĀ a public API. `registryEntry` / `registryFile` mirror types and `writeRegistry` / `readRegistry` / `mustReadFile` from #106 stay file-local and unchanged.
- **Equality, not byte-identity, for `LastActiveAt`.** `time.Time.Equal` per entry, not byte-equal on the file. `Equal` accepts today's exact roundtrip *and* tolerates a future re-encode through `time.Now().UTC()` (strips monotonic, preserves wall-clock ŌĆö the AC's "tight tolerance"); rejects loudly when the value is re-stamped to `time.Now()` because the 10-min / 1-hour spread dwarfs any plausible JSON-roundtrip drift. Asserting on byte-identity of the file would couple to `MarshalIndent` formatting (brittle); per-field `Equal` is durable.
- **Monotonic-clock trap: capture "want" via the same JSON trip the daemon takes.** `time.Time` written via `MarshalIndent` retains monotonic-clock state in the original Go value but strips it after the JSON unmarshal trip. Comparing pre-write in-memory vs. post-restart parsed would diverge on monotonic alone *even when bytes on disk are identical* ŌĆö masquerading as a real timestamp regression. `TestE2E_Restart_LastActiveAtSurvives` re-reads the file with `readRegistry` immediately after `writeRegistry` and uses *that* parsed value as the expectation. New lessons.md entry: ┬¦ JSON roundtrip strips monotonic-clock state from time.Time.
- **Why this works against today's pyry without code changes ŌĆö same chain as #106.** `loadRegistry` reads ŌåÆ `pickBootstrap` selects bootstrap, non-bootstrap entries not materialised ŌåÆ `reg != nil` skips cold-start save ŌåÆ `reconcileBootstrapOnNew` no-ops (no `~/.claude/projects/<encoded-cwd>` under test HOME) ŌåÆ bootstrap enters its lifecycle goroutine; SIGTERM cancels ctx ŌåÆ goroutine returns `ctx.Err` *before* `transitionTo`, no terminal save. The on-disk bytes for non-bootstrap entries are byte-stable across restart because pyry reads but does not rewrite. The two new tests lock in the no-save-without-state-change invariant alongside #106; future tickets that materialise non-bootstrap entries or re-stamp `lastActiveAt` during bootstrap will have to update production and these tests in lockstep.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~140 LOC, single file** (`internal/e2e/restart_test.go`: helper extraction + two new tests + refactor of the existing test to use the helper). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ Restart Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), `lessons.md ┬¦ JSON roundtrip strips monotonic-clock state from time.Time`.

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #111)
- **`internal/e2e/startup_test.go` ŌĆö `TestE2E_Startup_CorruptRegistryFailsClean`.** Single test under `//go:build e2e`: seeds `<home>/.pyry/test/sessions.json` with `{not valid json` via `newRegistryHome` (reused from `restart_test.go`), calls `StartExpectingFailureIn`, asserts `ExitCode != 0`, `bytes.Contains(res.Stderr, []byte("registry"))`, and `bytes.Equal(diskBytes, corruptBytes)`. The byte-equal assertion is the load-bearing one ŌĆö catches the worst-possible regression ("corrupt file ŌåÆ empty registry ŌåÆ drop everything") without depending on JSON-parsing the corrupt input. Substring `registry` chosen over the absolute path or `sessions.json`: path varies per run and `sessions.json` is just the filename, while "registry" is the operator-facing domain concept; production chain happens to contain it twice (`pool init: sessions: load registry: registry: parse <path>: <unmarshal err>`) so the assertion is robust to wrap-chain refactors.
- **`StartExpectingFailureIn(t, home) RunResult` ŌĆö failed-start sibling of `StartIn`.** The harness extension this ticket adds: spawns pyry against the caller-supplied HOME, expects it to exit before `readyDeadline`, returns the captured `RunResult`. No `Harness` returned ŌĆö there is no live daemon to drive, no socket to clean up. Caller pre-populates HOME (corrupt registry, missing claude binary in future tickets, ŌĆ”) and asserts on the streams. Two defensive `t.Fatalf` branches ŌĆö "daemon unexpectedly came up" and "neither exit nor readiness within `readyDeadline`" ŌĆö fire only on production regression or a hung test environment; both tear the daemon down via `killSpawned` (SIGTERM ŌåÆ `termGrace` ŌåÆ SIGKILL ŌåÆ `killGrace`, mirroring `Harness.teardown`) before failing.
- **Internal refactor: shared `spawn(t, home)` helper.** Extracted from `StartIn`'s body. `spawn` does fork + wait-goroutine + child-env wiring; deliberately does **not** register `t.Cleanup`, build the `Harness`, or call `waitForReady` ŌĆö each caller owns those policies. `StartIn` becomes `spawn` ŌåÆ build `Harness` ŌåÆ register cleanup ŌåÆ `waitForReady`; `StartExpectingFailureIn` becomes `spawn` ŌåÆ select-driven loop over `(net.Dial, doneCh, time.After(readyPollGap))`. Reuses existing `readyDeadline = 5s` and `readyPollGap` constants ŌĆö the corrupt-registry path exits in milliseconds (synchronous JSON parse), so 5s is generous. No new constants.
- **Why an alternate constructor (not Options on `StartIn`).** The ticket forbids "unused API surface" and "parallel implementation". `Options` field on `StartIn` would force a polymorphic return (`*Harness` doesn't fit the failure path); a lower-level public `spawn` helper would be bigger surface than the one test needs; the alternate constructor keeps the surface minimal, mirrors `Run`/`RunBare`, and shares the body via the private `spawn`. `StartExpectingFailure(t)` (zero-arg) declined: the failure path always wants caller-supplied HOME to seed the on-disk failure state, so the no-`In` form would be unused.
- **File split: `startup_test.go`, not extending `restart_test.go`.** Domain is *startup failure*, not *restart survival*. Future failed-start e2e tests (missing claude binary, unreachable workdir, port-in-use socket) have a natural home next to it; `StartExpectingFailureIn` is the primitive they reuse.
- **Coverage of the helper's defensive branches.** Only the success path of `StartExpectingFailureIn` is exercised (child exits before ready). The two `t.Fatalf` branches earn their keep as crash-loud guards, not as covered behaviours ŌĆö per the ticket's "exercised exclusively by this test" constraint, no unit tests added for them. Future failed-start tests provide implicit coverage as they land.
- **Production diff is zero.** The corrupt-registry failure path already exists (`loadRegistry` ŌåÆ `json.Unmarshal` returns `registry: parse %s: %w`; `Pool.New` wraps as `sessions: load registry: ŌĆ”`; `runSupervisor` wraps as `pool init: ŌĆ”`; `main` prints + `os.Exit(1)`). Test diff: ~70 LOC across 2 files (`harness.go`: +60 for `StartExpectingFailureIn` + `spawn` extraction + `killSpawned`; `startup_test.go`: +35 new file). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ Failed-Start Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/features/sessions-registry.md ┬¦ Load semantics](knowledge/features/sessions-registry.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1+ resize seam, ticket #136)
- **`Bridge.Resize(rows, cols uint16) error` + `Bridge.SetPTY(*os.File)` ŌĆö the typed supervisor-side resize seam.** `Bridge` gains a leaf-only `ptyMu` mutex over a per-iteration `*os.File`. `runOnce` calls `SetPTY(ptmx)` after `pty.Start`, then `SetPTY(nil)` **before** `EndIteration` so an in-flight `Resize` racing iteration teardown sees nil rather than a closed fd. `Resize` is a no-op (returns nil) when no PTY is registered (between iterations / foreground mode). `pty.Setsize` errors are wrapped + returned for the caller to log. The seam landed on `*Bridge` (not `*Supervisor` and not a `Run`-wired callback) because the `Session ŌåÆ Bridge` chain already exists for `Attach` and `BeginIteration`/`EndIteration` already brackets every iteration ŌĆö see [ADR 008](knowledge/decisions/008-bridge-resize-seam.md).
- **`Session.Resize(rows, cols uint16) error` ŌĆö one-line delegator.** Returns `ErrAttachUnavailable` when the session has no bridge (foreground mode). No `lcMu` taken, no `lastActiveAt` bump, no interaction with the activeŌåöevicted state machine. Pure pass-through to `Bridge.Resize`, whose own internal mutex handles the iteration-boundary race.
- **`internal/control.Session` interface gains `Resize(rows, cols uint16) error`.** Two implementers updated: `*sessions.Session` (production) and `*fakeSession` (tests). `handleAttach` calls `sess.Resize` between `Activate` and `Attach`, guarded by `payload != nil && payload.Cols > 0 && payload.Rows > 0`; `clampUint16(int) uint16` clamps pathological client sizes silently. The wire's cols-then-rows order is swapped at this single boundary site to match `Bridge.Resize`'s rows-then-cols (which mirrors `pty.Winsize` field order).
- **Resize errors do NOT fail the attach.** `pty.Setsize` failure is logged at Warn and the attach proceeds. Geometry is best-effort; a stale window size is recoverable on the next keystroke. `ErrAttachUnavailable` from a foreground-mode session is also swallowed ŌĆö foreground has its own SIGWINCH watcher in `winsize.go`.
- **Caveats rewritten in `protocol.go` and `supervisor.go`.** `AttachPayload`'s "server discards Cols/Rows" sentence dropped (kept the live-resize / SIGWINCH paragraph, cleared by #137). The Phase-0 caveat at `supervisor.go` lines 248-250 rewritten to reflect the new reality (handshake geometry now applied; live SIGWINCH still belongs to whichever client attaches). `attach_client.go:25-27` caveat untouched (cleared by #133).
- **Test coverage.** Control side: `TestServer_AttachAppliesHandshakeGeometry` + `TestServer_AttachZeroGeometryNoOp` (table-driven over four nil/zero combos) + `TestServer_AttachResizeErrorDoesNotFailAttach` against an extended `fakeSession` recording `resizeCalls`. Supervisor side: `TestBridge_ResizeAppliesToPTY` opens a real `pty.Open()` master/slave pair and asserts `pty.Getsize` reports the new dimensions; `TestBridge_ResizeNoPTYRegistered` and `TestBridge_ResizeAfterClearPTY` cover the silent no-op branches. Sessions package has no new tests ŌĆö `Session.Resize` is a one-line delegator already implicitly covered by the bridge tests + the existing nil-bridge `Attach` test.
- **Production diff ~95 LOC across 5 files** (`internal/supervisor/bridge.go` +30 for `SetPTY`/`Resize` + ptyMu field; `internal/supervisor/supervisor.go` runOnce +5 for `SetPTY`/`SetPTY(nil)` ordering; `internal/sessions/session.go` +15 for `Session.Resize`; `internal/control/server.go` +20 for `Session.Resize` interface method + `handleAttach` resize block + `clampUint16`; `internal/control/protocol.go` caveat rewrite). Test diff ~270 LOC (`bridge_test.go` +66; `attach_test.go` +160; `server_test.go` +33).
- **Stacks under #137 and #133 (both shipped).** The wire-protocol resize message (#137) consumes `Bridge.Resize` for live SIGWINCH propagation; the client-side SIGWINCH emitter (#133, `startWinsizeWatcher`) produces the message. Live-resize loop is closed end-to-end as of #133.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Attach: Handshake Geometry](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [knowledge/decisions/008-bridge-resize-seam.md](knowledge/decisions/008-bridge-resize-seam.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1+ resize wire + applier, ticket #137)
- **`VerbResize` + `ResizePayload` + `handleResize` ŌĆö live SIGWINCH propagation rides a side-channel one-shot conn, not a framed escape in the attach byte stream.** New verb on the JSON protocol; client dials a *fresh* control connection per resize, sends one `Request{Verb:"resize", Resize:&ResizePayload{SessionID, Cols, Rows}}`, reads one `Response{OK:true}` ack, closes ŌĆö same lifecycle as `VerbStatus`/`VerbStop`/`VerbLogs`. Independent of the long-lived attach conn so a malformed resize cannot tear down the attach session ŌĆö the property is **structural** (two `net.Conn`s, two independent handler goroutines), not coded. See [ADR 009](knowledge/decisions/009-resize-wire-shape.md) for the full trade-off matrix vs. framed-escape and against a *persistent* second connection.
- **`handleResize` mirrors `handleAttach`'s handshake-geometry block, minus connection handoff.** Resolve via `s.sessions.ResolveID(payload.SessionID)` ŌåÆ `Lookup` ŌåÆ swap (`rows = clampUint16(payload.Rows)`, `cols = clampUint16(payload.Cols)`) ŌåÆ `sess.Resize(rows, cols)` ŌåÆ encode `OK:true`. Cols-then-rows on the wire (mirroring `AttachPayload`); rows-then-cols at the seam (mirroring `pty.Winsize`); the swap is local to `handleResize`. Zero in either dim is the "don't touch" sentinel ŌĆö same rule as the handshake path.
- **Best-effort posture: OK ack even when the seam errors.** `pty.Setsize` failure is logged at Warn and the client gets `OK: true`. `ErrAttachUnavailable` (foreground session) is silently swallowed ŌĆö foreground has its own SIGWINCH watcher in `winsize.go`. The only error responses are pre-seam routing failures (`payload == nil` ŌåÆ `"resize: missing payload"`; `ResolveID`/`Lookup` errors ŌåÆ `"resize: <err>"`). The client has nothing useful to do with a "resize failed" response ŌĆö the next SIGWINCH will re-emit; the user's terminal already shows the new size locally.
- **Session-must-be-attached is NOT enforced.** A resize can arrive between `pyry attach` and the actual bridge handshake completing, or after a transient detach during a SIGWINCH burst. `Bridge.Resize` already silently no-ops when `ptmx` is nil. Letting the resize through unconditionally is simpler and matches `pty.Setsize`'s own semantics.
- **No new mutexes, channels, or goroutines.** The accept loop's existing one-goroutine-per-conn pattern absorbs resize handlers; each completes in ~1ms (one resolver lookup + one `pty.Setsize`). `Bridge.ptyMu` (#136) serialises concurrent resizes; last-write-wins matches the kernel's `ioctl(TIOCSWINSZ)`.
- **`SendResize(ctx, socketPath, sessionID, cols, rows) error` ŌĆö client helper next to `Status`/`Stop`/`Logs`, reusing `request()`.** A successful return means the server received and dispatched; the seam's own success is best-effort and not visible to the client. Defined here, consumed by #133's SIGWINCH handler in `pyry attach`.
- **Caveat status.** `internal/control/protocol.go` Phase-0 caveat (was lines 49-55) **rewritten** in #137 ŌĆö points to `VerbResize`/`ResizePayload`. The "(deferred to #133)" parenthetical was cleared in #133. `internal/control/attach_client.go:25-27` caveat **rewritten** in #133 (was: "Subsequent live resize events are not propagated in Phase 0 ŌĆö detach and reattach to update.").
- **Test coverage.** `internal/control/resize_test.go` (~290 LOC, single new file) reuses the existing `fakeSession` (already records `resizeCalls` from #136) + `fakeResolver` ŌĆö no test infra changes. Coverage: applies-to-seam end-to-end, table-driven zero-dim no-op (`{0,0}, {0,40}, {120,0}` plus `nil` payload), unknown-session error, seam-error-returns-OK, foreground-session-silent, oversize-dim clamp, `SendResize` round-trip + server-error wire string. The structural "decoding errors do not tear down the attach session" property is intentionally **not** unit-tested ŌĆö falls out of conn independence; documented in `handleResize`'s godoc instead (per CLAUDE.md "evidence-based fix selection").
- **Production diff ~95 LOC across 3 files** (`internal/control/protocol.go` +25 for `VerbResize` + `ResizePayload` + caveat rewrite; `internal/control/server.go` +42 for `handleResize` + dispatch; `internal/control/client.go` +26 for `SendResize`). Test diff ~290 LOC, single new file. No supervisor changes.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Resize: Live Wire Message and Applier](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [knowledge/decisions/009-resize-wire-shape.md](knowledge/decisions/009-resize-wire-shape.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1+ live-resize client trigger, ticket #133)
- **`startWinsizeWatcher` + `readTerminalSize` inside `internal/control/attach_client.go` ŌĆö closes the live-resize loop end-to-end.** `Attach` installs a SIGWINCH watcher *after* the handshake ack succeeds; the watcher converts each `SIGWINCH` into a `SendResize(ctx, socketPath, sessionID, cols, rows)` on a fresh control conn (independent of the long-lived attach conn). With #136 (`Bridge.Resize` seam) and #137 (`VerbResize` wire + server applier) already shipped, the full path is now: terminal resize ŌåÆ kernel SIGWINCH ŌåÆ watcher reads `pty.GetsizeFull(os.Stdin)` ŌåÆ `SendResize` ŌåÆ `handleResize` ŌåÆ `Session.Resize` ŌåÆ `Bridge.Resize` ŌåÆ `pty.Setsize` ŌåÆ child redraws. No more "detach and reattach to update."
- **No new exported type, no new file in `internal/control` for the watcher itself.** `startWinsizeWatcher` is a package-internal helper next to `Attach`; the watcher's lifetime is exactly `Attach`'s stack frame, so a struct receiver would inflate the change for no benefit. The helper takes its dependencies as function parameters (`read terminalSizeReader`, `send func(ctx, cols, rows) error`) ŌĆö keeps `os` and the network out of the watcher body, and lets unit tests inject stubs without a package-level `var` indirection (which would couple test substitution to global state shared with sibling tests).
- **Synchronous teardown is the load-bearing guarantee for AC#3.** `stop` does (1) `signal.Stop(sigCh)` to unsubscribe, (2) `close(done)` to wake the goroutine's `select`, then (3) blocks on `<-gone` until the goroutine has actually exited. No goroutine or signal subscription outlives the `defer stopWinsize()` call site ŌĆö leak-freeness is *structural*, not *eventual*. If `SendResize` is in flight when `stop` fires, `<-gone` waits out the in-flight call: detach cannot race a half-completed resize.
- **No initial-size priming after the handshake.** AC#2 prohibits regressing the handshake `AttachPayload.Cols`/`Rows` path; the first SIGWINCH (or, in the absent-resize case, the next one) covers any change between handshake and first event. Window is microseconds; priming would push a duplicate resize in the steady-state-no-change case for no benefit.
- **`os.Stdin` directly, not a fresh `*os.File` wrapper around `os.Stdin.Fd()`.** Same convention `internal/supervisor/winsize.go` follows for the same reason: a wrapper `*os.File` is finalizable, and finalizer-driven `close(2)` racing a subsequent `open(2)` is the classic fd-reuse race that makes `pty.Setsize` target the wrong file. Lessons.md ┬¦ Closing a fd to interrupt a goroutine's Read requires O_NONBLOCK has the adjacent shape; this case is its read-side cousin.
- **Best-effort posture, no logging.** `SendResize` errors silently dropped via `_ = send(ctx, cols, rows)`; the next SIGWINCH retries. Mirrors `SendResize`'s godoc and `handleResize`'s OK-on-seam-error posture (#137). The watcher logs nothing ŌĆö the package is library-level, and SendResize errors are uninteresting in practice (either "daemon went away" ŌĆö already surfaced by the attach conn dropping ŌĆö or transient hiccup ŌĆö corrected by the next resize).
- **Burst coalescing falls out of the buffered-cap-1 sigCh.** SIGWINCH arrivals during a `SendResize` collapse to one queued event; after `SendResize` returns, the goroutine reads the queued one and emits a *fresh* resize with the current size (re-read at signal time, not stale). Same coalescing shape as `supervisor/winsize.go`. Server-side `Bridge.ptyMu` serialises and last-write-wins matches `ioctl(TIOCSWINSZ)`'s native semantics.
- **Concurrency: three goroutines inside `Attach`, none share state.** Output copier (existing), input pump (calling goroutine, in `copyWithEscape`), and the new watcher. Watcher does NOT touch the attach `conn` ŌĆö each SIGWINCH is its own short-lived dial via `SendResize`. A malformed resize, daemon-side seam error, or transient dial failure lives entirely on the resize conn and never disturbs the byte stream on the attach conn (the property is structural, mirroring #137's design).
- **`defer stopWinsize()` ordering vs. `defer conn.Close()`.** `defer conn.Close()` is registered first (top of `Attach`), `defer stopWinsize()` second (after handshake ack). LIFO: stop the watcher first, then close the conn. Operationally irrelevant since resize uses its own conn anyway, but documents intent.
- **Caveat rewrite.** `internal/control/attach_client.go:25-27` Phase-0 sentence ("Subsequent live resize events are not propagated in Phase 0 ŌĆö detach and reattach to update.") **rewritten** to identify the SIGWINCH watcher as the live producer and `Bridge.Resize` as the seam. `internal/control/protocol.go` line 62 parenthetical updated from "deferred to #133" to point at `startWinsizeWatcher`.
- **Test coverage.** Two tests in new `internal/control/attach_winsize_test.go` (build tag `//go:build unix`, since `syscall.SIGWINCH` is unix-only and the project excludes Windows): `TestStartWinsizeWatcher_SIGWINCHEmitsResize` (hand-rolled `net.Listen` server, stub `read` returns `(120, 40, true)`, `syscall.Kill(syscall.Getpid(), syscall.SIGWINCH)` delivers the signal, server records the decoded `Request{Verb: VerbResize, Resize: &ResizePayload{Cols:120, Rows:40, SessionID:"abc"}}`); `TestStartWinsizeWatcher_StopIsSynchronousAndLeakFree` (50 iterations of start + Kill SIGWINCH + stop + cancel, samples `runtime.NumGoroutine()` before/after with small slack ŌĆö per-iteration leakage would dwarf any noise budget). Both tests run **without** `t.Parallel()`: `syscall.Kill(SIGWINCH)` is process-wide, so any concurrent test subscribing to SIGWINCH would race. Audit confirms no other test in `internal/control` does so today.
- **End-to-end coverage deferred to #126.** The CLI driver (`internal/e2e`) is the right home for full-Attach-with-real-PTY end-to-end resize coverage; #126 is the open ticket.
- **Production diff ~95 LOC across 2 files** (`internal/control/attach_client.go`: +75 for `startWinsizeWatcher` + `readTerminalSize` + `terminalSizeReader` type + `Attach` wiring + caveat rewrite; `internal/control/protocol.go`: -1/+1 line for the parenthetical). Test diff ~125 LOC, single new file.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Resize: Live SIGWINCH Watcher (#133)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #128)
- **`internal/e2e/attach_restart_test.go` ŌĆö `TestE2E_Attach_SurvivesClaudeRestart`.** Drives an attached `pyry attach` client across a forced supervised-claude restart and asserts: pre-restart byte round-trip, two distinct startup-marker PIDs (proves respawn), post-restart byte round-trip within 5s (proves the bridge re-bound to the new PTY), attach client process still alive after the respawn (`select { case <-a.attachDone: t.Fatalf(...); default: }`). Builds on #125's `AttachHarness` with no new harness API; reuses `tinyNonce` and `readUntilContains` verbatim. Build tag `//go:build e2e`; default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- **Architect's spec was billed as test-only; implementation surfaced a real production bug.** The supervisor's bridge input pump (`io.Copy(ptmx, bridge)` over an `io.Pipe`-backed `Bridge.Read`) blocked indefinitely after `cmd.Wait` + `ptmx.Close`, then raced with the *next* iteration's input goroutine for queued attach-client bytes. The leaked goroutine would consume bytes, write them to a closed ptmx, fail, and silently lose them. Symptom against the original code: post-restart `"post-restart-XXXXXXXX\n"` arrived at the test as `"restart-XXXXXXXX\n"` ŌĆö a 5-byte prefix consumed by the leak. **Production fix shipped in this ticket:** `*supervisor.Bridge` rewritten to use `chan []byte` + per-iteration cancel signal (`BeginIteration` / `EndIteration`); `runOnce` brackets the iteration and waits for both `io.Copy` goroutines to drain (was: one-of-two with a 250ms timeout). Net: ~140 production LOC across `bridge.go` (+124) and `supervisor.go:runOnce` (+18). See [ADR 007](knowledge/decisions/007-bridge-iteration-boundaries.md).
- **`TestHelperProcess` `echo` mode extended (#125 sibling) ŌĆö startup marker + two control lines.** On startup emits `PYRY_E2E_STARTED pid=<pid>\n` once before reading any input ŌĆö two distinct PIDs prove the supervisor restarted the helper. `__EXIT__\n` exits non-zero before echoing (drives the supervised crash); `__PID__\n` re-emits the marker without echoing the probe. The probe gates around a subtle race: the *first* startup marker writes before the attach client connects, so the bridge's `Write` discards it (no attached output sink). The probe captures pid1 deterministically once the attach is wired. Body is line-buffered (per-byte scan, `\n`-terminated branch on `string(line)`); preserves byte-exact contract for #125's round-trip test.
- **`-pyry-resume=false` on the attach harness daemon spawn.** `Config.ResumeLast` defaults to true, prepending `--continue` on every respawn after the first. The e2e helper is a Go test binary (`-test.run=TestHelperProcess`); it doesn't recognise `--continue` and exits with a flag-parse error on the first respawn. The fix is a one-line addition in `spawnAttachableDaemon`. #125 and #127 didn't need it because they never restarted the child.
- **`os.MkdirTemp` HOME for sun_path budget ŌĆö three callers now.** `TestE2E_Attach_SurvivesClaudeRestart` is a long test name; `t.TempDir()` would push `<home>/pyry.sock` past macOS's 104-byte limit. `StartAttach` now allocates HOME via `os.MkdirTemp("", "pyry-at-*")` + `t.Cleanup(os.RemoveAll)` ŌĆö third occurrence of the pattern (after #106's restart tests and #123's rotation primitive). Existing `TestE2E_Attach_RoundTripsBytes` and #127's detach test benefit transparently.
- **`readStartupMarker` ŌĆö file-local helper, regex-match shape.** Same caller-side timeout pattern as `readUntilContains` (PTY master fds on darwin reject `SetReadDeadline`, so timeouts run in user space via `time.After`). Reads in a goroutine, accumulates into `seen []byte`, matches `regexp.MustCompile(\`PYRY_E2E_STARTED pid=(\d+)\n\`)`. Reader goroutine left running on timeout is drained by the harness's teardown closing `Master`. ~40 LOC; not lifted to public surface ŌĆö single-file consumer, not yet a pattern.
- **Production diff is NOT zero (this ticket is the exception).** ~140 LOC of supervisor / bridge production code + 5 LOC of `lessons.md`. Test diff: ~190 LOC across `attach_pty.go` (+12), `attach_pty_test.go` (+58), and `attach_restart_test.go` (+123 new file). The fix is the ticket's primary deliverable; the test is what surfaced it and what guarantees it stays fixed.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ Attach Restart Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/decisions/007-bridge-iteration-boundaries.md](knowledge/decisions/007-bridge-iteration-boundaries.md), `lessons.md ┬¦ Bridge input pump must be scoped per-iteration to survive child restart`.

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #120)
- **`internal/e2e/rotation_test.go` ŌĆö `TestE2E_RotationWatcher_DetectsClear`.** Closes the binary-boundary gap on Phase 1.2b-B's live `/clear` rotation watcher (#39). Drives a real `pyry` daemon through one rotation against the real platform probe (`/proc/<pid>/fd` on Linux, `lsof` on macOS) using #122's `fakeclaude` binary via #123's `StartRotation` primitive ŌĆö production code (watcher, real probe, `Pool.RotateID`, `saveLocked`, `reconcileBootstrapOnNew`) exercised exactly as it ships; only the supervised child is replaced. Pre-creates `<initialUUID>.jsonl` in the encoded sessions dir ŌåÆ `StartRotation` (reconcile rotates bootstrap to `initialUUID` synchronously inside `Pool.New`, before the readiness gate) ŌåÆ poll registry until bootstrap id == `initialUUID` (5s deadline, 25ms cadence) ŌåÆ drop trigger ŌåÆ poll until id changes ŌåÆ assert UUIDv4 stem + `lastActiveAt` strictly advances + 200ms-sleep re-read still shows the new id. Build tag `//go:build e2e`; default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- **No harness changes.** All primitives needed already shipped in #122 (fakeclaude binary) and #123 (`StartRotation` + `ClaudeSessionsDir` field + fake-claude env wiring). #120 is a pure consumer ticket ŌĆö single new file, ~155 LOC. The "always split new package + first consumer" pattern (#122 ŌåÆ #123 ŌåÆ #120) keeps each slice's AC count inside budget; the original combined ticket (#55, #119) hit `max_turns` twice.
- **Local one-liner copies of two unexported helpers ŌĆö `encodeWorkdir` and `uuidStemPattern`.** `internal/sessions.encodeWorkdir` (replaces `/` AND `.` with `-` ŌĆö naive `/`ŌåÆ`-` silently looks in the wrong dir; doubled dash for paths under `.pyrycode-worktrees`) and `internal/sessions/rotation.uuidStemPattern` are unexported. The test file copies each verbatim rather than reaching into the package or adding test-only exported accessors. Spec explicitly recommended this; review confirmed it.
- **Pre-create the initial JSONL before `StartRotation`, not from inside fakeclaude.** `reconcileBootstrapOnNew` runs synchronously inside `Pool.New`, before the control socket starts listening. Pre-creating `<initialUUID>.jsonl` makes "registry reflects initialUUID" deterministic by the time `StartRotation` returns; otherwise fakeclaude's first open races pyry startup and reconcile may see an empty dir. fakeclaude opens with `O_APPEND|O_CREATE`, so writing to an already-existing file is harmless.
- **Poll the registry, not the JSONL dir or trigger file.** The registry write is the production-side observable this test exists to verify. `readBootstrapIfPresent` treats "file missing, parse error, no bootstrap entry" as keep-polling (first iteration may fire before `RotateID ŌåÆ saveLocked` produced the file; `saveRegistryLocked`'s temp+rename makes torn reads unreachable in practice). 25ms cadence ├Ś 5s = 200 reads ŌĆö well within budget.
- **AC#3 (`pyry list`) intentionally skipped.** The verb does not exist in `cmd/pyry/main.go` (`pyry sessions list` is tracked in #87 / #88, not yet shipped under that single-word form). Adding it would be a production change forbidden by the ticket. The on-disk registry assertions (AC#1/#2) already exercise every link in the chain end-to-end against the real probe; the control-plane re-check naturally lives in the e2e test for `pyry sessions list` itself once that ships. In-file comment references the architect's spec at `docs/specs/architecture/120-e2e-clear-rotation-watcher.md`.
- **5s deadline = ~10├Ś headroom.** Watcher worst case is `probeRetryDelays {0, 50ms, 200ms}` Ōēł 250ms + fsnotify (<50ms) + `saveLocked` rename (<10ms) + fakeclaude 50ms trigger poll ŌĆö round trip well under 500ms. Same "generous safety net, not steady-state expectation" tradeoff as the rest of the e2e suite.
- **Failure-mode visibility.** Every failure (reconcile misses initial jsonl, watcher misses CREATE, probe path mismatch, `RotateID` errors, fakeclaude misses trigger, stray second rotation) surfaces as a deterministic timeout with the latest registry contents printed via `mustReadFile`. No silent passes possible.
- **Supplements `TestPool_Run_StartsWatcher`; retirement deferred.** The unit test at `internal/sessions/pool_test.go:785` substitutes the real probe with a `dirProbe` test double and has been observed flaky under `-count=N` (2026-05-02). #120 closes the binary-boundary gap; retiring the unit is a follow-up contingent on multiple stable CI invocations of this e2e replacement.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~155 LOC, single new file.** Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ Rotation Watcher Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/features/rotation-watcher.md ┬¦ Testing](knowledge/features/rotation-watcher.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #123)
- **`Harness.StartRotation(t, home, sessionsDir, initialUUID, trigger) *Harness` ŌĆö wires the #122 fake-claude binary as pyry's supervised child.** Builds pyry, builds fakeclaude (`ensureFakeClaudeBuilt` mirrors `ensurePyryBuilt`: `sync.Once` + `os.MkdirTemp`-cached binary, `PYRY_E2E_FAKE_CLAUDE_BIN` short-circuit for CI prebuild), `os.MkdirAll(sessionsDir, 0o700)`, and spawns pyry with `-pyry-claude=<fakeBin>`, `-pyry-workdir=<home>`, and the three `PYRY_FAKE_CLAUDE_*` env vars set on `cmd.Env`. The supervisor inherits them via `os.Environ()` (`internal/supervisor/supervisor.go:234`) and propagates them to the supervised PTY child unchanged ŌĆö no `helperEnv` knob, no supervisor changes. New `Harness.ClaudeSessionsDir` field is populated to `sessionsDir`; left empty for `Start` / `StartIn`. Ten exported names now (was nine). Used today only by `TestE2E_StartRotation_PrimitiveWiresFakeClaude`; the next consumer ticket drives pyry's rotation watcher against this primitive.
- **Internal refactor: `spawn` is now a thin wrapper over a shared `spawnWith(t, home, spawnOpts)` core.** `spawnOpts{claudeBin, claudeArgs, extraEnv, extraFlags}` zero-value reproduces the historical `/bin/sleep 99999` shape, so `spawn(t, home, extraFlags...)` becomes a one-liner; `StartRotation` populates `spawnOpts` to swap in fake-claude + the three env vars. Existing call sites (`StartIn`, `StartExpectingFailureIn`) untouched. `spawnOpts` is unexported ŌĆö generalises cleanly when a third caller appears, without committing to a public-surface shape today. The ticket body offered `spawnRotation` as a sibling alternative; the architect chose `spawnWith` for the shared-core path.
- **`-pyry-workdir=<home>` pinned on the rotation spawn.** Without it, pyry's supervisor inherits the test process's cwd; `home` keeps the test's view of the supervised child's rooted-at directory aligned with pyry's. Flag exists today (`cmd/pyry/main.go:174-180`); no production change.
- **`TestE2E_StartRotation_PrimitiveWiresFakeClaude` ŌĆö primitive-only smoke test, deliberately does NOT touch `internal/sessions/rotation`.** `//go:build e2e` in `internal/e2e/fakeclaude_test.go`. Phases: `StartRotation` ŌåÆ assert `h.ClaudeSessionsDir == sessionsDir` ŌåÆ poll (5s deadline, 50ms gap) for `<sessionsDir>/<initialUUID>.jsonl` ŌåÆ drop trigger via `os.WriteFile(trigger, nil, 0o600)` ŌåÆ poll for a *different* `<uuid>.jsonl` (matching the canonical v4 stem regex) in the same dir ŌåÆ assert `os.Stat(rotated).Size() > 0` (combined with #122's strict close-OLD-before-open-NEW invariant, implies the initial fd is no longer being written). No assertion about pyry's session registry, no `/proc/<pid>/fd` probe, no watcher driving ŌĆö that's the next consumer ticket. When the consumer fails, it fails for one reason at a time.
- **`os.MkdirTemp("", "pyry-fc-*")` over `t.TempDir()` for HOME ŌĆö same `sun_path` budget rationale as the restart tests.** `TestE2E_StartRotation_PrimitiveWiresFakeClaude` is a long test name; `t.TempDir()` would push `<home>/pyry.sock` past macOS's 104-byte limit. `os.MkdirTemp` + `t.Cleanup(os.RemoveAll)` keeps the prefix tiny.
- **Always-split "new package AND its first consumer" pattern continues.** #122 shipped the binary in isolation; #123 wires it into the harness; the rotation-watcher driver test is the next slice. The original combined ticket (#55, then #119) hit AC-count and "and"-in-title red lines on every recovery attempt ŌĆö three split slices keep each AC count inside budget.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~130 LOC across 2 files** (`harness.go`: ~85 for `StartRotation` + `ensureFakeClaudeBuilt` + `spawnWith` extraction + `ClaudeSessionsDir` field; `fakeclaude_test.go`: ~105 new file). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ Rotation Primitive](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/features/fakeclaude-binary.md](knowledge/features/fakeclaude-binary.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #122)
- **`internal/e2e/internal/fakeclaude/main.go` ŌĆö test-only `package main` that mimics claude's on-disk fd behaviour for rotation tests.** Opens `<dir>/<initialUUID>.jsonl` (`O_WRONLY|O_APPEND|O_CREATE 0o600`, `WriteString("{}\n")`, `Sync()`), then polls a trigger file every 50ms. On first appearance: closes the OLD fd, mints `uuidV4()`, opens `<dir>/<newU>.jsonl` (write+fsync), removes the trigger, idles forever. Subsequent triggers ignored via a `rotated bool` guard. SIGTERM kills via Go's runtime default (no signal handler); the OS auto-closes the fd. ~90 LOC, env-only configuration (`PYRY_FAKE_CLAUDE_SESSIONS_DIR` / `_INITIAL_UUID` / `_TRIGGER`) ŌĆö no flags, no stdin. Inline `uuidV4()` mirrors `internal/sessions/id.go` byte-for-byte to avoid pulling production surface into a test binary for one function.
- **Strict close-OLD-before-open-NEW order is the load-bearing invariant.** What makes the *consumer* slice's exact-match probe check (`watcher.go:167`) deterministic: at the instant the watcher's CREATE-driven probe runs, only the new path is on the PID's fd table. If the binary kept both fds open across the rotation, the probe could match either path and the watcher's gate would race. Order enforced by code review of `main.go` (one `f.Close()` line, then one `openSession`); not directly observable from the in-isolation test (would race the 50ms poll).
- **`internal/e2e/internal/fakeclaude/main_test.go` ŌĆö single test, `//go:build e2e`, exercises the binary end-to-end without the harness or pyry.** `go build`s into `t.TempDir()`, `exec`s with the env vars set, polls until the initial JSONL appears (3s deadline), drops the trigger, polls until a fresh `<uuid>.jsonl` appears in the same dir whose stem matches `uuidStemPattern` and isn't the initial UUID, asserts the trigger is gone, sends SIGTERM, asserts `WaitStatus.Signaled() && Signal()==SIGTERM` within 3s. Hermetic ŌĆö no network, no writes outside tmp; defensive `t.Cleanup` SIGKILLs on early-fatal so a leaked process doesn't survive the test holding an fd in the now-deleted tmp dir.
- **`internal/e2e/internal/` nesting visibility-fences the binary** so only e2e-package code can import it. Mostly moot for `package main`, but the path signals intent. The binary itself has **no** build tag ŌĆö a tiny `package main` is essentially free to compile under `./...`, and not gating it means the test (and the next-ticket harness) can `go build` it without `-tags`. The *test* is gated by `e2e` so default `go test ./...` doesn't pay the build cost.
- **Always-split "new package AND its first consumer" pattern.** The harness consumer (`Harness.StartRotation`, `Harness.ClaudeSessionsDir`, `ensureFakeClaudeBuilt`) is the next ticket; the rotation-watcher driver test is the one after that. The original combined ticket (#55, then #119) hit AC-count and "and"-in-title red lines on every recovery attempt. Mirrors the introduce-then-rewire slicing pattern (#28 ŌåÆ #29).
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~215 LOC, two new files** (`main.go` ~90 + `main_test.go` ~125). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/fakeclaude-binary.md](knowledge/features/fakeclaude-binary.md).

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #115)
- **`internal/e2e/idle_test.go` ŌĆö `TestE2E_IdleEviction_EvictsBootstrap` + `TestE2E_IdleEviction_LazyRespawn`.** Two tests under `//go:build e2e` close the binary-boundary gap on Phase 1.2c-A's idle-eviction state machine and lazy respawn (#40). Idle eviction itself is exercised today only by package-level integration tests in `internal/sessions/` against in-process pool primitives ŌĆö neither the assembled `pyry` binary, the real on-disk `sessions.json`, nor the control-plane Activate-before-Attach call are exercised. #115 adds: (1) start pyry with `-pyry-idle-timeout=1s`, poll the registry file for the bootstrap entry's `lifecycle_state == "evicted"`, cross-check via `pyry status` (asserts negation: NOT `Phase: running`); (2) after eviction, dial the control socket directly and issue a raw `VerbAttach` (importing `internal/control`'s public types), assert the session returns to active and the supervisor reaches `Phase: running` while the conn is held open.
- **Variadic `extraFlags ...string` on `spawn` and `StartIn`.** The minimal harness extension AC#4 asks for. The standard flag set is built into a slice, `extraFlags` are appended, then `--` and the claude args. Go's `flag` package is left-to-right last-wins, so a caller passing `-pyry-idle-timeout=1s` overrides the harness default `=0`. Existing call sites (`Start(t)`, `StartIn(t, home)`, three restart tests, the corrupt-registry and missing-projects-dir tests) all unchanged ŌĆö variadic is backwards-compatible at every site. `StartExpectingFailureIn` was deliberately *not* extended (no failed-start test in #115 needs flags; one-line change when one does). No new exported names; net public API delta is zero.
- **Raw `VerbAttach` over `pyry attach` as a subprocess.** Determinism. `pyry attach` enters a stdin-byte loop (`copyWithEscape`) requiring careful pipe management to keep the conn alive while assertions run; closing stdin too early ends the attach before the next idle eviction fires. A `net.Dial("unix", ...)` + `json.NewEncoder.Encode(control.Request{Verb: VerbAttach, Attach: ...})` + `defer conn.Close()` lets the test own the timeline exactly. The control protocol's `Request` / `Response` / `AttachPayload` types are public on `internal/control`; importing them from `internal/e2e` is in-module and intended.
- **Sleep arg flipped from `infinity` ŌåÆ `99999`.** Pre-#115 the harness passed `infinity` to `/bin/sleep`. GNU coreutils accepts it; macOS BSD sleep does not ŌĆö exits immediately with the usage banner. Tests that don't depend on the supervised child surviving (`TestStatus_E2E`, the restart suite, etc.) didn't notice ŌĆö readiness gates on the control socket, not the child. Lazy respawn surfaces it: the test waits for `Phase: running` after a respawn, but if the child exits immediately the supervisor enters perpetual backoff and `Phase: running` is never observed. `99999` (a plain integer in seconds, ~27h) is portable across both Linux GNU sleep and macOS BSD sleep ŌĆö the only argv form that actually works on both. New lessons.md entry: ┬¦ Test helpers across packages, third bullet.
- **Poll registry first, `pyry status` as cross-check.** The registry is the load-bearing AC ("registry state observable"); `pyry status` is the cross-check, asserting *negation* (`!Contains "Phase:         running"`) so the test isn't coupled to which non-running phase shows up (`PhaseStopped` today, sibling tomorrow). The new file-local `waitForBootstrapState` helper polls the registry for `"evicted"` or `"active"` (the active arm tolerates either an empty/missing field ŌĆö today's `omitempty` default ŌĆö or the literal string, decoupling the test from a future toggle that writes the field explicitly).
- **Hold the conn open across the assertion phase.** `handleAttach` writes the OK ack and binds the bridge to the conn; the conn now streams PTY bytes from `/bin/sleep 99999` (which writes nothing) and back. The test never reads after the ack ŌĆö `defer conn.Close()` keeps `attached > 0` so the next idle eviction is deferred while the assertions run; bridge teardown fires server-side on test return.
- **Production diff is zero.** `-pyry-idle-timeout` already existed (`cmd/pyry/main.go:257`); the state machine, persistence, and Activate-before-Attach all shipped in #40. Test diff: ~125 LOC in `idle_test.go` plus the variadic-flags signature change in `harness.go` (~10 LOC). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ Idle-Eviction + Lazy-Respawn Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), [knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md ┬¦ Testing](knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md), `lessons.md ┬¦ Test helpers across packages`.

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #125)
- **`internal/e2e/attach_pty.go` + `attach_pty_test.go` ŌĆö PTY-simulation harness for `pyry attach` + first round-trip-bytes test.** Sibling to the existing daemon `Harness` in the same package and build tag (`e2e || e2e_install` for the harness, `e2e` for the test). New `AttachHarness` struct + `StartAttach(t *testing.T, sessionID string) *AttachHarness` constructor owns three OS resources: (1) a `pyry` daemon spawned in bridge mode whose `-pyry-claude=os.Args[0]` re-execs the e2e test binary as `TestHelperProcess` in echo mode (`GO_TEST_HELPER_PROCESS=1` + `GO_TEST_HELPER_MODE=echo`); (2) a `creack/pty` master/slave pair (`pty.Open` is the skip gate ŌĆö `t.Skip` on failure satisfies AC#5); (3) a `pyry attach` subprocess with `attachCmd.Stdin/Stdout/Stderr = slave` and `SysProcAttr{Setsid: true, Setctty: true}` so the slave is its controlling terminal. `TestE2E_Attach_RoundTripsBytes` writes a nonced payload to `Master`, reads back via `readUntilContains` (5s deadline), pre-payload banner bytes from the attach client are swallowed naturally.
- **Helper "claude" via `TestHelperProcess` re-exec, not a separate binary.** Echo is `term.MakeRaw(0); io.Copy(os.Stdout, os.Stdin)` ŌĆö one line of meaningful work. The test-binary re-exec pattern (already proven in `internal/supervisor/supervisor_test.go`) is the simplest fit: no second binary to build, no second `internal/e2e/internal/<name>` subdir, no `sync.Once` go-build cache to maintain. Coexists with #122's separate `package main` fakeclaude (rotation behaviour requires a stable build target the harness hands to pyry; echo doesn't). The test binary's `os.Args[0]` is unique per test binary ŌĆö patterns can't be shared across packages.
- **ECHO must be killed in the helper itself.** Bridge mode does NOT put the supervisor's PTY into raw mode (verified in `internal/supervisor/supervisor.go:226-268`); kernel line discipline runs with default ECHO on. Without `term.MakeRaw(stdin)` in the helper, the kernel reflects every input byte to the master *before* `io.Copy` runs, and the test sees each byte twice. The attach client's existing `term.MakeRaw(slave)` (`internal/control/attach_client.go:68-74`) silences the slave side; the helper's `term.MakeRaw` silences the supervisor's slave (which is the helper's stdin). Two MakeRaw calls, two distinct line disciplines.
- **Daemon env flows through to the supervised helper.** `supervisor.runOnce` does `cmd.Env = append(os.Environ(), s.cfg.helperEnv...)`, so env vars set on the daemon's `cmd.Env` (`GO_TEST_HELPER_PROCESS=1`, `GO_TEST_HELPER_MODE=echo`) reach the helper unchanged. New `lessons.md` entry pinning this contract.
