- **Setsid + Setctty so the slave becomes the attach client's controlling terminal.** Without these, the attach client inherits the test process's controlling terminal; `IsTerminal(0)` may return true on the slave fd but kernel writes go to the *test's* tty, not the slave. `Setsid` puts the attach client in a fresh session; `Setctty` makes the slave its tty. Now `term.MakeRaw(slave)` runs against the right fd and the round-trip is deterministic.
- **`SetReadDeadline` does not work on PTY masters on darwin.** The runtime poller reports `ErrNoDeadline` for PTY master fds on macOS, so per-read deadlines via `r.SetReadDeadline(time.Time{...})` cannot enforce the test's overall budget. `readUntilContains` enforces the timeout in the *caller* via `select { case <-readCh: ... case <-time.After(...) }` instead, leaving the reader goroutine running on timeout ŌĆö the harness's teardown closes `Master`, which unblocks the `Read` with EOF. New `lessons.md` entry: ┬¦ PTY master fds on darwin do not support SetReadDeadline.
- **Cleanup ordering: master ŌåÆ slave ŌåÆ SIGTERM attach ŌåÆ SIGTERM daemon ŌåÆ socket remove ŌåÆ term.Restore.** The harness's slave fd and the slave fds dup'd into `attachCmd.Stdin/Stdout/Stderr` are independent ŌĆö closing the harness's slave does NOT SIGHUP the attach client. The kill sequence does that explicitly. `killSpawned` from `harness.go` is reused. `term.Restore` on the parent's stdin state is defensive only (no path in this harness mutates it; AC#4 requires the safety net). Idempotent via `sync.Once`.
- **Skip-on-no-PTY at `pty.Open`, not at `IsTerminal(os.Stdin)`.** Some hosts (sandboxed CI, minimal containers) lack a usable `/dev/ptmx`; `pty.Open` exercises that gate directly. GitHub Actions `ubuntu-latest` lacks a *controlling* terminal but `pty.Open` works (see `lessons.md ┬¦ PTY Testing`). Probing before spawning the daemon avoids a spawn-then-skip-then-teardown round-trip.
- **`SocketPath` exposed for follow-up tickets.** Field is public so #127's clean-detach test can drive a second `pyry attach` against an already-bound bridge to assert `ErrBridgeBusy`. The current test attaches to the bootstrap session (`sessionID == ""`) ŌĆö the only session this harness creates. Fresh-session creation deferred until a follow-up needs it.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~351 LOC, two new files** (`attach_pty.go` ~232, `attach_pty_test.go` ~119). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ Attach PTY Harness Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), `lessons.md ┬¦ PTY master fds on darwin do not support SetReadDeadline`, `lessons.md ┬¦ Daemon env flows through to the supervised child via supervisor.runOnce`.

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #127)
- **`internal/e2e/attach_detach_test.go` ŌĆö `TestE2E_Attach_DetachesCleanly` proves the triple invariant of `Ctrl-B d` detach at the binary boundary.** Build tag `e2e`. Builds on #125's `AttachHarness`: writes bytes `0x02 0x64` into the PTY master, then asserts (1) the attach client exits 0 within a 5s deadline, (2) the daemon survives (`pyry status` against the same socket exits 0), (3) the supervised child is still alive (`pyry status` stdout contains the literal `Phase:         running` ŌĆö multi-space gap is significant; mirrors `idle_test.go`).
- **Two new methods on the existing `*AttachHarness` (`internal/e2e/attach_pty.go`, +32 LOC).** No new exported types, no new fields. `WaitDetach(t, timeout) int` blocks on the existing `attachDone` channel (closed by the wait goroutine after `attachCmd.Wait()` returns), reads `attachCmd.ProcessState.ExitCode()`, `t.Fatalf`s on timeout. `AttachHarness.Run(t, verb, args...) RunResult` mirrors `Harness.Run` against the attach harness's own `SocketPath` + `HomeDir`.
- **`runVerb` extracted as the shared body of `Harness.Run` and `AttachHarness.Run` (`internal/e2e/harness.go`, ~12 LOC of motion).** Package-private free function; both methods become 2-line wrappers (`return runVerb(t, h.SocketPath, h.HomeDir, verb, args...)`). `Harness.Run` had no callers outside the harness package, so the rename is private and `gofmt`-clean. Behaviour for existing `Harness.Run` callers is unchanged.
- **Master-drain goroutine in the test, not the harness.** `pyry attach`'s post-detach stderr write (`fmt.Fprintln(os.Stderr, "pyry: detached.")` with `cmd.Stderr = slave`) goes through the kernel PTY into the master buffer; with no consumer the buffer fills and the slave write blocks, so the attach client never returns from `runAttach` and `cmd.Wait()` never fires. The fix is one anonymous goroutine in the test that loops `Master.Read` until EOF (teardown closes Master, Read errors out, goroutine returns). The #125 round-trip test got away without one because `readUntilContains` consumed the master continuously through the assertion phase. Documented in `lessons.md ┬¦ PTY master backpressure stalls slave-side process exit`.
- **Channel close as the happens-before edge for `ProcessState`.** `attachDone` is closed exactly once by the wait goroutine in `StartAttach` (`attach_pty.go:120-124`), after `attachCmd.Wait()` returns. After the receive on `attachDone`, reads of `attachCmd.ProcessState` from the test goroutine see the writes performed by `Wait()` in the closing goroutine ŌĆö no extra locking. Subsequent calls to `WaitDetach` return the same exit code (channel stays closed; ProcessState stays set).
- **Generous 5s timeout is a safety net, not a steady-state expectation.** Steady-state detach is single-digit ms (no I/O between `Ctrl-B d` recognition and process exit). The budget gives 1ŌĆō2 orders of magnitude of headroom; a tight deadline would convert scheduler jitter into intermittent failures without catching real regressions earlier.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~99 LOC across two files** (`attach_detach_test.go` ~55, `attach_pty.go` +32, `harness.go` shared-body refactor ~12). `pyry attach`, `control.Attach`'s prefix-key state machine, and the detach handshake all shipped pre-#127.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ Attach Detach Pattern](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md), `lessons.md ┬¦ PTY master backpressure stalls slave-side process exit`.

### Codebase (test infra, ticket #112)
- **`internal/e2e/startup_test.go` extended with `TestE2E_Startup_MissingClaudeProjectsDir`.** Positive-outcome sibling of #111's corrupt-registry test, same file, opposite verdict. Asserts the binary-boundary contract for the first-run case: a `HOME` whose `.claude/projects/` does not exist must produce a daemon that comes up cleanly, answers `pyry status` with exit 0, and shuts down via `Stop` without error. The `MissingDir` branch in `internal/sessions/pool.go` already swallows `os.Stat` returning `fs.ErrNotExist`; this ticket pins it at the assembled-binary level (was unit-only).
- **No harness changes ŌĆö uses `StartIn` + `os.MkdirTemp`, not `Start(t)`.** `Start(t)` would suffice in principle (a fresh `t.TempDir()` HOME has no `.claude/projects/` by construction). Two reasons to use `StartIn(t, home)` with `os.MkdirTemp("", "pyry-mp-*")` + `t.Cleanup(os.RemoveAll)` instead: (1) `sun_path` budget ŌĆö the long test name overflows macOS's 104-byte socket-path limit when embedded into `t.TempDir()`'s path (same lesson as the restart tests); (2) structural parity with the failed-start sibling next door, which already uses `os.MkdirTemp` for the same reason. Net public API delta: zero.
- **Sanity check on the missing dir before spawning.** Three lines (`os.Stat` + `errors.Is(err, fs.ErrNotExist)`) before `StartIn` to guarantee the test premise: if a future harness change pre-creates `.claude/projects/`, this test fails loudly instead of silently passing on a different code path than the one it claims to cover. Cheap insurance.
- **Explicit `h.Stop(t)` despite `t.Cleanup`.** `StartIn` registers teardown via `t.Cleanup`, which handles process liveness and socket removal. But cleanup runs after the test function returns, so any `t.Logf` about a stuck shutdown gets attributed "after the test." Calling `h.Stop(t)` inside the test body makes "shuts down cleanly" a verdict-bearing step. `cleanupOnce` (existing `sync.Once`) makes this idempotent ŌĆö second fire is a no-op.
- **No log-line assertion on the missing-dir no-op.** Production may or may not log it; either is fine, and tying the test to a specific line would lock production into emitting it. Per ticket guidance, the contract is "comes up, is responsive, shuts down," not "logs X."
- **Why not a table-driven combination with the corrupt-registry test.** The two startup tests assert opposite outcomes (ready+responsive vs. exit-before-ready), use different harness entry points (`StartIn` vs. `StartExpectingFailureIn`), and return different types (`*Harness` vs. `RunResult`). A table that switches on outcome shape is more code than two flat tests. Keep them flat.
- **Production diff is zero. Test diff ~25 LOC, single file** (`internal/e2e/startup_test.go`: one new test). Default `go test ./...` unaffected.
- See [knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md ┬¦ `startup_test.go` ŌĆö `TestE2E_Startup_MissingClaudeProjectsDir`](knowledge/features/e2e-harness.md).

### Codebase (supervisor fix, ticket #78)
- **Foreground-mode stdin reader leak fixed** ŌĆö `runOnce` now opens `/dev/tty` (`os.O_RDONLY|syscall.O_NONBLOCK`) as a side fd for the input bridge instead of reading `os.Stdin`. On child exit, the per-cycle `input.Close()` wakes the in-flight `Read` via the Go runtime poller; the goroutine drains; nothing accumulates on `os.Stdin`'s `fdMutex`. Drain semantics flip from "drain one of two with timeout" to "drain both with timeout"; total worst-case `runOnce` return latency is `2 ├Ś goroutineDrainTimeout` (~200ms). Bridge-mode branch (`Config.Bridge != nil`) is unchanged.
- **`openTTYInput` + `stdinFallback`** ŌĆö unexported, internal to `internal/supervisor`. Fallback path (`stdinFallback{}` ŌĆö `Read` from `os.Stdin`, no-op `Close`) is taken when `/dev/tty` cannot be opened (headless containers, etc.); preserves the legacy leak in that environment by design rather than breaking the process by closing `os.Stdin`. Foreground mode is TTY-only by construction (`term.MakeRaw(stdinFd)` already early-returns on a non-TTY), so the fallback is a defensive seam, not the production path.
- **Why O_NONBLOCK is load-bearing.** Plain `os.OpenFile("/dev/tty", os.O_RDONLY, 0)` produces a blocking fd; `internal/poll.(*FD).Read` calls `syscall.Read` directly and parks in the kernel, where POSIX `close(2)` on another goroutine is a no-op for the in-flight read. With `O_NONBLOCK`, `Read` returns `EAGAIN`, the runtime parks the goroutine on the poller, and `Close` calls `runtime_pollUnblock` to wake it with `os.ErrClosed`. Drop the flag and the leak comes back.
- **Targeted test** ŌĆö `TestSupervisor_Foreground_NoStdinReaderLeak` runs ~3 child-restart cycles and asserts `runtime.NumGoroutine()` does not grow by more than 2; skips with `t.Skipf("no controlling tty: %v", err)` when `/dev/tty` cannot be opened (CI without a TTY). Verified clean under `go test -race -count=20`.
- **Unblocks the flake stack.** The leak was the root cause of `TestPool_ActiveCap_RaceConcurrentActivate` deadlock (#41), `TestPool_Run_StartsWatcher` flake (#39), and `TestPool_New_Reconciles_ColdStart_PicksNewestImmediately` flake (#73). Bridge-mode-fixture migration in session tests is now belt-and-suspenders rather than required.

### Codebase (Phase 1.1e-D, ticket #102)
- **`pyry attach [<id>]` CLI positional + help text** ŌĆö the operator-facing CLI surface for Phase 1.1e multi-session attach. `pyry attach` (no args) is byte-identical to v0.5.x: empty `SessionID` flows through `omitempty` ŌåÆ server's `Pool.ResolveID` resolves to bootstrap. `pyry attach <full-uuid>` and `pyry attach <prefix>` pass the selector verbatim through `AttachPayload.SessionID`; full-UUID and unique-prefix both attach. Ambiguous prefix / unknown id / `ErrBridgeBusy` / daemon-not-running propagate the existing wire-string error to stderr with exit 1; extra positionals (`pyry attach a b`) emit a usage line and `os.Exit(2)`. Closes Phase 1.1e end-to-end CLI surface.
- **`parseClientFlags` returns `rest []string`.** The shared CLI helper now surfaces `fs.Args()` as a third return so `runAttach` can read the post-flag positional. `runStatus` / `runLogs` / `runStop` bind to `_` ŌĆö same silent-ignore-of-stray-positionals behaviour as Phase 0; opportunistic "reject extra args" for sibling verbs intentionally deferred (out of scope per AC).
- **`attachSelectorFromArgs(rest []string) (string, error)` unit-testable seam.** Empty rest ŌåÆ `""`; one arg ŌåÆ verbatim; >1 ŌåÆ `errTooManyAttachArgs`. Lets the table test cover the argument-shape rule without intercepting `os.Exit(2)`. The exit lives inline in `runAttach` ŌĆö matches the file convention that runtime errors return up (exit 1) and usage errors exit directly (exit 2) so the two failure classes stay visually distinct.
- **`control.Attach` extended in place from `(ctx, socketPath, cols, rows)` to `(ctx, socketPath, cols, rows, sessionID)`.** Single external caller ŌĆö adding a sibling `AttachWithID` would split the call surface for no benefit. Empty `sessionID` produces `AttachPayload{Cols, Rows, SessionID:""}` which under `omitempty` (1.1e-C's load-bearing decision) marshals to `{"cols":80,"rows":24}` ŌĆö byte-identical to Phase 0. Pinned by `TestAttach_WireBackCompat_EmptySessionID` from #101.
- **No prefix matching, UUID parsing, or trimming on the client side.** The CLI is transport, not lint. `pyry attach " "` reaches the server's `Pool.ResolveID` which responds `ErrSessionNotFound`. Reviewer regression guard: `grep -rn 'HasPrefix\|uuid.Parse' cmd/pyry/ internal/control/attach_client.go` should be empty.
- **Production diff ~30 LOC across 2 files** (`cmd/pyry/main.go`: helper signature, new `attachSelectorFromArgs`, `runAttach` body, help text; `internal/control/attach_client.go`: signature + payload field). Tests carry the bulk: `args_test.go` extends with `TestParseClientFlags_ReturnsRest`; `internal/control/attach_test.go` gains `TestAttach_PassesSessionID_OnWire` proving no-arg / full-UUID / unique-prefix all reach the server with the expected `AttachPayload.SessionID`.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Attach: CLI Surface](knowledge/features/control-plane.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1e-C, ticket #101)
- **`AttachPayload.SessionID string` (`json:"sessionID,omitempty"`) + `handleAttach` routes via `Pool.ResolveID`** ŌĆö wire + server half of Phase 1.1e multi-session attach. `omitempty` is load-bearing: empty-`SessionID` payloads marshal byte-identically to v0.5.x output (`{"cols":80,"rows":24}`), so a v0.5.x client keeps working against a v0.7.x server during the rollover. `handleAttach` resolves `req.Attach.SessionID` through `Pool.ResolveID` BEFORE any bridge work, then re-fetches the session via `Pool.Lookup`. `nil req.Attach` is treated identically to empty `SessionID` ŌĆö both resolve to bootstrap. CLI surface (`pyry attach <id>`) intentionally deferred to 1.1e-D; the new field is reachable only via hand-crafted JSON or the test harness this slice.
- **`SessionResolver` interface gained `ResolveID(arg string) (sessions.SessionID, error)`.** Three implementations updated with 1-line passthroughs: `cmd/pyry/main.go` `poolResolver`, plus `fakeResolver` and `recordingResolver` in `internal/control/server_test.go`. No other call sites consume `SessionResolver` (verified by grep across `internal/control` and `cmd/pyry`).
- **Two-step ResolveID-then-Lookup, two sequential RLocks.** Honours #66's choice to return `SessionID` (not `*Session`) ŌĆö the second `Lookup` is the lock-clean guard against a session being removed between resolve and use. Race window is microseconds; `Lookup` returns `ErrSessionNotFound`, which encodes to the same `"attach: sessions: session not found"` wire string the resolver itself produces ŌĆö identical operator diagnostic. No new locking; concurrent attaches against different sessions remain fully parallel.
- **Errors encode as `"attach: <err>"` verbatim via `fmt.Sprintf("%v", err)`.** `ErrSessionNotFound` ŌåÆ `"attach: sessions: session not found"`; `ErrAmbiguousSessionID` flows through with its full multi-line `<uuid> (<label>)` match list. Bridge state is **untouched** on the error path ŌĆö `ResolveID` and `Lookup` both return before `conn.SetDeadline(time.Time{})`, before `Activate`, before `Attach`. Asserted in tests via `fakeSession.attachCalls == 0`, not just response-string match. Existing `sessions.ErrAttachUnavailable` mapping (foreground-mode wire string) untouched ŌĆö runs after `Attach`, no collision with the new error encoding.
- **Production diff ~10 LOC across 3 files** (`protocol.go`: one field; `server.go`: interface method + dispatcher pass-through + handler swap; `cmd/pyry/main.go`: 3-line resolver passthrough). Tests carry the bulk: `attach_resolve_test.go` (~400 LOC) covers all five AC cases plus the v0.5.x byte-identical baseline.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Attach: ResolveID-then-Lookup](knowledge/features/control-plane.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1e-A, ticket #66)
- **`Pool.ResolveID(arg string) (SessionID, error)` prefix resolver + `ErrAmbiguousSessionID` sentinel** ŌĆö typed loose-input resolver pairing with `Pool.Lookup` (full id only). Empty arg ŌåÆ bootstrap (same seam as `Lookup("")`); exact full-UUID match short-circuits via single map lookup (no extra scan cost beyond the existing lookup); otherwise `strings.HasPrefix` scan over `p.sessions` collects candidates. Zero matches ŌåÆ `ErrSessionNotFound` (reused); unique ŌåÆ that id; Ōēź2 ŌåÆ `ambiguousError(matches)` returning `fmt.Errorf("%w:\n%s", ErrAmbiguousSessionID, lines)` with each `<uuid> (<label>)` pair on its own line, sorted by `SessionID` asc. The internal seam Phase 1.1e-B's `pyry attach <id>` wire + CLI surface (and any future verb taking a session selector) consumes; 47-B / 48-B may opportunistically refactor onto it when next touched.
- **Sentinel + `fmt.Errorf("%w: ŌĆ”")` over a struct error type.** AC required "no new exported types beyond the new typed error" + "errors.Is matching cheap." Struct error with `Matches []SessionRef` would expose a second exported type and force CLI consumers to type-assert or duplicate the formatting. Sentinel-wrap gives one pointer compare via the wrapped chain and a verbatim-printable message in one syscall ŌĆö strictly simpler under the AC's exported-surface budget.
- **Synthetic `"bootstrap"` substitution mirrored in the formatter.** When the bootstrap entry's on-disk label is empty, the formatter writes `<uuid> (bootstrap)` rather than `<uuid> ()`. Mirrors `Pool.List`'s rule one-for-one ŌĆö divergence would surface as operator confusion (`pyry sessions ls` saying one name, the disambiguation prompt saying another) before it surfaced as a bug report. Same precedent as the `List` substitution: substitute at the read primitive, not at the renderer.
- **Pool.mu (RLock) only; no `Session.lcMu`.** Reads `id` (mutated by `RotateID` under `Pool.mu` write ŌĆö invariant documented at that site) and `label` (mutated by `Pool.Rename` under `Pool.mu` write). Both already in the `Pool.mu`-reader set. `lcState` and `lastActiveAt` are NOT consulted ŌĆö `ResolveID` does not filter by lifecycle state (an evicted session must still be resolvable for `pyry sessions rename <prefix>` / `pyry sessions rm <prefix>`). Lock-order graph (`Pool.capMu ŌåÆ Pool.mu ŌåÆ Session.lcMu`) unchanged.
- **Returns `SessionID`, not `*Session` / `SessionInfo`.** Smallest possible surface, symmetric with the wire/CLI flow: 1.1e-B unmarshals the id, calls `ResolveID`, then routes to `Lookup`/`Activate`/`Remove` with the resolved id. Returning `*Session` would tempt callers to skip the second lookup ŌĆö but the second lookup is the lock-clean way to guard against a session being removed between resolve and use. No CLI policies enforced at this layer (no minimum prefix length, no whitespace trimming) ŌĆö same posture as `Pool.Rename`/`Pool.Create` declining to validate `label`.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md ┬¦ Pool.ResolveID](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1d-A1, ticket #94)
- **`Pool.Remove(ctx context.Context, id SessionID) error` write primitive + `ErrCannotRemoveBootstrap` sentinel** ŌĆö terminates a session's claude process and drops its registry entry. The on-disk JSONL is **not** touched (disposition lands in 64-A2 / #95). Bootstrap is rejected via the new sentinel; unknown ids reuse `ErrSessionNotFound`. The internal seam the future `pyry sessions rm` CLI verb (#65) consumes instead of touching processes or `sessions.json` directly.
- **Delete-then-evict ordering is the load-bearing invariant.** `Pool.mu` covers the in-memory `delete(p.sessions, id)` + `saveLocked()`, then is released **before** calling `sess.Evict(ctx)`. The alternative (holding `Pool.mu` across `Evict`) deadlocks: the lifecycle goroutine's `transitionTo` reacquires `Pool.mu` via `Pool.persist`. Releasing `Pool.mu` after the in-memory delete commits is safe ŌĆö concurrent `Lookup`/`Activate`/`Rename`/`List` callers see the session as gone from that moment on, so no observer can witness a half-removed state and no re-spawn race exists. Same outer-mutex pattern as the cap-policy eviction (#41), here resolved by holding `Pool.mu` only during the cheap mutate phase rather than introducing a new outer lock.
- **Save-failure rollback mirrors `Pool.Rename`.** If `saveLocked` fails after the in-memory delete, restore `p.sessions[id] = sess` before unlocking. Disk and memory remain consistent at every observable point. `saveRegistryLocked`'s temp+rename discipline makes partial writes unreachable; the rollback is belt-and-suspenders for "destination dir vanished" / `ENOSPC`.
- **Termination reuses `Session.Evict`.** `Pool.Remove` does not re-implement SIGTERM/SIGKILL/grace logic ŌĆö `Session.Evict` already drives the supervisor's child via `exec.CommandContext` cancel ŌćÆ SIGKILL ŌćÆ `cmd.Wait` returns. The supervisor today does not have a SIGTERM grace window; SIGKILL is uncatchable, so no fallback path is needed (the AC's "SIGKILL fallback when child ignores SIGTERM" maps to "the existing kill-on-cancel terminates uncooperative children deterministically", verified in `TestPool_Remove_TerminatesUncooperativeChild` with a `trap "" TERM INT HUP; sleep 86400` shell child).
- **Lifecycle goroutine survives until pool shutdown.** After `Pool.Remove` returns, `sess.Run`'s loop transitions to `runEvicted` and parks on `activateCh` / `ctx.Done()`. The session is no longer reachable via `Pool.sessions`, so no caller can signal `activateCh`; the goroutine survives until `Pool.Run`'s `runCtx` cancels at pool shutdown. Bounded resource cost (one orphan goroutine + ~1KB `*Session` per `Remove` per pool lifetime) ŌĆö operationally invisible for pyrycode's expected workload. Per evidence-based fix selection, no per-session terminate signal until observed.
- **No `Session.lcMu` taken; lock order unchanged.** `Pool.Remove` does not read `lcState` / `lastActiveAt` / `attached`. Lock-order graph (`Pool.capMu ŌåÆ Pool.mu ŌåÆ Session.lcMu`) is unchanged. Empty-id is *not* the bootstrap shorthand it is in `Pool.Lookup` ŌĆö empty falls through to "not in map" and returns `ErrSessionNotFound`; destructive operations require an explicit id.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md ┬¦ Pool.Remove](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1d-A2, ticket #95)
- **`Pool.Remove` signature evolves to `(ctx, id, opts RemoveOptions) error` + `JSONLPolicy` enum** (`JSONLLeave` / `JSONLArchive` / `JSONLPurge`). Zero-value `RemoveOptions{}` preserves 1.1d-A1 behaviour byte-for-byte (JSONL untouched). `JSONLArchive` moves the live JSONL into `<pyry-data-dir>/archived-sessions/<uuid>.jsonl` (data-dir = parent of `registryPath`; subdir auto-created; errors wrapping `fs.ErrExist` if destination exists; source-absent is a no-op). `JSONLPurge` deletes the JSONL (source-absent is a no-op). The internal seam the future `pyry sessions rm --archive` / `--purge` CLI surface (#65) consumes.
- **Disposition runs under `Pool.mu` after `saveLocked`.** Single critical section, single observable transition: a concurrent `Pool.List` either sees the session present (registry + JSONL both untouched) or absent (registry + JSONL both at their final state). The held-lock window grows by one stat + one rename or unlink ŌĆö well inside the existing `saveLocked` envelope. Failure ordering: on `saveLocked` failure the in-memory delete rolls back and the JSONL is untouched; on disposition failure the registry is already committed and `Session.Evict` *still* runs (the registry says the session is gone, the child must follow), with the disposition error returned to the caller ŌĆö disposition error wins over Evict error.
- **Enum (not two booleans) and options struct (not a positional policy parameter).** The enum makes "exactly one disposition" type-level (zero value well-defined as Leave, switch is exhaustive, no representable-but-illegal `(true, true)`). The struct keeps future fields (`Force`, `Reason`, ŌĆ”) additive at zero call-site churn.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md ┬¦ Pool.Remove JSONL disposition](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1b-B1, ticket #87)
- **`VerbSessionsList` + `Lister` seam in `internal/control` ŌĆö wire-only addition that completes the fourth `sessions.*` namespace member and the first read-side member.** New verb `"sessions.list"`; the verb carries **no request payload** (`Request.Sessions` stays nil), so `SessionsPayload` gains no new field ŌĆö the verb name alone is the dispatch token. Server adds `handleSessionsList`; client `SessionsList(ctx, sock) ([]SessionInfo, error)` mirrors `SessionsRename`'s shape using the `request()` helper. CLI subcommand (`pyry sessions list`) is sibling ticket 61-B; the wire surface is reachable today only via the typed client.
- **`Lister { List() []sessions.SessionInfo }` is the fourth sub-interface embedded into `Sessioner` ŌĆö `NewServer` signature unchanged.** `*sessions.Pool` already satisfies the embedded shape via `Pool.List` (#60) ŌĆö no adapter, no `cmd/pyry/main.go` change. Continues the post-#98/#90 pattern: one named per-verb sub-interface embedded into the aggregate `Sessioner` facade rather than a new constructor parameter. `Lister` does NOT take `context.Context` ŌĆö `Pool.List`'s signature is `() []SessionInfo` and the operation is bounded by `Pool.mu` (RLock) + each `Session.lcMu` briefly; mirroring that shape keeps satisfaction adapter-free (same rationale as `Renamer` in #90).
- **New wire-level `Response.SessionsList *SessionsListPayload` (omitempty) + new wire-level `SessionInfo` struct in `protocol.go`.** `SessionInfo` is defined alongside the verbs rather than re-exporting `sessions.SessionInfo` so external Go callers / future hand-written wire clients don't transitively import `internal/sessions` for the package-private `lifecycleState` enum. Fields: `ID string`, `Label string`, `State string` (`"active"` / `"evicted"`), `LastActive time.Time` (RFC3339Nano on the wire), `Bootstrap bool` (omitempty). `protocol.go` import set gains stdlib `time` only ŌĆö the "import-free by design" rule from the wire-enums lesson is specifically about not dragging in `internal/sessions`; `time` is fine.
- **No new `ErrorCode` constants.** `Pool.List` does not return errors. The seam's only failure path is the nil-sessioner branch (`"sessions.list: no sessioner configured"`); the typed-sentinel envelope #98 introduced is unused on this verb. The empty-response client guard returns `"control: empty sessions.list response"` for symmetry with `SessionsNew`'s empty-result branch.
- **`State` encoded as a self-documenting string via `lifecycleState.String()` ŌĆö the same encoding the on-disk registry uses, so wire and registry agree on token spelling without a parallel translation table.** `parseLifecycleState` (the inverse) is NOT exported on the wire; the CLI consumes the string verbatim for display. The translation site is the seam (`handleSessionsList`), not the renderer ŌĆö the future 61-B renderer receives wire-level types and does not import `internal/sessions`.
- **`LastActive` encoded as `time.Time`, not a pre-formatted string.** Distinct from `StatusPayload`'s pre-formatted "310ms"/"1.5s" durations, which are display-only. `LastActive` is data 61-B's renderer does math on (relative-time formatting needs `time.Now().Sub(...)`); going string would force every consumer to re-parse RFC3339Nano. Marshal/unmarshal via `encoding/json` produces RFC3339Nano on the wire ŌĆö jq-debuggable, byte-stable. Tests that round-trip `LastActive` MUST use `time.Equal` (not `==` or `reflect.DeepEqual`) per the existing monotonic-clock-stripping lesson.
- **Sort order: pass-through.** The seam returns whatever order `Pool.List` returned (LastActiveAt desc, SessionID asc tiebreak). Final user-facing ordering is 61-B's responsibility; this layer does not re-sort ŌĆö `TestServer_SessionsList_PreservesPoolOrder` pins the contract by feeding the fake a deliberately out-of-order slice and asserting the wire response preserves it verbatim.
- **Backward-compat: `sessions.new` / `sessions.rm` / `sessions.rename` byte-identical post-`SessionsList` field addition.** `TestProtocol_SessionsRoundTripBackCompat` extended from a Request-only table into a (Request | Response) table covering `Response{}`, `Response{OK: true}`, and `Response{SessionsNew: &SessionsNewResult{SessionID: "abc"}}` ŌĆö the new omitempty `SessionsList` field's tag is the load-bearing invariant under test. The existing Request rows assert the no-payload-for-`sessions.list` shape is byte-stable.
- **Test coverage in `sessions_list_test.go` (~458 LOC).** `fakeSessioner` (in `sessions_new_test.go`) gained a `List` method on the existing struct + a FIFO of canned snapshots + a call counter ŌĆö no new fake type. Mandatory tests: success (full round-trip with `time.Equal` on `LastActive`); preserves-pool-order (asserts pass-through); nil-Sessioner branch; empty-state (zero entries decode to non-nil empty slice, no error); state encoding (`stateActive` ŌåÆ `"active"`, `stateEvicted` ŌåÆ `"evicted"`); bootstrap omitempty pinning at the marshal layer; extended back-compat byte-equality table; client wire shape (hand-rolled `net.Listen` captures `{"verb":"sessions.list"}\n` exactly ŌĆö no `Sessions` payload); empty-response-as-error; server-error verbatim propagation.
- **Production diff ~170 LOC across 3 files** (`internal/control/protocol.go`: +61 for `VerbSessionsList` + `SessionsListPayload` + wire-level `SessionInfo` + `Response.SessionsList` + stdlib `time` import; `internal/control/server.go`: +78 for `Lister` + `Sessioner` embed + dispatch + `handleSessionsList`; `internal/control/client.go`: +31 for `SessionsList`). Test diff ~500 LOC. CLI surface unchanged; runtime wiring is implicit because `*sessions.Pool` already satisfied the extended `Sessioner` (Pool.List shipped in #60).
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Sessions: list seam (1.1b-B1)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/87-control-sessions-list.md`](specs/architecture/87-control-sessions-list.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1c-B1, ticket #90)
- **`VerbSessionsRename` + `Renamer` seam in `internal/control` ŌĆö wire-only addition that completes the third `sessions.*` namespace member.** New verb `"sessions.rename"`; `SessionsPayload` extended with one further `omitempty` field `NewLabel` (existing `sessions.new` and `sessions.rm` requests stay byte-identical, pinned by extending `TestProtocol_SessionsRoundTripBackCompat` with a `sessions.rm` row). Server adds `handleSessionsRename`; client `SessionsRename(ctx, sock, id, newLabel) error` mirrors `SessionsRm`'s shape using the `request()` helper. CLI subcommand (`pyry sessions rename`) is a sibling ticket (63-B2); the wire surface is reachable today only via the typed client.
- **`Renamer { Rename(id sessions.SessionID, newLabel string) error }` is the third sub-interface embedded into `Sessioner` ŌĆö `NewServer` signature unchanged.** `*sessions.Pool` already satisfies the embedded shape via `Pool.Rename` (#62) ŌĆö no adapter, no `cmd/pyry/main.go` change. Continues the post-#98 pattern: one named per-verb sub-interface embedded into the aggregate `Sessioner` facade rather than a new constructor parameter.
- **`Renamer` does NOT take `context.Context`.** `Pool.Rename`'s signature is `(id, newLabel) error` (no ctx ŌĆö the operation is bounded by a single `Pool.mu` critical section + `saveLocked`). Three options were weighed (seam takes ctx and discards; seam takes ctx with 30s `WithTimeout` and discards; seam mirrors `Pool.Rename`); option three was chosen to keep satisfaction adapter-free and avoid lying about cancellability. `handleSessionsRename` correspondingly skips the 30s `context.WithTimeout` that `handleSessionsNew` / `handleSessionsRm` use; the conn's existing 5s `handshakeTimeout` covers the realistic blocking budget.
- **No new `ErrorCode` constants.** `Pool.Rename`'s only typed sentinel is `ErrSessionNotFound`, already pinned to `ErrCodeSessionNotFound` by #98. The `Response.ErrorCode` envelope and the token are reused verbatim ŌĆö the intended dividend of #98's wire-error infrastructure landing first.
- **Empty `NewLabel` is forwarded unchanged (clears the label).** Empty `NewLabel` serialises absent (omitempty), the server decodes it as the zero value `""`, and `Pool.Rename` treats `""` as "clear the on-disk label" per #62. No special-casing at any layer. Distinct from `Label` (used by `sessions.new`) at the field level: empty-string semantics differ per verb (sessions.new `""` ŌåÆ store empty, let `List` synthesize "bootstrap"; sessions.rename `""` ŌåÆ deliberate write of empty over a previously non-empty value), and the verb-family-payload pattern keeps per-verb intent explicit at every reading site.
- **Empty `ID` rejected at the handler boundary.** Server-side guard returns `"sessions.rename: missing id"` (no `ErrorCode`). Mirrors `handleSessionsRm`'s missing-ID guard for consistency ŌĆö passing `""` through to `Pool.Rename` would also work but produces the wrong `ErrorCode` (an empty ID is a malformed-input condition, not a "not found" condition).
- **Test coverage in `sessions_rename_test.go` (~280 LOC).** `fakeSessioner` (in `sessions_new_test.go`) gained one `Rename` method on the existing struct + a `recordedRenames()` helper ŌĆö no new fake type. Mandatory tests: byte-equality back-compat (extended `TestProtocol_SessionsRoundTripBackCompat` with a `sessions.rm` row to assert the new `NewLabel` omitempty tag holds); success path; empty-`NewLabel` forwarding (verifies `""` is forwarded unchanged through wire's omitempty + handler's no-guard path); typed `ErrSessionNotFound` round-trip (asserts `errors.Is` against the bare sentinel); other-pool-error untyped path (`errors.Is` against the typed sentinel returns false); nil-Sessioner branch; missing-ID guard (zero `Rename` calls on fake); wire shape (hand-rolled `net.Listen` captures the JSON line for two `(id, newLabel)` cases including empty-label omitempty); empty-response-as-error.
- **Production diff ~135 LOC across 3 files** (`internal/control/protocol.go`: +27 for `VerbSessionsRename` + `SessionsPayload.NewLabel`; `internal/control/server.go`: +76 for `Renamer` + `Sessioner` embed + dispatch + `handleSessionsRename`; `internal/control/client.go`: +32 for `SessionsRename`). Test diff ~313 LOC. CLI surface unchanged.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Sessions: rename seam (1.1c-B1)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/90-control-sessions-rename.md`](specs/architecture/90-control-sessions-rename.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1c-B2a, ticket #92)
- **`pyry sessions rename <id> <new-label>` CLI verb shipped (full UUID only).** Adds one `case "rename":` to `runSessions`, bumps `sessionsVerbList` from `"new, rm"` to `"new, rm, rename"`, updates `printHelp`'s sessions line and the top-level reserved-verb comment to match. Two new helpers in `cmd/pyry/main.go`: `parseSessionsRenameArgs` (flag-parse + arity, two positionals; mirrors `parseSessionsNewArgs`/`parseSessionsRmArgs`) and `runSessionsRename` (parse ŌåÆ `control.SessionsRename`, single typed-error branch). Consumes #90's `sessions.rename` wire and `Renamer` seam; plugs into #76's `runSessions` router. ~73 LOC production, ~72 LOC unit tests, ~163 LOC e2e.
- **The simplest `runSessions<Verb>` so far ŌĆö no prefix resolution in this slice.** `<id>` is forwarded verbatim to `control.SessionsRename`; AC#4 explicitly forbids prefix support. Non-UUID input falls through to the server's `ErrSessionNotFound` mapping. Rationale: the CLI-side prefix helper (`resolveSessionIDViaList` in #99) is currently a single-caller helper; adding rename as a second caller doesn't yet meet the "rule of three" extraction threshold. The follow-up ergonomic slice (sibling of #99's prefix slot) lifts the helper into shared code when the third caller (`pyry attach <id>` in 1.1e) arrives.
- **One typed-sentinel branch only ŌĆö no bootstrap-rejection.** `Pool.Rename` (#62) has no bootstrap special-case (renaming the bootstrap is allowed and useful ŌĆö operators may want to rename it to e.g. "primary"). #90's wire surface only propagates `ErrCodeSessionNotFound` for rename. The matched case prints `no session with id "<id>"` to stderr (no `pyry:` prefix) and `os.Exit(1)`; everything else flows through `fmt.Errorf("sessions rename: %w", err)` to main's top-level `pyry: ` printer. The `<id>` echoed in the message is the operator's input (today identical to canonical UUID; preserves message format when prefix resolution arrives).
- **Empty `<new-label>` is a valid value, not an arity hole.** `parseSessionsRenameArgs` checks `fs.NArg() == 2` (positional count), not "two non-empty values" ŌĆö so `pyry sessions rename <uuid> ""` parses as `(uuid, "")` and forwards through. `Pool.Rename` treats `""` as "clear the on-disk label" per #62. AC#1 explicitly requires this; no separate `--clear` flag.
- **Exactly 2 positionals (not "Ōēź2"); two-arg shape over `--name` flag.** Three or more positionals is rejected as a usage error so multi-word labels must be quoted: `pyry sessions rename <uuid> "hello world"`. Same shape as `git config` / `kubectl label`; prevents silent token loss like `pyry sessions rename <uuid> hello world` discarding `world`. `<old> <new>` mirrors `git mv` / `kubectl rename`; reusing `--name` (the create-time label flag on `pyry sessions new`) on rename would conflate two distinct semantics across verbs.
- **One `errSessionsRenameUsage` sentinel covers every parse-time failure.** Mirrors `errSessionsRmUsage`'s shape exactly. `runSessionsRename` matches with `errors.Is`, exits 2, prints `pyry sessions rename: <wrapped-msg>`. The FlagSet has no flags today ŌĆö exists for symmetry with `new` and `rm` so a future flag slots in mechanically.
- **No new ADR ŌĆö design follows #99's verbatim conventions.** Per-verb `flag.NewFlagSet`, usage-sentinel ŌåÆ exit 2, typed-sentinel ŌåÆ AC-prescribed plain-message + exit 1, other errors flow through `fmt.Errorf("sessions <verb>: %w", err)`.
- **Test coverage spans `cmd/pyry/sessions_test.go` (extended) + `internal/e2e/sessions_rename_test.go` (new file).** Unit: `TestParseSessionsRenameArgs` table covers no-args, only-`<id>`, `<id> <label>`, `<id> ""` (empty-label clear), trailing positional (rejected), label-with-embedded-space (single token ŌĆö passes), unknown flag. `TestRunSessions_RenameDispatch` pins router wiring against a bogus socket. E2E: five tests covering happy-path rename, empty-label clear, unknown UUID typed-error mapping, no-daemon dial failure, wrong-arity exit-2.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ `runSessionsRename` handler (1.1c-B2a ŌåÆ -B2b)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/92-cli-sessions-rename.md`](specs/architecture/92-cli-sessions-rename.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1c-B2b, ticket #93)
- **`pyry sessions rename <id> <new-label>` lifts to UUID-or-prefix.** Surgical edit to `runSessionsRename` (`cmd/pyry/main.go`): one call to `resolveSessionIDViaList` (the helper #99 introduced for `rm`) inserted above the wire call, plus a parallel `errors.Is(err, errAmbiguousPrefix)` branch in the existing error switch. The handler is now line-for-line `runSessionsRm`'s shape minus the bootstrap-rejection branch (renaming bootstrap is allowed per #62). No new helper, no new sentinel, no wire work ŌĆö `resolveSessionIDViaList` and `errAmbiguousPrefix` already exist because #99 shipped first.
- **The wire receives the canonical UUID; stderr echoes the operator's typed `<id>`.** `control.SessionsRename` is called with the resolver's output; the not-found / ambiguous / race-window stderr lines all use the original input string so `pyry sessions rename ab1 ŌĆ”` doesn't surprise the operator with an expanded `ab1c2d34-ŌĆ”` in the failure message. Same shape as `runSessionsRm`.
- **Two `ErrSessionNotFound` paths collapse to one stderr line.** Resolver-side (prefix matched nothing) and wire-side (TOCTOU: resolver matched, then concurrent `rm` landed before our rename) both render `no session with id "<input>"` + exit 1. Distinguishing them buys nothing operationally ŌĆö the operator's reaction is identical.
- **Confirms ADR 011's helper shape.** Caller #2 needed zero changes to `resolveSessionIDViaList`; the helper's exact-match-first / `strings.HasPrefix` / `errAmbiguousPrefix` contract scaled as-is. Lift to `internal/sessions` still defers to caller #3 (Phase 1.1e `attach`) ŌĆö the trigger remains "third caller", not "second confirms the shape."
- **Test coverage: `internal/e2e/sessions_rename_test.go` extended with two new e2e tests.** `TestSessionsRename_E2E_Success_Prefix` (rename via first 8 hex chars; the canonical-UUID forwarding is implicitly pinned end-to-end ŌĆö a wrong forward would surface as the wire's `ErrSessionNotFound`). `TestSessionsRename_E2E_AmbiguousPrefix` (mints sessions until pigeonhole-collision on first hex char, asserts non-zero exit + both matched ids+labels in stderr + **both sessions' on-disk labels unchanged** ŌĆö load-bearing AC#2 check that the resolver bails before any wire mutation; pigeonhole bound 17 over 16 hex digits, mirrored from `TestSessionsRm_E2E_AmbiguousPrefix`). Existing `TestSessionsRename_E2E_UnknownUUID` now traverses the resolver-side `ErrSessionNotFound` arm without test edits (input is a syntactically-valid UUID; resolver finds no match in a freshly-bootstrapped registry; same stderr fragment, same exit code).
- **No unit-test edits.** The parser is untouched (`TestParseSessionsRenameArgs` still passes verbatim) and `TestRunSessions_RenameDispatch` still pins the router wiring ŌĆö the resolver step happens after dispatch, doesn't change the dispatch-test's assertion. The resolver itself is unit-tested in #99's coverage; the dispatch test is the unit-level responsibility of `cmd/pyry/sessions_test.go`.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ `runSessionsRename` handler (1.1c-B2a ŌåÆ -B2b)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [ADR 011](knowledge/decisions/011-cli-prefix-resolution.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1d-B2, ticket #99)
- **`pyry sessions rm [--archive|--purge] <id>` CLI verb shipped.** Adds one `case "rm":` to `runSessions` (the #76 router), bumps `sessionsVerbList` from `"new"` to `"new, rm"`, updates `printHelp`'s sessions line to match. Three new helpers in `cmd/pyry/main.go`: `parseSessionsRmArgs` (flag-parse + arity, mirroring `parseSessionsNewArgs`), `resolveSessionIDViaList` (client-side prefix resolution via `control.SessionsList`), `runSessionsRm` (parse ŌåÆ resolve ŌåÆ `control.SessionsRm`, with AC-prescribed error messages on stderr + matching exit codes).
- **Prefix resolution is client-side (no new wire verb).** Architectural choice: extending the `sessions.rm` wire to accept prefixes would require a third `ErrorCode` (`ErrCodeAmbiguous`) plus a way to ship the match list over JSON. Reusing `sessions.list` (already shipped via #87) costs one extra round-trip per `rm` invocation ŌĆö negligible at Phase 1.1's expected pool size ŌĆö and keeps the wire surface stable. `resolveSessionIDViaList` mirrors `Pool.ResolveID`'s resolution order (exact match wins; otherwise `strings.HasPrefix` scan; zero/one/many ŌåÆ `ErrSessionNotFound`/canonical-id/`errAmbiguousPrefix`) so server-side and client-side resolution behave identically. The first of two/three CLI callers; per the ticket body, the shared-helper extraction defers to Phase 1.1e (`#49 attach refactor`) ŌĆö a third caller arriving turns "now opportunistic" into "now warranted".
- **AC-prescribed messages are printed via `fmt.Fprintln(os.Stderr, ...)` + `os.Exit(1)`, NOT returned through `main`'s `pyry: ` outer-error printer.** Three named-error cases (ambiguous prefix, unknown UUID, bootstrap rejection) emit plain text without the `pyry:` prefix; other errors flow through `fmt.Errorf("sessions rm: %w", err)` which `main` prepends with `pyry: `. The `runAttach` precedent uses the same shape for its exit-2 path. `os.Exit` skips the `defer cancel()` on the 30s timeout context, but the only state involved is a process-local timer reaped on exit ŌĆö no socket / file / goroutine leaks.
- **One `errSessionsRmUsage` sentinel covers every parse-time failure.** Mutually-exclusive flags, wrong arity, `flag.Parse` errors all wrap this sentinel via `fmt.Errorf("%w: ...", errSessionsRmUsage, ...)`. `runSessionsRm` matches with `errors.Is` and exits 2 + prints `pyry sessions rm: <wrapped-msg>`. The architect considered one-vs-two sentinels; one wrapper is sufficient because every error path out of the parser is, definitionally, a usage error.
- **Race window is documented but not retried.** Resolve-then-rm has a TOCTOU gap where another caller may remove the session between our `SessionsList` and `SessionsRm`. The wire returns `ErrSessionNotFound` from the second step; the CLI surfaces the *original typed `<id>`* (the operator's input string, possibly a prefix) rather than the canonical UUID ŌĆö preserves debugging context.
- **Test coverage spans `cmd/pyry/sessions_test.go` (extended) + `internal/e2e/sessions_rm_test.go` (new).** Unit: `TestParseSessionsRmArgs` table covers no-args, only-flags, id-only, `--archive` / `--purge`, both-flags-set (mutually exclusive), trailing positional, flag-after-positional (Go's `flag` halts at the first positional), unknown flag. `TestRunSessions_RmDispatch` pins the router wiring against a bogus socket. E2E: nine tests under build tag `e2e` covering happy path (default / prefix / `--archive` / `--purge`), ambiguous prefix (mints sessions until pigeonhole-collision on first hex char ŌĆö bound 17 over 16 hex digits), unknown UUID, bootstrap rejection, mutually-exclusive flags (exit 2), no-daemon dial failure (clean error, no panic).
- **Pre-seeded non-bootstrap registry entries are NOT loaded into the in-memory Pool on warm start (Pool.New hydrates only the bootstrap; non-bootstrap entries persist on disk between restarts via the "warm-start does not save" rule).** Discovered while writing the ambiguous-prefix e2e test: the architect's spec proposed seeding `aaaaaaaa-...-001` / `aaaaaaaa-...-002` directly into `sessions.json`, but `sessions.list` returns from `p.sessions` which on warm load contains only the bootstrap. Worked around by minting via `control.SessionsNew` and finding a pigeonhole collision on first hex char (typical run finds one in Ōēż5 mints, bound 17). If a future ticket needs deterministic prefix-collision e2e fixtures, the underlying issue is "warm-start hydrate of non-bootstrap entries" ŌĆö out of scope here.
- **Production diff ~155 LOC in `cmd/pyry/main.go`** (router case + parser + resolver + handler + `sort` import + help text + sentinels). Test diff: ~75 LOC unit + ~290 LOC e2e. Wire surface unchanged.
- See [`docs/specs/architecture/99-cmd-pyry-sessions-rm.md`](specs/architecture/99-cmd-pyry-sessions-rm.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1d-B1, ticket #98)
- **`VerbSessionsRm` + `Remover` seam in `internal/control` ŌĆö wire-only addition that completes the second `sessions.*` namespace member.** New verb `"sessions.rm"`; `SessionsPayload` extended with `omitempty` `ID` and `JSONLPolicy` fields (existing `sessions.new` requests stay byte-identical, pinned by extending `TestProtocol_SessionsRoundTripBackCompat`); new `Response.ErrorCode` field (omitempty, so non-error responses and untyped errors round-trip byte-identically). Server adds `handleSessionsRm` mirroring `handleSessionsNew`'s shape (fresh 30s background ctx, single-shot encode); client `SessionsRm(ctx, sock, id, policy) error` mirrors `SessionsNew`/`SendResize` shape using the `request()` helper. CLI subcommand (`pyry sessions rm`) is a sibling ticket; the wire surface is reachable today only via the typed client.
- **`Sessioner` aggregates per-verb sub-interfaces ŌĆö `NewServer` signature unchanged.** New named interface `Remover { Remove(ctx, sessions.SessionID, sessions.RemoveOptions) error }` lives next to `Sessioner` in `server.go` and is **embedded** into `Sessioner` rather than threaded through as a 7th `NewServer` parameter. `*sessions.Pool` already satisfies the embedded shape via `Pool.Remove` (#94/#95) ŌĆö no adapter, no `cmd/pyry/main.go` change. The 27-call-site fan-out the constructor-parameter route would require is the failure mode the post-#75 architect prompt was rewritten to prevent. Phase 1.1b/c/e (`list`, `rename`, `attach` orchestration) will continue this pattern: one method (or named sub-interface embed) per verb on the same aggregate facade.
- **Wire-level `Response.ErrorCode` for typed-sentinel propagation.** Two stable string tokens (`"session_not_found"`, `"cannot_remove_bootstrap"`) decouple `errors.Is` matching from `Response.Error` text. Server detects sentinels with `errors.Is` (so future server-side wrapping won't break the wire token) and populates both `Error` (verbatim message) and `ErrorCode`; client maps the token back to the bare sentinel (`sessions.ErrSessionNotFound` / `sessions.ErrCannotRemoveBootstrap`) so callers `errors.Is` against it. Renaming a sentinel's message string is no longer a wire-protocol break ŌĆö only the `ErrorCode` enum is. `omitempty` keeps non-typed-error responses byte-identical. `Pool.Remove` returns the sentinels bare today, so client returns the sentinel directly without `fmt.Errorf("%s: %w", resp.Error, sentinel)` (which would double-prefix the message: `"sessions: session not found: sessions: session not found"`).
- **Wire enum (`JSONLPolicy` string `"leave"`/`"archive"`/`"purge"`) deliberately distinct from `sessions.JSONLPolicy` (uint8).** Three motivations: (1) `protocol.go` stays import-free; (2) wire bytes are jq-debuggable strings rather than integers; (3) durable across protocol versions if the underlying enum order ever changes. Empty wire value maps to `JSONLLeave` (matches the internal zero value, so an omitted field gets the documented default); unknown values surface as `"sessions.rm: unknown jsonl policy %q"` in `Response.Error` (fail-loud, no silent fallback). Translation lives in one place ŌĆö `toSessionsPolicy` next to `handleSessionsRm`.
- **Empty `ID` rejected at the handler boundary.** Server-side guard returns `"sessions.rm: missing id"` (no `ErrorCode`). Passing `""` through to `Pool.Remove` would also work but produces the wrong `ErrorCode` (an empty ID is a malformed-input condition, not a "not found" condition). Mirrors `handleResize`'s `payload == nil` guard.
- **Test coverage in `sessions_rm_test.go` (~344 LOC).** `fakeSessioner` (in `sessions_new_test.go`) gained one `Remove` method on the existing struct ŌĆö no new fake type. Mandatory tests: byte-equality back-compat (asserts `sessions.new` payloads + `Response{}` + `Response{OK:true}` marshal byte-identically post-`ID`/`JSONLPolicy`/`ErrorCode` additions); success path; each `JSONLPolicy` value (`""`, `"leave"`, `"archive"`, `"purge"`); both typed-error sentinel propagations (assert `errors.Is` round-trips); other-pool-error untyped path (`errors.Is` against typed sentinels returns false); nil-Sessioner branch; missing-ID guard (zero `Remove` calls on fake); bad-policy guard (zero `Remove` calls on fake); wire shape (hand-rolled `net.Listen` captures the JSON line for three `(id, policy)` cases including empty-policy omitempty); empty-response-as-error.
- **Production diff ~205 LOC across 3 files** (`internal/control/protocol.go`: +55 for `VerbSessionsRm` + `JSONLPolicy` + `ErrorCode` + `SessionsPayload` fields + `Response.ErrorCode`; `internal/control/server.go`: +92 for `Remover` + `Sessioner` embed + dispatch + `handleSessionsRm` + `toSessionsPolicy`; `internal/control/client.go`: +35 for `SessionsRm`). Test diff ~412 LOC. CLI surface unchanged.
- See [knowledge/features/control-plane.md ┬¦ Sessions: removal seam (1.1d-B1)](knowledge/features/control-plane.md), [`docs/specs/architecture/98-control-sessions-rm.md`](specs/architecture/98-control-sessions-rm.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1c-A, ticket #62)
- **`Pool.Rename(id SessionID, newLabel string) error` write primitive** ŌĆö typed mutator for the `label` field. Resolves `id` under `Pool.mu` (write); unknown id ŌćÆ `ErrSessionNotFound` with on-disk and in-memory state byte-identical to before (no `saveLocked` call). No-op rename (`newLabel == sess.label`) also skips `saveLocked`, keeping registry mtime stable for idempotent calls (same precedent as `RotateID(x, x)`). Otherwise mutates `sess.label` and persists via `saveLocked`. The internal seam Phase 1.1c-B's `pyry sessions rename` CLI verb (#47-B) consumes instead of touching `sessions.json` directly.
- **Empty `newLabel` permitted; bootstrap substitution from #60 falls out for free.** `Rename` writes the verbatim string through to disk and does not branch on `sess.bootstrap`. `Rename(bootstrapID, "")` clears the on-disk label, then `Pool.List`'s synthetic `"bootstrap"` substitution resumes; `Rename(bootstrapID, "primary")` persists `"primary"` and `Pool.List` reflects it verbatim. Substitution rule lives in `List`, not in `Rename` ŌĆö uniform across consumers.
- **Save-failure rollback as belt-and-suspenders.** `saveRegistryLocked`'s temp+rename discipline makes partial writes unreachable, so disk state never disagrees with the rolled-back in-memory state. The `sess.label = prev` rollback exists so a subsequent retry has consistent inputs and a `Lookup` after a failed `Rename` doesn't return a label that isn't on disk. `saveLocked` error returned verbatim ŌĆö no `Rename:`-specific wrap, preserves `errors.Is` symmetry with other persist sites.
- **`Session.label` guarded by `Pool.mu`, not `Session.lcMu`.** Lifecycle goroutine in `Session.Run` does not read `label`; only readers are `Pool.List` (RLock) and `saveRegistryLocked` (Lock ŌĆö caller holds write). Same shape as `RotateID`'s mutation of `session.id` without `lcMu`. Doc-comment on `Session.label` updated to reflect mutation via `Pool.Rename`. No new lock-order edges.
- **No new exported types or sentinels.** `Pool.Rename` is the only new exported name; `ErrSessionNotFound` (existing) is the only sentinel. Strict full-`SessionID` only ŌĆö UUID-prefix resolution is a CLI/UX concern for 47-B that may reuse `Pool.List`. No validation of `newLabel` (length, character class, uniqueness) ŌĆö same posture as `Pool.Create`'s unvalidated `label` parameter.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md ┬¦ Pool.Rename](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1b-A, ticket #60)
- **`Pool.List() []SessionInfo` read primitive** ŌĆö typed snapshot of every session in the pool (bootstrap and minted alike), sorted by `LastActiveAt` desc with `SessionID` asc tiebreak for determinism. Each entry carries `ID`, `Label`, `LifecycleState`, `LastActiveAt`, `Bootstrap`. Read-only ŌĆö no `lastActiveAt` bump, no state transition, no `persist()`. The internal seam Phase 1.1b-B's `pyry sessions list` CLI verb (#46-B) consumes instead of touching `sessions.json` directly.
- **New `SessionInfo` value type, deep-copy-safe by construction** ŌĆö every field is a value (`SessionID`/`string`/`time.Time` are values; `lifecycleState` is a `uint8` enum). Mutating a `SessionInfo` cannot affect pool state or registry contents. No defensive cloning, no documentation contract that callers can violate.
- **Synthetic `"bootstrap"` label substitution at this layer, not in 46-B's renderer.** When the bootstrap's on-disk `label` is empty, `List` substitutes `"bootstrap"` ŌĆö but the on-disk registry entry is **not** mutated. An operator-set bootstrap label passes through verbatim; the `Bootstrap` bool is the discriminator, not the label string. Putting the substitution at the read primitive (rather than at the wire/CLI layer) means every future internal consumer gets the same UX guarantee.
- **Why a new type, not extending `SnapshotEntry{ID, PID}`** ŌĆö `SnapshotEntry` exists for the rotation watcher's closure-over-primitives boundary (`internal/sessions/rotation` cannot import `internal/sessions`). Adding `lifecycleState` to it would either bloat every rotation snapshot or push the enum into `rotation`'s import set. Two distinct types, one per consumer, is cleaner than a shared shape.
- **Lock order ŌĆö unchanged.** `Pool.mu` (RLock) ŌåÆ `Session.lcMu` (Lock). Identical to `Pool.saveLocked` and `Pool.pickLRUVictim`. `id`/`label`/`bootstrap` read off-`lcMu` (immutable post-`New`/`RotateID` from any reader holding `Pool.mu`); `lcState`/`lastActiveAt` read under `lcMu` (the lifecycle goroutine writes them there). Each session's pair is read under one `lcMu` acquire ŌĆö no torn reads.
- **No new ADR ŌĆö design follows existing patterns.** Typed read accessor; `sort.Slice` to match `registry.go`'s style; per-consumer value type per the existing `SnapshotEntry` convention; no new sentinel errors (the method has no error path).
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md ┬¦ Pool.List](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1a-A2, ticket #73)
- **`Pool.Create(ctx, label) (SessionID, error)`** ŌĆö user-facing primitive that mints a fresh non-bootstrap session: `NewID` ŌåÆ build `*Session` in `stateEvicted` (label verbatim, `bootstrap=false`, `ResumeLast=false`, `ClaudeArgs` cloned + `--session-id <uuid>` appended) ŌåÆ register-and-persist under `Pool.mu` (rollback on save failure) ŌåÆ `RegisterAllocatedUUID` (rotation skip-set) ŌåÆ `supervise` (#72's seam) ŌåÆ `Pool.Activate` (cap-aware spawn from #41). One well-tested entry point for Phase 1.1a-B's `sessions.new` verb (#71) and Phase 2.0's channel-driven auto-mint. Bootstrap unchanged (`Pool.Lookup("")` returns the same `*Session` pre/post `Create`).
- **Per-session template fields on `*Pool`** ŌĆö `sessionTpl SessionConfig` (shallow copy of `cfg.Bootstrap` captured at `New()`) + `idleTimeoutDefault time.Duration` (mirror of `Config.IdleTimeout`), both read-only after `New`. `Create` clones `tpl.ClaudeArgs` via `slices.Clone` (appending to the template directly would mutate it across calls), and mints a fresh `supervisor.NewBridge(p.log)` per session in service mode (`tpl.Bridge != nil`) ŌĆö sharing one bridge across N sessions would multiplex their I/O into a single client view.
- **Persist-then-activate ordering, with id-or-empty discriminator.** Save failure with claude already running would leave an unsupervised orphan whose JSONL has no on-disk record; a registry-only entry that didn't activate is benign (recoverable on next `Activate`). Returned `SessionID == ""` iff nothing persisted; non-empty id + non-nil err means "entry on disk, decide what to do." Caller uses `errors.Is(err, ErrPoolNotRunning)` to distinguish the not-running case from an Activate failure.
- **Cap pre-flight via `Pool.Activate` directly (choice (a))** ŌĆö the new session is in `stateEvicted` at cap-check time, so it doesn't increment `active`; `pickLRUVictim` excludes the target. No duplicated cap logic and no transient inconsistent view from `Snapshot`/`Lookup` (the alternative ŌĆö pre-flight before registering ŌĆö would create one).
- **Lock order unchanged.** `Pool.mu ŌåÆ Session.lcMu` for the persist couple; `capMu ŌåÆ Pool.mu ŌåÆ Session.lcMu` on the cap path. `Create` does NOT hold `p.mu` across `supervise`, `Activate`, or `RegisterAllocatedUUID` ŌĆö the lock is taken only for register+persist, then released. ctx-cancellation race documented: caller may see `(id, ctx.Err)` while the lifecycle goroutine spins up anyway (it respects the pool's run-ctx, not the caller's).
- **No new public types or sentinels.** `Pool.Create` is the only new exported name; `ErrPoolNotRunning` (from #72) is the only sentinel propagated.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md ┬¦ Pool.Create](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.1a-A1, ticket #72)
- **Pool supervisor fan-out seam** ŌĆö unexported `Pool.supervise(sess *Session) error` schedules `sess.Run(gctx)` on `Pool.Run`'s live errgroup. Returns the new sentinel `ErrPoolNotRunning` when called before `Run` has wired the handle or after `Run` has cleared it (matchable with `errors.Is`). The helper is the join point Phase 1.1a-A2's `Pool.Create(ctx, label)` consumes; the bootstrap fan-out inside `Pool.Run` is itself rewritten to call `supervise` so the helper is exercised in production from day one. Watcher fan-out is unchanged (not a `*Session`).
- **Supervisor handle on `*Pool`** ŌĆö `runGroup *errgroup.Group` + `runCtx context.Context`, both guarded by `Pool.mu` (RWMutex) and read together so a caller never sees a half-initialised handle. Set in `Pool.Run` under `Pool.mu` (write) right after `errgroup.WithContext`; cleared in a `defer` so a panicking goroutine still resets the handle. `supervise` reads under `Pool.mu` (RLock) and calls `g.Go` *off-lock*. No new lock-order edges (`Pool.mu ŌåÆ Session.lcMu` and `Pool.capMu ŌåÆ Pool.mu ŌåÆ Session.lcMu` unchanged) ŌĆö the helper does not touch `Session.lcMu`.
- **Why fields-on-Pool, not a separate guard struct** ŌĆö `Pool.mu` already protects every other "what's in this pool right now" read. A second mutex would double the lock count without buying anything; RWMutex matches the access pattern (N concurrent supervise readers, one-shot writes by `Run` setup/teardown). Concurrent `supervise` callers don't contend with each other.
- **Race-with-teardown is benign** ŌĆö a `supervise` call interleaved with the deferred clear either (a) acquires RLock first, schedules onto a group whose ctx is about to cancel, and `Session.Run` exits via the existing shutdown path, or (b) acquires after, observes `nil`, returns the sentinel. No silent leak, no deadlock.
- **Defensive wrap on the bootstrap call** ŌĆö `Pool.Run` does `if err := p.supervise(bootstrap); err != nil { return fmt.Errorf("sessions: supervise bootstrap: %w", err) }` even though the precondition is established two lines above. Cheap insurance against a future reordering bug.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-package.md ┬¦ Supervisor handle](knowledge/features/sessions-package.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.2c-B, ticket #41)
- **Concurrent active cap (LRU eviction)** ŌĆö `Config.ActiveCap` bounds the number of concurrently running claudes. `<= 0` is unset (uncapped, byte-identical to 1.2c-A); `>= 1` enforces. When activating one more session would exceed the cap, the LRU peer (oldest `lastActiveAt` among currently-active sessions, excluding the target) is evicted via the new public `Session.Evict` primitive before the new spawn proceeds. **No CLI flag yet** ŌĆö Phase 2.0 will wire `-pyry-active-cap` when the auto-mint workload makes it load-bearing.
- **`Session.Evict(ctx)` public primitive** ŌĆö symmetric to `Activate`. Force-eviction: unlike the idle timer, it does **not** defer for `attached > 0`. The cap is a hard limit; an attached caller will see EOF on its bridge. Phase 2.0 may add an attach-aware filter to the LRU candidate set; not in scope for #41. Pairs `evictCh` (buffered 1 signal) with `evictedCh` (closed-on-evicted broadcast), mirroring `activateCh`/`activeCh`.
- **`Pool.capMu` outermost lock** ŌĆö taken only on the cap path (`activeCap > 0`). Lock order: `Pool.capMu ŌåÆ Pool.mu ŌåÆ Session.lcMu`. Serialises cap-check + victim eviction + new spawn so concurrent `Activate`s can't both observe `active < cap` and both proceed. Never re-acquired by callees, so `Session.Evict`'s callback into `Pool.persist` (which takes `Pool.mu`) is deadlock-free. The uncapped path doesn't take `capMu` at all ŌĆö "byte-identical when unset" includes "doesn't even take the cap mutex".
- **`Pool.pickLRUVictim`** ŌĆö O(n) iteration over `pool.sessions` under `Pool.mu.RLock`, reads each `Session.lcState`/`lastActiveAt` under `lcMu`, returns the oldest-`lastActiveAt` peer (excluding target). Premature optimisation rejected: a heap/linked-list would defeat the zero-cost-when-unset property and add a counter-vs-truth drift class of bug for an O(n) cost that doesn't matter at pyry's scale (Ōēż 100s of sessions).
- **`Session.touchLastActive`** ŌĆö bumps `lastActiveAt` in-memory only on a cap-path `Activate` against an already-active session. **Not persisted** (the registry's `lastActiveAt` only flushes on transitions). Keeps in-memory LRU ordering reflective of the most recent touch.
- **`Pool.Activate` is now the spawn-path entry, not just a thin Lookup wrapper.** Phase 2.0's router calls this. Cap-unset path: one early-return branch and forward to `Session.Activate`. Cap-set path: cap check + victim eviction + new spawn under `capMu`.
- See [knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md](knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md), [ADR 006](knowledge/decisions/006-concurrent-active-cap-lru.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.2c-A, ticket #40)
- **Idle eviction + lazy respawn** ŌĆö per-`*Session` lifecycle goroutine drives a two-state machine (`active` Ōåö `evicted`). When `attached == 0` and the idle timer fires, the supervisor's inner ctx is cancelled and claude exits cleanly; the JSONL on disk is preserved. `Session.Activate(ctx)` respawns the supervisor pointing at the same JSONL on disk so the conversation continues. `Session.Run` rewritten from one-line supervisor delegate into a `runActive` / `runEvicted` loop; `Pool.Run` shape **unchanged** (multi-session fan-out is Phase 1.1's job).
- **Activity = attach state** ŌĆö while `attached > 0` the timer re-arms on fire (poll-with-grace; eviction may overshoot the configured timeout by up to one window). `last_active_at` is bumped on every state transition for the upcoming LRU follow-up's victim selection.
- **`-pyry-idle-timeout` flag** ŌĆö production default `15m`, `0` disables eviction entirely (test default + operator escape hatch). Wired through `Config.IdleTimeout` ŌåÆ `SessionConfig.IdleTimeout` (per-session override falls back to pool default).
- **Activate-before-Attach contract** ŌĆö `bridge.Attach` on an evicted session would block on the pipe forever. `internal/control.Session` interface gained `Activate(ctx)`; `handleAttach` calls it with a 30s timeout cap before binding the bridge. `handleStatus` does **not** activate (faithful `PhaseStopped` for evicted; no spurious wakeups from a poll). Wire response on respawn failure: `attach: activate: <err>`.
- **Registry `lifecycle_state` field** ŌĆö `"active"` / `"evicted"`, `omitempty` so the dominant active case stays off disk (preserves #34's idempotent-reload byte-stability). Old pyry binaries ignore the field; new pyry reading old files defaults to `"active"`. Bootstrap warm-starts in whatever state the registry says ŌĆö including starting in `evicted` if pyry was stopped while evicted.
- **Lock order: `Pool.mu ŌåÆ Session.lcMu`** ŌĆö `Session.lcMu` protects `lcState` / `attached` / `activeCh` / `lastActiveAt` (when read for the registry snapshot). `Session.transitionTo` releases `lcMu` before calling `Pool.persist` so `saveLocked`'s per-session re-acquire doesn't deadlock. `RotateID` mutates `session.id` without `lcMu` ŌĆö documented invariant (today's only callers run before any lifecycle goroutine observes the id).
- **Concurrency primitives** ŌĆö `activeCh` (closed-on-active broadcast) + `activateCh` (buffered 1 signal). `Activate` snapshots `activeCh` under `lcMu` *before* waiting so a concurrent evict-replace doesn't drop the wakeup. Concurrent `Activate`s collapse to one signal via the buffered send.
- See [knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md](knowledge/features/idle-eviction.md), [ADR 005](knowledge/decisions/005-idle-eviction-state-machine.md).

### Codebase (rotation fix, ticket #118)
- **Rotation-watcher path comparison resolves symlinks at construction.** `Watcher` gained an unexported `resolvedDir` (`filepath.EvalSymlinks(cfg.Dir)`, captured once in `New`). `handleCreate`'s match gate became `filepath.Clean(open) == filepath.Join(w.resolvedDir, base)`. Pre-#118 the gate compared `filepath.Clean(open)` to `filepath.Clean(fullPath)` from the fsnotify event ŌĆö `filepath.Clean` is lexical and never resolves symlinks, so on macOS where `/var ŌåÆ /private/var`, fsnotify's `/var/...` ev.Name and lsof's `/private/var/...` probe output never matched and rotation was silently dropped (symptom: session UUID stops updating after `/clear`). Affects every macOS user whose `~/.claude/projects/` lives behind a symlink (custom HOME, external-drive home) and every `t.TempDir`-based test on macOS ŌĆö surfaced by #55's e2e harness landing `t.TempDir()` under `/var/folders/...`.
- **Resolve once, not per event ŌĆö three properties.** (1) Zero per-event syscalls; (2) no race window between event and resolution (the directory's lifetime spans the watcher's, ducking the AC's "file unlinked between event and resolution" failure mode); (3) no API change ŌĆö `Config.Dir` stays as-is, `pool.go`'s call site untouched. `EvalSymlinks` failure at startup logs `Warn` and falls back to `cfg.Dir` unmodified ŌĆö the macOS-symlink case continues to fail in that specific run (no worse than today), startup proceeds.
- **`TestWatcher_DetectsRotationThroughSymlink` regression test.** Explicit `os.Symlink` from a side dir to the real sessions dir; watcher set up against the link; probe reports the *resolved* path (mimicking what `lsof` / `/proc/<pid>/fd` actually return). Fails on the pre-#118 code (gate rejects `Clean(real/...)` vs `Clean(link/...)` because they're different absolute paths); passes after the fix. Portable across Linux and macOS via the explicit `os.Symlink` ŌĆö Linux CI exercises the symlink branch even though Linux defaults don't put `t.TempDir` behind a symlink. Existing six tests that build a `dir` from `t.TempDir()` were updated to wrap with `filepath.EvalSymlinks(t.TempDir())` so probe-returned paths and the watcher's resolved view stay in the same canonical form.
- **Production diff: ~8 lines in `internal/sessions/rotation/watcher.go`** (one struct field, ~5 lines in `New`, one rewritten line in `handleCreate`). Test diff: ~30 LOC for the new test plus mechanical 2-line additions across the existing tests. Two files total. Zero consumer call sites touched.
- See [knowledge/features/rotation-watcher.md ┬¦ Symlink-resolved match path](knowledge/features/rotation-watcher.md), `lessons.md ┬¦ fsnotify reports as-watched, kernel probes report canonicalised`.

### Codebase (Phase 1.2b-B, ticket #39)
- **Live `/clear` rotation watcher** ŌĆö `internal/sessions/rotation` package: fsnotify on `cfg.ClaudeSessionsDir` + per-PID FD probe (Linux walks `/proc/<pid>/fd`, macOS shells out to `lsof -nP -p <pid> -F fn`). On a CREATE for `<new>.jsonl` whose UUID a tracked PID has open, calls `Pool.RotateID(old, new)` ŌĆö same seam #38 established. Detection latency ~250ms worst-case (probeWithRetry walks 0/50/200ms attempts to handle CREATE-before-open races).
- **`Pool.Run` errgroup wrap** ŌĆö `golang.org/x/sync/errgroup` ties the bootstrap supervisor and the watcher; cancellation propagates both ways. Phase 1.1's N-session fan-out reuses the same wrapper ŌĆö the extension point is one `g.Go` per pool entry.
- **Pyry-allocated UUID skip set on `Pool`** ŌĆö `RegisterAllocatedUUID` / `IsAllocated`. Consume-on-first-hit, 30s TTL pruned opportunistically, all under `p.mu` (write). No live caller in 1.2b-B (pyry still uses `--continue`); scaffolding lands now so Phase 1.1's `claude --session-id` is a one-liner.
- **`rotation.Config` closures over primitives** ŌĆö the rotation package never imports `internal/sessions`. The `SessionID Ōåö string` conversion happens once, inside `Pool.Run`'s closure wiring. `Pool.Snapshot` returns a small `SnapshotEntry` struct; `snapshotForRotation` translates to `rotation.SessionRef`.
- **Failure posture** ŌĆö rotation detection is never load-bearing. fsnotify init failure, missing `lsof`, missing `/proc`, save failure during `OnRotate` ŌĆö all logged warn/debug; pyry continues. `MkdirAll(dir, 0700)` for a not-yet-existing claude dir.
- **First new external runtime dep since `creack/pty`** ŌĆö `github.com/fsnotify/fsnotify` v1.10.0, justified in [ADR 004](knowledge/decisions/004-fsnotify-for-rotation-detection.md). `golang.org/x/sync` lands as a sibling for errgroup.
- See [knowledge/features/rotation-watcher.md](knowledge/features/rotation-watcher.md), [ADR 004](knowledge/decisions/004-fsnotify-for-rotation-detection.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.2b-A, ticket #38)
- **Startup JSONL reconciliation** ŌĆö `Pool.New` scans `~/.claude/projects/<encoded-cwd>/<uuid>.jsonl`, picks the most-recently-modified one, and rotates the registry's bootstrap entry to that UUID if it disagrees. Self-heals after `/clear` (claude rotates session UUIDs on `/clear`; without reconciliation, post-`pyry stop` the registry would still point at the pre-`/clear` UUID).
- **`Pool.RotateID(oldID, newID)`** ŌĆö atomic swap of in-memory map key + bootstrap pointer + `saveLocked`, all under `p.mu` (write). `RotateID(x, x)` is a no-op; unknown old id returns `ErrSessionNotFound`. Bumps `last_active_at`; preserves `created_at`. The load-bearing seam reused by Phase 1.2b-B (live-detection via fsnotify).
- **`encodeWorkdir`** ŌĆö claude maps both `/` AND `.` to `-` in its `~/.claude/projects/` path component (verified empirically 2026-05-02). `/foo/.bar` ŌåÆ `-foo--bar` (note the doubled dash). Unexported; encoding lives inside `internal/sessions` and `cmd/pyry` only sees the resolved path via `DefaultClaudeSessionsDir`.
- **JSONL location** ŌĆö files live directly in `<encoded-cwd>/<uuid>.jsonl`. There is **no** `sessions/` subdirectory (the ticket body claimed otherwise; the spec followed reality).
- **Failure posture** ŌĆö missing/unreadable claude dir is logged warn and ignored (startup proceeds). Save failure during rotation is fatal-at-startup (matches 1.2a cold-start). The pre-rotation JSONL is never deleted or modified ŌĆö only the registry pointer moves.
- **Expected one-time rotation in 1.2a** ŌĆö on the second `pyry` restart, claude's UUID ŌēĀ pyry's mint, so reconcile fires once and logs an Info line. Becomes rare after Phase 1.1+ wires `claude --session-id <uuid>`.
- See [knowledge/features/jsonl-reconciliation.md](knowledge/features/jsonl-reconciliation.md).

### Codebase (Phase 1.2a, ticket #34)
- **Session registry on disk** ŌĆö `~/.pyry/<sanitized-name>/sessions.json` (file 0600, dir 0700), sibling to the per-name socket. Schema: `version` (forward-marker), `sessions[]` with `id` / `label` / `created_at` / `last_active_at` / `bootstrap`. Default `encoding/json` decoder tolerates unknown fields for forward compat.
- **`Pool.New` load-or-mint** ŌĆö Cold start (missing or empty file) mints a fresh UUID and writes the registry before returning. Warm start reads the bootstrap-marked entry, reuses its UUID + metadata, and does **not** rewrite the file (warm reload is not a state change). Malformed JSON is fatal at startup ŌĆö operator must fix or remove.
- **Atomic write seam** ŌĆö `saveRegistryLocked` does `os.CreateTemp` ŌåÆ `Chmod 0600` ŌåÆ encode ŌåÆ fsync ŌåÆ close ŌåÆ `os.Rename`. Rename is the commit point; partial JSON is unreachable in the target. `defer os.Remove(tmp)` cleans up orphaned temps best-effort. `Pool.saveLocked` is the package-internal hook Phase 1.1's `Pool.Add` / `Rename` / `Remove` will call before returning success ŌĆö caller holds `Pool.mu` (write) across the disk I/O.
- **Bootstrap marker on disk** ŌĆö `bootstrap: true` is persisted explicitly so `Pool.Lookup("")` doesn't depend on file ordering. Phase 1.1's `pyry sessions rm <bootstrap-uuid>` thus has a clean question to answer (refuse, or promote another entry) instead of relying on array position. `omitempty` keeps non-bootstrap entries clean on disk.
- **Stable disk ordering** ŌĆö `sortEntriesByCreatedAt` (then by `ID`) before write makes the file's byte content a deterministic function of the in-memory set, defeating Go's randomized map iteration and giving the AC's idempotent-reload guarantee. Degenerate for 1.2a's single entry; the property is paid for upfront ahead of 1.1.
- See [knowledge/features/sessions-registry.md](knowledge/features/sessions-registry.md).
